- jolt-core/src/lib.rs — added `pub mod server;` and re-export of three names.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-022 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-023 (priority 23): "Implement JoltServer::new() → Self with sensible defaults (port 8080, threads = num_cpus)." `num_cpus` is not yet a workspace dependency — check `Cargo.toml` first. Two options: (a) add the `num_cpus` crate, or (b) use `std::thread::available_parallelism().map(NonZeroUsize::get).unwrap_or(1)`. Recommend (b): no new dep, std-only, available since Rust 1.59. The result type is `io::Result<NonZeroUsize>`; the `unwrap_or(1)` fallback covers the rare platforms where it returns Err. This keeps Cargo.toml stable and matches the workspace-dependencies-only philosophy from phase00.
- JOLT-RS-024 (priority 24): builder methods `port(u16) -> Self`, `threads(usize) -> Self`, `cors(CorsConfig) -> Self`. Note the asymmetry: `cors_config: Option<CorsConfig>` but the builder method is `cors(CorsConfig)` not `cors_config(Option<CorsConfig>)` — the builder takes a non-Option and wraps in Some(). PRD doesn't list a `tls(...)` builder in 024; that may show up in Phase 6 alongside the TLS fill-in. Don't add it speculatively.
- JOLT-RS-025 (priority 25): `start(self, router: Router) -> ...` binds 0.0.0.0:port, uses `tokio::signal` for graceful shutdown. The `axum-server` crate isn't a direct dep yet (it's named in the spec for Phase 6 TLS); for non-TLS start, plain `axum::serve` over `tokio::net::TcpListener` is enough. When TLS lands in Phase 6, the start path branches on `tls_config.is_some()`.
- JOLT-RS-026 (priority 26): `endpoint<E: Endpoint>(self) -> Self` requires the `Endpoint` trait, which is JOLT-RS-028's deliverable. Do 026 AFTER 028 unless a stub trait gets introduced earlier. Re-ordering note: phase05 (022..027) and phase06 (028..032) interleave at the trait surface — be alert to this when picking the next item. The strict priority order (lower-priority-first) may hit a compile error at 026 if 028 isn't in yet; if so, JOLT-RS-028 is the dependency to pull forward, not 026 to defer.
- The stub structs are CURRENTLY non-constructible from outside the crate via field syntax (no fields), but constructible via the unit-struct expression `CorsConfig` (just the name). This is intentional — when CORS/TLS land, fields get added and `pub` callers transition from `CorsConfig` to `CorsConfig { origins: vec![...], ... }`. If a builder method like `cors(CorsConfig)` ships in 024 before fields are added, the test `JoltServer::new().cors(CorsConfig)` will compile and work — useful for exercising the builder shape without needing real CORS semantics yet.
- No new workspace dependencies were added. Cargo.lock is unchanged. The next iteration should preserve this discipline: add deps only when an item explicitly needs one, not in advance.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-023: JoltServer::new() with sensible defaults

PRD item: JOLT-RS-023 (priority 23, phase05-server-builder) — Implement JoltServer::new() → Self with sensible defaults (port 8080, threads = num_cpus).

Verification:
- `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::server` → 1/1 passed (`new_uses_default_port_8080`); 0 failed; 65 filtered out; finished in 0.00s.
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 0.37s; no regressions.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 66 passed total (up from 65); 0 failed.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..022 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- Used `std::thread::available_parallelism().map(NonZeroUsize::get).unwrap_or(1)` per JOLT-RS-022's recommendation. No new workspace dependency (the alternative was the `num_cpus` crate). std-only since Rust 1.59. The `unwrap_or(1)` fallback covers the rare platforms where the call returns `Err`; a single-threaded fallback is the safest possible default — guarantees forward progress without claiming parallelism that isn't there.
- Did NOT add `impl Default for JoltServer`. Two reasons: (a) JOLT-RS-022's progress note explicitly flagged this — `JoltServer::new()` is the construction story for this type, not Default; (b) clippy's `new_without_default` lint would fire here, but clippy isn't part of the verification gate (no `clippy` invocation in any progress entry, no `[lints]` table in Cargo.toml). If clippy enforcement lands later, derive Default with `Default::default() -> Self::new()` then.
- Did NOT make the threads computation a const or a separate `default_threads()` helper. It's three lines and used in exactly one place. A helper would just hide the std call behind a name and force a future reader to chase the indirection. If JOLT-RS-024's `threads(usize)` builder ends up wanting "reset to default" semantics, factor at that point.
- Did NOT cache the available_parallelism result. The cost is a single syscall on construction; `JoltServer::new()` is called once per server lifetime. Caching would be premature.
- `pub fn new() -> Self` (not `&self` arg, no Result return). The PRD signature is unambiguous. `available_parallelism()` returning Err doesn't propagate up; we choose the fallback inline because the caller has no recovery action — the server should still start with a single thread rather than refusing to construct.
- Added one test only: `new_uses_default_port_8080` — the PRD-mandated verification. Did NOT add tests for `threads > 0` or `cors_config.is_none() / tls_config.is_none()`. Rationale: JOLT-RS-027 ("Write server builder unit tests: defaults, builder chain, port binding conflict handling") is the dedicated tests slice for phase05. Adding more default-coverage tests here would steal scope from 027 and leave it under-defined. The PRD verification uses singular ("Unit test:" not "Unit tests:") which reinforces the minimal-slice interpretation.
- Test lives in a new `mod server` submodule of `tests.rs`, sibling to `request_ext_extensions`. Matches the existing per-type-family test module convention (`method`, `status_code`, `request`, `response`, `request_ext`). The filter `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::server` will widen cleanly when 027 adds more tests.
- Module-level docstring on `server.rs` updated: removed "Defaults" from the list of subsequent PRD items (they've now landed); kept the rest. Anchors the next agent so they don't re-derive what's done.
- `use std::num::NonZeroUsize;` is at module scope rather than function scope. Matches the file's other top-level imports (when more arrive). Single-use imports as `use std::num::NonZeroUsize;` rather than fully-qualified paths inline keeps the body of `new()` readable.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-024 (priority 24): builder methods `port(u16) -> Self`, `threads(usize) -> Self`, `cors(CorsConfig) -> Self`. Standard chained-builder pattern: each takes `mut self`, mutates a field, returns `self`. Note again the asymmetry called out in JOLT-RS-022 notes: `cors_config: Option<CorsConfig>` field but the method is `cors(CorsConfig)` — the method wraps the arg in `Some(...)`. PRD doesn't list a `tls(...)` builder; resist the symmetry temptation — TLS lands in Phase 6 and adding it speculatively now is premature.
- JOLT-RS-024's verification test should chain `.port(3000).threads(4)` from `JoltServer::new()` and assert both fields are set. Reuses the `mod server` module added here.
- For JOLT-RS-024, decide between `mut self` (consumes-and-returns) vs `&mut self` (returns Self by clone). The `mut self` pattern is canonical Rust builders (e.g., axum's `Router`, hyper's request builders). Recommend `mut self` — no Clone needed, single ownership flows linearly through the chain.
- The `available_parallelism().unwrap_or(1)` fallback means in CI sandboxes that strip /proc/cpuinfo, the server defaults to 1 worker. If that's ever load-bearing for a test, override explicitly via `.threads(N)` from JOLT-RS-024 — don't add a second-tier fallback like a hardcoded `4`.
- JOLT-RS-024's `threads(usize)` accepts any usize including 0. PRD doesn't say "non-zero" — leave it permissive at this stage. If 0 turns out to be a foot-gun (some tokio runtime configs reject it), validate at `start()` time in JOLT-RS-025 rather than poisoning the builder, since the builder-vs-start error surface is what callers will hit.
- Clippy's `new_without_default` lint is suppressed-by-absence (no clippy gate), but if a future PRD adds `cargo clippy --workspace -- -D warnings` to verification, JOLT-RS-023 is the place where Default needs to land. Add `impl Default for JoltServer { fn default() -> Self { Self::new() } }` then; the existing `new_uses_default_port_8080` test still locks in the contract.
- JOLT-RS-026 still depends on the `Endpoint` trait from JOLT-RS-028 (called out in JOLT-RS-022 notes). When 026 is up next in priority order, expect a compile error against `E: Endpoint` and pull 028 forward — don't defer 026.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-024: JoltServer builder methods (port, threads, cors)

PRD item: JOLT-RS-024 (priority 24, phase05-server-builder) — Implement builder methods: `port(u16) -> Self`, `threads(usize) -> Self`, `cors(CorsConfig) -> Self`.

Verification:
- `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::server` → 4/4 passed (1 prior + 3 new); 0 failed; 65 filtered out; finished in 0.00s.
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 0.34s; no regressions.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 69 passed total (up from 66); 0 failed.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..023 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- Used `mut self` consume-and-return shape (not `&mut self`) per JOLT-RS-023's progress recommendation. Matches axum's `Router` and the canonical Rust builder pattern; ownership flows linearly through the chain so no Clone is needed and the type stays `!Clone`-friendly.
- `cors(CorsConfig) -> Self` takes a non-Option `CorsConfig` and wraps in `Some(...)` internally, per the asymmetry called out in JOLT-RS-022/023 notes. Callers write `.cors(CorsConfig)` rather than `.cors(Some(CorsConfig))` — fewer wrapper tokens at the call site, and "no CORS" is expressed by simply not calling `.cors(...)`.
- Did NOT add a `tls(TlsConfig) -> Self` builder. PRD-024 doesn't list it; the JOLT-RS-022/023 progress notes explicitly flag the symmetry temptation and recommend deferring TLS to Phase 6 alongside the TlsConfig field fill-in. Adding it speculatively would prejudge the TLS construction path (likely needs cert/key paths or PEM bytes, possibly fallible — `Result<Self, _>` rather than `Self`).
- Did NOT validate `threads != 0` in the builder, per JOLT-RS-023 progress note: leave the builder permissive; validate at `start()` in JOLT-RS-025 if a tokio runtime config rejects 0. This keeps the builder-vs-start error surface coherent (builders never fail; start can).
- Did NOT add a "reset to default" overload (`port_default()` etc.). YAGNI — no caller needs it, and `JoltServer::new()` already produces defaults so callers can re-construct if they truly want a reset.
- Three tests (one per method, plus a non-clobber test). The PRD-mandated test is `builder_chain_sets_port_and_threads` (chained `.port(3000).threads(4)` sets both). Added two more tightly-scoped ones: `cors_builder_wraps_arg_in_some` (locks in the Option-wrapping contract that the asymmetric signature creates) and `builder_methods_preserve_unspecified_defaults` (proves `.port()` doesn't clobber threads / cors / tls — the kind of regression a future "let me consolidate the builder into one fn" refactor could introduce). All three live in the existing `mod server` test module.
- The non-clobber test reads `JoltServer::new().threads` first to capture the platform-dependent default, then asserts equality after `.port(9090)`. Using a literal value would make the test brittle on different CI machines. The pattern matches the spirit of JOLT-RS-023's progress note about CI sandboxes that strip /proc/cpuinfo.
- All four `JoltServer` fields remain `pub`; the builder methods are additive. Tests still poke at fields directly (`server.port`, `server.threads`, etc.) — kept that way because (a) it matches the existing crate convention, (b) there's no explicit field encapsulation requirement in phase05, and (c) JOLT-RS-022's progress note explicitly noted that pub fields are easier to wall off later than to add back.
- No new workspace dependencies. Cargo.lock unchanged.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/server.rs — added three builder methods to `impl JoltServer`.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — extended `mod server` with 3 new tests; updated import to include `CorsConfig`.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-024 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-025 (priority 25): `start(self, router: Router) -> ...` binds 0.0.0.0:port, uses `tokio::signal` for graceful shutdown. Plain `axum::serve` over `tokio::net::TcpListener` is enough for non-TLS; `axum-server` lands with TLS in Phase 6. The `router: Router` parameter is axum's `Router`, NOT the project's eventual `jolt_core::Router` (that's JOLT-RS-033..037, a tower::Service wrapper). The phase05 contract is "consumer hands us an axum Router; we serve it" — keep it simple. The PRD verification is "Manual: server starts, curl localhost:8080 returns 404 (empty router)" — there's no automated test required; if you want one anyway, bind to `0.0.0.0:0` to let the OS pick a free port and use `tokio::time::timeout` to bound the test. `tokio::signal` is std-feature-gated in tokio's features; check Cargo.toml has `tokio = { ..., features = [..., "signal"] }` before the import. Currently jolt-core depends on `tokio = { workspace = true, features = ["full"] }` — `full` includes signal — but verify before assuming.
- JOLT-RS-025 also needs to decide: does `start` consume `self` or `&self`? PRD says `start(self, router)`, so consume. That's compatible with the builder chain `JoltServer::new().port(3000).start(router).await` since the chain ends in a `Self`.
- JOLT-RS-025's return type is unspecified in the PRD step. Recommended shape: `pub async fn start(self, router: axum::Router) -> std::io::Result<()>` — propagates bind failures (port-in-use, EACCES on low ports) to the caller; `tokio::signal` failures also fold into io::Result naturally.
- JOLT-RS-025 implies the threads field becomes load-bearing: tokio's multi-thread runtime worker count is set at `Runtime::new()` time, but `JoltServer::start` runs inside an existing `#[tokio::main]` runtime (caller's). Two paths: (a) ignore `self.threads` for now and document it as advisory until JOLT-RS-???-runtime-build lands, or (b) construct an inner `Runtime::new_multi_thread().worker_threads(self.threads)` and `.block_on(serve)`. (a) is simpler and preserves caller's runtime control; (b) duplicates the runtime and confuses async lifetime. Recommend (a) — leave a TODO that `self.threads` is currently unused at start; phase05 doesn't have a test for it.
- The `cors(CorsConfig) -> Self` builder doesn't yet APPLY the CORS config — it just stores it. The actual `tower-http::cors` layer wiring lands when Phase 2 (CORS middleware) gets reordered or filled in. Until then, a caller that calls `.cors(CorsConfig)` and then `.start()` will see no CORS effect. Document this when a phase02 task lands; not a blocker for phase05.
- JOLT-RS-026 (priority 26) still depends on the `Endpoint` trait from JOLT-RS-028 — call this out one more time. When 026 is the next priority, the right move is to pull JOLT-RS-028 forward (or add a stub trait), not defer 026. The strict-priority rule will produce a compile error otherwise.
- The 3 new tests bring the `mod server` filter total to 4. JOLT-RS-027's "Write server builder unit tests: defaults, builder chain, port binding conflict handling" can extend this module further. Port-binding-conflict needs an actual TCP bind, so that test will likely move into a `#[tokio::test]` flavor — keep it under `mod server` regardless.
- No need to introduce `Default for JoltServer` yet (still suppressed-by-absence per JOLT-RS-023 notes). If clippy gate is added, JOLT-RS-023 is the natural home.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-025: JoltServer::start (bind + serve + graceful shutdown)

PRD item: JOLT-RS-025 (priority 25, phase05-server-builder) — Implement `JoltServer::start(self, router: Router)` that binds axum on the configured port (0.0.0.0) with `tokio::signal`-driven graceful shutdown.

Verification:
- `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::server` → 5/5 passed (4 prior + 1 new); 0 failed; 65 filtered out; finished in 0.02s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 70 passed total (up from 69); 0 failed.
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean in 0.16s; no regressions.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..024 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- Signature: `pub async fn start(self, router: axum::Router) -> std::io::Result<()>`. Matches JOLT-RS-024's progress recommendation. Consume `self` per PRD ("start(self, router)"); compatible with the builder chain ending in `.start(...)`. `io::Result` propagates bind failures (port-in-use, EACCES on low ports) and signal-handler installation failures naturally.
- Bind to `Ipv4Addr::UNSPECIFIED` (i.e. `0.0.0.0`) with the configured port. PRD explicitly says "binds to 0.0.0.0", so no `127.0.0.1` shortcut even though it'd be safer in dev — that's a deployment-config concern, not phase05.
- Used plain `axum::serve(listener, router).with_graceful_shutdown(shutdown_signal()).await`. Did NOT pull in `axum-server` — that's reserved for Phase 6 TLS per JOLT-RS-024 notes. `axum::serve` over `tokio::net::TcpListener` is the canonical non-TLS path.
- `shutdown_signal()` is a private async fn that selects between SIGINT (`tokio::signal::ctrl_c()`) and, on unix, SIGTERM (`tokio::signal::unix::signal(SignalKind::terminate())`). On non-unix the SIGTERM branch becomes `std::future::pending::<()>()` so the select still compiles. This is the well-known axum example pattern. Signal-handler installation panics with `expect(...)` since failure here is unrecoverable and a runtime invariant — the alternative (return io::Error) would force callers to handle a path that's effectively unreachable.
- `self.threads` is intentionally NOT consumed in `start`. Per JOLT-RS-024's progress note: tokio's worker-thread count is set at `Runtime::new()` time, but `start` runs inside the caller's `#[tokio::main]` runtime, so threading the field through here would either (a) be ignored or (b) require constructing an inner runtime — duplicating runtimes confuses async lifetimes. Documented as "advisory" in the function's doc comment; a future runtime-build PRD item can wire it through without changing the signature.
- `self.cors_config` and `self.tls_config` are also NOT consumed yet — wiring CORS through `tower-http::cors::CorsLayer` is phase02 territory, and TLS is phase06 (axum-server). The fields are stored on the server but `start` ignores them today. Documented in JOLT-RS-024's progress notes; not a blocker for phase05.
- Added one new automated test (`start_binds_and_serves_404_on_empty_router`) under `mod server`. The PRD verification is "Manual: ... curl localhost:8080 returns 404", but I automated it because (a) it locks in a regression contract for the bind path and (b) JOLT-RS-027's "port binding conflict handling" test will need similar machinery, so the patterns can be reused. The test uses the canonical port-0 probe trick: bind 127.0.0.1:0, capture the OS-assigned port, drop the probe, then `start` on that port. Retry-connect with a 1s budget (50 × 20ms) handles startup latency without arbitrary sleeps. Read/write are wrapped in `tokio::time::timeout(2s)` so the test surfaces hangs as proper failures rather than CI timeouts. Aborts the spawned task at the end since `start` only returns on signal.
- The test sends a raw HTTP/1.1 request via `TcpStream` rather than pulling in `reqwest` or `hyper`. Cheaper dependency-wise and locks in that the server speaks HTTP/1.1 (which axum 0.7 + `axum::serve` does by default). Asserts the status line starts with `"HTTP/1.1 404"` — that's what an empty `Router` returns, satisfying the PRD's manual-verification spirit.
- TOCTOU on the port-0 probe is acknowledged but not mitigated. The window is microseconds; if a test on this machine ever flakes from port re-allocation, JOLT-RS-027 can replace this with a more robust pattern. Documented inline in the test.
- No new dependencies. `tokio = { workspace = true, features = ["full"] }` already includes `signal` and `net`; `axum::serve` is part of axum 0.7 by default.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/server.rs — added imports (`std::net::{Ipv4Addr, SocketAddr}`, `axum::Router`); added `pub async fn start(self, router: Router) -> std::io::Result<()>` and private `async fn shutdown_signal()`; updated module docstring to reflect that `start` has landed.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — added `start_binds_and_serves_404_on_empty_router` to `mod server`.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-025 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-026 (priority 26): `endpoint<E: Endpoint>(self) -> Self` registers an endpoint into the internal registry. As called out repeatedly in JOLT-RS-022/023/024 progress notes, this depends on the `Endpoint` trait from JOLT-RS-028. The strict-priority rule means JOLT-RS-026 is next, but it WILL produce a compile error against undefined `E: Endpoint`. The right move is to pull JOLT-RS-028 forward (define the `Endpoint` trait first) rather than defer 026 — same outcome, cleaner ordering. Also: `JoltServer` needs a registry field to register into — phase06 introduces `EndpointRegistry`, so either (a) add a `Vec<Box<dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync>>` field to `JoltServer` directly in 026, or (b) pull 028+029 forward and use the proper `EndpointRegistry`. Recommend (b) — phase05/phase06 are tightly coupled and the registry abstraction belongs in phase06.
- JOLT-RS-027 ("Write server builder unit tests: defaults, builder chain, port binding conflict handling") — defaults and builder chain are already covered by `mod server`'s 4 existing tests; the only new ground is "port binding conflict handling". The shape of that test: bind a probe TcpListener and HOLD it (don't drop), then call `JoltServer::new().port(held_port).start(Router::new())` and assert the returned `io::Result` is `Err` with `ErrorKind::AddrInUse`. The retry-connect pattern from JOLT-RS-025's test is unnecessary there since we expect the bind to fail synchronously. Adding it under the same `mod server` module keeps the filter clean.
- The `start_binds_and_serves_404_on_empty_router` test is the first `#[tokio::test]` with a network bind in this crate. It'll add ~50-100ms to the test run. If test-time becomes a concern, JOLT-RS-027 should consolidate network-using tests under a `mod server::network` submodule that can be filtered with `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::server::network` — but premature today.
- `start` currently swallows the `self.threads`, `self.cors_config`, `self.tls_config` fields. When wiring lands (phase02 CORS, phase06 TLS, future runtime-build), `start`'s signature stays the same — only the body grows. No PRD-26-blocker yet.
- The `expect(...)` on signal-handler installation could become a `?` if a future PRD requires fully-recoverable startup. Today the panic is fine: failure-to-install-SIGINT-handler means the runtime is broken in a way the caller can't meaningfully handle.
- If a clippy gate ever lands (per JOLT-RS-023 notes), `Default for JoltServer` becomes the natural fix; `start`'s code wouldn't need to change.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-028: Endpoint trait (pulled forward, opens phase06)

PRD item: JOLT-RS-028 (priority 28, phase06-endpoint-registry) — Define the `Endpoint` trait with `path() -> &str`, `method() -> Method`, and `handler(Request) -> Pin<Box<dyn Future<Output = axum::response::Response> + Send>>`.

Why pulled out of strict-priority order: JOLT-RS-026 (priority 26) is `endpoint<E: Endpoint>(self) -> Self` and JOLT-RS-027 (priority 27) is the server-builder test suite. JOLT-RS-026 references `E: Endpoint` and cannot compile without the trait first. Every prior progress note (JOLT-RS-022/023/024/025) flagged this and recommended pulling JOLT-RS-028 forward. Per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first, then integration points), the trait is the load-bearing abstraction — JOLT-RS-026, 029, 030, 031, 033, 034, 036, 037 all consume it. Picking 028 unblocks the entire phase05/phase06 chain in one move; picking 026 first would force a stub trait now and a refactor when 028 lands.

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-core` → clean in 0.82s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib -- tests::endpoint` → 2/2 passed (object-safety + handler-future), 70 filtered out, 0.00s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 72 passed (up from 70); 0 failed.
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean in 0.29s; no regressions in any sibling crate.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..025 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- `pub trait Endpoint { fn path(&self) -> &str; fn method(&self) -> Method; fn handler(&self, req: Request) -> EndpointFuture; }` lives in a new `jolt-core/src/endpoint.rs`. Re-exported as `pub use endpoint::{Endpoint, EndpointFuture}` from `lib.rs` so callers write `jolt_core::Endpoint` rather than `jolt_core::endpoint::Endpoint` (matches the existing flat re-export shape — cf. `Cookie`, `Method`, `Request`, `Response`, `JoltServer`, `StatusCode`).
- Did NOT make `Send + Sync` supertraits of `Endpoint`. PRD-029 specifies `Vec<Box<dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync>>` — the `+ Send + Sync` adds the auto traits at the trait-object site, so requiring them on the trait itself is redundant and forecloses the option of holding endpoint values in non-shared contexts (e.g. a single-threaded test harness, or a future single-threaded runtime path). This matches the PRD spec verbatim.
- Did NOT make the trait async via `async-trait` or trait `async fn` (Rust 1.75+). PRD-028 explicitly specifies the desugared `Pin<Box<dyn Future<Output = Response> + Send>>` shape — and that's the shape that lets the trait stay object-safe with no compiler-version pinning. `async fn` in traits would force the registry's `Box<dyn Endpoint>` to deal with associated-type-position-impl-trait dyn-safety which is a Rust 1.75+ unstable interaction; explicit boxing is the conservative, mechanically-clear choice the PRD picked. Adding a type alias `EndpointFuture` keeps callers from re-typing the long signature.
- Type alias `pub type EndpointFuture = Pin<Box<dyn Future<Output = Response> + Send>>;` is genuinely useful — handler implementations in JOLT-RS-039+ (the macro-generated impls) will reference this name. Public so downstream crates can name it too.
- Endpoint module docstring forward-references JOLT-RS-026 and JOLT-RS-029 to make the dependency chain explicit for the next iteration; the trait docstring explains *why* `Send + Sync` are not supertraits (the registry adds them at the use site).
- Two tests under `mod endpoint`:
  1. `trait_is_object_safe_with_send_sync_bounds` — assigns `Box<dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync> = Box::new(StaticHello)`. This is the load-bearing assertion: if a future change adds an associated type or generic method to the trait, the object-safety check fails at compile time, breaking JOLT-RS-029's `Vec<Box<dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync>>`. Catches the regression at the trait level rather than at the registry level.
  2. `handler_future_resolves_to_axum_response` — calls `endpoint.handler(req).await` and asserts the response status + body bytes. Locks in that the Pin<Box<dyn Future>> pattern actually works end-to-end, not just at the type level.
- The test fixture `StaticHello` uses `axum::response::Response::builder().body(Body::from("hello"))` rather than constructing through `crate::Response<T>` — keeps the test isolated to the Endpoint contract (doesn't pull in `JsonBody`/`Response<T>` bridging machinery, which has its own test module).
- `empty_request()` is duplicated from `mod request`'s helper rather than imported. Two reasons: (a) `mod request`'s helper is private to that module, (b) duplication is cheap and keeps test modules independently-readable. If a third module needs it, hoist to a shared `mod tests::fixtures`.
- No new dependencies. `axum` and `tokio` are already in `jolt-core/Cargo.toml`.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/endpoint.rs — new file: `Endpoint` trait + `EndpointFuture` type alias.
- jolt-core/src/lib.rs — added `pub mod endpoint;` and `pub use endpoint::{Endpoint, EndpointFuture};`.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — new `mod endpoint` with 2 tests, inserted before `mod server`.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-028 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-026 (priority 26) is now unblocked. Implementation: add a `Vec<Box<dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync>>` field to `JoltServer` (or pull JOLT-RS-029 `EndpointRegistry` forward and embed that — recommended; JOLT-RS-022/023/024/025 progress notes prefer (b)). The PRD signature is `endpoint<E: Endpoint>(self) -> Self`. Open question for JOLT-RS-026: does `E` need `+ Send + Sync + 'static`? Yes — the registry stores boxed `dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync`, so the bound on the generic must be at least as strong. The PRD step text omits these bounds; add them and document. The `'static` bound is needed because trait objects without explicit lifetimes default to `'static`.
- JOLT-RS-029 (priority 29) `EndpointRegistry` struct + `register(endpoint)`. Trivial now that the trait exists. Recommend implementing `Default` + `new()` to match the JoltServer constructor shape; PRD doesn't mandate it but the test-fixture ergonomics reward it.
- JOLT-RS-030 path-length-descending sort: subtle — "longest path first" means `cmp` is `b.path().len().cmp(&a.path().len())`. Stable sort preserves insertion order for equal-length paths, which the PRD doesn't specify but matches the principle of least surprise. Use `sort_by_key(|e| std::cmp::Reverse(e.path().len()))` for clarity.
- JOLT-RS-031 `build_router()` → `axum::Router`: the trick is that axum's `Router::route(path, MethodRouter)` wants a `MethodRouter` typed by the verb. Switch on `endpoint.method()` to call the matching axum builder (`get(handler)`, `post(handler)`, etc.). The handler closure needs to capture the endpoint (Arc it, not Box, since it'll be cloned per request) and call `endpoint.handler(req)`. Plan to convert each registered Endpoint into an axum handler that takes axum's request, builds a Jolt `Request`, calls `endpoint.handler(jolt_req).await`, and returns. This Request-construction step is the hidden dependency on phase04 request-extraction (already done — Request struct exists with all fields).
- JOLT-RS-027 (priority 27 — server builder unit tests, particularly port-binding-conflict handling): not yet done. Recommended shape (already documented in JOLT-RS-025 progress notes): bind a probe `TcpListener` and HOLD it (don't drop), then `JoltServer::new().port(held_port).start(Router::new())` and assert `Err(io::ErrorKind::AddrInUse)`. Could be done now or after 026/029/030/031 — no dependency either way. The current `mod server` already has 4 builder-shape tests + 1 bind-and-serve test (5 total); 027 just needs the conflict-path test to round it out.
- Pulling 028 forward leaves 026 and 027 as the only phase05 holdouts. Once both land, phase05 is complete and 029-032 finish phase06.
- No clippy gate yet; if added later, `Default for JoltServer` and possibly `Default for EndpointRegistry` are the natural homes.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-029: EndpointRegistry struct + register (pulled forward, opens 026)

PRD item: JOLT-RS-029 (priority 29, phase06-endpoint-registry) — Define `EndpointRegistry` struct backed by `Vec<Box<dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync>>`; implement `register(endpoint)`.

Why pulled out of strict-priority order (same rationale as JOLT-RS-028): the next strict-priority item, JOLT-RS-026, is `JoltServer::endpoint<E: Endpoint>(self) -> Self`. It needs somewhere to put the registered endpoint. Every prior progress note (022/023/024/025/028) flagged that 029's `EndpointRegistry` is the right home rather than a one-off `Vec` field on `JoltServer` that gets refactored away when 029 lands. Per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), the registry is a load-bearing data primitive that 026, 030, 031, 032, 033, 034, 036, 037 all consume — defining it now means 026 lands as a one-line `self.registry.register(endpoint)` rather than as an inline `Vec` field that needs refactoring later.

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-core` → clean in 0.72s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib -- tests::endpoint_registry` → 3/3 passed (PRD-mandated length-2 test + empty/default contracts), 72 filtered out, 0.00s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 75 passed total (up from 72); 0 failed.
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean in 0.26s; no regressions in any sibling crate.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..028 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- New file `jolt-core/src/endpoint_registry.rs` (one-type-per-file matches existing convention: `cookie.rs`, `endpoint.rs`, `method.rs`, `request.rs`, etc.). Re-exported as `pub use endpoint_registry::EndpointRegistry` from `lib.rs` so callers write `jolt_core::EndpointRegistry`.
- `register<E: Endpoint + Send + Sync + 'static>(&mut self, endpoint: E)` — generic over concrete type, boxes internally. Picked over a `Box<dyn ...>` parameter because (a) it matches axum's `Router::route(path, handler)` style of accepting concrete types and hiding the boxing, (b) it keeps call sites free of `Box::new(...)` noise, and (c) JOLT-RS-026's `endpoint<E: Endpoint>(self)` will forward generically — no double boxing. The `+ Send + Sync + 'static` bound is required because the trait-object slot adds those auto traits; without `'static`, trait objects default to `'static` lifetime anyway, but making it explicit on the bound surfaces the requirement at the call site rather than buried in a compiler error.
- `&mut self` return type for `register`, not `&mut Self` for chaining. Rationale: the registry isn't the user-facing builder — `JoltServer` is. The chain happens at the JoltServer layer in JOLT-RS-026 (`endpoint(self) -> Self`); the registry just gets mutated in place. Mirrors the `Vec::push` shape that the registry wraps.
- `len()` and `is_empty()` are public. PRD verification ("registry has length 2") forces `len()`, and clippy's `len_without_is_empty` lints push `is_empty()` alongside it. Both are useful for JOLT-RS-031's `build_router()` ("if registry is empty, return empty Router") and JOLT-RS-032's tests.
- Inner `endpoints` Vec stays private. JOLT-RS-030 (sort) and JOLT-RS-031 (build_router) will add their methods to this same impl block — no need to expose the field. This contrasts with `JoltServer`'s pub fields (which the JOLT-RS-022 progress note documented as deliberately permissive); the registry is structurally simpler and benefits from encapsulation now.
- `#[derive(Default)]` plus `pub fn new() -> Self { Self::default() }`. Matches the `JoltServer` constructor shape (`JoltServer::new()`) and lets `JoltServer` embed an `EndpointRegistry` field with `..Default::default()` syntax later if useful. The progress note for 028 explicitly recommended this — implemented as predicted.
- Three tests under `mod endpoint_registry`: (1) `register_two_endpoints_yields_length_two` — the PRD-mandated test verbatim, (2) `new_registry_is_empty` — locks in the empty-registry contract that JOLT-RS-031's `build_router()` will lean on (an empty registry should produce an empty axum Router; if `new()` ever starts seeding entries, 031 breaks), (3) `default_matches_new` — proves the `Default` derive and `new()` agree, so future callers can pick either freely.
- Test fixture `Stub { path, method }` is a minimal `Endpoint` implementor parameterized by path + method so two distinct endpoints can be registered without two struct types. Body returns `Body::empty()` rather than reusing `mod endpoint`'s `StaticHello` "hello" body — the registry tests don't care about handler body bytes; keeping the fixture local keeps the test module self-contained and matches `mod endpoint`'s decision to duplicate the empty-request helper.
- No new dependencies. The crate already pulls in `axum` (for `Body` in tests) and the `Endpoint` trait + `Method` from sibling modules.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/endpoint_registry.rs — new file: `EndpointRegistry` struct + `new`, `register`, `len`, `is_empty`.
- jolt-core/src/lib.rs — added `pub mod endpoint_registry;` and `pub use endpoint_registry::EndpointRegistry;`.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — new `mod endpoint_registry` with 3 tests, inserted between `mod endpoint` and `mod server`.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-029 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-026 (priority 26) is now fully unblocked. Implementation shape: add a `pub registry: EndpointRegistry` field to `JoltServer`, default to `EndpointRegistry::new()` in `JoltServer::new()`, then `pub fn endpoint<E: Endpoint + Send + Sync + 'static>(mut self, endpoint: E) -> Self { self.registry.register(endpoint); self }`. The `+ Send + Sync + 'static` bounds on `E` are mandatory (the registry's `register` requires them); the PRD step text omits them but compiler will reject without. This is a ~5-line addition. The PRD verification is "register an endpoint, verify it appears in registry" — assert `server.registry.len() == 1` after `JoltServer::new().endpoint(Stub)`.
- JOLT-RS-026 also raises a question about field visibility on `JoltServer.registry`. Two options: (a) `pub` (matches existing `pub port`, `pub threads`, etc.); (b) `pub(crate)` with `fn registry(&self) -> &EndpointRegistry` for read access. (a) is consistent with the JOLT-RS-022 stance; (b) starts walling off access ahead of phase07's Router/tower::Service work where the registry will be consumed-and-moved into the Router. Recommend (a) for now — consistency over speculative encapsulation, easy to flip later.
- JOLT-RS-027 ("port binding conflict handling") is still unrelated to the 029→026→030/031/032 chain — can land any time. Same pattern as the JOLT-RS-025 test but with the probe `TcpListener` HELD (don't drop) and asserting `Err(io::ErrorKind::AddrInUse)`.
- JOLT-RS-030 (sort): the recommended `sort_by_key(|e| std::cmp::Reverse(e.path().len()))` from JOLT-RS-028's progress note still stands. Will need access to the inner Vec — add the method on `EndpointRegistry::sort(&mut self)`. Keep the field private; the sort method is the only mutation surface needed.
- JOLT-RS-031 (build_router): converts `EndpointRegistry` → `axum::Router`. Two non-trivial moves: (a) consume `self` (or `&self` with `Arc`-clones of each endpoint) so handler closures can hold the endpoint across `await`, (b) match on `endpoint.method()` and dispatch to `axum::routing::{get,post,put,patch,delete,options,head}`. The handler closure receives an `axum::extract::Request`, builds a Jolt `Request` (path/method/headers/body/cookies — all phase02/phase04 primitives are landed), calls `endpoint.handler(jolt_req).await`, and returns. The Request-conversion step is the hidden cross-phase glue; the existing `Request` struct covers all fields the PRD asks for.
- The `is_empty()` getter will be load-bearing for JOLT-RS-031 — guard the empty-registry case explicitly before iterating, since `axum::Router::new()` is the right return for that case.
- No clippy gate yet; the pub `len()`/`is_empty()` pair I added would survive one cleanly. `Default for EndpointRegistry` is derived, so no manual impl needed.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-026: JoltServer::endpoint builder (closes priority gap, completes phase05 endpoint registration)

PRD item: JOLT-RS-026 (priority 26, phase05-server-builder) — Implement `JoltServer::endpoint<E: Endpoint>(self) -> Self` to register an endpoint into the internal registry.

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-core` → clean in 0.68s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib -- tests::server` → 8/8 passed (3 new endpoint tests + the 5 prior server-builder tests, including the live bind-and-serve test); 70 filtered out, 0.02s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 78 passed total (up from 75); 0 failed; 0 ignored.
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean in 0.35s; no regressions in any sibling crate.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..029 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- `pub registry: EndpointRegistry` field added to `JoltServer`, initialized via `EndpointRegistry::new()` in `JoltServer::new()`. Picked `pub` over `pub(crate)` per the JOLT-RS-022 progress note's stated stance (consistency with `pub port`, `pub threads`, etc.; easier to flip to private later than back). The JOLT-RS-029 progress note flagged the visibility question; `pub` is the answer for now.
- `pub fn endpoint<E: Endpoint + Send + Sync + 'static>(mut self, endpoint: E) -> Self { self.registry.register(endpoint); self }`. The `+ Send + Sync + 'static` bounds are inherited verbatim from `EndpointRegistry::register`'s signature (the registry's trait-object slot adds those auto traits). The PRD step text omits them, but the compiler rejects without — added them explicitly and called out the inheritance in the docstring so readers don't have to chase the bound.
- Removed `#[derive(Debug)]` from `JoltServer`. `EndpointRegistry` doesn't implement Debug (its inner `Vec<Box<dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync>>` doesn't have Debug because the trait isn't `Debug`-bounded), so deriving on the parent would fail to compile. Searched for `JoltServer` usage in `format!`/`{:?}`/`dbg!` contexts — no callers exist anywhere in the workspace, so removing the derive is purely a compiler-mechanics decision, not a behavioral one. If a future PRD wants `Debug` back, the right move is a manual `impl Debug for EndpointRegistry` that prints `endpoints.len()` rather than re-bounding the Endpoint trait.
- Three new tests added to `mod server` (sandwiched after `new_uses_default_port_8080`, before the existing 4 tests): (1) `new_starts_with_empty_registry` — locks in the default-empty contract that 030/031 will assume; (2) `endpoint_builder_registers_into_registry` — the PRD-mandated verification verbatim, asserting `server.registry.len() == 1` after a single `endpoint()` call; (3) `endpoint_builder_chains_with_other_builder_methods` — proves the `(self) -> Self` shape composes with `port`, `threads`, and a second `endpoint` call without dropping prior state. Test (3) is the test that would fail-to-compile if a future change accidentally took `&mut self`, which is the mistake the JOLT-RS-029 progress note explicitly warned against.
- Local `StubEndpoint` test fixture lives in `mod server` rather than imported from `mod endpoint` or `mod endpoint_registry`. Each test module's stub is intentionally self-contained — matches the convention `mod endpoint` + `mod endpoint_registry` already established (each defines its own minimal Endpoint impl). Avoids cross-module test coupling that would force one test module's fixture renames to ripple.
- No new dependencies. `axum::body::Body`, `Endpoint`, `EndpointFuture`, `Method`, `Request` are already exported from the crate.
- Did NOT add `Default for JoltServer`. Same rationale as JOLT-RS-023's note: no clippy gate yet, and `JoltServer::new()` is the construction story. If clippy enforcement lands, derive Default with `Default::default() -> Self::new()` then.

Same fixture pattern as the existing `start_binds_and_serves_404_on_empty_router` test, but the probe `TcpListener` is HELD (not dropped) and the assertion is `Err(io::ErrorKind::AddrInUse)` from `JoltServer::start`.

Implementation site: same `impl EndpointRegistry` block in `endpoint_registry.rs`. Stable sort preserves insertion order for equal-length paths — matches Vec::sort_by_key's documented guarantee. Test should register `["/"," /api"," /api/hello"]` (intentionally out of order), call sort, then expose the ordering somehow — either by adding a `pub iter(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item=&dyn Endpoint>` method on the registry, or by walking `len()` against a public-but-test-only accessor. `iter()` is the cleaner answer and 031's `build_router()` will need it anyway.

Plan to use `Arc<dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync>` so the closure can `Arc::clone` per request rather than consuming the registry — that keeps `build_router(&self)` rather than `build_router(self)`, which is friendlier for testability.

Not needed for any current PRD item.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-030: EndpointRegistry::sort + iter (phase06 longest-path-first)

PRD item: JOLT-RS-030 (priority 30, phase06-endpoint-registry) — Implement `EndpointRegistry::sort()`: sort by path length descending so `/api/hello` matches before `/api`.

Why picked over the strict-priority next item (JOLT-RS-027, port-binding-conflict test): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first; "polish" last), the path-length-descending sort is a load-bearing primitive that JOLT-RS-031's `build_router` consumes — it determines which route wins on overlapping prefixes, which is core HTTP routing semantics. JOLT-RS-027 is a single port-conflict test on already-shipped server code (polish). 027 still has no upstream dependencies and can land in any subsequent iteration to close phase05.

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-core` → clean in 0.52s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib -- tests::endpoint_registry` → 6/6 passed (3 prior + 3 new sort tests), 75 filtered out, 0.00s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 81 passed total (up from 78); 0 failed; 0 ignored.
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean in 0.30s; no regressions in any sibling crate.

Note on harness instructions: same as prior items — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- `sort_by_key(|e| Reverse(e.path().len()))` over a custom `sort_by(|a,b| b.len().cmp(&a.len()))`. `Reverse` reads as "descending" at the call site and is the idiomatic Rust spelling — matches the JOLT-RS-028 progress-note recommendation. `Vec::sort_by_key` is documented stable; equal-length paths keep insertion order, which `sort_is_stable_for_equal_length_paths` pins so a future swap to `sort_unstable_by_key` (which would shave ns but produce nondeterministic route order) trips the test.
- Added `pub fn iter(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item = &(dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync)>`. JOLT-RS-029's progress note flagged the choice between (a) adding `iter()` and (b) a public-but-test-only accessor; picked (a) because the sort method is untestable without some read API, and `iter()` is the natural collection contract every JOLT-RS-031 sketch in the prior progress notes assumed. Returning `&(dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync)` rather than `&dyn Endpoint` preserves the Send/Sync auto-trait info in the iteration item type — a future caller that needs to box clone or move across threads keeps those capabilities. Used `b.as_ref()` (Box::as_ref returns `&T` where T is the boxed dyn) rather than `&**b`; the former reads cleaner.
- Did NOT preemptively switch to `Vec<Arc<dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync>>` for JOLT-RS-031's anticipated needs. JOLT-RS-029's progress note flagged that 031 will likely need `Arc` so per-request handler closures can clone references without consuming the registry — but that's a 031 concern. Ship 030 with `Box` (no behavioral change) and let 031 negotiate the Arc switch when it actually needs it. Avoids speculative refactor.
- Three new tests in `mod endpoint_registry`: (1) `sort_orders_paths_by_length_descending` — the PRD-mandated verification verbatim using the `["/" / "/api/hello" / "/api"]` registration order; (2) `sort_is_stable_for_equal_length_paths` — pins the stable-sort contract by registering `/aaa /bbb /ccc` (same length) and asserting the post-sort order matches insertion order; (3) `sort_on_empty_registry_is_a_noop` — proves `sort` on zero entries doesn't panic, which JOLT-RS-031's `build_router` will rely on when handed an empty registry.
- Reused the existing `Stub { path: &'static str, method: Method }` fixture from `mod endpoint_registry` — already parameterized by path/method, exactly what the sort test needs. No new fixture types.
- No new dependencies. Only a `use std::cmp::Reverse;` added to `endpoint_registry.rs`.
- Updated the module docstring on `endpoint_registry.rs` to reflect that `sort` + `iter` have landed; `build_router` is the only remaining JOLT-RS-031 method.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/endpoint_registry.rs — added `pub fn sort(&mut self)` + `pub fn iter(&self) -> impl Iterator<...>`. Added `use std::cmp::Reverse;`. Updated module docstring.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — added 3 sort tests inside the existing `mod endpoint_registry`.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-030 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-031 (priority 31, `EndpointRegistry::build_router() -> axum::Router`) is the next phase06 item and the natural successor — it consumes both `iter()` (added now) and the longest-first ordering (also added now). Plan: `pub fn build_router(&self) -> axum::Router { let mut router = axum::Router::new(); for endpoint in self.iter() { match endpoint.method() { Method::Get => router = router.route(endpoint.path(), get(handler_for(endpoint))), ... } } router }`. The handler closure has to (a) take `axum::extract::Request`, (b) build a Jolt `Request` (path/method/headers/query/body/cookies extraction — phase02/phase04 primitives are all landed), (c) call `endpoint.handler(jolt_req).await`, (d) return the response. The endpoint reference held by the closure must outlive the closure → either consume `self` into Arcs at build time (`Arc<dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync>`, one Arc::clone per route closure), or change the registry storage to `Vec<Arc<...>>` upfront. The Arc-at-build-time approach (build_router takes `&self`, internally Arc::news each endpoint) is cleanest and keeps the registry's storage shape unchanged for now.
- JOLT-RS-032 (priority 32) is the test bundle for 030+031: register/sort-order/duplicate-path/wildcard tests. Most of 030's coverage already lives in `mod endpoint_registry`; 032 will add the 031-side tests once build_router exists. Duplicate-path detection isn't implemented yet — open question for 032: does duplicate registration error, last-wins, or first-wins? PRD step text doesn't say; recommend deferring the decision to 032 and documenting whichever is picked (axum's `Router::route` panics on duplicate path+method, which is a natural escape hatch — let it propagate or pre-check in build_router).
- JOLT-RS-027 (priority 27, port-binding-conflict test) is still the only phase05 holdout. Same shape as the prior progress notes describe: bind a probe `TcpListener` and HOLD it (don't drop), then call `JoltServer::new().port(held_port).start(Router::new()).await` and assert `Err(io::ErrorKind::AddrInUse)`. ~10 lines including the imports.
- The `iter()` method's return type intentionally exposes `&(dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync)` (not `&dyn Endpoint`). If a future PRD wants to relax Send/Sync requirements at the trait-object site, this iter() return type would be the visible contract change.
- No clippy gate yet; if added later, the new `iter()` method is clippy-clean (no `len_without_is_empty` style lints apply to returned iterators).

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-031: EndpointRegistry::build_router (registry → axum::Router)

PRD item: JOLT-RS-031 (priority 31, phase06-endpoint-registry) — Implement `EndpointRegistry::build_router() -> axum::Router`: iterate registered endpoints, add routes matching method + path. This is the load-bearing integration point that makes registered endpoints actually serve traffic.

Why picked over the strict-priority next item (JOLT-RS-027, port-binding-conflict test): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("integration points" > "polish"), build_router is the cross-phase glue connecting JOLT-RS-028/029/030's registry abstraction to axum's actual routing. JOLT-RS-027 is still a single-test polish task on already-shipped server code and can land any subsequent iteration. JOLT-RS-031 also unblocks JOLT-RS-032 (the registry test bundle) and is a prerequisite for JOLT-RS-033..037 (the tower::Service Router wrapper) being meaningful.

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-core` → clean in 0.79s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib -- tests::endpoint_registry` → 10/10 passed (6 prior + 4 new build_router tests in `mod build_router` submodule), 75 filtered out, 0.00s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 85 passed total (up from 81); 0 failed; 0 ignored.
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean in 0.35s; no regressions in any sibling crate.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..030 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- **Switched storage from `Box<dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync>` to `Arc<dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync>`** in `EndpointRegistry::endpoints`. JOLT-RS-029/030 progress notes both flagged this would be needed; build_router's per-route handler closure has to capture an owned reference to the endpoint that outlives the closure, and `Arc::clone` is the only zero-cost-per-route way to give each route closure its own owned handle while keeping the registry intact (so `build_router(&self)` is possible). `Box` would have forced either consuming the registry or erecting a parallel Arc storage at build time. Public API unaffected — `register<E>` still takes a concrete value and wraps internally; `iter()` still yields `&(dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync)` since `Arc::as_ref` returns `&T` exactly like `Box::as_ref`. All existing tests passed without modification.
- `pub fn build_router(&self) -> Router` over `pub fn build_router(self) -> Router`. `&self` keeps the registry usable after the call (e.g. for inspection in tests, or for re-building with different layers later) and matches the JOLT-RS-029 progress note's recommendation. Arc::clone per route is the cost; that's a single refcount bump per registered endpoint at build time, not per request.
- **Sort responsibility stays with the caller.** PRD-031 says "iterate sorted endpoints" but build_router takes `&self` (can't call sort which is `&mut`). Documented in the doc-comment that callers should `sort()` first if longest-path-first matching matters. For axum's `Router` specifically, the underlying matchit-based matcher has its own precedence rules for distinct exact paths (it doesn't just match in registration order), so for this build target the sort is mostly cosmetic. The sort will be load-bearing when JOLT-RS-033..037 builds Jolt's own Router/tower::Service wrapper that does literal sequential matching.
- Per-method dispatch via a `match endpoint.method()` over `axum::routing::{get, post, put, patch, delete, options, head}` — one branch per Method variant. The closure's signature doesn't change between methods, so all seven branches return the same `MethodRouter` shape. Clean and exhaustive; if a Method variant gets added (e.g. CONNECT, TRACE), the match becomes non-exhaustive and the compiler trips it.
- The handler closure is `move |req: AxumRequest| { let endpoint = Arc::clone(&endpoint); async move { ... } }`. The OUTER closure captures `endpoint: Arc<dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync>` by move (per-route, set when build_router runs). The INNER `async move` block clones the Arc per request — that's the per-request cost (one refcount bump), which is the canonical pattern for shared-handler axum usage. axum's Handler trait is implemented for `Fn(AxumRequest) -> impl Future<Output = R>` where `R: IntoResponse`, and `axum::response::Response` impls IntoResponse trivially, so the closure satisfies Handler without any helper traits.
- Added `build_jolt_request(AxumRequest) -> Request` private helper that performs the cross-phase glue: parses Method via FromStr (already exists from JOLT-RS-008), takes path from `parts.uri.path()`, parses query string with a tiny `parse_query` helper (split on '&', then on '='), parses Cookie header with `parse_cookies` (split on ';', then on '=', trimmed), reads body with `axum::body::to_bytes` capped at `u32::MAX` bytes (~4GB safety valve, NOT a policy decision — real body limits land with middleware), keeps headers as-is, sets `finished: false`. Method::from_str failure falls back to Method::Get rather than 500-ing — axum's matchit only routes to a registered (path, method) combo, so by the time this runs the method already matched something the framework knows how to spell, and any fallback here is unreachable unless axum's parsing diverges from ours. Kept as a defensive default rather than a panic; if JOLT-RS-032 wants stricter handling it can be tightened then.
- Cookie/query parsing is intentionally minimal (no URL-decoding, no quoted-string handling). The PRD scope for build_router is "produce a Router with correct routes," not "ship a full request-extraction stack." Real URL-decoding will likely arrive when an explicit phase07 or extractor PRD lands; a `// TODO` in the body would just rot, so the choice is documented here in progress notes instead. The 4 tests cover the happy paths.
- Added `tower = { version = "0.5", features = ["util"] }` to workspace `[workspace.dependencies]` (was `tower = "0.5"` — no features). The `util` feature exposes `tower::ServiceExt`, which provides the `oneshot(req)` adapter used in the new tests. This is the canonical axum-test pattern (cf. axum's own examples) and keeps the build_router tests fully in-process with no TCP bind / signal handling — orders of magnitude faster than the network-based pattern used in `start_binds_and_serves_404_on_empty_router`. jolt-core is currently the only workspace member that depends on tower, so the feature add has no blast radius beyond its own crate.
- Did NOT add a per-route layer or middleware hook in build_router. The PRD step is just route construction; CORS/auth/middleware wiring happens at the Router/tower::Service level (JOLT-RS-033..037) or at the JoltServer.start() level (when CORS/TLS configs become non-stub).
- Did NOT pre-validate duplicate (path, method) pairs. axum's `Router::route` panics on duplicate path with the same method — letting that propagate is fine for now; JOLT-RS-032's "duplicate path detection" test will pin the contract (recommend pre-checking in build_router and returning a Result, since axum's panic is fatal at server startup which is the wrong shape for a library). Documented in next-iteration notes.
- Four tests under a new nested `mod build_router` submodule inside `mod endpoint_registry`. Submodule keeps the build_router tests groupable via `cargo test -- tests::endpoint_registry::build_router` and avoids polluting the parent module's namespace with two new fixtures (EchoEndpoint, CapturingEndpoint). Tests cover: (1) `empty_registry_yields_router_that_404s` — proves the empty-registry path returns axum's default 404 router (locks in the contract that JOLT-RS-029 + JOLT-RS-030's `is_empty()`/`sort()` build atop); (2) `two_endpoints_each_dispatch_correctly` — the PRD-mandated verification verbatim, with two endpoints differing in path AND method to prove dispatch is keyed on both; (3) `wrong_method_for_registered_path_is_405` — pins axum's MethodRouter contract (path matches, verb doesn't → 405 not 404), so a future build_router refactor that accidentally falls back to a catch-all handler trips here; (4) `handler_sees_method_path_query_body_and_cookie` — single test that exercises the entire build_jolt_request glue at once (method, path, query param, body bytes, Cookie header), so a regression in any one field surfaces as a focused assertion failure.
- Test fixture `EchoEndpoint { path, method, body }` is parameterized over all three so a single struct can produce N distinct routes; matches the `Stub` fixture pattern in `mod endpoint_registry`. `CapturingEndpoint` is its own type because its handler builds a deterministic-format string from the request — single-purpose, no parameterization needed.
- The `body_string(resp).await` helper in the test module reads the response body to bytes and string-decodes. Cap is 4096 (more than enough for the test fixtures' short bodies); uses `axum::body::to_bytes` directly rather than via `hyper`/`http-body-util` to avoid pulling in additional deps.

Files changed:
- Cargo.toml — added `features = ["util"]` to workspace `tower` dep so `tower::ServiceExt::oneshot` is available for tests (and any future Service::call ergonomics).
- jolt-core/src/endpoint_registry.rs — switched storage from `Box<dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync>` to `Arc<dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync>` (transparent to existing API); added `pub fn build_router(&self) -> Router`, plus private helpers `method_router_for`, `build_jolt_request`, `parse_query`, `parse_cookies`. Added imports for axum routing/extract/HeaderMap and crate Cookie/Method/Request. Updated module docstring to reflect build_router has landed.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — added nested `mod build_router` inside `mod endpoint_registry` with EchoEndpoint + CapturingEndpoint fixtures, body_string helper, and 4 tests.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-031 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- Phase06 endpoint-registry is now substantively done at the data + axum-glue level. JOLT-RS-032 (priority 32) is the test bundle: register/sort-order/duplicate-path/wildcard-extraction tests. Sort + register coverage already lives in `mod endpoint_registry` (JOLT-RS-029/030); the 032 work is (a) duplicate-path detection (open question — see below), (b) wildcard / path-param extraction tests. axum's `Router::route` accepts `:param` and `*wildcard` patterns natively and feeds them through axum's `Path` extractor; build_router's handler closure DOES NOT currently propagate matchit's captured params into the Jolt Request (no field for them today). 032 will likely need either (i) a `path_params: HashMap<String, String>` field on Request and a build_jolt_request update to read `axum::extract::Path` from `parts.extensions`, or (ii) a documented limitation. Recommend (i) — small, contained change; the Request struct already holds query_params so the shape generalizes.
- Duplicate-path-detection design choice for JOLT-RS-032: axum's `Router::route(path, method)` panics if the same path is registered twice with overlapping verbs. Three options for the registry: (a) pre-check in build_router, return `Result<Router, BuildRouterError>` listing the conflict (changes the signature — breaking); (b) pre-check and panic in build_router with a clearer message before axum's; (c) leave axum's panic as-is and document. Recommend (a) since build_router is currently infallible and the cost of changing the signature is low (no callers yet beyond tests); a startup-time panic in a library is the wrong shape and (a) lets JoltServer::start propagate the error via io::Result naturally. JOLT-RS-032 should make the call.
- `Method::from_str` fallback in build_jolt_request currently swallows unknown methods to Method::Get. axum doesn't route to unregistered methods so this branch is unreachable in practice, but JOLT-RS-032 should consider tightening (e.g. returning a 500 directly without invoking the handler). Not a current bug.
- `parse_query` and `parse_cookies` do no URL-decoding. Real-world `?n=hello%20world` will produce `"hello%20world"` not `"hello world"`. Not a JOLT-RS-031 concern (PRD verification is "correct routes," not "correct extraction"). When a phase07 / request-extractor PRD lands, swap in `form_urlencoded::parse` (already a transitive dep of axum/url) for both. The 4 build_router tests use only ASCII-safe values; they won't trip the limitation.
- 4GB body cap (`u32::MAX`) is a safety valve not a policy. Real body-limit middleware will land in a later phase; the cap exists today only to bound the unbounded `to_bytes` call. Don't depend on this being the long-term default.
- Workspace `tower` now ships with `util` enabled. Total compile cost: negligible (already pulled transitively by axum). No other workspace member uses tower today, so the feature add is effectively scoped to jolt-core. If a future crate wants to depend on tower without `util`, it can override per-crate; the workspace pin is just a default.
- JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict test) is still the only phase05 holdout. Same shape as repeatedly described in prior progress notes: probe `TcpListener::bind(("127.0.0.1", 0))`, capture port, HOLD the probe (don't drop), then call `JoltServer::new().port(held_port).start(Router::new()).await` and assert `Err(io::ErrorKind::AddrInUse)`. ~10 lines.
- JOLT-RS-033..037 (Router as tower::Service wrapping the axum Router with RequestExt injection + finished-flag short-circuit) is the next architectural item after 032. The Arc-stored endpoints in EndpointRegistry are now in the right shape for that work — Router will consume the registry's iter() to dispatch, and per-request handler invocation will mirror build_router's closure pattern.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-033: tower::Service for Router (opens phase07)

PRD item: JOLT-RS-033 (priority 33, phase07-router-tower-service) — Implement `tower::Service` for `Router`: wraps an `axum::Router` and injects `RequestExt` into every incoming request before dispatch.

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), JOLT-RS-033 is the load-bearing entry point for phase07. The whole middleware layering story (CORS in phase09, body parsing in phase10, query parsing in phase11, tracing in phase12, JWT auth in phase13, WS auth in phase14) reads `Arc<RequestExt>` out of request extensions and toggles its `finished` latch. Without 033's injection at the outermost service layer, none of those middlewares can exist as standalone tower layers — they'd each need to lazy-init the latch defensively, which fragments the contract. Landing 033 first means 034/035/036/037 (and every later middleware PRD) can assume the extension is always present and read-only-shaped (the latch itself is `AtomicBool`, hence `Arc` rather than `Box`). JOLT-RS-027 stays a polish task with no upstream dependencies; JOLT-RS-032 is a test bundle that's blocked on small but unresolved design questions (duplicate-path detection error shape, path-param Request field) that should land alongside an actual consumer rather than ahead of one.

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-core` → clean in 0.84s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib -- tests::router` → 3/3 passed (Service impl compiles + 2 behavioral tests covering the injection contract and inner-router transparency), 85 filtered out, 0.00s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 88 passed total (up from 85); 0 failed; 0 ignored.
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean in 0.38s; no regressions in any sibling crate.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..031 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- New file `jolt-core/src/router.rs` (one-type-per-file, matching the existing convention: `cookie.rs`, `endpoint.rs`, `endpoint_registry.rs`, `method.rs`, `request.rs`, `request_ext.rs`, `response.rs`, `server.rs`, `status.rs`). Re-exported as `pub use router::Router` from `lib.rs` so callers write `jolt_core::Router` (matches the PRD-036 `Router::new(EndpointRegistry)` shape that lands later).
- **Storage shape: `inner: axum::Router` (one field).** Keeping the wrapper a thin pass-through is the minimum the PRD step asks for. The handler-dispatch + finished-flag short-circuit are explicitly JOLT-RS-034/035 territory; trying to combine them with 033 here would conflate three different changes and make the eventual 035 test set harder to scope. The doc-comment names which sibling PRD owns each follow-up so the next iteration has a checklist.
- **Injection target: `Arc<RequestExt>`, not `RequestExt` itself.** The latch is `AtomicBool`-backed, so cloning is the correct sharing primitive when downstream middlewares spawn parallel work or need to capture the latch into a future. Box would force one-owner semantics that the existing `RequestExt` shape (`AtomicBool` for `finished`) explicitly avoids. Stored under the typed extension key `Arc<RequestExt>` so subsequent middlewares fetch with `req.extensions().get::<Arc<RequestExt>>()`. This is the canonical contract every phase09+ middleware will read.
- **Overwrite-on-call semantics for the extension.** `req.extensions_mut().insert(Arc::new(RequestExt::new()))` unconditionally replaces any previously inserted `Arc<RequestExt>`. Pinned by the `service_call_overwrites_caller_supplied_request_ext` test: a caller that pre-populated a finished latch (e.g. some upstream proxy/test fixture) MUST NOT leak that flag into the handler. Otherwise JOLT-RS-035's short-circuit contract is poisoned at the entry. This is one of the non-obvious correctness invariants of phase07; documenting it as a test now means a future "performance" optimization that skips the insert when one already exists trips the test.
- **Constructor: `Router::from_axum(inner: axum::Router)` only.** Did NOT add `Router::new()`. PRD-036 reserves `pub fn new(registry: EndpointRegistry) -> Self` as the primary public constructor. A no-arg `new()` would shadow that. `from_axum` is a deliberately lower-level entry that stays useful for tests + future composition helpers (mounting an axum::Router built externally, e.g. for serving static assets or third-party axum routers). Document the JOLT-RS-036 boundary in the rustdoc so the constructor proliferation is intentional, not accidental.
- **`#[derive(Clone)]` on Router.** `axum::Router` is `Clone` (cheap — internally a `MakeService` that clones cheaply), and tower::Service callers commonly clone services to call from multiple tasks. Skipping Clone would force every test that wants to call the service twice to rebuild it. Cost is zero; benefit is real.
- **Service impl shape: `Service<axum::extract::Request>`** (axum's default `Request<Body>`), `type Response = axum::response::Response`, `type Error = Infallible`, `type Future = Pin<Box<dyn Future<Output = Result<Response, Infallible>> + Send>>`. Matches axum::Router<()>'s own Service signature exactly so the wrapper can be substituted at any axum::serve call site. Boxed future because the call body is async (`inner.call(req).await`); Box<dyn Future> avoids leaking RouteFuture<Infallible> from axum's internals into Router's public API and keeps the type stable across axum upgrades. Tradeoff: per-request heap allocation for the boxed future. Acceptable here — 034's full registry-driven dispatch will need an async path anyway, and the alternative (a manual `enum Future { ... }`) is significant complexity for a still-evolving service shape.
- **`poll_ready` forwards to inner.** Uses qualified path `<axum::Router as Service<AxumRequest>>::poll_ready(&mut self.inner, cx)` to disambiguate; axum::Router has multiple Service impls in scope through Tower's blanket impls and the explicit qualification spells out exactly which one we mean.
- **`call`'s clone-and-move pattern** mirrors the canonical tower wrapper recipe: `let mut inner = self.inner.clone(); Box::pin(async move { inner.call(req).await })`. The clone is cheap (axum::Router uses Arc internally for its routes); the move into the async block avoids holding `self`'s mutable reference across the `.await`, which the borrow checker otherwise rejects.
- **Did NOT add `Default for Router`**. Same rationale as JOLT-RS-023's `JoltServer` decision: no clippy gate yet, and `from_axum` is the construction story until 036 lands `new(registry)`. Once 036 is in, `Default` could derive cleanly via `Default::default() -> Self::new(EndpointRegistry::default())`.
- **Three tests under new `mod router` (inserted between `mod endpoint_registry` and `mod server` to follow the dependency order in lib.rs):**
  1. `service_call_injects_request_ext_into_extensions` — happy-path injection. Uses an in-process probe handler that inspects `req.extensions().get::<Arc<RequestExt>>()` and returns 200 / 500 based on presence. Asserts the freshly-injected latch defaults to not-finished, locking in `RequestExt::new()`'s contract from the consumer side.
  2. `service_call_overwrites_caller_supplied_request_ext` — the non-obvious invariant. Pre-inserts a finished `Arc<RequestExt>` on the request, then verifies the handler sees a not-finished latch. This is the test that catches a future "skip insert if already present" optimization.
  3. `service_call_forwards_to_inner_axum_router_for_unmatched_paths` — transparency on the routing dimension. Empty inner Router → 404 still flows through the wrapper. Pins that 033 hasn't accidentally introduced a catch-all that swallows axum's default not-found behavior.
- **`tower::ServiceExt::oneshot`** for test invocation — same fixture pattern as `mod endpoint_registry::build_router`. The workspace `tower` dep already ships with `features = ["util"]` (added in JOLT-RS-031), so no new dep work.
- **No new dependencies.** All imports are already in jolt-core's tree: `axum::{body::Body, extract::Request, http::StatusCode, routing::get}`, `tower::{Service, ServiceExt}`, `std::{sync::Arc, convert::Infallible, future::Future, pin::Pin, task::{Context, Poll}}`.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/router.rs — new file: `Router` struct + `from_axum` constructor + `Service<AxumRequest>` impl with `RequestExt` injection.
- jolt-core/src/lib.rs — added `pub mod router;` and `pub use router::Router;` (alphabetical with siblings).
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — new `mod router` with 3 tests (injection happy path, overwrite-on-call invariant, inner-router transparency), inserted between `mod endpoint_registry` and `mod server`.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-033 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-034 (priority 34, `Router::call` does path/method matching against the sorted endpoint registry) is the next phase07 item. **Open question: does 034 replace the `inner: axum::Router` field with `registry: EndpointRegistry`, or does it keep both?** PRD-034 says "match against sorted endpoint registry," which sounds like it bypasses axum's matchit and does literal sequential matching keyed on (path, method) — that's why JOLT-RS-030's longest-path-first sort exists at all (axum's own matcher already handles precedence; the sort would be redundant if we kept routing through axum). Recommend: 034 swaps the storage to `Arc<EndpointRegistry>` and rewrites `call` to walk `registry.iter()` looking for the first (path, method) match, returning 404 on miss / 405 on path-match-method-miss. The `from_axum` constructor stays as an escape hatch for callers wanting axum's full router (it just won't see the registry-driven dispatch) — or gets removed entirely when 036 lands `new(registry)` as the only blessed entry. Worth deciding when 034 starts.
- JOLT-RS-035 (finished-flag short-circuit): plugs into 034's call path. After dispatching to a layer/handler, check `req.extensions().get::<Arc<RequestExt>>()?.is_finished()`; if true, skip subsequent layers and return whatever response the finishing middleware produced. Implementation depends on 034's chosen shape — if 034 keeps tower::Layer composition, 035 is just a guard inside each layer's response handling; if 034 builds a manual middleware stack, 035 lives in the loop.
- JOLT-RS-036 (`Router::new(registry: EndpointRegistry) -> Self`): blocked on 034's storage decision. If 034 swaps to `Arc<EndpointRegistry>`, 036 is `pub fn new(registry: EndpointRegistry) -> Self { Self { registry: Arc::new(registry) } }`.
- JOLT-RS-037 (test sweep): path matching, 404 unknown, 405 method mismatch, finished-flag short-circuit. Reuse the `EchoEndpoint` / `CapturingEndpoint` fixtures from `mod endpoint_registry::build_router` once 034 lands — they parameterize over (path, method, body) which is exactly what 037's matrix needs.
- The boxed future allocation (`Pin<Box<dyn Future ...>>`) is one of the few real per-request costs in the wrapper. If profiling later shows it's hot, consider switching to `pin_project_lite` + a manual Future enum that wraps `RouteFuture<Infallible>` directly — but only after measuring. The current shape is the canonical tower wrapper recipe and shouldn't be optimized speculatively.
- JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict test) is still the only phase05 holdout. Same ~10-line shape from prior progress notes.
- The `#[derive(Clone)]` opens up multi-task usage but doesn't yet exercise it. JOLT-RS-034/035 might rely on Clone to distribute the service across worker tasks; if they end up needing `Arc<Mutex<...>>` instead, revisit.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-034: Router::call registry-driven dispatch

PRD item: JOLT-RS-034 (priority 34, phase07-router-tower-service) — `Router::call`: parse path + method from request, match against sorted endpoint registry. On match, call handler. On no match, return 404.

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), 034 is the load-bearing dispatch decision for phase07. JOLT-RS-035/036/037 all build directly on top of whatever shape Router takes here — 035 plugs the finished-flag short-circuit into the dispatch loop, 036 renames a registry-based constructor as the canonical entry, and 037's test sweep targets this exact dispatch path. Landing the dispatch shape first means the next three items have a stable contract to extend rather than a moving target. JOLT-RS-027 stays a polish task with no upstream dependencies; JOLT-RS-032 is a test bundle that benefits from waiting until 037 lands path-param extraction (the natural place for it).

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-core` → clean in 0.85s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib -- tests::router` → 8/8 passed (3 prior 033 tests still passing under the new `Inner::Axum` variant + 5 new `registry_dispatch` tests), 85 filtered out, 0.00s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 93 passed total (up from 88); 0 failed; 0 ignored.
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean in 0.43s; no regressions in any sibling crate.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..033 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- **Storage shape: `Inner` enum with two variants (`Axum(axum::Router)` and `Registry(Arc<EndpointRegistry>)`)** rather than swapping `inner: axum::Router` for `Arc<EndpointRegistry>` outright. The 033 progress notes flagged this as the open question. Both options preserve the `Service<AxumRequest>`-with-RequestExt-injection contract; the enum keeps `Router::from_axum` (and its 3 existing tests) load-bearing for JOLT-RS-033's verification while introducing the registry path that 035/036/037 build atop.
