Rejected because (a) `compile_error!` already handles multi-error rendering poorly — multiple `compile_error!` invocations don't always show all messages clearly in cargo output; (b) syn's error-combining (`syn::Error::combine`) is awkward when each error needs its own span — the combined error is rendered as a chain at one span; (c) once the first method's validation passes, the user re-runs and sees the next; this is the rust-compiler norm (not "show me all type errors", just "show me the first one with a clean span"). If a future PRD wants accumulate-all behavior, switching to `syn::Error::combine` is a 5-line change. Pinned by `validate_methods_surfaces_error_from_offending_method` (asserts the second method's error surfaces; doesn't claim both are reported).
- **Did NOT wire `scan_methods` + `validate_methods` into the `endpoint` proc-macro entry point in lib.rs.** Per 039's progress notes, the recommendation was to start consuming `scan_methods` "in 040 (when validation joins parsing)." Did not follow that recommendation because: parsing the input as `ItemImpl` and re-emitting it would surface the magic-marker `#[get]`/`#[post]`/etc. attributes to rustc, which would then error with "cannot find attribute `get` in this scope." The fix is the `strip_verb_attrs` helper that 041's progress notes already flag as that iteration's work. Trying to do it now would either (a) duplicate 041's stripping work (violating "Keep the change small and focused") or (b) leave the entry point in a broken state where `#[endpoint]` rejects every existing test fixture. Cleaner to land the validation helper alone, leave lib.rs unchanged, and let 041 wire both `scan_methods` and `validate_methods` once it has the strip pass. Documented this in the rustdoc on `validate_methods` and `validate_signature` (both `#[allow(dead_code)]` with a comment naming the next-iteration consumer — same pattern as 039).
- **Test fixtures use `syn::parse_str::<ImplItemFn>` via a `parse_sig(method_src: &str)` helper, NOT impl-block parsing.** 039's tests use `syn::parse_str::<ItemImpl>` because they walk `impl.items`. 040's tests target a single `Signature`, and going through an impl block would force every fixture to wrap the method in a containing `impl X { ... }` — adding visual noise to ~16 tests. `ImplItemFn` is the right granularity: it's the smallest syn type that holds a `Signature` with the expected receiver/return-type shape. The helper hides the `.expect("test input parses as ImplItemFn")` so individual tests stay focused on the assertion.
- **Diagnostic message style matches `parse_endpoint_attr`'s style.** Each error uses `syn::Error::new_spanned(...)` with a clear "what was expected" + "what was found" + "why" sentence. Style examples: "endpoint method must take `&self`, not `&mut self` (handlers must be safe to call concurrently on the same `&Endpoint`)" — names the rule, names the offender, names the constraint. This reads better than generic "expected `&self`" diagnostics, especially for `&mut self` where the user likely thinks `&mut self` is a fine, equivalent shape.

Files changed:
- jolt-macros/src/endpoint.rs — added `validate_methods(&[DiscoveredMethod]) -> syn::Result<()>` and `validate_signature(&Signature) -> syn::Result<()>` public-to-crate helpers + private `validate_receiver` / `validate_return_type` / `last_path_segment` helpers. Updated module docstring to mark 039 landed and 040 current. Added 16 new unit tests under `mod endpoint::tests` covering the 4-shape happy path, all 6 receiver rejection cases, all 5 return-type rejection cases, and 2 walker-level tests for `validate_methods`.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-040 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-041 (priority 41, phase08): "Generate a match per discovered method mapping (Method, path) → handler fn." This is now the path-of-least-resistance phase08 closer. The handler-match emit reads `EndpointAttr.path` (the `#[allow(dead_code)]` on `path` comes off here) AND each `DiscoveredMethod.{http_method, sig.ident}`. Match-arm shape: `(::jolt_core::Method::Get, "/api/test") => Self::hello(&self).await.into()` (or similar — the `.await` and `.into()` will depend on whether 042/043 land the inventory + axum-bridge plumbing first; this iteration is just the match-arm codegen). The magic-marker verb attribute MUST be stripped from the re-emitted impl. Recommend: extract a `endpoint::strip_verb_attrs(item: &mut ItemImpl)` helper that walks `item.items` and, for each `ImplItem::Fn`, retains only attributes that are NOT magic-marker verbs (i.e. `verb_from_attr(attr).is_none()`). The magic-marker semantics decided in 039 make this trivial.
- The `endpoint` macro entry point in lib.rs STILL does not consume `scan_methods` or `validate_methods` after this iteration. 041 is the natural place to wire them in: parse `item` as `ItemImpl`, run `scan_methods` → `validate_methods`, then run `strip_verb_attrs` and emit the codegen. The current "validates path is a string literal, re-emits item" no-op behavior is unchanged.
- `HttpMethod::as_jolt_core_variant_ident` (mentioned in 039's docstring) needs to be added as part of 041 to produce `::jolt_core::Method::Get` etc. as a quoted path. Five-line match.
- Validation is currently shape-only ("does this look like Response/Result<Response>?"). When 041 emits dispatch code that calls `Self::handler(&self).await` and tries to convert the result via `Into<axum::Response>`, rustc will catch (a) ill-formed `Response` types, (b) error types that don't implement `IntoResponse`, etc. — the rustc-on-generated-code gate. If a future PRD wants stricter macro-level checks (e.g. "first generic arg of `Result` must specifically be `Response`, not `Self::Response`"), the `validate_return_type` Result branch grows; for now the laxness keeps user-side ergonomics broad.
- Signature validation does NOT check `sig.asyncness`, `sig.unsafety`, or generic parameters. Async is the expected default for handlers but not a hard requirement (sync handlers boxed via `async move { ... }.boxed()` are valid too — phase11 will decide which shape codegen emits). `unsafe` handlers don't fundamentally break anything but probably indicate a user mistake; if a future PRD wants to reject them, the check is `sig.unsafety.is_some()` → 1-line addition. Generic params (lifetime, type, const) on the method are accepted as-is and rustc enforces what's representable in dispatch.
- The `mod endpoint::tests` module now has 31 tests. Still flat. The submodule-split threshold flagged in 037's progress note (~25) is now exceeded; recommend splitting into `mod attr_parsing` (extracts/rejects) + `mod method_scanning` (discovery, marker matching) + `mod signature_validation` (receiver, return-type checks) before phase08 closes (likely during 041 or as a tracker-item cleanup). This is purely organizational, not behavioral, and not in scope for any PRD item.
- JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict test) and JOLT-RS-032 (endpoint-registry test bundle) are still the two phase05/phase06 holdouts. Same status as prior entries.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-041: emit (Method, path) → handler dispatch match

PRD item: JOLT-RS-041 (priority 41, phase08-endpoint-macro-parsing) — generate a match per discovered method mapping `(Method, path)` → handler fn. Closes phase08's parsing+codegen-shaping ladder.

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), 041 is the architectural closer for phase08 — it locks in the dispatch match shape (`(::jolt_core::Method::<variant>, "/path") => Self::<handler>`) that JOLT-RS-042 (inventory registration) and JOLT-RS-043 (handler-wrapper codegen) build on. Landing it now means 042/043 build on a stable `generate_dispatch_match` helper rather than each inventing a new arm-emission shape. JOLT-RS-027/032 remain pure-polish/test-bundle items with no upstream dependencies.

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-macros` → clean in 0.61s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-macros` → 35/35 passed (the 31 prior 038/039/040 tests + 4 new 041 tests covering the PRD-mandated 2-method/2-arm case + arm-pattern/handler-fn-ref correctness + empty-methods catch-all-only + per-arm path-literal sharing).
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean in 0.30s; no regressions in any sibling crate.

The PRD-mandated verification ("Unit test: two methods (get + post) → generated code has two match arms") is satisfied by `generates_two_arms_for_get_and_post`. The test parses the generated TokenStream as `syn::ExprMatch` and asserts `parsed.arms.len() == 3` — 2 explicit arms (Get/Post) plus 1 wildcard catch-all — with explicit `matches!(.., syn::Pat::Tuple(_))` and `Pat::Wild(_)` checks per arm so a regression that emitted the right COUNT but wrong SHAPE (e.g. all wildcards, or all tuples and no catch-all) would still fail.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..040 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool. (No `package.json`, no `server/` directory.)

Key decisions:
- **`generate_dispatch_match` returns a complete `match` expression, NOT a Vec of arm tokens.** Considered returning `Vec<TokenStream>` (one element per arm) so the caller could splice arms into whatever surrounding match it wanted. Rejected because (a) the caller needs to know which scrutinee idents the arms reference (`__method`, `__path`) — exposing that as an implicit caller obligation invites bugs when 042/043 wire it up; (b) the wildcard catch-all is part of the dispatch contract (the match must be exhaustive, period), and putting that responsibility on the caller means every caller has to reinvent the unreachable-fallback message; (c) parse-testing the output as a complete `syn::ExprMatch` is strictly more rigorous than counting Vec elements — a Vec-of-tokens regression that emitted broken arm tokens would still pass `len() == N`. The complete-match shape is also what 042/043 will literally splice into the generated `Endpoint::handler` body, so emitting that shape now means downstream callers don't have to re-wrap.
- **Scrutinee idents are `__method` and `__path` (double-underscore prefixed).** A leading `__` reduces the chance of colliding with a user-defined name in the surrounding scope where 042/043 will splice this match. Single-underscore names (`_method`, `_path`) would also work but `_`-prefixed idents conventionally signal "intentionally unused" in Rust, which is the opposite of what these are. Considered using `proc_macro2::Span::mixed_site()` hygiene for true name-isolation, but that adds complexity (constructing `Ident::new(name, Span::mixed_site())`) for no observable benefit at this scope — `__method` / `__path` will only ever be referenced by lines emitted from the same proc-macro, and double-underscore is the established convention for proc-macro-internal binding names (e.g. serde's `__Visitor`, futures' `__Pin`).
- **Catch-all body is `::core::unreachable!(...)`, NOT `panic!`, `unimplemented!`, or `Option::None`.** `unreachable!` is the right shape: the router only invokes this dispatch AFTER it has matched the (path, method) pair against the registry, so reaching the catch-all is a contract violation in well-formed code. `panic!` is less precise (panics are normal control flow in some patterns; `unreachable!` is specifically "this is dead code" with rustc's nicht-erreicht-coverage hint). `unimplemented!` is wrong (it suggests "TODO", but the code IS implemented). Returning `None` would commit to an `Option<HandlerFn>` return type for the surrounding match, which 042/043 may or may not pick. Documented this in the rustdoc on `generate_dispatch_match`. Used the fully-qualified `::core::unreachable!` (not bare `unreachable!`) to be hygiene-safe in user crates that might `use my_macros::unreachable;`.
- **Match arm bodies are `Self::<handler>` fn-references, NOT calls.** `Self::list` evaluates to a fn-pointer, not a return value — the surrounding generated code (042/043) will be responsible for actually invoking the handler. This keeps 041's emitted code uncoupled from JOLT-RS-029/043's handler-trait shape (which still has open questions per 040's progress notes — async vs sync, what argument types the wrapper layer passes through, whether it goes through `Endpoint::handler` or a generated dispatch). When 042/043 actually wire up dispatch, they can either splice this match into a `let handler = match ...` binding and then call `handler(self, req).await`, or rewrite the arm bodies as full call expressions — both options stay open. A regression that emitted call expressions (e.g. `Self::list()` or `Self::list(self)`) would force 042/043 into one specific shape with no ergonomic way to back out. Pinned by `arms_reference_jolt_core_method_variants_and_handler_fn_names`'s `Self :: list` / `Self :: destroy` token-string assertions (which would fail if the arms were `Self::list()` because the `()` would render between).
- **`HttpMethod::as_jolt_core_variant_ident` returns `proc_macro2::Ident`, NOT `&'static str` or a quoted path.** Considered returning `&'static str` and having the caller do `format_ident!(...)`. Rejected because (a) `format_ident!` at the call site duplicates the matching, and (b) the caller would need to know to run it on every codegen path, an easy thing to forget. Considered returning the full path TokenStream (`::jolt_core::Method::Get`). Rejected because the path prefix is consistent across all variants — keeping the prefix in the `quote!` template at the call site is more readable than building it inside the helper. The `Ident`-returning shape gives the call site exactly the splice fragment it needs and nothing more. The 5 variants map 1:1 with `jolt_core::Method` (which has 7 — HEAD/OPTIONS aren't user-routable so there's no `HttpMethod` variant for them); if a future PRD adds user-routable HEAD/OPTIONS handlers, this enum grows and so does this helper's match.
- **Test surface: 4 new tests (PRD-mandated + 3 supporting).** The PRD asks for one happy-path test (2 methods → 2 arms). The 3 supporting tests pin: (a) `arms_reference_jolt_core_method_variants_and_handler_fn_names` — which Method variant + which handler fn each arm names (the rendered token-string assertions catch any regression that emitted the same variant for every arm or the same handler ref for every arm — both real classes of bug); (b) `empty_methods_emits_only_catch_all_arm` — empty discovered list still produces a parseable match (a regression that depended on at-least-one-arm to flush a buffer would silently emit empty tokens, then `parse2::<ExprMatch>` would fail with a confusing message); (c) `arms_share_the_same_path_literal_across_all_methods` — every arm references the SAME path, since all methods on a single `#[endpoint]` block share the path attribute. The cost was ~80 lines of test code; each test pins one independently-observable contract that 042/043 will rely on.
- **Test fixtures use `parse_path_lit` + `parse_match` helpers.** Mirrors the 039/040 helper-style convention. `parse_match` parses the generated tokens as `syn::ExprMatch` and `.expect`s the parse — so any malformed token-stream output (unbalanced braces, missing `=>`, ...) surfaces at the test site with a clean failure rather than as a downstream rustc error in 042/043's wiring. The token-string assertions in `arms_reference_jolt_core_method_variants_and_handler_fn_names` deliberately check the rendered string with embedded spaces (e.g. `:: jolt_core :: Method :: Get`) because that's what `proc_macro2::TokenStream::to_string()` produces — a regression that switched to display-without-spaces would also fail this test, and that's fine since the rendered shape IS observable to anyone reading expansion output.
- **Did NOT wire `scan_methods` + `validate_methods` + `generate_dispatch_match` into the `endpoint` proc-macro entry point in lib.rs.** The 040 progress notes recommended doing this in 041, but 040 itself deferred the wiring because of the magic-marker `strip_verb_attrs` requirement: re-emitting an `ItemImpl` whose `#[get]`/`#[post]`/etc. attributes are still in place causes rustc to error with "cannot find attribute `get` in this scope" (since those magic markers are recognized only by `#[endpoint]`'s scanner and have no proc-macro registration of their own — see 039's progress notes). Doing the strip pass + the wiring + the codegen splice in this iteration would have been the full phase09 opener (JOLT-RS-042 + 043 + 044), violating the auto-prompt's "Keep the change small and focused" rule. The clean split is: 041 produces the dispatch-match HELPER; 042 (registry registration) wires `scan_methods` + `validate_methods` + `strip_verb_attrs` + `generate_dispatch_match` into the proc-macro entry point alongside an `inventory::submit!` block. Documented this in `generate_dispatch_match`'s rustdoc + flagged `strip_verb_attrs` as 042/043's work in the doc-comment cross-reference.
- **`#[allow(dead_code)]` on `generate_dispatch_match` is deliberate, same pattern as 038/039/040's parse helpers.** The proc-macro entry point in lib.rs does NOT call this function yet (042+ wires it in). Without the allow, dead-code warnings fire on the production build; cfg(test) reads it via the new tests, but not the proc-macro entry point. The allow names the next-iteration consumer in a comment so removal is mechanical when 042 lands.
- **Did NOT add submodule splits (`mod attr_parsing` / `mod method_scanning` / `mod signature_validation` / `mod codegen`) flagged by 040's progress notes.** The `mod tests` module now has 35 tests total (was 31 after 040). The submodule-split threshold flagged in earlier progress notes (~25) is exceeded, but the split is purely organizational, not behavioral, and not in scope for any PRD item. Tag for future cleanup: when phase08 fully closes (after 042/043 land if they keep accreting tests in the same module), do the split as a tracker-item cleanup. Doing it during 041 would conflate organizational churn with the architectural change and make the diff harder to review.

Files changed:
- jolt-macros/src/endpoint.rs — added `quote::{format_ident, quote}` and `proc_macro2::Ident` imports; added `HttpMethod::as_jolt_core_variant_ident(self) -> Ident` (no `#[allow(dead_code)]` — it's consumed by `generate_dispatch_match` in the same module); added `generate_dispatch_match(path: &LitStr, methods: &[DiscoveredMethod]) -> proc_macro2::TokenStream` with `#[allow(dead_code)]`; updated module docstring to mark 040 landed and 041 current. Added 4 new unit tests under `mod endpoint::tests` plus `parse_path_lit` and `parse_match` test-helpers. Updated the doc comment on the `HttpMethod` enum to point at `generate_dispatch_match` (was previously a forward-reference to JOLT-RS-041).
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-041 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- **Phase08 is now closed (038..041 all landed).** Phase09 (JOLT-RS-042, "static registration function via inventory or linkme") is the next architectural item and the next phase entry. Step text: "Generate a static registration function (inventory or linkme pattern) that calls EndpointRegistry::register(path, method, handler)." This is where the proc-macro entry point in lib.rs finally starts consuming `scan_methods` + `validate_methods` + `generate_dispatch_match` — alongside a new `strip_verb_attrs` helper (recommended below) and an `inventory::submit!` block (or linkme equivalent) that registers the endpoint at static-init time. Verification mentions an integration test ("define struct with #[endpoint("/test")], verify it appears in registry at server start") so 042 likely needs an `examples/` or `tests/` integration crate to be added to the workspace alongside the codegen change.
- **`endpoint::strip_verb_attrs(item: &mut ItemImpl)` is the recommended 042 helper.** Walks `item.items`, for each `ImplItem::Fn` retains attributes where `verb_from_attr(attr).is_none()` (i.e. drops the magic-marker verb attrs). The magic-marker semantics decided in 039 make this a 5-line implementation. It's needed because the proc-macro must re-emit the impl block — and rustc will error on `#[get]` if it's still there. Recommend pairing the strip with a unit test fixture that asserts the re-emitted item parses without the verb attrs (`syn::parse2::<ItemImpl>(stripped)` and check `impl_item.attrs` is verb-free).
- **The `inventory` vs `linkme` decision in 042 is open.** `inventory` is the more battle-tested crate (used by clap, dotenvy, tonic) and works on stable Rust without ld-script tricks. `linkme` is faster at runtime (zero scan) but requires nightly on some platforms (NetBSD, Wasm). Recommend `inventory` for the initial port — the per-startup scan cost is negligible (microseconds for hundreds of endpoints) and the portability story is cleaner. If a future need (e.g. wasm32-wasi) requires linkme, the swap is straightforward since both crates expose the same `iter::<T>()` API shape.
- **The `generate_dispatch_match` scrutinee idents (`__method`, `__path`) need surrounding bindings in 042/043's wiring.** Two natural shapes: (a) the generated `Endpoint::handler` body destructures `req.method` and `req.path` into `__method` and `__path` before the match; (b) the generated code uses `let __method = req.method; let __path = req.path.as_str();` inline. Either works; (b) is more explicit and probably cleaner. If 042/043 prefers a different naming scheme (e.g. `m` and `p` for brevity), the helper signature grows a `scrutinees: (Ident, Ident)` parameter — a one-line addition to `generate_dispatch_match` and a one-line update to existing tests.
- **Path-parameter extraction (e.g. `/users/:id`) is still NOT implemented.** The `parse_endpoint_attr` parser accepts colon-prefixed segments as opaque path-string content (pinned by `extracts_path_with_param_placeholder`), but neither the registry nor the dispatch match interprets `:id` as a wildcard binding. JOLT-RS-032's deferred test bundle includes path-param extraction; that work is most naturally landed alongside 042/043 since the dispatch match needs to know whether to compare the path literally (current shape: `"/users/:id"` matches only that literal request path) or to invoke a path-param matcher. Recommend treating path-params as a separate PRD item or absorbing into 042 — the design choice is non-trivial (axum-style `:param` capture into a HashMap; phf-or-trie static dispatch; or keeping the full path-string match and routing path-param logic into endpoint code). Spec_rust.md should be re-read for the canonical answer before 042 lands.
- **`HttpMethod` is still 5 variants (no HEAD/OPTIONS).** Same status as 039's note. Auto-OPTIONS / Allow-header machinery handles those at the router level (per JOLT-RS-037's 405 work).
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict test) and JOLT-RS-032 (endpoint-registry test bundle) are still the two phase05/phase06 holdouts.** With phase08 closed, these are now the only test-bundle items still open before phase09 starts. 032 has a path-param-extraction prerequisite (mentioned above); 027 is unchanged from prior progress notes. Both can be picked up between phase items as polish.
- **The `mod endpoint::tests` module now has 35 tests — strongly past the ~25 split-by-concern threshold.** Recommended split: `mod attr_parsing` (extracts/rejects, ~7 tests) + `mod method_scanning` (discovery, magic-marker matching, ~8 tests) + `mod signature_validation` (receiver/return-type checks, ~16 tests) + `mod codegen` (dispatch-match emission, ~4 tests). Purely organizational; not in scope for any PRD item. Tag for tracker-item cleanup, ideally after 042/043 land if they continue accreting tests in the same module.
- **`generate_dispatch_match`'s emit shape commits to `Self::<handler>` (fn-pointer references), not full call expressions.** If 042/043 needs a different shape (e.g. handlers must be invoked through a generated `__dispatch_<name>` shim that adapts the user signature to a tower::Service-compatible async fn), the helper grows a parameter for the arm-body shape OR splits into `generate_dispatch_match_with_handler_refs` / `generate_dispatch_match_with_handler_calls` siblings. Right now the helper assumes the caller wraps the resulting fn-pointer in whatever invocation shape it needs.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-042: inventory-based static endpoint registration

PRD item: JOLT-RS-042 (priority 42, phase09-endpoint-macro-codegen) — "Generate a static registration function (inventory or linkme pattern) that calls EndpointRegistry::register(path, method, handler)." Verification: integration test where `#[endpoint("/test")]` is defined and the entry appears in the registry at server start.

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), 042 is the next architectural item — it picks the inventory crate (vs linkme), defines the static `RegisteredEndpoint` schema that 044 will iterate, and wires the parse/scan/validate ladder built in 038–041 into the proc-macro entry point so user code can finally annotate impl blocks productively. JOLT-RS-027/032 remain pure polish/test-bundle holdouts with no upstream dependencies; 043+ all build on 042's record schema and macro shape.

Verification:
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean.
- `cargo test --workspace` → 111 jolt-core unit + 42 jolt-macros unit + 1 new integration test (`tests/inventory_registration.rs`) = 154 tests pass; no regressions in any sibling crate.
- `cargo build --workspace` → clean, no warnings.
- The PRD-mandated "Integration test: define struct with #[endpoint("/test")], verify it appears in registry at server start" is satisfied by `endpoint_macro_registers_one_entry_per_verb_method_in_inventory` in `jolt-core/tests/inventory_registration.rs`. The test defines a `Probe` struct with `#[endpoint("/probe")]`, two verb-tagged methods (`#[get] fn ping`, `#[post] fn record`), and asserts `inventory::iter::<RegisteredEndpoint>()` returns exactly two entries with matching path + methods. This is the macro→inventory→consumer pipeline end-to-end (the consumer in 042 is the test itself; in 044 it will be `JoltServer::start`).

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..041 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory). Cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- **Picked `inventory` over `linkme`.** Followed the recommendation from 041's progress notes. `inventory` is stable, used by clap/dotenvy/tonic, works cross-platform without nightly tricks. The per-startup scan cost is negligible at the scale of an HTTP framework. If a future need (wasm32-wasi, etc.) requires linkme, both expose the same `iter::<T>()` shape so the swap is local. Pinned by adding `inventory = "0.3"` to `Cargo.toml`'s `[workspace.dependencies]` and to `jolt-core/Cargo.toml`'s `[dependencies]`.
- **`RegisteredEndpoint` carries `path` + `method` ONLY this iteration; the handler fn-pointer is JOLT-RS-043's add.** Considered putting the handler field in immediately so 042's record matches the eventual full-shape. Rejected because (a) the handler shape depends on JOLT-RS-043's wrapper-codegen design (fn pointer? boxed closure? trait object?), and committing to one now means renegotiating it in 043; (b) `inventory::submit!` records must be `'static` and `Send + Sync`, which forces `path: &'static str` (not `String`) — same constraint applies to whatever handler shape 043 picks, but the choice between `fn(Request) -> EndpointFuture` and a trait-object pointer is open until then; (c) the integration test's "appears in registry at server start" check is satisfied by metadata-only registration — the handler invocation contract is JOLT-RS-045's e2e check. Splitting metadata from handler keeps 042's diff small and lets 043 adjust the schema without touching this iteration's wiring. The test defines two `unimplemented!()` handlers to make this explicit: their bodies are intentionally not invoked.
- **`RegisteredEndpoint` lives in its own module `jolt-core/src/registered_endpoint.rs`, not in `endpoint.rs` or `endpoint_registry.rs`.** Considered colocating with the `Endpoint` trait or with `EndpointRegistry`. Rejected because (a) `RegisteredEndpoint` is a *static-init* record collected by inventory, while `Endpoint` is a *runtime* trait — different lifetimes and different ownership semantics; (b) `EndpointRegistry` is a *runtime collection* of `Arc<dyn Endpoint>` instances, while `RegisteredEndpoint` is a *compile-time-collected* metadata record — different storage shapes; (c) the `inventory::collect!(RegisteredEndpoint)` invocation must be at module scope, and putting it in `endpoint_registry.rs` would imply the registry directly stores `RegisteredEndpoint` values (it doesn't). The standalone module makes the static-vs-runtime split visually obvious and gives 044 a clear file to reach into when wiring `inventory::iter()` calls into `JoltServer::start`.
- **`jolt-core` re-exports both `inventory` and `jolt_macros::endpoint`.** Considered making users import `inventory` directly into their own `Cargo.toml`. Rejected because (a) it forces every user crate that uses `#[endpoint]` to add a transitive dep they don't directly invoke; (b) the macro emits `::jolt_core::inventory::submit!`, so the path must resolve through `jolt-core` regardless — making the re-export load-bearing; (c) re-exporting `jolt_macros::endpoint` lets users `use jolt_core::endpoint;` instead of pulling jolt-macros directly, which is the planned long-term shape per spec_rust.md and 039's progress notes. The `pub use inventory; pub use jolt_macros::endpoint;` lines in `jolt-core/src/lib.rs` are explicit re-exports (not blanket `pub use jolt_macros::*;`) so a future PRD that adds new macros to jolt-macros can choose which to surface through jolt-core's prelude.
- **Added `jolt-macros = { path = "../jolt-macros" }` to `jolt-core`'s `[dependencies]` (NOT `[dev-dependencies]`).** Considered the dev-dep route since the only on-disk consumer of the macros today is the integration test in `jolt-core/tests/`. Rejected because the `pub use jolt_macros::endpoint;` re-export in `jolt-core/src/lib.rs` is a runtime contract — production users importing `jolt_core::endpoint` need it resolved at compile time through the regular dep graph. Dev-dep would make the re-export visible only in test builds. There's no cycle risk because jolt-macros does NOT depend on jolt-core (it emits `::jolt_core::*` paths but does so via `quote!`, never naming jolt-core in `Cargo.toml`).
- **Magic-marker verb attrs are stripped from the re-emitted impl via `strip_verb_attrs`.** Mandatory: rustc errors with "cannot find attribute `get` in this scope" on any `#[get]`/`#[post]`/etc. that survives macro expansion (since they're not registered as their own proc-macros — see 039's progress notes for the rationale). The implementation is a 5-line walk over `item.items` filtering each `ImplItem::Fn`'s attrs by `verb_from_attr(attr).is_none()`. Pinned by `strip_verb_attrs_removes_get_and_post_keeps_others` (verifies non-verb attrs like `#[inline]`, `#[doc]` survive — strip is name-narrow, not class-broad) and `strip_verb_attrs_does_not_touch_non_fn_items` (`const`/`type` items are skipped).
- **`expand_endpoint` is the single top-level driver; the proc-macro entry point in `lib.rs` is now a 3-line shim.** Considered keeping the parse/scan/validate ladder inline in `lib.rs`. Rejected because (a) `lib.rs` would then mix proc-macro registration with codegen logic — currently it's a thin "convert TokenStream wrapper" layer with all the codegen in `endpoint.rs`; (b) `expand_endpoint` returns `proc_macro2::TokenStream` (not the proc-macro `TokenStream`), which means it can be called directly from unit tests (proc-macro entry points cannot, see 038's progress notes). Pinned by `expand_endpoint_emits_impl_plus_submit_for_single_method`, `expand_endpoint_surfaces_compile_error_on_bad_signature`, and `expand_endpoint_surfaces_compile_error_on_non_impl_item` — three tests covering happy path, validation failure, and parse failure respectively.
- **On any failure, `expand_endpoint` emits `original_item_tokens + compile_error!`, never panics.** This mirrors the 038-era convention: preserve the original item so the user gets ONE compile error (the macro's diagnostic) rather than a cascade of "use of undeclared type Probe" errors from later code that names the (now-missing) item. The failure modes covered: (1) attribute parse failure (path is not a string literal), (2) item parse failure (item is not an `ItemImpl`), (3) scan failure (multi-verb attribute on a single method), (4) validation failure (bad signature). Each routes through the same `quote! { #item #err_tokens }` shape. Pinned by `expand_endpoint_surfaces_compile_error_on_non_impl_item` (covers 2) and `expand_endpoint_surfaces_compile_error_on_bad_signature` (covers 4); 1 and 3 are covered by the existing 038/039 unit tests on `parse_endpoint_attr` and `scan_methods`.
- **Did NOT use `generate_dispatch_match` from `expand_endpoint`.** That helper is JOLT-RS-041's emit; it produces a `match (__method, __path) { ... }` expression that takes scrutinees as inputs. The 042 macro doesn't have those scrutinees yet — they live in JOLT-RS-043's generated handler body. Calling `generate_dispatch_match` from 042 would mean the produced match expression dangles unused at the impl-block level (or worse, would need a synthetic surrounding fn just to host it). Cleanest: 043 will call both `generate_dispatch_match` and the new submit-emission, splicing them into the generated `Endpoint::handler` body. The `#[allow(dead_code)]` on `generate_dispatch_match` stays for one more iteration.
- **Integration test lives in `jolt-core/tests/inventory_registration.rs`, not in `jolt-macros/tests/`.** A proc-macro crate's own `tests/` directory cannot exercise its proc-macros directly — only `trybuild`-style harnesses can, and those test compile failures rather than runtime behavior. The integration must run in a downstream crate that has both `jolt-macros` (for the macro) and `inventory` (transitively via jolt-core's re-export) on the dep graph. `jolt-core` is the natural home: it owns `RegisteredEndpoint`, re-exports the macro, and is already a workspace member. The test asserts the inventory contents directly via `jolt_core::inventory::iter::<RegisteredEndpoint>()`; in JOLT-RS-044 the same iteration will happen inside `JoltServer::start`. The test deliberately filters by `e.path == "/probe"` so a future PRD that registers other endpoints via inventory (e.g. in a benchmark binary) doesn't bleed into this test's count assertion.
- **Test surface: 7 new unit tests in `endpoint::tests` + 1 integration test = 8 new tests for 042.** The unit tests pin: (a) strip-removes-verbs-keeps-others; (b) strip-skips-non-fn-items; (c) generate-submits emits one per method with right variants/path; (d) generate-submits empty-methods emits nothing; (e) expand-endpoint happy path emits impl + submit + strips verb attr; (f) expand-endpoint signature failure emits compile_error and NO submit; (g) expand-endpoint non-impl item failure emits compile_error. The integration test pins the cross-crate macro→inventory→consumer round-trip. Total `mod endpoint::tests` count: 35 → 42.

Files changed:
- `Cargo.toml` — added `inventory = "0.3"` to `[workspace.dependencies]`.
- `jolt-core/Cargo.toml` — added `inventory = { workspace = true }` and `jolt-macros = { path = "../jolt-macros" }`.
- `jolt-core/src/registered_endpoint.rs` (new) — `RegisteredEndpoint` struct with `path: &'static str` and `method: Method` fields, plus `inventory::collect!(RegisteredEndpoint)`. Module docstring spells out the static-vs-runtime split and the 042/043/044 lifecycle.
- `jolt-core/src/lib.rs` — registered the new module, re-exported `RegisteredEndpoint`, added `pub use inventory;` and `pub use jolt_macros::endpoint;` so user crates only need jolt-core as a dep to use `#[endpoint]`.
- `jolt-core/tests/inventory_registration.rs` (new) — PRD-mandated integration test. Defines `Probe` with `#[endpoint("/probe")]` + `#[get]` + `#[post]` methods; asserts `inventory::iter::<RegisteredEndpoint>()` has the two expected entries.
- `jolt-macros/src/endpoint.rs` — added `strip_verb_attrs(&mut ItemImpl)`, `generate_inventory_submits(&LitStr, &[DiscoveredMethod]) -> TokenStream`, and `expand_endpoint(attr, item) -> TokenStream` driver. Updated module docstring to mark phase08 closed and phase09's 042 landed. Added 7 unit tests under `mod endpoint::tests` covering the new helpers and the driver's failure modes.
- `jolt-macros/src/lib.rs` — collapsed the proc-macro entry point to a 3-line shim that delegates to `endpoint::expand_endpoint`. Updated rustdoc to enumerate the now-active 038→042 pipeline.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-042 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- **JOLT-RS-043 (priority 43, phase09): "Generate handler wrapper: converts the user's fn(Request) → impl Into<axum::Response> into a tower-compatible async fn."** Now has stable inputs to build on: the proc-macro entry point already produces `Vec<DiscoveredMethod>` + `EndpointAttr.path` and emits one `inventory::submit!` per method. 043's job is to extend `RegisteredEndpoint` with a handler field (recommended shape: `pub handler: fn(jolt_core::Request) -> jolt_core::EndpointFuture`) and have `expand_endpoint` emit a generated handler fn per discovered method that constructs a `Self` (open question: how — `Default`? a generated `__new` ctor?), invokes the user method via `Self::<ident>(...)`, and adapts the return type via `Into<axum::Response>`. The `generate_dispatch_match` helper from 041 is the natural building block: 043 will likely emit one `__handler_<verb>_<ident>` fn per discovered method whose body invokes the dispatched user method directly, then submit one `RegisteredEndpoint { path, method, handler: __handler_... }`. Open: is each `RegisteredEndpoint` *one method* (current shape — 1:N submit-per-method) or *one impl block* (1:1 submit-per-impl with internal dispatch)? The current 042 shape commits to 1:N; if 043 wants 1:1 it'll need to flatten the per-method submits into a single submit with a dispatch-match-driven handler. 1:1 has the advantage that the registry sees one entry per route, matching how `EndpointRegistry::register` works today.
- **The construct-Self problem in 043 is non-trivial.** The user's struct (`Probe` in the test) has no fields and is stateless, so `Probe` could be constructed at static-init time. But future endpoint structs may carry state (e.g. a `db_pool: Pool`, a `cache: Arc<Cache>`). Three options: (a) require user structs to implement `Default` and have the macro emit `Probe::default()` on each request — limits user flexibility but is the simplest shape; (b) have the macro emit a thread-local or static `OnceCell<Probe>` that's lazily initialized — works for `Default`-constructible but punts the with-state case; (c) require a user-provided `__new()` constructor or accept an instance from the user via `JoltServer::endpoint(MyEndpoint::new())` — most flexible but requires invasive changes to the static-init flow (inventory entries can't carry runtime instances). Spec_rust.md should be re-read for the canonical answer; the Zig version's approach is the natural reference.
- **`HttpMethod::as_jolt_core_variant_ident` is now consumed by both `generate_dispatch_match` (041) and `generate_inventory_submits` (042).** No more `#[allow(dead_code)]` migration pending on this helper — it's now load-bearing for the macro-emit pipeline. If 043 introduces a third codegen consumer, the 5-arm match stays cheap.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict test) and JOLT-RS-032 (endpoint-registry test bundle) are still the only phase05/phase06 holdouts.** With phase09 now opened (042 landed), 043/044/045 are the natural next architectural items. 027/032 remain test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies.
- **`generate_dispatch_match` has `#[allow(dead_code)]` for one more iteration.** 043 will consume it (per the recommended-shape note above), at which point the allow comes off. If 043 instead opts for a per-method handler fn (one inventory submit + one fn pointer per method, no dispatch match), `generate_dispatch_match` becomes dead and can be removed as part of 043's cleanup.
- **`mod endpoint::tests` is now at 42 tests, well past the ~25 split-by-concern threshold.** Still flat. Recommended split when phase09 closes: `mod attr_parsing` (extracts/rejects, 7 tests) + `mod method_scanning` (discovery, magic-marker, 8 tests) + `mod signature_validation` (receiver/return-type, 16 tests) + `mod codegen_dispatch_match` (4 tests) + `mod codegen_inventory_submits` (4 tests) + `mod expand_endpoint_driver` (3 tests). Purely organizational, not in scope for any PRD item.
- **The `RegisteredEndpoint` schema commits to `path: &'static str`.** This works as long as the macro emits string-literal paths (the `#[endpoint("/literal")]` shape). If a future PRD adds dynamic paths (e.g. `#[endpoint(path_from_env!("API_PREFIX"))]`), the schema must change to `path: Cow<'static, str>` or `path: fn() -> String`. Not a current concern but flag-worthy if the API surface ever grows runtime path computation.
- **Workspace integration tests run automatically with `cargo test --workspace`.** No special flags needed — the new `tests/inventory_registration.rs` is picked up by cargo's default test discovery. If 045 adds more integration tests, they go in the same `jolt-core/tests/` directory or in a future per-feature integration crate.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-043: handler-wrapper codegen + IntoResponse bridge

PRD item: JOLT-RS-043 (priority 43, phase09-endpoint-macro-codegen) — "Generate handler wrapper: converts the user's fn(Request) → impl Into<axum::Response> into a tower-compatible async fn." Verification: "Handler wrapper compiles and can be called with a Request."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first, then "integration points"), 043 is the next architectural item. It commits to per-request `Default::default()` construction of endpoint instances, picks `axum::response::IntoResponse` (over `Into<axum::response::Response>`) as the return-type bridge, and decides to emit wrappers in a SECOND `impl <SelfTy>` block alongside the user's. All three of those decisions are load-bearing for 044 (`RegisteredEndpoint.handler` field shape), 045 (e2e dispatch test), and 046+ (auto-middleware will replace `let _ = __req;` with field extraction). 027/032 remain pure test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies.

Verification:
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean.
- `cargo test --workspace` → 111 jolt-core unit + 3 jolt-core integration (was 1; +2 wrapper tests) + 47 jolt-macros unit (was 42; +5 wrapper-codegen tests) = 161 tests pass; no regressions in any sibling crate.
- `cargo build --workspace` → clean, no new warnings (the 2 pre-existing `new_without_default` clippy warnings on `JoltServer` and `RequestExt` are baseline; verified by `git stash && cargo clippy && git stash pop`).
- `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets` → same 2 pre-existing warnings, 0 new ones.
- The PRD-mandated "Handler wrapper compiles and can be called with a Request" is satisfied by `handler_wrapper_invokes_user_method_and_bridges_to_axum_response` in `jolt-core/tests/inventory_registration.rs`. The test calls `Probe::__jolt_handler_ping(req).await` and asserts the resulting `axum::response::Response` carries status 200 + body `b"pong"` from the user's `Probe::ping(&self) -> Response<&'static str>`. A second test (`handler_wrappers_are_distinct_per_method`) pins that each verb method gets its own wrapper rather than sharing a dispatcher (POST → 201 + `b"recorded"`).

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..042 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory). Cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- **Per-request `Default::default()` construction.** Picked over `OnceLock<Self>` (works only for stateless), per-route static instance (same limitation), and a user-provided `__new()` constructor (would require invasive changes to the macro's input shape). `Default` is forward-compatible: it works for stateless unit structs (`#[derive(Default)]`), works for state-bearing structs whose fields all have sensible defaults, and a future PRD that swaps to a state-injected constructor (e.g. via JoltServer's app-state extension) can change the wrapper body without touching its external `fn(Request) -> EndpointFuture` signature. The `Self: Default` bound is enforced by rustc on the generated code; users get a clear "the trait `Default` is not implemented for `MyEndpoint`" error at the wrapper site if they forget to derive it. Considered making the macro itself emit `#[derive(Default)]` on the user's struct — rejected because the macro receives an `impl` block, not the struct definition, so it cannot reach the struct decl from where it expands.
- **`axum::response::IntoResponse` over `Into<axum::response::Response>` as the return-type bridge.** axum has a blanket `impl<T, E> IntoResponse for Result<T, E> where T: IntoResponse, E: IntoResponse`. By emitting `IntoResponse::into_response(__result)` in the wrapper, both `Response<T>` and `Result<Response<T>, E>` (the two shapes JOLT-RS-040 validates) compile through the same wrapper body. The alternative — pattern-matching on Ok/Err in the macro and emitting two `.into()` calls — would force the macro to inspect the return-type shape at expand time, which is more brittle than letting axum's existing trait machinery handle the dispatch. Added a one-line `impl<T> IntoResponse for Response<T> where Response<T>: Into<axum::response::Response>` in `jolt-core/src/response.rs` to unlock this; the conditional bound means the impl only kicks in when the existing `From<Response<T>>` conversions cover T (currently `T: JsonBody`, `T = String`, `T = &str`).
- **Wrappers emitted in a SECOND `impl <SelfTy>` block, not spliced into the user's.** Considered pushing each wrapper into `item.items` as an additional `ImplItem::Fn` so the user's impl block grows in place. Rejected because (a) `strip_verb_attrs` already mutates `item.items` in place and adding splice-in logic on top is fragile; (b) Rust allows multiple inherent impls per type, so a sibling impl is semantically equivalent and keeps the user's block lossless except for verb-attr strip; (c) a sibling impl makes the wrapper block visually distinct in expanded output (helpful when debugging `cargo expand`) and lets future codegen (say, a `__jolt_metadata` impl block in 044) compose without contention; (d) `#[automatically_derived]` on the sibling block makes it clear in diagnostics that the impl was machine-generated. Pinned by `generate_handler_wrappers_threads_self_ty_through_impl_block` (ensures the user's `self_ty`, including path-style types like `crate::api::User`, is spliced verbatim into the new impl block, not hard-coded as `Self`).
- **`__req: ::jolt_core::Request` is bound but immediately discarded via `let _ = __req;`.** The user's method takes `&self` only (per JOLT-RS-040's validation contract); there is no body / query / req parameter to feed yet. Three options considered: (a) take `__req` by value AND immediately drop it (current choice); (b) take `_: ::jolt_core::Request` to silence the unused-variable warning at the binding site; (c) take no Request at all and have 044 wire request → wrapper later. Picked (a) because: it commits the wrapper signature to `fn(Request) -> EndpointFuture` *now*, which 044 can store as a fn-pointer in `RegisteredEndpoint.handler` without any signature renegotiation; the `let _ = __req;` pattern is conventional and survives `clippy::unused_variables` (verified — clippy reports zero new warnings); when JOLT-RS-046 (auto-middleware) lands the `let _ = __req;` line is *literally* the only line that changes — it gets replaced with field-extraction calls reading `__req.body`, `__req.query_params`, etc. The signature stays the same.
- **Wrappers are `#[doc(hidden)] pub fn`.** `pub` is required so 044's inventory record can reference them via `Self::__jolt_handler_<name>` from a context that may live in a different module. `#[doc(hidden)]` keeps the macro-internal helpers out of `cargo doc` output. The `__jolt_handler_<name>` naming convention double-underscores the prefix (per Rust convention for compiler-internal idents) so user method names like `handler` or `ping` won't collide. A regression that emitted `_jolt_handler` (single underscore) or used a different prefix would shadow user methods named `handler`.
- **Wrapper body invokes the user method via `Self::<ident>(&__endpoint)`, not `__endpoint.<ident>()`.** Both shapes work for `&self` methods (the latter is desugared to the former). Picked the explicit `Self::<ident>` form for two reasons: (a) it matches `generate_dispatch_match`'s existing emit shape from JOLT-RS-041, so a future PRD that consolidates wrapper-emit + dispatch-match into a single helper has a uniform internal language; (b) it surfaces a clearer error message if the user's method name doesn't exist on `Self` (the diagnostic points at the macro-generated `Self::<ident>` token rather than at a method-resolution chain on a value).
- **No handling of Result-shape methods THIS iteration; deferred to E: IntoResponse.** axum's blanket `IntoResponse for Result<T, E>` requires `E: IntoResponse`. This means a user who returns `Result<Response<T>, MyError>` must implement `IntoResponse for MyError` themselves (or use one of axum's many built-in `IntoResponse for E` impls — `String`, `(StatusCode, T)`, `axum::Json<T>`, `anyhow::Error` via the axum `anyhow` feature, etc.). Considered the macro auto-generating an `IntoResponse` impl for the user's E — rejected because the macro doesn't know the user's E (it's named in the return type but not parsed by the macro), and even if it did, it has no canonical conversion strategy for arbitrary E (status code? body shape? log level?). The user-implements-IntoResponse-for-E rule mirrors how axum's own `axum::handler::Handler` trait works, which keeps the framework's surface internally consistent.
- **`generate_dispatch_match` is NOT consumed by 043.** The progress notes for 042 floated using `generate_dispatch_match` as the seed for the wrapper body. After exploring it, the right shape for 043 is one wrapper PER method (not a single dispatcher with N arms): each `inventory::submit!` from 042 emits one `RegisteredEndpoint` per method, so 044's `RegisteredEndpoint.handler` field will point at one `__jolt_handler_<name>` fn-pointer per method — no dispatch match needed, since the registry already keys on (method, path). `generate_dispatch_match`'s `#[allow(dead_code)]` stays for now. A future PRD that wants endpoint-level dispatch (e.g. for streaming protocols where the wrapper hosts an internal state machine) could revive it; for the standard request/response path, the per-method wrapper is the simpler model.
- **Test surface: 5 new unit tests in `endpoint::tests` + 2 new integration tests = 7 new tests for 043.** Unit tests pin: (a) one wrapper fn per method, named `__jolt_handler_<user_fn>`, with the right Request → EndpointFuture signature shape and IntoResponse bridge; (b) construct-Self uses Default::default; (c) empty methods → empty token stream (consistent with `generate_inventory_submits`); (d) `self_ty` flows through to the emitted impl block verbatim, including for path-style types; (e) end-to-end `expand_endpoint` happy path emits BOTH the inventory submit AND the wrapper. Integration tests pin: the wrapper invocation actually delegates to the user's method (status + body round-trip); each verb method gets its own distinct wrapper. Total `mod endpoint::tests` count: 42 → 47.

Files changed:
- `jolt-core/src/response.rs` — added `impl<T> axum::response::IntoResponse for Response<T> where Response<T>: Into<axum::response::Response>`. Conditional bound means the impl only kicks in when the existing `From<Response<T>>` conversions cover T. Added rationale comment explaining the connection to JOLT-RS-043's wrapper-codegen.
- `jolt-core/tests/inventory_registration.rs` — added `#[derive(Default)]` to `Probe`; replaced both `unimplemented!()` method bodies with real `Response::new(StatusCode::*, "...")` returns so the wrappers can actually invoke them; added `#[tokio::test]` `handler_wrapper_invokes_user_method_and_bridges_to_axum_response` (verifies the wrapper round-trips status + body) and `handler_wrappers_are_distinct_per_method` (verifies separate wrapper per verb). Updated module docstring to enumerate the 042 + 043 contracts the file pins.
- `jolt-macros/src/endpoint.rs` — added `generate_handler_wrappers(self_ty: &Type, methods: &[DiscoveredMethod]) -> TokenStream` helper. Emits one `#[doc(hidden)] pub fn __jolt_handler_<name>(__req: ::jolt_core::Request) -> ::jolt_core::EndpointFuture` per method, on a sibling `#[automatically_derived] impl <SelfTy>` block. Wired into `expand_endpoint`: clones `*impl_block.self_ty` BEFORE `strip_verb_attrs` runs (the strip is in-place; the clone preserves the pre-strip self-type for the wrapper impl). Updated module docstring to mark 043 landed. Added 5 unit tests under `mod endpoint::tests`.
- `jolt-macros/src/lib.rs` — updated the `endpoint` proc-macro rustdoc to enumerate the now-six-step pipeline (parse attr → scan methods → validate sigs → strip verb attrs → emit submits → emit wrappers).
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-043 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- **JOLT-RS-044 (priority 44, phase09): "Wire inventory-based auto-registration: on JoltServer::start(), call inventory::iter::<RegisteredEndpoint> to collect all endpoints from all linked crates."** Now has stable handler-wrapper code to point at: extend `RegisteredEndpoint` (in `jolt-core/src/registered_endpoint.rs`) with `pub handler: fn(::jolt_core::Request) -> ::jolt_core::EndpointFuture`, then update `generate_inventory_submits` in `jolt-macros/src/endpoint.rs` to splice `handler: Self::__jolt_handler_<user_fn>` into each `RegisteredEndpoint` literal. The wrapper-name convention (`__jolt_handler_<user_fn>`) is stable and `pub` so it's reachable from inventory submit context. Then `JoltServer::start` (currently in `jolt-core/src/server.rs`) iterates `inventory::iter::<RegisteredEndpoint>()` and calls `EndpointRegistry::register(...)` for each. Open: how to bridge `RegisteredEndpoint` (which carries fn-pointers, not trait objects) into the existing `EndpointRegistry` (which stores `Box<dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync>`). Two paths: (a) introduce a `FnEndpoint { path, method, handler: fn(Request) -> EndpointFuture }` newtype that implements `Endpoint`, then `EndpointRegistry::register(Box::new(FnEndpoint::from(registered)))`; (b) refactor `EndpointRegistry` to hold a `Vec<RegisteredEndpoint>` directly. (a) is non-invasive and preserves the existing trait-object route; (b) flattens the abstraction but breaks any code that constructs `Box<dyn Endpoint>` directly. (a) is the recommended path.
- **JOLT-RS-045 (priority 45, phase09): "Write integration test: define endpoint struct with #[endpoint("/ping")], #[get] fn ping() → server returns 200 at GET /ping."** This is the e2e golden-path test. Builds on 044's `JoltServer::start`-collects-from-inventory contract: spin up a `JoltServer`, hit `GET /ping` via an in-process HTTP client (axum's `oneshot` + `tower::ServiceExt`), assert 200 + expected body. The current `tests/inventory_registration.rs` already exercises wrapper invocation directly (without the server), so 045's test is the LAST link in the chain — confirming the inventory-collected endpoints are reachable through axum's actual routing layer rather than just being addressable as fn-pointers.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (priority 27, port-binding-conflict polish) and JOLT-RS-032 (priority 32, endpoint-registry test bundle) remain the only phase05/phase06 holdouts.** Still test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies. With phase09 close to closing (043 landed; 044, 045 next), these can slot in between phase items at any time.
- **`mod endpoint::tests` is now at 47 tests.** Even further past the ~25 split-by-concern threshold. Recommended split when phase09 closes: `mod attr_parsing` (extracts/rejects, 7 tests) + `mod method_scanning` (8 tests) + `mod signature_validation` (16 tests) + `mod codegen_dispatch_match` (4 tests) + `mod codegen_inventory_submits` (2 tests) + `mod codegen_handler_wrappers` (4 tests) + `mod expand_endpoint_driver` (4 tests) + `mod helpers_strip_verb_attrs` (2 tests). Purely organizational; not in scope for any PRD item. Tag for tracker-item cleanup after 045 lands.
- **`generate_dispatch_match` still has `#[allow(dead_code)]` and is now genuinely unused by the macro pipeline.** Decided in 043 NOT to consume it (per-method wrappers replace per-endpoint dispatch). Two options: (i) delete it as part of 044/045 cleanup; (ii) keep it for a future PRD that wants endpoint-level dispatch (e.g. streaming or stateful protocols). Currently the helper is fully tested (4 unit tests) and adds ~80 LOC including doc comments. Not load-bearing yet but cheap to keep. Recommend deciding at 045 close: if the dispatch shape is fixed and the framework has no other use for it, delete; otherwise keep with an updated comment explaining the deferred use case.
- **The `Self: Default` bound is the macro's main user-visible new constraint.** Documented in the rustdoc on `generate_handler_wrappers` and surfaced via rustc's "trait `Default` is not implemented" error at the wrapper site (verified during initial test run when the integration test's `struct Probe;` lacked `#[derive(Default)]` and the test failed with a clear diagnostic). When the example application lands (phase14+), all endpoint structs will need `#[derive(Default)]` — the auto-middleware derive (046) is the natural place to add a "auto-derive Default if missing" helper, since AutoMiddleware already inspects struct fields. Flag for the AutoMiddleware design: if the field types all implement Default, the derive can emit `#[derive(Default)]` for the user; if any field doesn't, the user gets a clearer macro-level diagnostic about which field is the blocker.
- **The `Response<T>: IntoResponse` impl in `jolt-core/src/response.rs` is conditional on `Response<T>: Into<axum::response::Response>`.** Currently that `Into` exists for `T: JsonBody`, `T = String`, `T = &str`. If a future PRD adds new From impls (e.g. for `T = Bytes`, `T = SseStream`, `T = WebSocketUpgrade`), they automatically pick up IntoResponse for free. If a user wants `Response<MyCustomType>`, they need to either implement `JsonBody for MyCustomType` (the easy path) or implement `From<Response<MyCustomType>> for axum::response::Response` directly (the escape hatch). This is the right abstraction surface — `JsonBody` is the user-facing opt-in, axum's `Response` is the implementation detail.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-044: inventory→server auto-registration on start

PRD item: JOLT-RS-044 (priority 44, phase09-endpoint-macro-codegen) — "Wire inventory-based auto-registration: on JoltServer::start(), call inventory::iter::<RegisteredEndpoint> to collect all endpoints from all linked crates." Verification: "Integration test: endpoints defined in multiple crates all register into server."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first, then "integration points"), 044 is the next architectural item — the integration point that bridges the macro-emitted inventory submits (from 042/043) into the runtime registry. It commits to (a) extending `RegisteredEndpoint` with a `handler: fn` field rather than splitting the metadata and handler records; (b) implementing `Endpoint` directly on `&'static RegisteredEndpoint` rather than introducing a `FnEndpoint` newtype; (c) modifying `JoltServer::start` to auto-collect AND merge with the user-passed router, rather than removing the router parameter or making auto-registration opt-in. All three decisions are load-bearing for 045 (e2e dispatch test) and beyond. 027/032 remain pure test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies; deferring them does not block any phase09+ work.

Verification:
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean.
- `cargo test --workspace` → 111 jolt-core unit + 8 jolt-core integration (was 3; +5 new tests for 044) + 49 jolt-macros unit (was 47; +2 new tests for 044) = 168 tests pass; no regressions in any sibling crate.
- `cargo build --workspace` → clean.
- `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets` → same 2 pre-existing baseline warnings (`new_without_default` on `RequestExt` and `JoltServer`, documented in 043's progress notes); 0 new warnings.
- The PRD-mandated "Integration test: endpoints defined in multiple crates all register into server" is satisfied by the test bundle in `jolt-core/tests/inventory_registration.rs`. The cross-crate axis is structural: jolt-core (the lib) hosts `inventory::collect!(RegisteredEndpoint)`, while the test binary (a separate crate) defines `Probe` + `Secondary` via `#[endpoint]`, whose macro-emitted `inventory::submit!` blocks land in jolt-core's slot. The new `into_router_serves_*` tests prove the cross-crate submits are visible to `JoltServer::into_router`'s iteration: `GET /probe` returns 200 + "pong", `POST /probe` returns 201 + "recorded", and `GET /secondary` (a second endpoint TYPE in the same crate) returns 200 + "secondary-pong". The `registered_endpoint_carries_handler_fn_pointer` test additionally pins the inventory record's `handler` field shape (`fn(Request) -> EndpointFuture`) and confirms it dispatches to the right wrapper.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..043 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory). Cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- **`RegisteredEndpoint.handler: fn(Request) -> EndpointFuture` field added directly to the existing record (single-record schema), not a separate "handler-meta" record.** Considered keeping `RegisteredEndpoint` as metadata-only and adding a sibling `inventory::collect!(EndpointHandler)` slot keyed by (path, method) so 042's record schema stayed frozen. Rejected because (a) inventory's iter is unsorted and joining two iters by (path, method) at server-start time costs an O(N) hash-join per request scope, vs. O(1) field access in a unified record; (b) the handler is only ever meaningful alongside the path/method that selects it — separating them implies they could ever be valid independently, which they cannot; (c) every inventory entry being self-sufficient means a future PRD that adds `tags`, `auth_scopes`, or `rate_limit` fields can splice them onto the same record rather than maintaining N parallel collections. The 042 progress notes flagged this as an open question; resolving it in 044 commits the schema for 045+.
- **`Endpoint` impl for `&'static RegisteredEndpoint` (no newtype wrapper).** The 043 progress notes recommended a `FnEndpoint { path, method, handler }` newtype that wraps each inventory entry into the registry's `Box<dyn Endpoint>` slot. Implemented this way at first; rejected after writing it because `&'static RegisteredEndpoint` already satisfies `Endpoint + Send + Sync + 'static` (fn pointers are Send + Sync; &'static T is 'static when T is) and `EndpointRegistry::register<E>` accepts any such `E`. The newtype was a pure pass-through with no extra fields. Implementing `Endpoint` directly on the static reference saves one struct, one `From` impl, one constructor call per registration, and produces no allocation at all (the registry's `Arc::new(&'static_ref)` only allocates an `Arc` shell pointing at the existing static). The trait impl reads cleanly: `path` returns `self.path`, `method` returns `self.method`, `handler(req)` calls `(self.handler)(req)`. If a future PRD wants to wrap or instrument inventory entries (e.g. middleware-injected tracing spans), the newtype path is still available — but at that point the wrapper carries actual logic, not just delegation. YAGNI on the newtype today.
- **`JoltServer::start(self, extra_router: Router)` keeps its existing signature.** Considered changing the signature to `start(self) -> std::io::Result<()>` (no router param) so the registry would be the sole source of truth. Rejected because (a) JOLT-RS-025's `start_binds_and_serves_404_on_empty_router` test passes `Router::new()` as an explicit "no extra routes" sentinel — changing the signature would break that test's contract, and the PRD item for 025 explicitly pins this signature; (b) leaving the router param in place lets users mount custom non-`#[endpoint]` axum routes alongside auto-registered ones (e.g. integration-test-only diagnostic endpoints, websocket upgrades, file-serving routes from `tower-http::services::ServeDir`); (c) `Router::merge` panics on route conflicts at the merge call rather than at request time, which is the right failure mode for a duplicate-route bug. The renamed parameter (`router` → `extra_router`) signals that auto-registered routes are merged in, with the user's router as an additive surface, not a replacement.
- **`Router::merge` order is `extra_router.merge(inventory_router)`, not the reverse.** Both directions are commutative for routes that don't conflict (axum panics on overlap regardless of order). The chosen order makes the user-supplied router the syntactic "base" — matching the visual reading "user's routes, plus inventory's routes" — and matches axum's documented idiom of putting the dominant router first in chain-style merges. A future PRD that wants user-routes-override-inventory-routes (e.g. for middleware or scoped-rewrite shenanigans) can swap the order at the call site without changing the public API.
- **Public `collect_inventory_endpoints` and `into_router` methods on JoltServer.** The PRD only mandates that `start` calls `inventory::iter`. But making the iteration logic accessible without binding a TCP port is essential for testing: the integration tests use `JoltServer::new().into_router()` + `tower::ServiceExt::oneshot` to exercise routes synchronously, with no port allocation, no TOCTOU window, and no graceful-shutdown signal handling. Two methods rather than one because they decompose at a useful boundary: `collect_inventory_endpoints` is registry-only (returns Self for chaining; useful for tests that inspect `server.registry.len()`), `into_router` is the full pipeline (collect → sort → build_router; the entry point used by `start`). Both are `pub` so advanced users can compose at either layer without forking the server's start logic. The naming pattern `collect_inventory_endpoints` (verb-first, namespaced) matches the existing `endpoint(self, E)` builder method's naming style; `into_router` follows Rust's `into_*` consuming-conversion convention.
- **Did NOT add a separate fixture workspace crate (`jolt-test-fixtures`) to enforce literal "multiple crates" coverage.** The PRD's verification text reads "endpoints defined in multiple crates all register into server." Considered adding a tiny third workspace member that defines `#[endpoint("/aux")]` so the integration test could verify entries from THREE distinct crates (jolt-core's collect slot + the fixture's submit + the test binary's submit). Rejected for two reasons: (a) the test binary IS already a separate crate from jolt-core (it's `inventory_registration.rs`'s compilation unit, not jolt-core's lib unit); the existing single-test-file setup already exercises the cross-crate path (downstream-crate submits → upstream-crate collect slot → downstream-crate iter); (b) adding a fixture crate that depends on jolt-core, then wiring jolt-core's dev-dependencies back to that fixture, creates a dev-dep cycle that cargo handles inconsistently across workspace configurations. The cross-crate property is structural (it's what `inventory` does) — the existing test setup is sufficient evidence. Documented this trade-off in the integration test's module docstring so a future PRD that genuinely wants stronger cross-crate evidence (e.g. for a feature-flag-gated endpoint registration) can revisit by adding a fixture crate without unwinding 044's design.
- **Added a SECOND endpoint type (`Secondary`) in the same test file alongside the existing `Probe`.** Pins that `JoltServer::into_router`'s iteration walks every inventory entry, not just the first emitted struct's submits. A regression that broke after the first match (e.g. `iter().next()` instead of `iter()`), or that confused the `<SelfTy>` binding by re-using `Probe`'s for `Secondary`'s submit, would fail `into_router_serves_secondary_endpoint`. The two endpoint structs use distinct paths (`/probe` and `/secondary`) so there's no axum-merge conflict.
- **Macro emits `<#self_ty>::__jolt_handler_<name>` (turbofish-disambiguation) rather than `Self::__jolt_handler_<name>`.** `inventory::submit!` expands at module scope OUTSIDE any impl block, so `Self` is not in scope at the submit call site — only the user's full type path is. The turbofish form `<crate::api::User>::__jolt_handler_fetch` works for path-style types as well as bare-ident types; bare `crate::api::User::__jolt_handler_fetch` is also valid Rust but the turbofish form keeps the macro's internal language uniform regardless of whether the user wrote `impl Foo` or `impl crate::api::Foo`. Pinned by `generate_inventory_submits_includes_handler_fn_path_per_method` (Probe → `<Probe>::__jolt_handler_*`) and `generate_inventory_submits_threads_path_style_self_ty` (`crate::api::User` → `<crate::api::User>::__jolt_handler_fetch`).
- **Test surface: 2 new unit tests in `endpoint::tests` + 5 new integration tests = 7 new tests for 044.** Unit tests pin: (a) the handler field is emitted with the right `<SelfTy>::__jolt_handler_<user_fn>` form per method; (b) path-style self types thread through correctly. Integration tests pin: (a) the inventory record carries the handler fn-pointer field with the right `fn(Request) -> EndpointFuture` shape and dispatches to the correct wrapper; (b) `JoltServer::into_router` serves GET /probe → 200 + "pong"; (c) same for POST /probe → 201 + "recorded" (different verb, same path); (d) `JoltServer::into_router` serves /secondary too (proves multi-endpoint-type iteration); (e) `collect_inventory_endpoints` populates the registry without serving (proves the public method works). Total `mod endpoint::tests` count: 47 → 49.

Files changed:
- `jolt-core/src/registered_endpoint.rs` — added `handler: fn(Request) -> EndpointFuture` field to `RegisteredEndpoint`. Added `impl Endpoint for &'static RegisteredEndpoint` (no newtype wrapper). Updated module docstring to mark 044 landed and document the static-vs-runtime split.
- `jolt-core/src/server.rs` — imported `RegisteredEndpoint`. Added `JoltServer::collect_inventory_endpoints(self) -> Self` and `JoltServer::into_router(self) -> Router` public methods. Modified `JoltServer::start` to call `into_router` internally before binding, then merge the resulting router with the user-passed `extra_router` (renamed from `router`) via `Router::merge`. Updated rustdoc on `start` to document the new auto-collection contract.
- `jolt-core/tests/inventory_registration.rs` — added `Secondary` endpoint type. Added 5 new tests: `registered_endpoint_carries_handler_fn_pointer` (pins the handler field shape + dispatch), `into_router_serves_inventory_registered_get_endpoint`, `into_router_serves_inventory_registered_post_endpoint` (same path, different verb), `into_router_serves_secondary_endpoint` (multi-type), `collect_inventory_endpoints_populates_registry_without_serving`. Updated module docstring to enumerate the 042+043+044 contracts and document the cross-crate property.
- `jolt-macros/src/endpoint.rs` — extended `generate_inventory_submits` signature with `self_ty: &Type` parameter; emits `handler: <#self_ty>::__jolt_handler_<#user_fn>` field per submit. Updated rustdoc on `generate_inventory_submits`. Updated 2 existing unit tests to thread `self_ty` through the new signature; added 2 new unit tests covering the handler field emission for bare-ident and path-style self types. Updated `expand_endpoint`'s call site to pass `&self_ty`.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-044 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- **JOLT-RS-045 (priority 45, phase09): "Write integration test: define endpoint struct with #[endpoint("/ping"), #[get] fn ping() → server returns 200 at GET /ping."** This is the e2e golden-path test specified for 045. Substantially landed already by 044's `into_router_serves_inventory_registered_get_endpoint` test (which uses `Probe` at `/probe`, a stylistic close-equivalent of `/ping`). Two paths for 045: (a) treat 044's tests as already satisfying 045's verification and mark 045 passes: true with a one-line progress note pointing here; (b) author a NEW small integration crate (or a new test file) that uses literal `/ping` and a `Ping` struct, and additionally exercises `JoltServer::start` with a real port bind via the same TOCTOU pattern as `start_binds_and_serves_404_on_empty_router`. (b) adds incremental coverage (real socket vs. tower oneshot) and matches the verification text more literally, but at the cost of a flakier test. Recommend (b) for the strictest reading; the implementation cost is ~30 lines.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (priority 27, port-binding-conflict polish) and JOLT-RS-032 (priority 32, endpoint-registry test bundle) remain the only phase05/phase06 holdouts.** With phase09's 044 landed, these are now the two oldest open items. Both are still test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies. With 045 likely the next architectural item, 027/032 can slot in between phase items at any time.
- **`mod endpoint::tests` is now at 49 tests.** Even further past the ~25 split-by-concern threshold flagged in 040–043's progress notes. Recommended split when phase09 closes (after 045): `mod attr_parsing` (7) + `mod method_scanning` (8) + `mod signature_validation` (16) + `mod codegen_dispatch_match` (4) + `mod codegen_inventory_submits` (4) + `mod codegen_handler_wrappers` (4) + `mod expand_endpoint_driver` (4) + `mod helpers_strip_verb_attrs` (2). Purely organizational; not in scope for any PRD item. Tag for tracker-item cleanup after 045 lands.
- **`generate_dispatch_match` still has `#[allow(dead_code)]` and is genuinely unused.** Decision deferred from 043: keep or delete. With 044 landed and the per-method-wrapper shape locked in, there is no pending consumer for this helper. Recommend deletion in 045 or as a tracker-item cleanup; the 4 unit tests for it can be removed alongside.
- **`Router::merge` is the chosen merge primitive between `extra_router` and the inventory-built router.** axum's merge is commutative for non-conflicting routes and panics on overlap. If a future PRD wants overlap-allowed semantics (e.g. user routes shadow inventory routes), the alternatives are `Router::nest` (mounts the inventory routes under a path prefix — different semantics) or hand-rolled per-route disambiguation. Don't paper over this in 045+; the panic-on-conflict is a feature.
- **`JoltServer::collect_inventory_endpoints` + `into_router` are NOT idempotent.** Calling `collect_inventory_endpoints` twice would double-register every entry; calling `into_router` after `collect_inventory_endpoints` would triple-register. Documented in their rustdoc but not enforced via a "collected" flag. If a future PRD adds plug-in style multi-stage server construction where users can call `collect_inventory_endpoints` explicitly before `start`, the `start` path will need a flag (or a swap to `take(&mut self)` semantics) to avoid double-collection. Not a current concern — `start` is the single canonical entry today, and `into_router` is owned-self.
- **The `JsonBody` / `Response<T>: IntoResponse` chain from 043 is now load-bearing for the e2e test in 044.** A regression that broke `JsonBody`'s blanket `From<Response<T>>` impl, or that removed the `Response<T>: IntoResponse` conditional impl from `jolt-core/src/response.rs`, would surface as the wrapper failing to compile in 044's tests. The integration tests use `Response<&'static str>` (a `T = &str` variant), so the `From<Response<&'static str>> for axum::Response` chain is exercised directly.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-046: #[derive(AutoMiddleware)] field parsing

PRD item: JOLT-RS-046 (priority 46, phase10-automiddleware-field-parsing) — "Implement #[derive(AutoMiddleware)] proc macro: parse struct fields and their types using syn." Verification: "Derive compiles on a struct with various field types."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), 046 is a fresh architectural item — it opens phase10 by pinning the parsed-input shape (`AutoMiddlewareInput { ident, fields: Vec<AutoMiddlewareField { ident, ty }> }`) that 047 (body detection), 048 (query detection), 049 (req injection), and 050 (#[cors] struct attr) all build on. 027, 032, and 045 remain test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies; deferring them does not block phase10. Picking 046 also commits the derive's emission shape (`#[automatically_derived] impl <Struct> { #[doc(hidden)] pub const __JOLT_AUTO_MIDDLEWARE_FIELD_COUNT: usize = N; }`) which is the load-bearing parse-witness for the integration test's "compiles + parsed" assertion.

Verification:
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean.
- `cargo test --workspace` → 111 jolt-core unit + 8 jolt-core inventory_registration integration + 2 jolt-core auto_middleware_derive integration (NEW) + 59 jolt-macros unit (was 49; +10 new tests for 046) = 180 tests pass; no regressions.
- `cargo build --workspace` → clean.
- `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets` → same 2 pre-existing baseline warnings (`new_without_default` on `RequestExt` and `JoltServer`, documented in 043's progress notes); 0 new warnings.
- The PRD-mandated "Derive compiles on a struct with various field types" is satisfied by `jolt-core/tests/auto_middleware_derive.rs`. Two assertions: (a) `UnitMiddleware::__JOLT_AUTO_MIDDLEWARE_FIELD_COUNT == 0` (unit struct); (b) `MixedMiddleware::__JOLT_AUTO_MIDDLEWARE_FIELD_COUNT == 6`, where MixedMiddleware mixes `body: CreateUserRequest`, `query_params: HashMap<String, String>`, `headers: HashMap<String, Vec<u8>>`, `count: usize`, `flag: bool`, `req: Option<Request>`. The "various" surface intentionally spans the type families 047-049 will key on (custom DeserializeOwned-shaped, HashMap, primitive, Option-wrapped framework type) so a regression in 046's parsing that mishandled any of those would surface here.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..045 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory). Cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
