Iteration: 2026-05-10 (JOLT-RS-055 — define CorsConfig struct fields)
PRD item: JOLT-RS-055 (priority 55, phase12-cors-middleware)
Description: "Define CorsConfig struct: allow_origins (Vec<String>), allow_methods (Vec<Method>), allow_headers (Vec<String>), max_age (u32)."
PRD verification: "Struct compiles with defaults."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish; JOLT-RS-054 phase11 closing test): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), 055 introduces the load-bearing CORS data shape that JOLT-RS-056..058's tower::Layer impls read at request time. Picking 055 over 054 (phase11 closing) follows the rule's literal ordering — 054 is a phase-closing test (polish bucket), 055 is a new core abstraction (top bucket). The Cargo.lock + workspace already compiles with the unit-struct stub from 042; replacing it now means 056 can build directly against the final field shape rather than chasing two CorsConfig migrations. 027/032/045/054 remain test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies; deferring them does not block 056..058.

Implementation notes:
- **Field shape mirrors the PRD verbatim**: `allow_origins: Vec<String>`, `allow_methods: Vec<Method>`, `allow_headers: Vec<String>`, `max_age: u32`. All fields `pub` so the upcoming layer impl reads them directly without accessor boilerplate. Public-field surface lets the struct double as a config record AND a literal-construction site, which the new `cors_config_constructed_with_explicit_fields` test pins.
- **`allow_methods` uses `crate::method::Method`**, not a string list. Holding the parsed enum lets the CORS layer serialize via `Method::as_str()` without re-parsing, and rejects typos at construction time. A future PRD that wants user-defined verbs ("PURGE", "REPORT") will need to widen Method first; for now the seven standard verbs cover the spec.
- **`max_age: u32`** — RFC 6454 caps `Access-Control-Max-Age` at implementation-defined limits well under 2^31, so `u32` covers the effective range without sign concerns. Held as a raw integer (not a `Duration`) because the CORS header is serialized as a bare seconds count; converting back from Duration would require an extra `.as_secs()` cast at every emit site.
- **Default impl: empty vecs + `max_age = 0`** — i.e. fully restrictive. Decision: defaults must NOT enable CORS for any origin; opening up the policy is an explicit caller choice. A permissive default (`allow_origins: vec!["*"]`, etc.) would be footgun-shaped for a security-relevant header. Pinned by `cors_config_default_is_empty_and_restrictive`.
- **Derives: `Debug, Clone, Default`.** Debug carried from the prior unit-struct stub. Clone added because the upcoming tower::Layer impl will need to clone the config into per-request layer instances (Layer trait requires Clone on the config it carries, per the existing tower 0.5 contract). Default derived rather than hand-written because every field type is itself `Default` (Vec is Default, u32 is Default).
- **Module rustdoc updated**: removed the "stub markers" wording that covered both CorsConfig and TlsConfig in the old shape, and split into a dedicated CorsConfig paragraph naming the four fields and the empty/restrictive default contract. TlsConfig stays a stub marker — that's a separate future PRD.
- **Existing test migration**: `cors_builder_wraps_arg_in_some` previously constructed `CorsConfig` as a unit (`JoltServer::new().cors(CorsConfig)`), which no longer compiles. Migrated to `CorsConfig::default()`. The test's intent (builder wraps the arg in `Some`) is unchanged; only the construction shape changed.

Verification:
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean.
- `cargo check --workspace --tests` → clean.
- `cargo test --workspace` → 113 jolt-core unit (was 111; +2 new for 055) + 6 jolt-core auto_middleware_derive integration + 8 jolt-core inventory_registration integration + 130 jolt-macros unit = 257 tests pass; no regressions in any sibling crate.
- `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets` → same 2 pre-existing baseline warnings (`new_without_default` on `RequestExt` and `JoltServer`); 0 new warnings.
- The PRD-mandated "Struct compiles with defaults" verification is satisfied by `cors_config_default_is_empty_and_restrictive` in `jolt-core/src/tests.rs`. The test calls `CorsConfig::default()`, asserts each field's default value (empty Vec, empty Vec, empty Vec, 0). Pairs with `cors_config_constructed_with_explicit_fields` (literal-construction surface witness) and the migrated `cors_builder_wraps_arg_in_some` (now uses `CorsConfig::default()` against the new shape).

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..053 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory). Cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- **Empty/restrictive defaults, NOT permissive.** Three considered shapes: (a) empty Vecs + max_age 0 (current choice — no origin is allowed unless explicitly listed); (b) `allow_origins: vec!["*"]` + standard methods + max_age 86400 (browser-ergonomic but security-footgun); (c) `Default::default()` only on the derive macro, no hand-written semantic — yields (a) anyway via the field types' own Defaults. Picked (a) on principle: a CORS config that says "allow nothing" is the correct null-object — equivalent to having no CORS layer at all. A permissive default would be a silent attack-surface expansion the moment any caller calls `CorsConfig::default()` thinking it's inert.
- **`Vec<Method>`, NOT `Vec<String>` for allow_methods.** Two considered shapes: (a) hold parsed Method enum (current) — typo-rejecting, no per-emit re-parse; (b) hold raw String — flexible for future custom verbs. Picked (a) because Jolt's Method covers the seven standard verbs the spec mentions and any future custom-verb support belongs in Method itself, not in a per-config string-bag escape hatch. The PRD text says "allow_methods (Vec<Method>)" verbatim, so this matches the spec literally.
- **`max_age: u32`, NOT `Duration` or `u64`.** The CORS header's wire format is a plain integer count of seconds; `u32` covers the effective range (~136 years) without sign concerns and serializes via a bare ToString. `Duration` would force a `.as_secs() as u32` at every emit; `u64` is overkill for a value the spec caps well under 2^31.
- **Public fields, not private + getters.** The struct is a config record — the constructor IS the API. Pinned by the literal-construction test (`cors_config_constructed_with_explicit_fields`). If a future PRD wants validation on construction (e.g. reject invalid origin URLs), it will need to flip to private fields + a `with_*` builder; that's a separate refactor with explicit migration. For now, public fields keep the surface minimal.
- **`Clone` derived on the struct.** Required by tower 0.5's Layer contract: `impl Layer<S> for SomeLayer where SomeLayer: Clone`. Without Clone, JOLT-RS-056..058's layer impl would either need to wrap the config in `Arc<CorsConfig>` (extra indirection, allocation per-server) or hand-roll a Clone impl. Deriving now keeps the layer impl clean.
- **Migrated `cors_builder_wraps_arg_in_some`, didn't add a parallel test.** The existing test's intent ("`.cors()` wraps the arg in `Some`") is unchanged by 055; only the construction shape changed. Adding a `cors_builder_wraps_default_arg_in_some` parallel would be redundant. The migration is the minimal mechanical fix to keep the existing assertion green against the new shape.
- **TlsConfig left untouched.** The PRD's `JOLT-RS-055` text only mentions CorsConfig. TlsConfig is a separate stub awaiting its own TLS-phase PRD; touching it now would be scope creep.

Files changed:
- `jolt-core/src/server.rs` — replaced `pub struct CorsConfig;` with the four-field record (`allow_origins: Vec<String>`, `allow_methods: Vec<Method>`, `allow_headers: Vec<String>`, `max_age: u32`), derived `Debug, Clone, Default`. Added `use crate::method::Method;` import. Updated module-level rustdoc to split CorsConfig (now real) from TlsConfig (still a stub marker), naming the four fields and the empty/restrictive default contract. Added struct-level rustdoc explaining each field's correspondence to a CORS preflight response header and the `Default` semantics.
- `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` — migrated `cors_builder_wraps_arg_in_some` from `CorsConfig` (unit-struct construction) to `CorsConfig::default()`. Added `cors_config_default_is_empty_and_restrictive` (PRD-mandated defaults witness) and `cors_config_constructed_with_explicit_fields` (literal-construction surface witness). Total `mod server::tests` count: +2 net.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-055 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- **JOLT-RS-056 (priority 56, phase12): "Implement CorsLayer as tower::Layer: on OPTIONS request, return 204 with Access-Control-Allow-Origin, Allow-Methods, Allow-Headers, Access-Control-Max-Age headers. Set RequestExt::mark_finished()."** Now has the final `CorsConfig` shape to read at construction time. The layer struct will likely be `pub struct CorsLayer { config: CorsConfig }` with a `Clone` derive (config is already Clone). The `Layer<S>` impl wraps an inner service in a `CorsService<S>` that also holds the config; on `OPTIONS`, the service returns the 204 short-circuit; otherwise it delegates to inner.call. The `mark_finished` semantics live on `RequestExt`, so the wrapper service will need access to `RequestExt` — that means `Service<Request>` (NOT generic over `__Req`). This is the "Jolt-aware" layer the 053 progress notes flagged as a future need.
- **JOLT-RS-058 (priority 58, phase12): CORS unit tests** — the `cors_config_default_is_empty_and_restrictive` test pinned at 055 covers the "empty origins → no allow header" edge case; 058 will need to add wildcard, specific match, and preflight tests against the actual layer (not just the config struct).
- **`AutoMiddleware`'s `#[cors]` attribute (050)** is parsed but unconsumed by codegen. Once the CorsLayer (056) ships, the next phase11/12 boundary item should wire `#[cors]` → "use the server's `CorsConfig` via the shared `CorsLayer`" in the auto-middleware derive's chain. Currently the chain emits a `jolt::middleware::step::cors` marker statement (per 052) that's never replaced — a `#[cors]` derive currently doesn't actually short-circuit OPTIONS. The wiring task isn't in the PRD by ID I can see; flag it for whichever iteration closes phase12.
- **`JoltServer.cors()` builder takes `CorsConfig` by value, not `Into<CorsConfig>` or by ref.** That's still correct for the new shape — the config is `Clone` so the server stores its own copy. If a future PRD wants `.cors(impl Into<CorsConfig>)` for ergonomics ("pass me a Vec<String> and I'll wrap it"), that's a backwards-compatible change. Not needed at 055.
- **Method's `Vec<Method>` ordering is not normalized.** The CORS layer should probably emit methods in a stable order regardless of construction order (so a `Vec<Method>::new().push(Get).push(Post)` and a `Vec<Method>::new().push(Post).push(Get)` produce the same `Access-Control-Allow-Methods` header). 056 should decide whether to sort at construction, sort at emit, or accept the caller's ordering verbatim. Not a 055 concern.
- **TlsConfig is still a stub.** The TLS phase is a separate future PRD — touching TlsConfig now would be scope creep. Flagged here so whichever iteration takes on TLS doesn't have to re-discover.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test bundle), 045 (endpoint-integration test), 054 (phase11 closing test).** The pre-046 holdouts plus the just-deferred 054. With phase12 now started, these are even lower priority — recommend continuing to defer until a polish-pass between phase12 closing (after 058) and whatever phase13 brings.

================================================================================
Iteration: 2026-05-10 (JOLT-RS-056 — CorsLayer tower::Layer with OPTIONS preflight short-circuit)
PRD item: JOLT-RS-056 (priority 56, phase12-cors-middleware)
Description: "Implement CorsLayer as tower::Layer: on OPTIONS request, return 204 with Access-Control-Allow-Origin, Allow-Methods, Allow-Headers, Access-Control-Max-Age headers. Set RequestExt::mark_finished()."
PRD verification: "Unit test: OPTIONS /api/test → 204 with CORS headers, finished flag set."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish; JOLT-RS-054 phase11 closing test): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), 056 is the load-bearing seam that 057 (non-OPTIONS origin/expose-header injection) and 058 (CORS unit-test bundle) both build on. Picking 056 over the test-bundle holdouts pins the LAYER SHAPE (`CorsLayer { config: CorsConfig }` + `CorsService<S> { inner: S, config: CorsConfig }`), the SERVICE DOMAIN (`Service<axum::extract::Request>` not generic over `__Req`, matching the "Jolt-aware" pattern Router uses for `RequestExt` extension access), the SHORT-CIRCUIT MECHANISM (return the 204 directly from `call()` rather than stash-and-delegate via `RequestExt::set_response`), and the EMPTY-CONFIG SEMANTICS (`CorsConfig::default()` produces a bare 204 with no headers, matching 055's restrictive-default contract). All four decisions are load-bearing for 057+. 027/032/045/054 remain test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies; deferring them does not block any phase12+ work.

Implementation notes:
- **New module `jolt-core/src/cors.rs`** holds `CorsLayer`, `CorsService<S>`, and the private `build_preflight_response(&CorsConfig) -> axum::response::Response` helper. Pulled out into its own file (rather than appended to `server.rs`) because `server.rs` is the config-record home; the layer/service is the request-time machinery and warrants a sibling module. 057-058 will extend this same file rather than spilling further across the crate.
- **`CorsLayer { config: CorsConfig }`** with `Clone, Debug` derives — `Clone` is required by `tower::ServiceBuilder` composition and `tower::Layer`'s contract is to be cheap to clone per layer-stack instantiation. `CorsConfig` itself is already `Clone` (per JOLT-RS-055), so the derive is free.
- **`CorsService<S> { inner: S, config: CorsConfig }`** — the `Layer::layer(&self, inner) -> CorsService<S>` impl hands the produced service its OWN `CorsConfig` clone, so a long-lived `CorsLayer` and a per-stack `CorsService` are independent. The clone happens once per stack instantiation; per-request `call()` reads the field by reference, no further cloning.
- **`Service<AxumRequest> for CorsService<S>`** with bounds `S: Service<AxumRequest, Response = axum::response::Response> + Clone + Send + 'static, S::Future: Send + 'static, S::Error: Send + 'static`. The `Send + 'static` bounds are needed because the `Future` returned from `call()` is `Pin<Box<dyn Future<...> + Send>>` (matches Router's `Service::Future` type and lets the layer compose under `axum::serve`). `S::Error` flows through unchanged so the layer is composable with both Infallible and fallible inner services.
- **`AxumRequest = axum::extract::Request`, NOT generic `__Req`.** Three considered shapes: (a) generic-over-`__Req` like `auto_middleware`'s codegen — rejected because we need to read/write `req.extensions()` for `Arc<RequestExt>`, which only `axum::extract::Request` (and its `axum::http::Request<Body>` alias) provides; (b) generic with `R: HasExtensions` trait bound — rejected as speculative scaffolding for a single concrete consumer; (c) bound to `axum::extract::Request` (current choice) — pins the layer to the same wire-shape Router consumes, so `ServiceBuilder::new().layer(CorsLayer::new(cfg)).service(jolt_router)` composes cleanly. The progress notes from JOLT-RS-053 flagged this as the "Jolt-aware tower layer" need; 056 lands the first instance of the pattern.
- **OPTIONS short-circuit returns directly from `call()` — does NOT stash via `RequestExt::set_response`.** Two considered shapes: (a) build the 204, call `mark_finished()`, return `Box::pin(async move { Ok(response) })` (current choice); (b) build the 204, call `set_response(response)` + `mark_finished()`, then call `inner.call(req)` and let Router's existing JOLT-RS-035 short-circuit path surface the stashed response. Picked (a) because: (i) the layer is the response producer for OPTIONS, so producing it inline is the simplest thing that works; (ii) (b) requires the inner to be a Jolt Router specifically (not a bare service_fn or a chained tower layer), which would constrain composition; (iii) `mark_finished()` is still set as an OBSERVABILITY signal so any downstream observer (or test) can see the layer ran — but the response itself doesn't round-trip through the stash. The PRD spec says "Set RequestExt::mark_finished()" — that's satisfied by (a)'s `mark_finished()` call alone; the stash isn't required.
- **Preserve-or-inject `Arc<RequestExt>`** mirrors Router's JOLT-RS-035 contract: if the caller has placed an Arc in extensions (e.g. an outer test, a future composing layer that wants observability), preserve it; otherwise inject a fresh one so the layer's `mark_finished()` always has a target. Without this, a CorsLayer composed OUTSIDE a Router would have no place to set the finished flag and the spec's contract would be unfulfillable in that composition.
- **Standard tower `inner.clone() + std::mem::replace(...)` delegation pattern** for non-OPTIONS requests. The pattern is documented inline: `poll_ready` was driven on the current `self.inner`, so `call` must use that same instance — replacing with a clone (which the caller's NEXT poll_ready will ready) preserves the readiness contract.
- **Per-header conditional emission**: each of the four CORS response headers is emitted only when the matching `CorsConfig` field is non-empty / non-zero. Empty `allow_origins` → no `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` (so 055's restrictive default produces a bare 204). Empty `allow_methods` → no `Access-Control-Allow-Methods`. Empty `allow_headers` → no `Access-Control-Allow-Headers`. `max_age == 0` → no `Access-Control-Max-Age` (emitting `Max-Age: 0` would be opinionated; absence matches the "no opinion" stance of the default).
- **`Access-Control-Allow-Origin` emits the FIRST entry of `allow_origins`**, not a join. Per the spec, the header carries a single value per response — request-Origin matching against multiple configured origins is JOLT-RS-058's territory. For 056 the simple "first entry" semantics handle the common cases (single specific origin OR `vec!["*"]` wildcard) and the PRD verification's expected value (`"https://example.com"`).
- **`Access-Control-Allow-Methods` emits a comma-joined `Method::as_str()` listing**, e.g. `"GET, POST, OPTIONS"`. Method order is preserved from the config Vec — the 055 progress notes flagged "Vec<Method> ordering is not normalized" as a 056 decision; landed on "respect caller order" as the simplest contract. A future PRD that wants stable ordering can sort at construction or at emit; both are backwards-compatible with the current shape.
- **`HeaderValue::from_str(..)` checked, not `unwrap`.** Method::as_str returns ASCII-only, and the test's allow_origins/allow_headers values are ASCII, so the parse is unreachable in practice. The `if let Ok(value) = ...` guard skips the header on parse failure rather than panicking — defensive against a future config with non-visible-ASCII bytes (which is a config bug, but better to skip the header than crash the request handler).
- **`HeaderValue::from(config.max_age)`** uses the infallible `From<u32>` impl rather than `from_str(&config.max_age.to_string())` — saves an allocation and the impl is provided by the http crate.

Verification:
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean.
- `cargo test --workspace` → 114 jolt-core unit (was 113; +1 new for 056) + 6 jolt-core auto_middleware_derive integration + 8 jolt-core inventory_registration integration + 130 jolt-macros unit = 258 tests pass; no regressions in any sibling crate.
- `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets` → same 2 pre-existing baseline warnings (`new_without_default` on `RequestExt` and `JoltServer`); 0 new warnings. (Initial run flagged an unused `Service` import in the test module — fixed by trimming the import to `tower::{Layer, ServiceExt}` since the `.layer()` and `.oneshot()` calls are the only direct trait usages.)
- The PRD-mandated "OPTIONS /api/test → 204 with CORS headers, finished flag set" verification is satisfied by `cors::options_request_returns_204_with_cors_headers_and_marks_finished` in `jolt-core/src/tests.rs`. The test builds a populated CorsConfig (origin, three methods, two allowed headers, max_age=600), wraps a panicking inner service that asserts "OPTIONS never reaches inner" structurally (any non-panic outcome by definition exercised the short-circuit), sends `OPTIONS /api/test` carrying a caller-supplied `Arc<RequestExt>`, then asserts: status == 204, all four CORS headers present with the expected joined-or-passed-through values, and the caller's `Arc<RequestExt>::is_finished()` returns true.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..055 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory). Cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- **CorsLayer is `Service<axum::extract::Request>`, NOT `Service<jolt_core::Request>`.** The Jolt `Request` is the snapshot type passed to user handlers AFTER the registry walk has built it via `endpoint_registry::build_jolt_request`. Tower layers compose around the `axum::Router` / `jolt_core::Router` boundary, where the wire shape is `axum::extract::Request`. Pinning the layer to that domain matches the existing Router service shape and avoids re-implementing body-buffering (which is what `build_jolt_request` does).
- **OPTIONS short-circuit returns directly from `call()`, NOT via `RequestExt::set_response` + delegation.** Three-shape decision matrix documented inline in the implementation notes. The decisive factor: composition flexibility. (a) keeps the layer working with any inner service; (b) requires the inner to be a Router that respects the finished-flag stash. Composability matters because a future PRD (e.g. wiring `#[cors]` from `auto_middleware`) may want CorsLayer in a tower chain where the inner ISN'T Router.
- **Preserve-or-inject Arc<RequestExt> mirrors Router's JOLT-RS-035 contract.** The choice was either (a) require the caller to install RequestExt before this layer (rejected — a hidden contract that crashes at runtime if missed), (b) error out if RequestExt is missing (rejected — over-strict; a layer that doesn't actually need to stash anything shouldn't fail just because no one set up extension state), or (c) preserve-or-inject (current — mirrors the existing canonical pattern). The fresh-injected ext is dropped at request end if no one else holds a clone; the cost is one Arc allocation per request that didn't have one already, which is dwarfed by axum's per-request allocations anyway.
- **Empty/zero CorsConfig fields skip their headers entirely.** Two considered shapes: (a) skip-if-empty (current — produces a bare 204 for default config, matching 055's "default never opens up CORS" contract); (b) emit-empty-string headers (rejected — would add `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: ` with no value, which most browsers treat as malformed and many proxies strip). The skip-if-empty contract makes the default config a no-op (which is the spec's intent) and the explicit-fields contract intuitive (set a field, get a header).
- **First-origin selection for `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` (056-only).** The header is single-valued per the CORS spec, so a multi-origin config requires per-request `Origin`-header matching — that's JOLT-RS-058's territory. For 056 the simple "first entry" rule covers the common shapes (single specific origin, `vec!["*"]` wildcard) and pins the test verification. The first-entry rule is documented inline so 058 can replace it with the matching logic without surprise.
- **`max_age == 0` skips the Max-Age header.** Two considered shapes: (a) skip if zero (current — preserves the "default never opts in" semantic; absence means "no opinion, browser default"); (b) always emit (rejected — `Max-Age: 0` tells browsers to never cache the preflight, which is opinionated and not what an absent header means). The skip-if-zero rule lets a caller opt into caching by setting `max_age` and opt out by leaving it at the default — clean binary signal.
- **`pub use cors::{CorsLayer, CorsService};` in lib.rs** — both types are user-facing surface (CorsLayer for explicit construction, CorsService for type-spec / where-bounds in user-defined helpers). Exposing both at the crate root matches the existing pattern (`Router`, `Endpoint`, `RequestExt` all re-exported the same way).
- **Test stub uses `tower::service_fn` with an explicit `Ok::<Response, Infallible>(...)` unreachable line.** Two considered shapes: (a) hand-written stub struct implementing Service<AxumRequest> manually (rejected — boilerplate for a single test); (b) `service_fn` closure with type-annotation hint after the panic (current — the unreachable Ok arm gives the compiler enough info to resolve the closure's Future Output type without forcing the test to construct a real Response). The `#[allow(unreachable_code)]` is local to the closure.

Files changed:
- `jolt-core/src/cors.rs` — new file. `CorsLayer` (config holder, `Clone + Debug`), `CorsService<S>` (inner-service wrapper, generic over inner, `Clone + Debug`), `tower::Layer<S> for CorsLayer` impl producing `CorsService<S>`, `tower::Service<AxumRequest> for CorsService<S>` impl with OPTIONS short-circuit + non-OPTIONS delegation, private `build_preflight_response(&CorsConfig)` helper. Module-level rustdoc explains the layer's role, the four headers, the preserve-or-inject `Arc<RequestExt>` contract, and the empty-default semantics. Per-impl rustdoc on `CorsLayer`, `CorsLayer::new`, and `CorsService` documents the Clone rationale, the consumed-by-value config, and the wrapper's role respectively.
- `jolt-core/src/lib.rs` — added `pub mod cors;` declaration alongside the existing modules. Added `pub use cors::{CorsLayer, CorsService};` re-export alongside the existing `Cookie` / `Endpoint` / etc. exports.
- `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` — appended new `mod cors` test module with `options_request_returns_204_with_cors_headers_and_marks_finished` (PRD-mandated verification). Test imports `tower::{Layer, ServiceExt}` (no `Service` direct usage), builds a populated `CorsConfig`, wraps a panicking `service_fn` inner via `layer.layer(inner)`, sends `OPTIONS /api/test` carrying a caller-supplied `Arc<RequestExt>`, asserts status + all four CORS headers + finished flag.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-056 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- **JOLT-RS-057 (priority 57, phase12): "On non-OPTIONS requests, inject Access-Control-Allow-Origin (and optionally Access-Control-Expose-Headers) into the response."** The current `CorsService::call`'s non-OPTIONS branch is `Box::pin(async move { inner.call(req).await })` — a bare delegation. 057 will need to: (a) `.await` the inner future, (b) inspect the resulting `Response` (or borrow it via headers_mut), (c) inject `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` (matching the request's Origin header against `config.allow_origins`, OR using the first-entry rule like 056 if the spec allows), (d) optionally inject `Access-Control-Expose-Headers` from a (currently nonexistent) `expose_headers` field on CorsConfig — flag that 057 may need to extend `CorsConfig` to add the field, or accept that "optionally" means "skip for now and add in a polish PRD". The first-entry simplification from 056 should probably be REPLACED in 057 with proper origin matching — both 056's preflight and 057's response injection would benefit from a shared `select_allowed_origin(&config, &req) -> Option<&str>` helper.
- **JOLT-RS-058 (priority 58, phase12): "Write CORS unit tests: wildcard origin, specific origin match, no-match returns no CORS header, preflight returns correct methods."** The 056 `mod cors` test module is the natural home — 058 will add ~4 sibling tests covering wildcard, specific match, no-match, preflight-methods-correctness. The `panicking_inner` pattern from 056 is directly reusable for any test that should NOT reach the inner service (i.e. all OPTIONS tests). For non-OPTIONS tests (057's domain), the inner needs to actually return a response so the layer's injection logic has something to mutate.
- **`Access-Control-Allow-Origin` first-entry simplification is a known TODO.** The 056 test uses `vec!["https://example.com"]` (single entry), which works correctly under the simplification. A wildcard test (`vec!["*"]`) would also work. A multi-origin config where the test's `Origin` header should select the SECOND entry would NOT — that's 058's coverage gap to close.
- **`Access-Control-Expose-Headers` is NOT in `CorsConfig`** as of 055/056. The 057 description says "optionally Access-Control-Expose-Headers". If 057 wants to inject this header, it'll need to either (a) extend CorsConfig with `pub expose_headers: Vec<String>` (small, additive, no breaking change), or (b) defer to a polish PRD. Recommend (a) at 057 entry — keeping the config record complete for the layer's full surface.
- **CorsLayer doesn't yet handle the `Access-Control-Allow-Credentials` header.** Not in the PRD spec for 056-058. If a future PRD wants credential-bearing CORS, it'll need to extend CorsConfig with `pub allow_credentials: bool` and inject the header on both OPTIONS and non-OPTIONS responses (typically alongside the origin header). Out of scope for now.
- **`AutoMiddleware`'s `#[cors]` attribute (050) is still parsed but unconsumed by codegen.** Now that CorsLayer ships, the wiring task ("when a derive has `#[cors]`, splice CorsLayer into its middleware chain pulling from the server's CorsConfig") is unblocked but still unscheduled in the PRD. The `jolt::middleware::step::cors` marker statement from 052 is the splice point. Flag for the iteration that closes phase12.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test bundle), 045 (endpoint-integration test), 054 (phase11 closing test).** Still the only pre-046 holdouts plus 054. Recommendation unchanged: defer to a polish-pass between phase12 closing (after 058) and whatever phase13 brings.
- **`CorsLayer` is NOT yet auto-installed by `JoltServer::start`.** A user who calls `.cors(config)` on the server today still doesn't get a CorsLayer in their tower stack — `cors_config` is stored but never wired. The wiring task isn't in the PRD by ID I can see; the natural place is in `JoltServer::start` (or `into_router`), conditionally on `cors_config.is_some()`. Flag for the iteration that closes phase12 OR the auto-middleware-`#[cors]`-wiring item (which may subsume it).

================================================================================
JOLT-RS-057 (priority 57, phase12-cors-middleware) — non-OPTIONS Allow-Origin / Expose-Headers injection
================================================================================

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish; JOLT-RS-054 phase11 closing test; JOLT-RS-058 CORS test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("standard implementation" before "polish"), 057 is the load-bearing non-OPTIONS branch that completes the CorsLayer's request-time surface. 056 shipped the OPTIONS short-circuit; 057 closes the symmetric requirement that NORMAL responses (GET/POST/PUT/PATCH/DELETE) also carry the CORS response headers a browser-side script needs. 058's test bundle (wildcard origin / specific match / no-match / preflight-methods) presupposes both the OPTIONS branch (056, done) AND the non-OPTIONS branch (057, this iteration) — so 058 cannot land before 057. 027/032/045/054 remain test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies; deferring them does not block any phase12+ work and matches the prior iteration's recommendation.

Implementation notes:
- **Extended `CorsConfig` with `pub expose_headers: Vec<String>` (additive, after `max_age`)**. The 057 PRD spec parenthesizes "(and optionally Access-Control-Expose-Headers)" — without a config field there's no way for the caller to opt in, so the "optionally" semantics would be unimplementable in any testable way. Two considered shapes: (a) skip Expose-Headers entirely in 057, defer to a polish PRD (rejected — leaves the spec's parenthetical literally unimplemented); (b) extend `CorsConfig` with `pub expose_headers: Vec<String>` (current — small, additive, no breaking change to consumers since field is `Vec<String>::default()` = `vec![]`). The previous iteration's 056 progress notes flagged exactly this decision and recommended (b) at 057 entry.
- **`CorsService::call` non-OPTIONS branch now `.await`s the inner response, then mutates headers in place** via the new private `inject_response_cors_headers(config, response)` helper. The branch is no longer a bare `inner.call(req).await` delegation — the future now: (1) clones `self.config` into the async block (cheap; CorsConfig is `Clone` and the Vecs are short), (2) `.await`s `inner.call(req)` and propagates `?` on `S::Error`, (3) calls `inject_response_cors_headers(&config, &mut response)`, (4) returns the mutated response. The `Box::pin(async move { ... })` future shape is unchanged from 056 so no `Service::Future` type bound updates were needed.
- **`inject_response_cors_headers` is a NEW free function** (private to `cors.rs`), not a method on `CorsService` — keeps it independently testable from the service-call wiring and matches the existing `build_preflight_response` shape (also a free function). Two header injections live there; future Allow-Credentials (out of scope) would slot in as a third.
- **`Access-Control-Allow-Origin` injection mirrors the OPTIONS branch's first-entry rule**, deliberately so. Per-request `Origin`-header matching against multiple configured origins is JOLT-RS-058's territory. For 057, "first entry of `allow_origins`" handles: (i) the single-origin case (echoes the origin), (ii) the wildcard case (`vec!["*"]` echoes `*`), (iii) the empty case (no header). Both branches now consume the same simplification, which means 058's matching refactor will land in ONE place (the future `select_allowed_origin(&config, &req) -> Option<&str>` helper) rather than two.
- **`Access-Control-Expose-Headers` injection emits a comma-joined `expose_headers` list** when non-empty. Empty config → no header (matches the 055 restrictive-default contract). The join uses `Vec::join(", ")` which is the standard CORS-header serialization shape used by every browser CORS implementation; the leading-space-after-comma is conventional but not strictly required by the spec.
- **Both injections check `headers.contains_key(...)` BEFORE inserting** — the layer is ADDITIVE, not authoritative. If the inner service (e.g. a per-route handler that wants origin-specific policy) has already set either header, the layer leaves it alone. Two considered shapes: (a) always overwrite (rejected — silently shadows handler-level CORS decisions, surprising); (b) only fill if absent (current — handler decisions win, the layer is a default-filling backstop). The new `non_options_response_preserves_inner_set_cors_headers` test pins (b)'s contract.
- **Existing JOLT-RS-035 short-circuit semantics preserved**: the non-OPTIONS branch does NOT call `mark_finished()`. Only the OPTIONS branch flips that flag (it represents "the layer produced the response"). For non-OPTIONS the inner produced the response and the layer is just decorating headers — no observability signal needed. The new `non_options_response_gets_allow_origin_and_expose_headers_injected` test pins this with `assert!(!ext.is_finished())`.
- **Module rustdoc updated** to describe the non-OPTIONS injection contract: which two headers, the additive (preserve-existing) semantic, and the link to `ACCESS_CONTROL_EXPOSE_HEADERS` constant. The "JOLT-RS-057's territory" placeholder from 056 was replaced with the actual contract.
- **Test module gets +3 new tests** (sibling to 056's `options_request_returns_204_with_cors_headers_and_marks_finished`): `non_options_response_gets_allow_origin_and_expose_headers_injected` (PRD-mandated GET verification + Expose-Headers exercise), `non_options_response_skips_headers_when_config_is_empty` (default-config no-leak guarantee), `non_options_response_preserves_inner_set_cors_headers` (additive contract). All three reuse the `tower::service_fn` inner stub pattern from 056 — for non-OPTIONS the inner returns a real `Response` (panicking would be wrong since the layer DOES delegate).

Verification:
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean, ~1s incremental.
- `cargo test --workspace` → 117 jolt-core unit (was 114; +3 new for 057) + 6 jolt-core auto_middleware_derive integration + 8 jolt-core inventory_registration integration + 130 jolt-macros unit = 261 tests pass; no regressions in any sibling crate.
- `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets` → same 2 pre-existing baseline warnings (`new_without_default` on `RequestExt` and `JoltServer`); 0 new warnings.
- The PRD-mandated "GET /api/test → response includes CORS origin header" verification is satisfied by `cors::non_options_response_gets_allow_origin_and_expose_headers_injected` in `jolt-core/src/tests.rs`. The test builds a populated CorsConfig (origin, two methods, one allow header, max_age=600, two expose headers), wraps an inner that returns `200 OK` with body `"hello"`, sends `GET /api/test` carrying a caller-supplied `Arc<RequestExt>`, then asserts: status == 200, `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` == "https://example.com", `Access-Control-Expose-Headers` == "x-request-id, x-trace-id", finished flag NOT set.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..056 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory). Cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- **`expose_headers` lives on `CorsConfig`, not on a separate `ExposeHeadersConfig`.** Two considered shapes: (a) standalone `ExposeHeadersConfig` struct attached to a separate `ExposeHeadersLayer` (rejected — splits the layer surface for one closely-related field; an Expose-Headers layer always implies a CORS context); (b) extend `CorsConfig` (current — keeps the CORS surface in one record, matches how every mainstream CORS library models the field). The cost is one additional Vec on the struct; the benefit is single-record configuration ergonomics.
- **First-entry rule for `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` (non-OPTIONS), mirroring 056's OPTIONS branch.** Two considered shapes: (a) implement proper Origin-header matching now, and refactor 056's OPTIONS branch to share the helper (rejected — drags 056 into 057's scope, expands the diff, and 056's test would need an Origin header added; cleaner to land matching as a single 058 refactor that touches both branches uniformly); (b) mirror 056's first-entry rule (current — keeps 057 narrowly focused on the response-injection contract; 058's coming test bundle for "wildcard / specific / no-match" will reveal the matching is needed and the refactor will land in one place rather than two iterations). The progress notes from 056 explicitly recommended this layering.
- **Layer is ADDITIVE — preserves inner-set CORS headers rather than overwriting.** Two considered shapes: (a) always overwrite (rejected — a per-route handler that explicitly sets `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` for an origin-specific policy decision would be silently shadowed; debugging this would be miserable since the handler call site looks correct); (b) only inject when absent (current — handler decisions win; layer is a default-filling backstop). The contract is documented in module rustdoc and pinned by `non_options_response_preserves_inner_set_cors_headers`. A future PRD that wants strict layer-wins semantics (e.g. compliance-driven CORS enforcement) can add a `force` flag to `CorsConfig`.
- **`mark_finished()` is NOT called on non-OPTIONS requests.** The OPTIONS branch flips it because the LAYER produced the response (short-circuit observability). On non-OPTIONS, the inner produced the response — the layer is just decorating headers, not claiming authorship. Setting `finished` would falsely signal "the response is final, downstream layers can skip" which is not what header injection means. Pinned by `assert!(!ext.is_finished())` in the new GET test.
- **`inject_response_cors_headers` is a free function, not a method on `CorsService`.** Matches the existing `build_preflight_response` shape (also a free function), independently testable, and avoids threading `&self.config` through async-block lifetimes (the function takes `&CorsConfig` directly). The future shared `select_allowed_origin` helper (058) will fit the same shape.
- **Default values for `expose_headers` rely on `Vec<String>::default() = vec![]`.** No explicit default needed in `CorsConfig::default()` since the derive-Default already produces `vec![]` for the Vec field. The 055 default-test was extended with one additional `assert!(cfg.expose_headers.is_empty())` line; the 056 OPTIONS test gets `expose_headers: vec![]` in its literal CorsConfig construction (with an inline comment explaining why it's empty for the OPTIONS-focused test).

Files changed:
- `jolt-core/src/server.rs` — added `pub expose_headers: Vec<String>` field to `CorsConfig`, after `max_age`. Extended the rustdoc to describe the field's purpose, the empty-default semantics, and the JOLT-RS-057 attribution.
- `jolt-core/src/cors.rs` — added `ACCESS_CONTROL_EXPOSE_HEADERS` to the imported header constants. Updated module rustdoc: replaced the "JOLT-RS-057's territory" placeholder with the actual non-OPTIONS injection contract (Allow-Origin first-entry rule, Expose-Headers join, additive/preserve-existing semantic, link to the constant). Replaced the non-OPTIONS branch's bare `Box::pin(async move { inner.call(req).await })` delegation with an `await`-then-decorate body that calls the new `inject_response_cors_headers(&config, &mut response)` helper. Added the private `inject_response_cors_headers` free function with rustdoc explaining the additive contract and the per-header skip-if-empty rules.
- `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` — extended the JOLT-RS-055 default test to assert `cfg.expose_headers.is_empty()`. Extended the JOLT-RS-055 explicit-fields test to construct with `expose_headers: vec!["x-request-id".to_string()]` and assert the field round-trips. Extended the JOLT-RS-056 OPTIONS test's `CorsConfig` literal with `expose_headers: vec![]` plus an inline comment explaining why the OPTIONS-focused test leaves it empty. Appended three new sibling tests in the `cors` module: `non_options_response_gets_allow_origin_and_expose_headers_injected` (PRD-mandated GET verification + Expose-Headers exercise + finished-flag-NOT-set assertion), `non_options_response_skips_headers_when_config_is_empty` (default-config no-leak guarantee), `non_options_response_preserves_inner_set_cors_headers` (additive contract — inner-set headers survive the layer).
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-057 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- **JOLT-RS-058 (priority 58, phase12): "Write CORS unit tests: wildcard origin, specific origin match, no-match returns no CORS header, preflight returns correct methods."** The natural shape: introduce a shared `select_allowed_origin(&config: &CorsConfig, req: &AxumRequest) -> Option<HeaderValue>` helper in `cors.rs` and refactor BOTH branches (the OPTIONS preflight in `build_preflight_response` and the non-OPTIONS injection in `inject_response_cors_headers`) to consume it. Helper logic: (a) if `allow_origins` contains `"*"` → return `Some("*")`; (b) else if request has an `Origin` header AND `allow_origins` contains its value → return that origin; (c) else → `None`. Then write the four tests: wildcard (Origin set, allow_origins=`vec!["*"]` → `*`), specific match (Origin set, allow_origins=`vec![origin]` → echo), no-match (Origin set, allow_origins disjoint → no header), preflight methods (OPTIONS with allow_methods configured → comma-joined methods header). The 056 OPTIONS test will need an `Origin` header added to keep it passing under the new matching logic — flag this as a small mechanical update during 058. The 057 GET tests will likewise need Origin headers, OR the matching helper can be designed to fall back to the first-entry rule when no Origin is present (less correct CORS semantics but preserves backwards compat with the 056/057 tests).
- **`CorsLayer` is STILL not auto-installed by `JoltServer::start`.** A user who calls `.cors(config)` on the server today still doesn't get a CorsLayer in their tower stack — `cors_config` is stored but never wired. Not in 058's PRD; the natural place is in `JoltServer::start` (or `into_router`), conditionally on `cors_config.is_some()`. Likely the 058-or-after iteration that closes phase12.
- **`AutoMiddleware`'s `#[cors]` attribute (050) is still parsed but unconsumed by codegen.** Now that CorsLayer ships full request-cycle behavior (OPTIONS preflight + non-OPTIONS injection), the wiring task ("when a derive has `#[cors]`, splice CorsLayer into its middleware chain pulling from the server's CorsConfig") is fully unblocked but still unscheduled in the PRD by ID I can see. The `jolt::middleware::step::cors` marker statement from 052 is the splice point.
- **`Access-Control-Allow-Credentials` is NOT in CorsConfig** as of 055/056/057. Out of scope for phase12 by PRD spec. If a future PRD wants credential-bearing CORS, it'll need to extend `CorsConfig` with `pub allow_credentials: bool` and inject the header on both OPTIONS and non-OPTIONS responses (typically alongside the origin header, and with a constraint that `Allow-Origin` cannot be `*` when credentials are allowed).
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test bundle), 045 (endpoint-integration test), 054 (phase11 closing test).** Still the only pre-046 holdouts plus 054. Recommendation unchanged from 055/056 progress: defer to a polish-pass between phase12 closing (after 058 + the auto-installation wiring) and whatever phase13 brings.

================================================================================
JOLT-RS-058 (priority 58, phase12-cors-middleware) — shared select_allowed_origin helper + four PRD-mandated tests
================================================================================

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish; JOLT-RS-054 phase11 closing test): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" before "polish"), 058 introduces the shared `select_allowed_origin` matching helper that BOTH the OPTIONS preflight (056) and non-OPTIONS injection (057) now route through — that's a small core abstraction, not just a test bundle. Closing phase12 with the matching helper + the four tests makes the CorsLayer's request-time surface complete and unblocks the still-unscheduled "JoltServer auto-installation" and "AutoMiddleware #[cors] codegen wiring" follow-ups. 027/032/045/054 remain test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies; deferring them does not block any phase12+ work.

Implementation notes:
- **New `select_allowed_origin(config: &CorsConfig, req: &AxumRequest) -> Option<HeaderValue>` private helper in `cors.rs`.** Logic in spec order: (1) if `allow_origins` contains `"*"` → return `Some("*")` regardless of request Origin (wildcard short-circuit, before the Origin lookup); (2) else if the request carries an `Origin` header AND that origin appears verbatim in `allow_origins` → return the echoed origin; (3) otherwise → `None` (no Allow-Origin header is emitted, refusing the CORS grant). `HeaderValue::from_str` is checked with `.ok()` even though it cannot fail on an ASCII `*` literal — keeps the helper total/panic-free for any future change to the matching string set.
- **Both `build_preflight_response` and `inject_response_cors_headers` now take `allowed_origin: Option<HeaderValue>` instead of computing first-entry locally.** The matching is computed ONCE in `CorsService::call` (BEFORE branching into OPTIONS/non-OPTIONS) and threaded into whichever helper runs. This keeps the matching rule in a single location (058's helper) instead of duplicated across two helpers — a future Allow-Credentials or origin-set extension lands in one place. Computing before the branch also dodges a borrow-checker issue: the non-OPTIONS branch consumes `req` in `inner.call(req)` so we cannot borrow `req` to extract its Origin from inside the async block.
- **Existing 056 OPTIONS test (`options_request_returns_204_with_cors_headers_and_marks_finished`) updated** to add `Origin: https://example.com` to the request. Without an Origin header (or wildcard config), the new matching helper returns None and Allow-Origin is omitted — that's the spec-correct behavior, but the test's verification assertion on `Access-Control-Allow-Origin == "https://example.com"` would fail. Adding Origin keeps the verification path active. The "no-match → no header" case is now covered explicitly by `no_origin_match_omits_allow_origin_header`.
- **Existing 057 `non_options_response_gets_allow_origin_and_expose_headers_injected` test updated** with the same `Origin: https://example.com` header for the same reason — its assertion on the echoed Allow-Origin only holds under proper matching.
- **Existing 057 `non_options_response_skips_headers_when_config_is_empty` test NOT updated** — empty `allow_origins` means no `*` and no possible match regardless of Origin header presence, so the test's "no Allow-Origin emitted" assertion holds without modification.
- **Existing 057 `non_options_response_preserves_inner_set_cors_headers` test NOT updated** — the additive contract (`headers.contains_key` short-circuits before matching kicks in) means the layer leaves the inner-set Allow-Origin alone whether or not matching would have produced a value. Test passes unchanged.
- **Updated `tests.rs` cors module imports** to include `ACCESS_CONTROL_EXPOSE_HEADERS` and `ORIGIN` from `axum::http::header`. Replaced two `axum::http::header::ACCESS_CONTROL_EXPOSE_HEADERS` literal paths in the 057 tests with the imported constant for consistency.
- **Four new sibling tests** appended after the 057 tests (PRD-mandated coverage):
  1. `wildcard_origin_emits_star_regardless_of_request_origin` — `allow_origins=["*"]` + GET with Origin → response has `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`. Pins the wildcard short-circuit before the Origin lookup.
  2. `specific_origin_match_echoes_request_origin` — multi-entry allow-list with the request's Origin landing on the SECOND entry → response echoes the request's Origin (NOT the first config entry). Pins that the matching helper does an actual lookup, not the prior first-entry simplification.
  3. `no_origin_match_omits_allow_origin_header` — Origin set to a value NOT in allow-list (and no `*`) → response has NO Allow-Origin header. Pins the spec-correct refusal behavior.
  4. `preflight_emits_correct_allow_methods_header` — OPTIONS with `allow_methods=[Get, Post, Delete]` → response has `Access-Control-Allow-Methods: "GET, POST, DELETE"`. Uses wildcard origin to keep matching out of the way; the panicking-inner pattern from 056 enforces the OPTIONS short-circuit.
- **Module rustdoc updated** to describe the JOLT-RS-058 matching rule (numbered list of the three branches) and to replace the 056-era "first entry" wording with the helper-based shape. The 057 entry pointing at "JOLT-RS-058's territory" was already removed when 057 landed; the 058 update folds the matching contract into the module-level docs alongside the OPTIONS/non-OPTIONS contracts already there.

Verification:
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean, ~1.25s incremental.
- `cargo test --workspace` → 121 jolt-core unit (was 117; +4 new for 058) + 6 jolt-core auto_middleware_derive integration + 8 jolt-core inventory_registration integration + 130 jolt-macros unit = 265 tests pass; no regressions in any sibling crate.
- `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets` → same 2 pre-existing baseline warnings (`new_without_default` on `RequestExt` and `JoltServer`); 0 new warnings.
- The PRD-mandated `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::cors passes` verification is satisfied: the 8 `tests::cors::*` tests (4 existing + 4 new) all pass cleanly. Each of the four PRD bullet points (wildcard origin, specific origin match, no-match returns no CORS header, preflight returns correct methods) maps to one of the new tests above.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..057 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory). Cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- **Single matching point in `CorsService::call`, not duplicated across helpers.** Two considered shapes: (a) call `select_allowed_origin` from inside both `build_preflight_response` and `inject_response_cors_headers`, threading `&req` into both (rejected — `inject_response_cors_headers` runs AFTER `inner.call(req).await`, so the request is already consumed by then; would require buffering the Origin header upfront anyway, just in two places instead of one); (b) compute once before the branch in `call`, pass the result into whichever helper runs (current — single source of truth, no buffering, no borrow-checker contortions in the async block). The cost is one extra `Option<HeaderValue>` parameter per helper; the benefit is the matching rule lives in exactly one location.
- **Wildcard short-circuits BEFORE the Origin-header lookup.** Two considered shapes: (a) require an Origin header even for wildcard (rejected — the wildcard contract grants any origin access; demanding a specific Origin would fail in test scenarios that don't supply one and would surprise callers who think `vec!["*"]` is permissive); (b) wildcard returns `Some("*")` immediately (current — matches the spec's "any origin allowed" semantic; `vec!["*"]` works whether or not the request advertises an Origin). Documented inline in the helper rustdoc.
- **`HeaderValue::from_str("*").ok()` checked despite being unfailable today.** The helper's signature is `Option<HeaderValue>` and the wildcard branch returns `HeaderValue::from_str("*").ok()` rather than `Some(HeaderValue::from_static("*"))`. Two considered shapes: (a) `HeaderValue::from_static("*")` (rejected — slightly faster but introduces a panic surface if the string ever changes to non-static-compatible bytes during a future refactor); (b) `from_str(...).ok()` (current — total, panic-free, consistent with the specific-origin branch which also uses `.ok()`). The cost is one branch on a result that's always `Ok`; the benefit is a uniform fallback path.
- **Existing 056/057 tests updated by adding Origin headers, NOT by relaxing the helper.** Two considered shapes: (a) make the helper fall back to first-entry when no Origin is present (rejected — breaks the spec-correct refusal semantics; an unauthenticated request without an Origin would receive Allow-Origin echoing the first configured origin, which is exactly the leak the no-match test is meant to prevent); (b) update tests to send Origin (current — keeps the helper spec-correct, every test now reads as a clear "send X, expect Y" assertion). The 056/057 progress notes from the prior iteration explicitly recommended this layering ("The 056 OPTIONS test will need an `Origin` header added to keep it passing under the new matching logic").
- **Per-test fresh `panicking_inner` reused only where the layer must NOT delegate.** The `preflight_emits_correct_allow_methods_header` test is OPTIONS-only, so it reuses the panicking inner pattern from the 056 test to structurally enforce the short-circuit contract (any non-panic outcome means the layer bypassed inner). The three non-OPTIONS tests use a normal `service_fn` returning a populated Response so the layer's injection logic has something to mutate.
- **Multi-entry allow-list test deliberately puts the request's Origin on the SECOND entry.** Two considered shapes: (a) single-entry allow-list with matching Origin (rejected — passes under both the new matching helper AND the prior first-entry simplification, so wouldn't pin the regression); (b) multi-entry where the matching origin is NOT first (current — fails under first-entry, passes under proper matching, so the test is a true regression-pin for the matching helper). The helper logic walks `iter().any(|o| o == origin_str)` which is order-independent.

Files changed:
- `jolt-core/src/cors.rs` — added `ORIGIN` to the imported header constants. New private `select_allowed_origin(config: &CorsConfig, req: &AxumRequest) -> Option<HeaderValue>` helper with rustdoc explaining the spec-order matching rule. `build_preflight_response` signature changed from `(&CorsConfig)` to `(&CorsConfig, Option<HeaderValue>)`; the inline first-entry block was replaced with `if let Some(value) = allowed_origin { ... }`. `inject_response_cors_headers` signature changed from `(&CorsConfig, &mut Response)` to `(&CorsConfig, Option<HeaderValue>, &mut Response)`; the inline first-entry block was replaced with the same `if let Some(value)` pattern. `CorsService::call` now computes `let allowed_origin = select_allowed_origin(&self.config, &req);` BEFORE the OPTIONS branch and threads it into both helpers. Module rustdoc updated to describe the JOLT-RS-058 matching rule alongside the OPTIONS/non-OPTIONS contracts.
- `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` — extended the cors module's import block to include `ACCESS_CONTROL_EXPOSE_HEADERS` and `ORIGIN`. Added `Origin: https://example.com` header to the 056 OPTIONS test's request (so its Allow-Origin assertion still holds under proper matching). Added the same Origin header to the 057 GET-injection test. Replaced two `axum::http::header::ACCESS_CONTROL_EXPOSE_HEADERS` literal paths with the now-imported constant. Appended four new sibling tests: `wildcard_origin_emits_star_regardless_of_request_origin`, `specific_origin_match_echoes_request_origin`, `no_origin_match_omits_allow_origin_header`, `preflight_emits_correct_allow_methods_header`.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-058 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- **`CorsLayer` is STILL not auto-installed by `JoltServer::start`.** Now that phase12's CorsLayer surface is complete (055 config + 056 OPTIONS + 057 non-OPTIONS + 058 matching/tests), the natural next item is auto-installation. A user who calls `.cors(config)` on the server still doesn't get a CorsLayer in their tower stack — `cors_config` is stored but never wired. Not currently in the PRD by ID I can see; the natural place is in `JoltServer::start` (or `into_router`), conditionally on `cors_config.is_some()`. Recommend filing a follow-up task or surfacing this when phase13 starts.

Not in 058's PRD; would close the gap between the auto-middleware machinery and the CorsLayer. Likely the iteration after auto-installation lands.
- **The `select_allowed_origin` helper is an obvious extension point for Allow-Credentials.** A future PRD that adds `pub allow_credentials: bool` to `CorsConfig` could either (a) extend the helper to return both an origin and a credentials flag (tuple return), or (b) add a sibling `select_allow_credentials(config, allowed_origin)` helper that returns whether to emit `Access-Control-Allow-Credentials: true` (and enforces the spec rule that credentials cannot be combined with `*` origin). Out of scope for phase12; flag for whichever PRD opens credential-bearing CORS.
