The CorsLayer / CorsService public surface is unchanged. A caller who built against 057 sees no breakage from 058.

Iteration: 2026-05-10 (JOLT-RS-059 — ParseBodyLayer tower::Layer)
PRD item: JOLT-RS-059 (priority 59, phase13-body-parsing)
Description: "Implement ParseBodyLayer as tower::Layer: reads request body bytes into Vec<u8>. If the middleware struct has a body: T field, attempt serde_json::from_slice::<T>."
PRD verification: "Unit test: valid JSON body → T populated in middleware struct."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish; JOLT-RS-054 phase11 closing test): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), 059 is the load-bearing seam that 060 (parse-failure 400 + mark_finished), 061 (String body extraction), and 062 (body-parsing test bundle) all build on. Picking 059 over the deferred test-bundle holdouts pins the LAYER SHAPE (`ParseBodyLayer<T>` parameterized over body type, not the middleware struct), the EXTENSION CHANNEL (parsed T lands in axum request extensions, NOT in RequestExt — control state vs data state separation), the BODY-RESTORATION POLICY (buffered Bytes re-armed onto the request before delegating, so downstream `build_jolt_request` re-read in the registry path still sees the body), and the SILENT-FAILURE-IN-059 stance (parse Err → no extension insert + delegate, with 060 to replace the failure branch with a 400 short-circuit). All four decisions are load-bearing for 060+. 027/032/045/054 remain test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies; deferring them does not block any phase13+ work.

Implementation notes:
- `ParseBodyLayer<T>` carries `PhantomData<fn() -> T>` so the layer is Send + Sync regardless of T's auto-traits, and clones without requiring `T: Clone` on the marker itself. Manual Clone impl (not derive) for the same reason — derive would propagate a spurious `T: Clone` bound to the layer.
- The `Service<AxumRequest>` impl mirrors `CorsService::call`'s tower delegation dance: `poll_ready` drove `self.inner`, so `call` `std::mem::replace`s inner with a clone we don't invoke (caller's next `poll_ready` readies the cloned slot before their next `call`). That keeps the `Service::poll_ready/call` contract sound under ServiceBuilder composition.
- `T: DeserializeOwned + Clone + Send + Sync + 'static` is the runtime bound on the Service impl. `Clone` is required by `http::Extensions::insert<T: Clone + Send + Sync + 'static>` (axum 0.8 / http 1.4) — extensions get cloned on `req.extensions().clone()` paths. The marker on the layer/service itself stays unbounded.
- Body cap mirrors `build_jolt_request`'s `u32::MAX as usize`. Pulled into a `buffer_body(Body) -> Bytes` helper so a future configurable-limit PRD item edits one site rather than two. The double-buffer (layer + registry both call `to_bytes`) is acknowledged in the module docs as collapsible by 062+ via a `BufferedBody(Bytes)` extension.

Key decisions pinned for 060+:
1. Layer parameterized over body type T, not middleware struct. The macro-driven `__jolt_extract_from(&Request)` already runs per-field `serde_json::from_slice` (see `jolt-macros::auto_middleware::field_init_expr`); parameterizing the layer over the middleware struct would duplicate field-shape inspection at tower-stack assembly time. Layer-over-T composes via `tower::ServiceBuilder` without needing to know about user middleware structs.
2. Parsed T lands in axum request extensions (typed by T). `RequestExt` is reserved for cross-layer control flow (finished latch, stashed Response); body content is data, not control state.
3. Body bytes are restored onto the request via `Body::from(bytes.clone())` BEFORE attempting the parse, so even the silent-failure-in-059 branch delivers a fully-formed request to the inner service. Downstream `build_jolt_request` re-reads the body — without restoration, ParseBodyLayer would silently zero out the body for every non-extensions consumer.
4. Parse failure in 059 is silent (no extension insert, delegate to inner). JOLT-RS-060 will replace the failure branch with a 400 + `RequestExt::mark_finished()` short-circuit; pinning the layer shape here keeps that change additive (one new branch inside `call`, not a rebuilt service).

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/parse_body.rs (new): `ParseBodyLayer<T>` + `ParseBodyService<S, T>` with the four decisions above pinned in module docs.
- jolt-core/src/lib.rs: register `parse_body` module + re-export `ParseBodyLayer` and `ParseBodyService` alongside the other tower-layer types.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs: append `parse_body` test module with the PRD-mandated `valid_json_body_is_parsed_and_inserted_into_extensions` test. The single test exercises BOTH 059 contracts (extension insertion AND body restoration) by capturing both observations from one inner-service call.

Verification:
- `cargo build --workspace` → clean.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::parse_body` → 1 passed (PRD verification).
- `cargo test -p jolt-core` → 122 unit + 6 + 8 integration passed, 0 failed.
- `cargo clippy -p jolt-core` → 2 pre-existing errors (`RequestExt::new()` / `JoltServer::new()` missing Default — confirmed by stashing this iteration's changes and re-running on master; both errors persist). My new `parse_body.rs` is clippy-clean.

Blockers / next notes:
- JOLT-RS-060 replaces the silent-failure branch with `Response::bad_request()` carrying "Invalid JSON: ..." plus `RequestExt::mark_finished()`. Implementation hint: the failure branch already has access to the `serde_json::Error`; pipe its `.to_string()` into the body. The 400 response should be stashed via `RequestExt::set_response` (mirroring how Router consumes stashed responses) rather than returned directly from `call` — that way an OUTER layer (e.g., CorsLayer wrapping ParseBodyService) still gets to inject Allow-Origin onto the 400.
- JOLT-RS-061's String body needs a different code path (String can be `DeserializeOwned`'d but only from a JSON string literal — `r#""hello""#`, not `r#"hello"#`). Likely needs a separate `ParseBodyStringLayer` or a const-generic switch on T; revisit when the item lands.
- The double-buffer (ParseBodyLayer + build_jolt_request both call `to_bytes`) is collapsible by 062+ via a `BufferedBody(Bytes)` extension that build_jolt_request checks before re-reading.
- Pre-existing clippy errors on `RequestExt::new()` and `JoltServer::new()` (missing Default) should be cleaned up in a future polish iteration — not blocking but worth fixing if a Default-on-all-stateless-new sweep lands.

Iteration: 2026-05-10 (JOLT-RS-060 — ParseBodyService 400 short-circuit on parse failure)
PRD item: JOLT-RS-060 (priority 60, phase13-body-parsing)
Description: "On deserialization failure, return Response::bad_request() with error message ('Invalid JSON: ...') and set RequestExt::mark_finished()."
PRD verification: "Unit test: invalid JSON → 400 response with error details."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish; JOLT-RS-054 phase11 closing test): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("integration points" + "core abstractions" before polish), 060 is the failure-rejection contract that 061 (String body extraction) and 062 (test bundle) build on. 059 explicitly pinned the silent-failure branch as a one-line hole that 060 fills additively; closing it now unblocks the AutoMiddleware codegen `.expect(...)` removal flagged in the 059 module docs and gives 061 a clean "success path inserts T into extensions; failure path 400s" surface to mirror for String. 027/032/045/054 remain test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies.

Implementation notes:
- **400 returned directly from `call()`, NOT stashed via `RequestExt::set_response`.** The 059 progress note recommended stashing "so an OUTER layer (e.g., CorsLayer wrapping ParseBodyService) still gets to inject Allow-Origin onto the 400." On re-examination, the recommendation was wrong on two counts: (1) Router's stash/take dance is the consumer of `set_response`, but ParseBodyLayer sits OUTSIDE Router in the typical wiring — Router's `is_finished()` check fires only when the registry walk runs, which won't happen if the request never reaches Router (because ParseBodyService short-circuited). (2) An outer CorsLayer wrapping ParseBodyService already sees the returned 400 as the result of its `inner.call(req).await`, then runs `inject_response_cors_headers` on it — exactly the layer composition we want. Returning directly is both simpler AND preserves the outer-layer decoration semantic.
- **`Arc<RequestExt>` preserve-or-inject mirrors `CorsService::call` (056) and `Router::call` (033/035).** Three layers now share this idiom for the same reason: a flipped `finished` latch must be observable to whoever holds the same Arc, and inserting a fresh ext when none is present means the contract holds even when the layer composes outside Router. Pulled the lookup out of `req.extensions()` onto `parts.extensions` because we destructure `req.into_parts()` to buffer the body anyway — saves a redundant `extensions()` borrow.
- **Body restoration via `Body::from(bytes.clone())` kept on BOTH branches.** On the success branch the inner service's downstream body re-readers (notably `build_jolt_request`) keep working. On the failure branch we never reach the inner service, so the rebuild is technically dead code — but keeping a single rebuild site avoids a second branch on `req.into_parts` and matches the 059 contract that "the request is fully formed regardless of parse outcome." A future reader who adds another success-path branch (e.g. partial-parse fallback) gets the restored body for free.
- **`bad_request_for_parse_error(&serde_json::Error)` is a free function, not a method.** Matches the existing `not_found` / `method_not_allowed` shape in `router.rs` (also free functions). Independently testable; no `&self` lifetime entanglement; one obvious edit site if a future PRD wants to switch the error body to JSON or add a structured error envelope.
- **Body MIME `text/plain; charset=utf-8`.** Matches the framework's other ad-hoc error responses (Router's 404/405 bodies are bare empties; a text body for the 400 is the simplest add that still carries the `Invalid JSON: ...` payload). The PRD spec doesn't pin a content type. JSON would have been an alternative but introduces a serialization step and surface area for nested-error issues; text is the path of least surprise.
- **Body format `"Invalid JSON: {err}"` uses `Display` on `serde_json::Error`.** `serde_json::Error::to_string()` already produces a human-readable message including line/column position when available (e.g. `expected value at line 1 column 2`). No need to format the error fields manually.

Key decisions:
- **Direct return vs. set_response stash.** Two considered shapes: (a) stash via `RequestExt::set_response` and let Router's existing short-circuit path surface it (rejected — Router never runs in the parse-failure path because ParseBodyService is the outermost-shy layer; the stash would be set but never taken); (b) return the 400 directly from `call()` (current — outer layers naturally see it as the inner-call result, and `mark_finished` is preserved as an observability signal for any composed observer). Documented inline in the call's failure branch.
- **`mark_finished` flip kept even though the 400 is returned directly.** Two considered shapes: (a) skip the flip (the 400 is already the response, no further processing needed; rejected — breaks the "any composed observer sees the same finished-flag contract" invariant the 059 module docs pinned, and would surprise a future test that asserts the latch flipped on every layer-emitted response); (b) flip the latch even though the response is returned directly (current — the flip is purely an observability signal as the 056 OPTIONS branch already documents, and consistency across layers is worth the one-line cost). Documented in the module-docs point 4 update.
- **Test inserts a panicking `service_fn` as the inner service.** Two considered shapes: (a) regular service_fn with a "was-called" flag (rejected — adds a Mutex<bool> assertion the test would have to read, and the flag-was-flipped path could theoretically race with a buggy delegate-then-return implementation that flips the flag before the 400 reaches the caller); (b) panicking inner (current — structurally enforces the no-delegation contract; any leak past the failure branch crashes the test rather than silently passing). Same idiom 058's `preflight_emits_correct_allow_methods_header` uses for its OPTIONS short-circuit test.
- **Test pre-injects `Arc<RequestExt>` rather than letting the layer create one.** Two considered shapes: (a) let the layer inject a fresh ext, then somehow hook into it after the call (rejected — the layer drops its `Arc` clone after the call returns, leaving the test with no handle on the same Arc to assert `is_finished()`); (b) pre-inject the Arc onto the request, observe both the latch flip and the no-stash assertion through the test's own clone (current — the standard observability pattern Router/CorsService tests already use). Also pins the preserve-existing branch of the layer's preserve-or-inject contract.
- **Test asserts `take_response().is_none()` to pin the "direct return, not stashed" decision.** Two considered shapes: (a) just assert the 400 (rejected — would pass under both the direct-return AND the alternative stash-via-set_response shape, so wouldn't pin the regression); (b) also assert no response was stashed (current — explicitly fails if a future change accidentally stashes the response too, regardless of whether the call also returned it). Adds one line to the test in exchange for a true regression-pin on the architectural choice.
- **Body assertion uses `starts_with("Invalid JSON: ")` + a `.len() >` check, NOT exact equality.** Two considered shapes: (a) hardcode the full expected message for the specific malformed input (rejected — `serde_json::Error::Display` formatting is a serde-internal contract that could shift across crate versions; the test would break on a benign serde upgrade); (b) prefix-match plus a length check that the underlying error text was actually appended (current — pins the "Invalid JSON: " contract without locking in serde's exact wording). The length check guards against a regression that emits the prefix but drops the error detail.

Files changed:
- `jolt-core/src/parse_body.rs` — added `std::sync::Arc`, `axum::http::header::CONTENT_TYPE`, `axum::http::{HeaderValue, StatusCode}`, and `crate::request_ext::RequestExt` to the imports. Updated module-docs point 4 from the silent-failure-in-059 placeholder to the 060 contract (400 + mark_finished + observability-signal note + AutoMiddleware-codegen-unreachable note). Updated `ParseBodyService` rustdoc accordingly. Replaced the `if let Ok(parsed) = ... { req.extensions_mut().insert(parsed); } inner.call(req).await` block with a `match serde_json::from_slice::<T>(&bytes)` that branches into the success path (insert + delegate) or the failure path (mark_finished + 400 direct return). Added `Arc<RequestExt>` preserve-or-inject lookup against `parts.extensions` BEFORE the rebuild so the failure path always has a valid ext to flip. Added the private `bad_request_for_parse_error(&serde_json::Error) -> Response` helper with rustdoc explaining the text/plain format, the `"Invalid JSON: <serde error>"` body, and the parallel to `router::not_found` / `router::method_not_allowed`.
- `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` — extended the parse_body module's import block with `crate::request_ext::RequestExt`. Updated the module-docs note from "lives in its own module when that item lands" to point at the new sibling test. Appended `invalid_json_body_short_circuits_with_400_and_marks_finished` as a sibling test: panicking inner service, pre-injected Arc<RequestExt>, malformed JSON body, asserts on (1) StatusCode::BAD_REQUEST, (2) Content-Type starts with "text/plain", (3) body starts_with "Invalid JSON: " AND has serde error detail appended, (4) RequestExt::is_finished returns true, (5) take_response returns None (pins direct-return-not-stashed).
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-060 passes: true.

Verification:
- `cargo build --workspace` → clean, ~2.93s (jolt-core recompile).
- `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::parse_body` → 2 passed (PRD verification + 059's existing valid-body test). Each PRD bullet point ("400 response", "error details") maps to one of the assertions in the new test.
- `cargo test --workspace` → 123 jolt-core unit (was 122; +1 new for 060) + 6 jolt-core auto_middleware_derive integration + 8 jolt-core inventory_registration integration + 130 jolt-macros unit = 267 tests pass; no regressions in any sibling crate.
- `cargo clippy -p jolt-core --all-targets` → same 2 pre-existing baseline warnings (`new_without_default` on `RequestExt` and `JoltServer`); 0 new warnings. The new helper, imports, and test are clippy-clean.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..059 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory, confirmed by ls). Cargo is the verification tool.

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-061 (priority 61, phase13): "Support String body extraction: if the body field is typed String or &str, read body as UTF-8 string."** The natural shape: a separate `ParseBodyStringLayer` (no T parameter) that buffers the body bytes, runs `String::from_utf8(bytes.to_vec())` (or `std::str::from_utf8(&bytes).map(str::to_string)`), and inserts the resulting `String` into request extensions. On UTF-8 decode failure, mirror 060's 400 + mark_finished short-circuit (body: `"Invalid UTF-8: <error>"`). Reasoning for separate layer over generic over T: `String` is technically `DeserializeOwned`, but `serde_json::from_slice::<String>(&b"hello"[..])` would fail because raw text isn't a JSON string literal — only `serde_json::from_slice::<String>(&br#""hello""#[..])` works. Trying to make a single `ParseBodyLayer<T>` handle both content types would either require a content-type sniff or const-generic dispatch, both of which feel heavier than two sibling layers. The shared body-buffer + extension-insert + Arc<RequestExt> preserve-or-inject + 400 short-circuit pattern can be hoisted into a private `buffer_body_into(...)` helper if the duplication feels like it; my recommendation is to keep them as two simple layers and accept the small duplication for now.
- **`AutoMiddleware`'s body-extraction codegen `.expect(...)` is now unreachable in the wired-server path** (per the updated module docs). 062+ should remove the `.expect` (or replace it with `.unwrap_or_else(|_| unreachable!("ParseBodyLayer rejected the request"))`) once the entire phase13 surface lands. Out of scope for 060.
- **`ParseBodyLayer` is STILL not auto-installed by `JoltServer::start` or by the AutoMiddleware codegen.** Same gap CorsLayer has — a user who derives `#[derive(AutoMiddleware)]` on a struct with a `body: T` field gets `__jolt_extract_from` codegen that calls `serde_json::from_slice` directly, with no ParseBodyLayer in the tower stack. The wiring task ("when a derive has `#[parse_body]` or a `body: T` field, splice ParseBodyLayer<T> into its middleware chain") is fully unblocked by 060 but still unscheduled in the PRD. Recommend filing a follow-up or surfacing when phase14 starts.
- **Double-buffer (ParseBodyLayer + build_jolt_request both call `to_bytes`) still unresolved.** 062+ can collapse via a `BufferedBody(Bytes)` extension. Out of scope for 060.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test bundle), 045 (endpoint-integration test), 054 (phase11 closing test).** Same pre-046 holdouts plus 054 — phase13 continues with 061 next. Recommendation unchanged: defer to a polish-pass once phase13 closes.
- **First user-visible scope from 060 IS a public-surface behavior change** — in the success path nothing changed, but in the failure path callers who previously got delegated-to-inner (with T missing from extensions) now get a synchronous 400 from the layer. Any test that wired ParseBodyLayer ahead of an inner that handled the missing-extension case will need updating — the new test suite is the only such caller in-tree.

Iteration: 2026-05-10 (JOLT-RS-061 — ParseBodyStringLayer for raw text/plain bodies)
PRD item: JOLT-RS-061 (priority 61, phase13-body-parsing)
Description: "Support String body extraction: if the body field is typed String or &str, read body as UTF-8 string."
PRD verification: "Unit test: POST with text/plain body → extracted as String."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish; JOLT-RS-054 phase11 closing test; JOLT-RS-062 body-parsing test bundle; JOLT-RS-063 phase14 ParseQueryLayer): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("standard implementation" of an in-flight phase before polish), 061 is the missing String-body counterpart to 059/060's JSON-body layer in phase13. The 060 progress note explicitly mapped the natural shape (separate `ParseBodyStringLayer`, mirrored failure-rejection contract) and 062 (body-parsing test bundle) builds on the assumption that BOTH success paths (JSON via 059 + String via 061) exist. Picking 061 before 062 keeps the test bundle's surface complete; picking 063 (phase14 ParseQueryLayer) would open a new phase while phase13 still has a half-laid surface. 027/032/045/054 remain test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies; deferring them does not block any phase13+ work.

Implementation notes:
- **`ParseBodyStringLayer` is a sibling layer, NOT `ParseBodyLayer<String>`.** Three considered shapes: (a) parameterize ParseBodyLayer over T and let the user pick `String` (rejected — `serde_json::from_slice::<String>(b"hello")` fails because raw text isn't a JSON string literal; only `serde_json::from_slice::<String>(br#""hello""#)` succeeds, which is the opposite of what the user means by a `text/plain` body field); (b) const-generic dispatch on a sniff-content-type flag (rejected — heavier than two simple layers, couples content-type sniffing to the parse path); (c) separate layer with no generic (current — matches the prior 060 progress note's recommendation, the surface is unambiguous, and the user picks the layer whose contract matches their field type). Documented inline in `ParseBodyStringLayer`'s rustdoc.
- **`ParseBodyStringLayer` has NO type parameter** because the output is always `String`. The struct is a unit `Default + Clone + Debug` so the standard `tower::ServiceBuilder` composition path works without any manual trait impls (unlike `ParseBodyLayer<T>` whose `PhantomData<fn() -> T>` field forced manual `Clone`/`Debug` impls).
- **Empty body decodes to `String::new()`, NOT 400.** Three considered shapes: (a) treat empty body as failure (rejected — empty bytes ARE valid UTF-8 by definition, the empty string; rejecting them would force every caller to special-case empty-body validation upstream of this layer, and the failure surface should be reserved for genuinely-malformed UTF-8); (b) skip the extension insert on empty body and delegate (rejected — leaves a hole where downstream `req.extensions().get::<String>()` returns None for a perfectly-valid empty payload, which is inconsistent with the success contract); (c) insert `String::new()` and delegate (current — empty-body rejection is the user's responsibility, matching how the JSON layer treats `null` / `""`). Pinned with the `empty_body_decodes_to_empty_string` test.
- **UTF-8 decode uses `std::str::from_utf8(&bytes)` then `.to_owned()`, not `String::from_utf8(bytes.to_vec())`.** Two considered shapes: (a) `String::from_utf8(bytes.to_vec())` (rejected — clones the bytes upfront EVEN ON THE SUCCESS PATH where we then re-clone them onto the restored body; doubles the byte-copy cost when the input is large and valid); (b) `std::str::from_utf8(&bytes)` borrows from the buffered bytes, and `.to_owned()` allocates only on success after the body has already been restored (current — one allocation on success, zero on failure, and the error type is `std::str::Utf8Error` which carries the same actionable detail as `String::FromUtf8Error::utf8_error()` without the wrapping). The current code restores the body from `bytes.clone()` for the registry-walk re-read regardless of which decode API is used.
- **`bad_request_for_utf8_error(&std::str::Utf8Error)` mirrors `bad_request_for_parse_error(&serde_json::Error)` exactly.** Same `text/plain; charset=utf-8` content type, same `"Invalid <kind>: {err}"` body format, same builder-can't-fail expect message. The visual parallel makes the two failure surfaces easy to compare for any future reader auditing the layer pair's behavior.
- **`Arc<RequestExt>` preserve-or-inject pattern duplicated, not extracted into a helper.** Three callers now share it: `CorsService::call` (056), `ParseBodyService::call` (059), `ParseBodyStringService::call` (061). Two considered shapes: (a) extract into a private `acquire_request_ext(&mut Extensions) -> Arc<RequestExt>` helper (rejected — the 060 progress note explicitly recommended "keep them as two simple layers and accept the small duplication for now", and the three call sites differ slightly in their surrounding async-block shape so the helper would have to thread the extensions reference through a closure; the extraction is a polish item, not a blocker); (b) inline duplication (current — three identical 7-line blocks, consistent across the three layers, with the same trade-off the 060 iteration already validated). Same recommendation: defer the helper extraction to a polish iteration once a fourth caller (or a fourth contract variant) shows up.

Key decisions:
- **Distinct layer vs. generic over T.** Documented above; the JSON-string-literal trap is the load-bearing reason.
- **Failure body format `"Invalid UTF-8: {err}"`.** Two considered shapes: (a) `"Invalid request body: {err}"` (rejected — too generic; a future caller routing through a chain of body-decoding layers wouldn't be able to tell whether they hit the JSON or the UTF-8 surface); (b) `"Invalid UTF-8: {err}"` (current — mirrors `"Invalid JSON: {err}"` from 060, and `Utf8Error::Display` already produces a useful "invalid utf-8 sequence of N bytes from index M" detail). Pinned in the test's `body_text.starts_with("Invalid UTF-8: ")` assertion.
- **Test asserts `body_text.len() > "Invalid UTF-8: ".len()` to pin the error-detail-must-be-appended contract.** Two considered shapes: (a) just assert the prefix (rejected — a regression that emits the prefix but drops the underlying `Utf8Error::Display` output would pass); (b) prefix + length check (current — mirrors 060's invalid-JSON test's structure, guards against a regression that produces a useless `"Invalid UTF-8: "` response with no actionable byte-index detail).
- **Third test (`empty_body_decodes_to_empty_string`) added BEYOND the PRD's single mandated test.** Two considered shapes: (a) one test (the PRD verification) (rejected — empty body is an obvious edge case at the failure/success boundary, and the layer's contract on empty input is a load-bearing architectural decision that 062's "empty body → error" verification might tempt a future reader to copy-paste into this layer without realizing the surfaces differ); (b) three tests (current — success / UTF-8 failure / empty body, each pinning a distinct contract). The third test is cheap and pins a decision that the 062 test bundle's wording could otherwise muddle.
- **Test uses `0xff 0xfe 0xfd` for invalid UTF-8 bytes.** `0xff` is never a valid UTF-8 leading byte (the 11111xxx pattern is reserved); `0xfe` and `0xfd` are also outside the valid leading-byte range. Two considered shapes: (a) a truncated multi-byte sequence (e.g. `0xe2 0x82` — start of `0xe2 0x82 0xac` = `€` but with the third byte missing; rejected — passes the test today but a future relaxation of strictness in `from_utf8` could potentially accept partial-sequences in some hypothetical mode); (b) bytes that are NEVER valid UTF-8 under ANY interpretation (current — `0xff` is unambiguous and structurally invalid). The 062 test bundle can reuse this byte pattern.

Files changed:
- `jolt-core/src/parse_body.rs` — module rustdoc updated to describe the JOLT-RS-059..061 surface as a sibling-layer pair (JSON via `ParseBodyLayer<T>`, raw UTF-8 via `ParseBodyStringLayer`), with the JSON-string-literal trap documented as the load-bearing reason for the split. Added `ParseBodyStringLayer` (unit struct with `Default + Clone + Debug` derives), `ParseBodyStringService<S>` (single `inner` field, `Clone + Debug` derives), and `bad_request_for_utf8_error(&std::str::Utf8Error) -> Response` private helper. The Service impl mirrors `ParseBodyService::call` (same `poll_ready`/`call` swap, same body-buffer-then-restore dance, same `Arc<RequestExt>` preserve-or-inject pattern) but decodes via `std::str::from_utf8(&bytes)` and stashes the resulting `String` via `req.extensions_mut().insert(text.to_owned())`. On UTF-8 failure: `request_ext.mark_finished()` + direct 400 return.
- `jolt-core/src/lib.rs` — extended the `parse_body` re-export from `{ParseBodyLayer, ParseBodyService}` to `{ParseBodyLayer, ParseBodyService, ParseBodyStringLayer, ParseBodyStringService}`.
- `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` — appended new `parse_body_string` test module with three tests: `text_plain_body_is_decoded_and_inserted_into_extensions` (PRD verification: success path + body restoration), `non_utf8_body_short_circuits_with_400_and_marks_finished` (failure path, mirrors 060's invalid-JSON test structurally), `empty_body_decodes_to_empty_string` (empty-body-is-valid-input edge case).
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-061 passes: true.

Verification:

- `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::parse_body` → 5 passed (3 new for 061 + 2 existing from 059/060). The PRD-mandated `text_plain_body_is_decoded_and_inserted_into_extensions` test maps directly to the PRD verification ("POST with text/plain body → extracted as String").

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-062 (priority 62, phase13 closing): "Write body parsing unit tests: empty body → error, oversized body → error, valid JSON → success, string body → success."** The phase13 closing test bundle. The "valid JSON → success" / "string body → success" cases are already covered by 059/060/061's sibling tests; 062's new contribution is "empty body → error" (likely meaning empty JSON body, since the String layer treats empty as valid) and "oversized body → error" (which the current `u32::MAX` cap doesn't actually surface — `axum::body::to_bytes` returns an Error variant that the current `unwrap_or_default()` swallows into an empty buffer; 062 either needs a tighter cap with a 413 short-circuit OR a test that exercises the existing cap with a deliberately-oversized payload). Recommend revisiting the `buffer_body` helper's `unwrap_or_default()` to surface a 413 (or 400) at the layer rather than letting an oversized body silently parse as `null`. Out of scope for 061.
- **JOLT-RS-063 (priority 63, phase14): "Implement ParseQueryLayer as tower::Layer: extract query string from request URI, parse into key-value pairs."** Opens phase14. The natural shape mirrors the parse_body layer pair: a `ParseQueryLayer<T>` over a query-deserialize target (likely via `serde_urlencoded::from_str::<T>` on the URI's query string), stashing the parsed T into extensions. Empty/missing query string can default to `T::default()` if `T: Default` — the prior 048 progress notes flagged `HashMap<String, String>` as a separate shape, so 063 might benefit from the same sibling-layer split (ParseQueryLayer<T> vs. ParseQueryMapLayer) the body-parsing surface ended up adopting.
- **`AutoMiddleware`'s String-body codegen still emits `__req.json::<String>()`** (see `jolt-macros/src/auto_middleware.rs` around line 1035), which is the JSON-string-literal trap PRD-061 specifically routes around. The macro wiring that picks `ParseBodyStringLayer` for `body: String` fields (vs. `ParseBodyLayer<T>` for other `T: DeserializeOwned`) is still unscheduled in the PRD. Recommend filing a follow-up; out of scope for 061.
- **The `Arc<RequestExt>` preserve-or-inject helper extraction is now a 3-call-site obligation.** With 056/059/061 sharing the pattern verbatim, the polish cost of extracting a private `acquire_request_ext(&mut Extensions) -> Arc<RequestExt>` helper is now low and the consistency win is high. Recommend extracting in a 062+ polish iteration.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test bundle), 045 (endpoint-integration test), 054 (phase11 closing test).** Same pre-046 holdouts — phase13 is now 3/4 done (059 ✓, 060 ✓, 061 ✓; 062 pending). Recommendation unchanged: defer to a polish-pass once phase13 closes (062 done) and phase14 (063+) opens.

Iteration: 2026-05-10 (JOLT-RS-063 — ParseQueryLayer foundational key-value extraction)
PRD item: JOLT-RS-063 (priority 63, phase14-query-parsing)
Description: "Implement ParseQueryLayer as tower::Layer: extract query string from request URI, parse into key-value pairs."
PRD verification: "Unit test: ?id=42 → id parsed as \"42\"."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish; JOLT-RS-054 phase11 closing test; JOLT-RS-062 phase13 closing test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" before polish), 063 opens phase14 with a NEW tower::Layer abstraction that 064/065/066/067 build directly on top of (typed int/float/bool/Vec extractors + closing test bundle). 062 is a phase13 closing test bundle — pure polish. 027/032/045/054 are also test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies. Picking 063 unblocks the entire phase14 surface; deferring 062 only delays a closing test that the existing 059/060/061 sibling tests already partly cover.

Implementation notes:
- **Output type is a `QueryParams(HashMap<String, String>)` newtype, NOT raw `HashMap<String, String>`.** Three considered shapes: (a) insert raw `HashMap<String, String>` directly (rejected — request extensions are keyed by `TypeId`, so any other layer or handler that happens to stash a `HashMap<String, String>` for an unrelated purpose would collide with this layer's value); (b) insert via `Extension(map)` axum wrapper (rejected — adds an unnecessary axum-layer dependency to the consumer side and makes the extraction pattern asymmetric with parse_body's bare `T` insertion); (c) define a `QueryParams(HashMap<String, String>)` newtype and insert that (current — unique extension key, one `Deref` from the underlying map for ergonomics, matches the prior 048 progress note's "QueryParams<T>" naming gesture). Documented inline in the module docs decision 2 + the QueryParams rustdoc.
- **No type parameter on the layer** because 063 mandates only "key-value pairs" and the typed extraction lands in 064–066 as CONSUMERS of this map. A future `ParseQueryLayer<T>` over a deserializable struct (mirroring `ParseBodyLayer<T>`) would be a SIBLING layer targeting `serde_urlencoded::from_str` with a different failure mode — not a parameterization of this one. Pinned in module docs decision 1.
- **Empty / missing query string inserts an empty QueryParams.** Three considered shapes: (a) insert `Some(map)` only when query is non-empty (rejected — forces every downstream consumer to handle two shapes for the same logical state: present-empty vs. absent); (b) insert `None` extension shape (rejected — same problem, plus the standard `req.extensions().get::<QueryParams>()` pattern wouldn't work without an `Option<QueryParams>` wrapper); (c) ALWAYS insert a QueryParams, empty when missing (current — single shape, downstream can `.get::<QueryParams>().unwrap()` without a `?…` upstream). Pinned with the `missing_query_string_inserts_empty_params` test.
- **Parsing is infallible.** Malformed pairs (`?foo&bar=1`'s `foo`) are silently dropped — same shape as `endpoint_registry::parse_query` which has been the framework's de-facto query parser since JOLT-RS-034. Two considered shapes: (a) reject malformed pairs as 400 (rejected — more strict than the existing `Request::query` contract; would be a behavior change for any code path that already relies on the permissive shape); (b) silently drop (current — matches the existing parser's behavior, and 064+ typed extractors that DO surface 400s will do so on per-VALUE type errors rather than per-PAIR shape errors). Pinned in module docs decision 4.
- **No body buffering, no `Arc<RequestExt>` preserve-or-inject.** Unlike ParseBodyLayer/CorsLayer, this layer doesn't fail and doesn't short-circuit, so it has no reason to flip a finished latch. The request flows through unchanged except for the inserted extension. The async block is also a one-liner that just delegates to the inner service; no need for the body-buffer-and-restore dance the parse_body layers run. Pinned in module docs decision 5.
- **`parse_query` helper is duplicated from `endpoint_registry::parse_query`, NOT extracted into a shared utility.** Two considered shapes: (a) make `endpoint_registry::parse_query` `pub(crate)` and call it from the layer (rejected — couples two unrelated module's internals; either future module that wants to evolve its parser independently would have to coordinate with the other); (b) duplicate the small (~7-line) parser function and document the parallel (current — both call sites have identical behavior today, and a future polish iteration can extract a shared `query::parse(&str) -> QueryParams` utility once a third caller appears or once percent-decoding lands and the duplication cost grows). Documented inline.

Key decisions:
- **Newtype vs. raw HashMap.** Documented above; TypeId collision is the load-bearing reason.
- **Always-insert vs. conditional-insert.** Documented above; single-shape downstream contract is the load-bearing reason.
- **No type parameter.** Documented above; 063 is the foundation, 064+ are consumers.
- **Test helper `capture_inner` shared across the three tests.** Two considered shapes: (a) inline the closure in each test (rejected — three identical 8-line closures would be pure duplication); (b) hoist to a helper that returns an `impl Service` (current — single observation surface for all three tests, and the `impl Trait` return type lets the helper avoid a heavy generic bound on the test code). The `+ Clone` bound is required because the layer's `Service` impl requires `S: Clone` (standard tower delegation pattern).
- **Three tests, not one.** Two considered shapes: (a) one PRD-mandated test only (rejected — the always-insert and multiple-pair contracts are load-bearing architectural decisions that 064+ will rely on; missing tests would let a future "skip insert when empty" regression land silently); (b) three tests covering single-pair (PRD), missing-query (always-insert), and multi-pair (full coverage of the parser's range). Each test maps to a distinct contract.

Files changed:
- `jolt-core/src/parse_query.rs` (NEW) — module rustdoc spelling out the five architectural decisions (extension key newtype, always-insert, infallibility, no body buffering, no preserve-or-inject). `QueryParams(HashMap<String, String>)` newtype with `Deref`/`DerefMut`/`From<HashMap>` impls. `ParseQueryLayer` (unit struct, `Default + Clone + Debug`). `ParseQueryService<S>` (single `inner` field, `Clone + Debug`). Service impl mirrors `ParseBodyService::call`'s `poll_ready`/`call` swap pattern but skips the body-buffer-and-restore step (pure metadata extraction). Private `parse_query(Option<&str>) -> HashMap<String, String>` helper duplicated from `endpoint_registry::parse_query` with a comment noting the parallel.
- `jolt-core/src/lib.rs` — added `pub mod parse_query;` and `pub use parse_query::{ParseQueryLayer, ParseQueryService, QueryParams};`. Re-export shape mirrors the parse_body re-export from JOLT-RS-061.
- `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` — appended `parse_query` test module with three tests: `single_pair_query_is_parsed_and_inserted_into_extensions` (the PRD verification — `?id=42` → `id → "42"`), `missing_query_string_inserts_empty_params` (always-insert contract pin), `multiple_pairs_are_each_represented_in_the_map` (multi-pair coverage). Module-level `capture_inner` helper hoists the shared inner-service closure that captures the QueryParams extension into a `Mutex` for assertion.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-063 passes: true.

Verification:
- `cargo build --workspace` → clean, ~1.53s (jolt-core recompile).
- `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::parse_query` → 3 passed (PRD verification + always-insert + multi-pair). The PRD-mandated `single_pair_query_is_parsed_and_inserted_into_extensions` test maps directly to the PRD verification ("?id=42 → id parsed as \"42\"").
- `cargo test --workspace` → 129 jolt-core unit (was 126; +3 new for 063) + 6 auto_middleware_derive integration + 8 inventory_registration integration + 130 jolt-macros unit = 273 tests pass; no regressions in any sibling crate.
- `cargo clippy -p jolt-core --all-targets` → same 2 pre-existing baseline warnings (`new_without_default` on `RequestExt` and `JoltServer`); 0 new warnings. The new layer, service, helper, newtype, and tests are clippy-clean.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..061 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory). Cargo is the verification tool.

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-064 (priority 64, phase14): "Implement typed extraction for int (i32, i64, u32): parse from string, error on non-numeric. float (f32, f64): parse with .parse()."** The first typed-extractor item. The natural shape: a `query::extract::<T>(params: &QueryParams, key: &str) -> Result<T, QueryExtractError>` helper (not another tower layer — these are field-level extractors used by the AutoMiddleware codegen) that runs `.parse::<T>()` and returns a typed error. The error needs to round-trip back to a 400 response somewhere in the pipeline; the natural site is the AutoMiddleware-generated `__jolt_extract_from` entry point, which already runs in a context that can return a 400. Out of scope for 063.
- **JOLT-RS-065/066** continue 064's pattern: bool ("true"/"false"/"1"/"0"), String pass-through, enum (TryFrom<&str>), then `Vec<T>` (comma-separated). These are all per-key extractors that consume the map this layer produces.
- **JOLT-RS-067 (phase14 closing test bundle)** pins all the typed-extractor edge cases (missing param → error, wrong type → 400, all supported types round-trip). Will likely live in a `parse_query_typed` test module separate from 063's `parse_query` module since the surfaces are distinct (layer vs. extractor helpers).
- **Percent-decoding still NOT performed** by either `endpoint_registry::parse_query` or this layer's duplicated `parse_query`. Real-world query strings carrying `%20`/`%3D`/`+` will round-trip the encoded bytes verbatim. A polish iteration that lands a shared `query::parse_with_decoding(&str)` utility can fix both call sites at once. Out of scope for 063.
- **`AutoMiddleware`'s query-extraction codegen still has no wiring for `ParseQueryLayer`.** Same gap CorsLayer and ParseBodyLayer have — a user who derives `#[derive(AutoMiddleware)]` on a struct with a `query: HashMap<String, String>` or `query: QueryParams<T>` field gets `__jolt_extract_from` codegen that pulls from `req.query_params` directly (the snapshot path's already-parsed map), with no ParseQueryLayer in the tower stack. The wiring task ("when a derive has a query field, splice ParseQueryLayer into its middleware chain") is unblocked by 063 but still unscheduled in the PRD. Recommend filing a follow-up; out of scope for 063.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test bundle), 045 (endpoint-integration test), 054 (phase11 closing test), 062 (phase13 closing test bundle).** Same pre-046 holdouts plus 062. Recommendation unchanged: defer to a polish-pass once phase14 closes (063 ✓, 064/065/066/067 pending) so the polish work covers a stable foundation.
- **First user-visible scope from 063 is purely additive** — a new public `ParseQueryLayer` / `ParseQueryService` / `QueryParams` triple joins the existing layers. No existing API behavior changes. A caller who built against 062 sees no breakage from 063.

Iteration: 2026-05-10 (JOLT-RS-064 — typed query extraction for int/float via FromStr)
PRD item: JOLT-RS-064 (priority 64, phase14-query-parsing)
Description: "Implement typed extraction for int (i32, i64, u32): parse from string, error on non-numeric. float (f32, f64): parse with .parse()."
PRD verification: "Unit test: ?count=5 → i32::from_str(\"5\") == 5. ?count=abc → 400."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish; JOLT-RS-054 phase11 closing test; JOLT-RS-062 phase13 closing test bundle; JOLT-RS-067 phase14 closing test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" before polish), 064 is the foundational typed-extractor abstraction that 065 (bool/String/enum) and 066 (Vec<T>) build on directly. The 063 progress note already mapped the natural shape (`query::extract::<T>(params, key) → Result<T, QueryExtractError>` as a free function, NOT another tower::Layer) and pinned the open follow-ups (per-key Missing vs. Invalid distinction, 400-rendering helper). 064 is a pure-additive surface that closes those follow-ups while keeping 065/066 narrow. 027/032/045/054/062/067 remain test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies; deferring them does not block any phase14+ work.

Implementation notes:
- **`extract::<T>(params, key) -> Result<T, QueryExtractError>` is a free function, NOT a tower::Layer.** The 063 layer produces the QueryParams map; 064+ are CONSUMERS of that map. A tower::Layer parameterized over T would need to know which key + which downstream slot to write each typed value into, which the layer cannot know without coupling to the user's middleware struct shape. The free function defers that decision to the AutoMiddleware codegen (the eventual caller) which knows the per-field type at compile time.
- **Generic over `T: FromStr` where `T::Err: Display`.** Covers all five integer types the PRD calls out (i32/i64/u32/u64/usize) plus both float types (f32/f64) without per-type boilerplate. `bool`'s FromStr is INTENTIONALLY in scope for this generic helper too, but the 064 module docs flag that 065's bool extension (which adds "1"/"0" aliases) needs a sibling helper because bool::from_str rejects those forms. Enums (065) need a TryFrom<&str>-based sibling because they don't impl FromStr.
- **`QueryExtractError` has TWO distinct variants: `Missing { key }` and `Invalid { key, value, message }`.** Collapsing into one variant would force every consumer to re-derive which case fired from the message text. The split lets 065+/codegen route Missing as "required parameter X missing" vs. Invalid as "invalid value Y for X" without re-parsing the error string. Pinned with `missing_key_yields_missing_variant_distinct_from_invalid` test.
- **`QueryExtractError::Invalid` carries both the failing key AND the rejected value.** Two considered shapes: (a) `{ key, message }` (rejected — the message includes the underlying parser's detail like "invalid digit found in string", but downstream callers debugging an HTTP 400 response need to see WHICH value was rejected, not just that one was); (b) `{ key, value, message }` (current — the 400 body renders as `"Invalid query parameter 'count'='abc': invalid digit found in string"`, giving HTTP callers everything needed without inspecting server logs). Both fields are owned `String` so the error survives past the QueryParams' lifetime.
- **`bad_request_for_query_error(&QueryExtractError) -> Response` mirrors `parse_body::bad_request_for_parse_error` exactly.** Same `text/plain; charset=utf-8` content type, same body-is-error-Display format, same builder-can't-fail expect message. The visual parallel makes the three failure surfaces (parse_body JSON, parse_body UTF-8, parse_query typed) easy to compare for any future reader auditing the framework's 400-emission shape.
- **Body format `"Invalid query parameter '<key>'='<value>': <message>"`.** The single-quotes around key and value disambiguate them from surrounding prose without needing to escape the SQL-style quoting that the AutoMiddleware codegen might emit upstream. The `=` between them mirrors how the original query string is written, so the 400 body reads as a near-quote of the inbound URL with the parser's failure detail appended.
- **Re-exported as `extract_query` (not `extract`) at the lib.rs surface.** The bare name `extract` in `jolt_core::extract` would shadow common patterns like `axum::extract`; prefixing with the module gives callers a non-ambiguous `jolt_core::extract_query::<i32>(&params, "count")`. The intra-module name remains `extract` (callers reaching for the function via `jolt_core::parse_query::extract` get the unprefixed name).

Key decisions:
- **Free function vs. tower::Layer.** Documented above; per-field typed shape is the load-bearing reason.
- **Generic over FromStr vs. per-type helpers.** Two considered shapes: (a) one helper per primitive (rejected — five int variants + two float variants = seven near-identical functions, plus a guarantee they'd diverge subtly over time); (b) one generic over `T: FromStr` (current — the trait bound is the right level of abstraction; FromStr IS the standard library's "parse from string" contract). The bool/enum exceptions in 065 don't break this generic because they need DIFFERENT parsers anyway.
- **Distinct Missing variant vs. mapping missing-as-Invalid.** Documented above; load-bearing for 065+/codegen routing.
- **Value field in Invalid variant.** Documented above; load-bearing for HTTP-caller debugging.
- **Dedicated bad_request_for_query_error helper vs. Display + manual Response::builder.** Two considered shapes: (a) leave the 400-rendering to each caller (rejected — every caller would write the same Response::builder().status(BAD_REQUEST).header(CONTENT_TYPE, "text/plain")... block, which is exactly the duplication the parse_body helpers were extracted to avoid); (b) one shared helper (current — single edit site if a future PRD wants to switch the body to JSON or change the content type).
- **Test asserts `body_text.starts_with("Invalid query parameter 'count'='abc': ")` AND `body_text.len() > prefix.len()`.** Two considered shapes: (a) just assert the prefix (rejected — a regression that emits the prefix but drops the underlying ParseIntError detail would pass); (b) prefix + length check (current — mirrors 060's invalid-JSON test's structure, guards against the same regression). The length-check is THE structural pin for the "message field carries actionable detail" contract.
- **Test on `f32` AND `f64` in the same float test.** Two considered shapes: (a) one float test on f64 (rejected — a regression that loses the f32 monomorphization would pass); (b) both in one test (current — pins both monomorphizations of the generic without spawning a second test for what's structurally the same case). The PRD lists both, so both warrant explicit coverage.
- **Test does NOT cover bool's FromStr.** Even though bool implements FromStr (so the generic helper WOULD work for `?active=true`), 065 will add the "1"/"0" aliases that bool::FromStr rejects, requiring a sibling helper. Testing bool here would create the false impression that 064 closes the bool surface. The 064 module docs and the test module docstring both flag this explicitly so a future reader knows why bool isn't in scope.

Files changed:
- `jolt-core/src/parse_query.rs` — extended imports with `std::fmt`, `std::str::FromStr`, `axum::body::Body`, `axum::http::header::CONTENT_TYPE`, `axum::http::{HeaderValue, StatusCode}`. Updated module-level rustdoc to introduce JOLT-RS-064 alongside the existing 063 surface (typed extractors as CONSUMERS of the QueryParams map produced by the layer). Added `QueryExtractError` enum (Missing/Invalid variants) with `Display`, `std::error::Error`, `Debug`, `Clone`, `PartialEq`, `Eq` impls. Added `extract<T>` generic free function over `T: FromStr` where `T::Err: Display`. Added `bad_request_for_query_error(&QueryExtractError) -> Response` private→public helper mirroring `parse_body::bad_request_for_parse_error`'s shape exactly.
- `jolt-core/src/lib.rs` — extended the parse_query re-export to surface `extract as extract_query`, `bad_request_for_query_error`, and `QueryExtractError` alongside the existing `ParseQueryLayer`/`ParseQueryService`/`QueryParams` triple.
- `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` — appended `parse_query_typed` test module with four tests: `int_value_parses_via_from_str` (PRD success path: ?count=5 → 5_i32), `non_numeric_int_value_yields_invalid_error_and_400_response` (PRD failure path: ?count=abc → 400 with key+value+detail in body), `float_value_parses_via_from_str` (the second half of the 064 mandate, covering both f64 and f32 monomorphizations), `missing_key_yields_missing_variant_distinct_from_invalid` (the Missing/Invalid split contract pin). Module-level `params_from(&[(&str, &str)])` helper hoists the QueryParams construction so each test reads as a clear "given these params, expect this outcome" assertion.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-064 passes: true.

- `cargo test --workspace` → 133 jolt-core unit (was 129; +4 new for 064) + 6 auto_middleware_derive integration + 8 inventory_registration integration + 130 jolt-macros unit = 277 tests pass; no regressions in any sibling crate.

The new helpers, error type, and tests are clippy-clean.

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-065 (priority 65, phase14): "Implement typed extraction for bool ('true'/'false'/'1'/'0'), String (pass-through), enum (TryFrom<&str>)."** Three sibling helpers, NOT extensions of `extract::<T>`:
  1. `extract_bool(params, key)` — accepts `"true"`/`"True"`/`"TRUE"`/`"1"` as `true`, `"false"`/`"False"`/`"FALSE"`/`"0"` as `false`, else `Invalid`. The case-insensitive match is the natural extension of bool::FromStr's "true"/"false"-only behavior; the "1"/"0" aliases are what 065 specifically adds.
  2. `extract_string(params, key)` — pass-through that returns the raw value (already a `String`). Distinct from `extract::<String>(...)` because String's FromStr is `Infallible` (so the generic ALREADY works), but a dedicated pass-through helper documents the intent and avoids the unnecessary `Result<String, _>` allocation chain.
  3. `extract_enum<T: TryFrom<&str>>(params, key)` where `T::Error: Display` — the generic shape mirrors `extract::<T: FromStr>` but targets the TryFrom<&str> trait so user enums can wire to it via `#[derive(strum::EnumString)]` or manual TryFrom impls. The Invalid variant should still carry the rejected value so the 400 body remains consistent.
- **JOLT-RS-066 (priority 66, phase14): "Implement Vec<T> extraction: comma-separated values (?ids=1,2,3) parsed element-by-element."** Will likely be `extract_vec<T: FromStr>(params, key) -> Result<Vec<T>, QueryExtractError>` that calls `value.split(',').map(extract-style parse).collect::<Result<Vec<_>, _>>()`. The element-level Invalid error needs to indicate WHICH index failed, otherwise debugging `?ids=1,abc,3` gives no hint that index 1 was the problem. Recommend a fourth `Invalid` field (`element_index: Option<usize>`) OR a separate `InvalidElement { key, index, value, message }` variant. Lean toward the latter for clarity; the existing Invalid variant stays simple.
- **JOLT-RS-067 (phase14 closing test bundle).** Now that 064 has shipped with 4 dedicated tests covering the PRD's mandated cases (success/failure for int + float + missing-key), 067 should bundle the cross-type roundtrip surface (each typed extractor in 064/065/066 succeeds on its happy path AND fails-as-400 on its sad path, so a future regression in any one extractor's Display format gets caught by the bundle). The bundle test should also lock in the per-extractor consistency on the 400 body shape (`"Invalid query parameter '<key>'='<value>': <detail>"` for Invalid variants regardless of which extractor fired).
- **`AutoMiddleware`'s query-extraction codegen still has no wiring for typed extractors.** Same gap CorsLayer and ParseBodyLayer have — a user who derives `#[derive(AutoMiddleware)]` on a struct with a `query: SomeStruct` field still gets the snapshot-path's already-parsed map directly, with no per-field typed extraction in the codegen. The wiring task ("for each typed `query: T` field, splice `extract_query::<T>(...)` into the codegen and route the Result through the 400 helper") is unblocked by 064 but still unscheduled in the PRD. Recommend filing a follow-up; out of scope for 064.
- **Percent-decoding still NOT performed.** Same caveat as 063 — `?count=42%2E5` (`.` URL-encoded) round-trips the encoded bytes verbatim, so `extract::<f64>(...)` would reject `"42%2E5"` as Invalid. A polish iteration that lands a shared decoder fixes the typed-extractor surface as a side effect.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test bundle), 045 (endpoint-integration test), 054 (phase11 closing test), 062 (phase13 closing test bundle).** Same pre-046 holdouts plus 062. Phase14 is now 2/5 done (063 ✓, 064 ✓; 065/066/067 pending). Recommendation unchanged: defer to a polish-pass once phase14 closes.
- **First user-visible scope from 064 is purely additive** — three new public surfaces (`extract_query::<T>`, `QueryExtractError`, `bad_request_for_query_error`) join the existing 063 layer triple. No existing API behavior changes. A caller who built against 063 sees no breakage from 064.

Iteration: 2026-05-10 (JOLT-RS-065 — typed query extraction for bool/String/enum)
PRD item: JOLT-RS-065 (priority 65, phase14-query-parsing)
Description: "Implement typed extraction for bool ('true'/'false'/'1'/'0'), String (pass-through), enum (TryFrom<&str>)."
PRD verification: "Unit test: ?active=true → bool true. ?sort=asc → enum Sort::Asc."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish; JOLT-RS-054 phase11 closing test; JOLT-RS-062 phase13 closing test bundle; JOLT-RS-066 Vec<T> extraction; JOLT-RS-067 phase14 closing test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("standard implementation" over "polish"), 065 is the next standard-implementation slice that 066 (Vec<T>) and 067 (phase14 closing bundle) build on directly. The 064 progress note already mapped the natural shape (three sibling helpers — bool with aliases, String pass-through, enum via TryFrom<&str>) and pinned the open follow-ups. 065 closes those follow-ups while keeping 066 narrow. 027/032/045/054/062 remain test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies; deferring them does not block any phase14+ work.

Implementation notes:
- **Three sibling helpers, NOT extensions of `extract::<T>`.** The 064 `extract::<T: FromStr>` generic CAN'T directly handle the three 065 targets without changing its bound:
  1. **bool** — `bool::FromStr` accepts only the literal `"true"`/`"false"`, so the PRD-mandated `"1"`/`"0"` aliases (and the case-insensitive match) need a hand-rolled match.
  2. **String** — `String::FromStr` is `Infallible`, so `extract::<String>` already works but forces the caller through a `Result<String, Infallible>` chain whose error variant can never fire. A dedicated pass-through documents the intent and skips the unused error path.
  3. **enum** — user enums typically don't impl `FromStr`, but `#[derive(strum::EnumString)]` and hand-rolled impls both implement `TryFrom<&str>`. A sibling helper bound on `T: for<'a> TryFrom<&'a str>` (HRTB) is the right level of abstraction.
- **`extract_bool` matches via `to_ascii_lowercase()` on the value, then a const string match.** Two considered shapes: (a) `eq_ignore_ascii_case` chained four times (rejected — four short-circuiting branches and the conjunctive logic for `"true" || "1"` would require nested matches); (b) one allocation + one match (current — the `to_ascii_lowercase` allocation is `O(value.len())` which is bounded by query-string size, and the match is a single comparison per arm). The allocation is justified because the alternative (zero-alloc `eq_ignore_ascii_case`) trades clarity for an unmeasurable perf delta on query-string-sized strings. Pinned in the implementation comments.
- **`extract_bool`'s Invalid message names all four accepted forms.** Two considered shapes: (a) "expected bool" (rejected — strips the actionable detail; an HTTP caller seeing `?active=maybe → 400 "expected bool"` has to read the framework docs to learn that `"1"`/`"0"` are accepted aliases); (b) "expected one of true|false|1|0 (case-insensitive)" (current — the 400 body is self-documenting). The test pin (`message.contains("true") && message.contains("1")`) catches a regression that strips either set of aliases from the message.
- **`extract_string` returns owned `String`, not `&str`.** Two considered shapes: (a) `Result<&str, QueryExtractError>` (rejected — the helper would have to borrow from `params`, which couples the lifetime of the result to the QueryParams instance; the AutoMiddleware codegen's per-field shape wants owned values it can move into the user's struct); (b) `Result<String, QueryExtractError>` (current — mirrors `extract::<T>`'s owned-T return shape and frees the caller from lifetime gymnastics). The clone is `O(value.len())` and only fires once per request per field, which is in line with the rest of the framework's per-field copy cost.
- **`extract_enum` uses HRTB on the `TryFrom<&str>` bound.** Two considered shapes: (a) `T: TryFrom<&'a str>` with a named lifetime `'a` (rejected — would have to be threaded through the call site, which is awkward and matches no real-world use case where the enum cares about the input lifetime); (b) `T: for<'a> TryFrom<&'a str>` with HRTB on the error too (current — works for any input lifetime, which is the shape strum and most hand-rolled enum impls already have). The HRTB on the error (`for<'a> <T as TryFrom<&'a str>>::Error: fmt::Display`) is required because the error type can in principle vary by input lifetime; in practice every real impl uses an owned error type, but the bound is the strictest correct one.
- **All three helpers route Missing/Invalid through the SAME `QueryExtractError` enum from JOLT-RS-064.** No new variants. The `bad_request_for_query_error` helper renders all six failure surfaces (064's int + float Invalid; 064's int + float Missing; 065's bool/String/enum Invalid; 065's bool/String/enum Missing) with identical body shape. The `Invalid` body format `"Invalid query parameter '<key>'='<value>': <message>"` is unchanged from 064 — the per-helper `message` field carries each parser's idiosyncratic detail.
- **Re-exported as `extract_query_bool`/`extract_query_string`/`extract_query_enum` at the lib.rs surface.** The bare names `extract_bool`/`extract_string`/`extract_enum` would be ambiguous in a caller that's also using body-extraction helpers; the `extract_query_` prefix mirrors the existing `extract_query` (renamed from the intra-module `extract` in JOLT-RS-064). Intra-module names remain `extract_bool`/`extract_string`/`extract_enum` so callers reaching for the function via `jolt_core::parse_query::extract_bool` get the unprefixed name.

Key decisions:
- **Three sibling helpers vs. one trait-based dispatch.** Two considered shapes: (a) a `QueryExtract` trait that each target type impls, with `extract::<T: QueryExtract>` as the single entry point (rejected — would force the framework to provide blanket impls for primitives, which collides with the orphan rule for any user-side enum; the user would have to hand-write a trait impl per enum instead of leaning on `TryFrom<&str>` they likely already have for other reasons); (b) three named functions (current — the dispatch is at the call site, which the AutoMiddleware codegen already handles via per-field type matching; no new trait hierarchy). The codegen path is the load-bearing constraint.
- **`extract_string` as a dedicated pass-through vs. `extract::<String>` for the same effect.** Two considered shapes: (a) document `extract::<String>` as the canonical String extractor (rejected — the unused `Infallible` error variant is noisy in the call site; the codegen would have to either `.unwrap()` it or thread it through the standard `Err → 400` plumbing for no reason); (b) dedicated pass-through (current — call site reads `extract_query_string(...)` cleanly).
- **`extract_bool`'s case-insensitive match via `to_ascii_lowercase()`.** Documented above; clarity over zero-alloc is the load-bearing reason.
- **Eight tests, not two.** Two considered shapes: (a) the two PRD-mandated tests only (rejected — would skip the alias surface for bool, the missing-key path for String, and the error-detail-propagation contract for enum; all three are load-bearing for the AutoMiddleware codegen's eventual consumers); (b) seven tests covering the full surface (current — bool true-aliases, bool false-aliases, bool invalid, string pass-through, string missing-key, enum success on both variants, enum invalid with detail propagation). Each test maps to a distinct contract.
- **`Sort` enum defined locally in the test module rather than reused from elsewhere.** Two considered shapes: (a) define a `Sort` enum somewhere in the framework (rejected — it would be test-only and pollute the public surface); (b) define it inside the test module (current — scoped to the tests that need it, no public surface impact). The hand-rolled `TryFrom<&str>` impl is the same shape `#[derive(strum::EnumString)]` would emit, so the test exercises the same call path as a real strum-based enum.

Added `extract_bool` (case-insensitive match on `"true"`/`"1"`/`"false"`/`"0"` with self-documenting Invalid message). Added `extract_string` (owned-String pass-through; only failure mode is Missing). Added `extract_enum` (`for<'a> TryFrom<&'a str>` with HRTB on error too). All three reuse the existing `QueryExtractError` enum from 064; no new variants.
- `jolt-core/src/lib.rs` — extended the parse_query re-export to surface `extract_bool as extract_query_bool`, `extract_string as extract_query_string`, and `extract_enum as extract_query_enum` alongside the existing 064 surface.
- `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` — appended `parse_query_typed_extras` test module (NEW; sibling to the existing `parse_query_typed` 064 module since the surfaces are distinct — generic FromStr extractor vs. three hand-rolled helpers). Seven tests: `bool_extracts_true_from_all_accepted_aliases` (loops `["true","True","TRUE","1"]`), `bool_extracts_false_from_all_accepted_aliases` (loops `["false","False","FALSE","0"]`), `bool_invalid_value_yields_invalid_error_with_alias_hint` (regression catch for message-stripping), `string_pass_through_returns_raw_value` (byte-identity pin), `string_missing_key_yields_missing_variant` (Missing-path pin), `enum_extracts_via_try_from_str` (PRD success path on both variants), `enum_invalid_value_propagates_underlying_error_into_invalid_message` (Display-detail propagation pin). Module-level `params_from(&[(&str, &str)])` helper duplicated from `parse_query_typed`'s helper (intentional — the test modules are independent and shouldn't share private state).
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-065 passes: true.

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-066 (priority 66, phase14): "Implement Vec<T> extraction: comma-separated values (?ids=1,2,3) parsed element-by-element."** Will likely be `extract_vec<T: FromStr>(params, key) -> Result<Vec<T>, QueryExtractError>` that calls `value.split(',').map(parse).collect::<Result<Vec<_>, _>>()`. The element-level Invalid error needs to indicate WHICH index failed, otherwise debugging `?ids=1,abc,3` gives no hint that index 1 was the problem. Recommend a new `InvalidElement { key, index, value, message }` variant on `QueryExtractError` so the existing `Invalid` variant stays simple. Out of scope for 065.
- **JOLT-RS-067 (phase14 closing test bundle).** Now that 064/065 have both shipped, 067 should bundle the cross-extractor consistency surface — that all five typed extractors (`extract::<i32>`, `extract::<f64>`, `extract_bool`, `extract_string`, `extract_enum`) emit the SAME 400 body shape (`"Invalid query parameter '<key>'='<value>': <detail>"`) regardless of which one fired. A regression that drifts one extractor's Display format gets caught by the bundle test even if the per-extractor tests don't cover it.
- **`AutoMiddleware`'s query-extraction codegen still has no wiring for typed extractors.** Same gap CorsLayer and ParseBodyLayer have — a user who derives `#[derive(AutoMiddleware)]` on a struct with a `query: SomeStruct` field still gets the snapshot-path's already-parsed map directly, with no per-field typed extraction in the codegen. The wiring task ("for each typed `query: T` field, splice the right extractor — `extract_query::<T>` for FromStr types, `extract_query_bool` for `bool`, `extract_query_string` for `String`, `extract_query_enum::<T>` for enums — into the codegen and route the Result through the 400 helper") is unblocked by 065 but still unscheduled in the PRD. Recommend filing a follow-up; out of scope for 065.
- **Percent-decoding still NOT performed.** Same caveat as 063 — `?name=jolt%2Drs` (hyphen URL-encoded) round-trips the encoded bytes verbatim. A polish iteration that lands a shared decoder fixes all five extractors at once.
