Phase14 is now 3/5 done (063 ✓, 064 ✓, 065 ✓; 066/067 pending). Recommendation unchanged: defer to a polish-pass once phase14 closes.
- **First user-visible scope from 065 is purely additive** — three new public helpers (`extract_query_bool`, `extract_query_string`, `extract_query_enum`) join the existing 064 surface. No existing API behavior changes. A caller who built against 064 sees no breakage from 065.

Iteration: 2026-05-10 (JOLT-RS-066 — Vec<T> typed query extraction with element-level error position)
PRD item: JOLT-RS-066 (priority 66, phase14-query-parsing)
Description: "Implement Vec<T> extraction: comma-separated values (?ids=1,2,3) parsed element-by-element."
PRD verification: "Unit test: ?ids=1,2,3 → Vec<i32> = [1,2,3]."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish; JOLT-RS-054 phase11 closing test; JOLT-RS-062 phase13 closing test bundle; JOLT-RS-067 phase14 closing test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("standard implementation" over "polish"), 066 is the next standard-implementation slice that 067 (phase14 closing bundle) builds on directly. The 065 progress note already mapped the natural shape (`extract_vec<T: FromStr>` + new `InvalidElement { key, index, value, message }` variant on `QueryExtractError`) and pinned why a separate variant beats reusing `Invalid` with an `Option<usize>` field. 027/032/045/054/062 remain test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies; deferring them does not block any phase14+ work.

Implementation notes:
- **`extract_vec<T: FromStr>` is a sibling of `extract::<T>`, not a parameterization.** The 064 generic produces a single `T` from a single value; 066 produces a `Vec<T>` from a comma-separated value via `value.split(',').enumerate().map(parse).collect::<Result<Vec<T>, _>>()`. The shape difference (loop with per-element error reporting vs. one-shot parse) makes the sibling form the right choice — parameterizing `extract` over Vec/non-Vec would require either type-system gymnastics (`extract<T, C: Collect<T>>`) or a runtime branch on whether the value contains a comma. Both are heavier than two simple sibling helpers.
- **New `InvalidElement` variant on `QueryExtractError`, NOT a reused `Invalid` with `Option<usize>`.** Two considered shapes: (a) extend `Invalid` with `element_index: Option<usize>` so `extract::<i32>` still emits `Invalid { element_index: None, ... }` and `extract_vec::<i32>` emits `Invalid { element_index: Some(idx), ... }` (rejected — `Option<usize>` smuggles the variant distinction through a nullable field, which forces every consumer to either pattern-match the option AND fork on its discriminant or accept a less-informative error message; collapses two distinct semantic cases into one variant); (b) a dedicated `InvalidElement { key, index, value, message }` variant (current — the variant IS the discriminant, so a future router can branch on `match err { ... InvalidElement {..} => ... }` without re-deriving anything from a nullable field). Matches the existing module ethos pinned in the comment on `QueryExtractError`: "Two variants kept distinct so a future caller can map them differently."
- **Per-element `value` field on `InvalidElement` carries the FAILING element's raw string, not the whole comma-separated payload.** The 400 body should name what the caller actually has to fix — `?ids=1,abc,3` makes "element [1]='abc'" actionable, while echoing `'1,abc,3'` would force the caller to count commas themselves. The `index` field PLUS the element-only `value` is the minimum information that lets an HTTP caller pinpoint the bad element from the response alone.
- **Display format: `"Invalid query parameter '{key}' element [{index}]='{value}': {message}"`.** Two considered shapes: (a) `"Invalid query parameter '{key}'[{index}]='{value}': {message}"` (rejected — the bracket notation glommed onto the key name reads like Python list indexing, which is misleading because the `key` is the parameter NAME not a sequence); (b) `"Invalid query parameter '{key}' element [{index}]='{value}': {message}"` (current — the literal word "element" disambiguates the index from any other meaning). The 400-body test pins this shape via a `starts_with` assertion so a future drift gets caught.
- **Empty value `?ids=` yields `InvalidElement { index: 0, value: "", … }`, NOT `Ok(vec![])`.** Two considered shapes: (a) treat `""` as the empty list (rejected — silently accepts a "did you mean to omit ids?" case where the caller's intent is ambiguous; collapses two distinct cases into one shape); (b) propagate the underlying parser's rejection of the empty string verbatim (current — `"".parse::<i32>()` fails, the helper emits `InvalidElement` for the failing element, the caller gets a clear "element [0]='' rejected" 400). Callers wanting "absent → empty vec" semantics should match on the `Missing` variant themselves rather than asking this helper to fold two cases together. Documented in the rustdoc.
- **Whitespace is NOT stripped.** `?ids=1, 2, 3` would split to `["1", " 2", " 3"]` and fail on element 1 because `i32::from_str(" 2")` rejects. Two considered shapes: (a) silently `trim()` each element before parsing (rejected — a caller relying on whitespace being preserved for some other element type would be surprised by the silent normalization); (b) keep the parser's strict shape and let the caller URL-encode their values correctly (current — strict parsing matches the rest of the parse-query surface, which doesn't decode anything either; module docs already pin "Percent-decoding is NOT performed" as a separate caveat). The eventual percent-decoding polish item subsumes the whitespace question for free.
- **Re-exported as `extract_vec as extract_query_vec` at lib.rs.** Mirrors the 065 surface (`extract_query_bool`/`extract_query_string`/`extract_query_enum`); the bare `extract_vec` name on the public surface would collide with future body/header vec extractors. Intra-module name remains `extract_vec` for the same reason 064/065 keep the unprefixed forms.

Key decisions:
- **Sibling helper vs. parameterizing `extract`.** Documented above; the per-element loop and per-element error reporting make the sibling form the right shape.
- **`InvalidElement` as a dedicated variant.** Documented above; matches the module's existing distinct-variants ethos.
- **Per-element `value` field carries only the failing element.** Documented above; the index plus the element-only value is the minimum information for an HTTP caller to fix the bad element from the response alone.
- **Six tests, not one.** Two considered shapes: (a) the single PRD-mandated test only (rejected — would skip the single-value path, the float generic shape, the `InvalidElement` variant contract, the 400 rendering with index, and the missing-key path; all five are load-bearing for the AutoMiddleware codegen's eventual consumers); (b) six tests covering the full surface (current — happy path with multiple elements, single-element edge case, float generic shape, element-level failure with index, 400 body shape, missing-key distinct from empty-vec). Each test maps to a distinct contract.

Files changed:
- `jolt-core/src/parse_query.rs` — extended module rustdoc with a JOLT-RS-066 section explaining `extract_vec` and the new `InvalidElement` variant. Added the `InvalidElement { key, index, value, message }` variant on `QueryExtractError` with a doc comment pinning why it's distinct from `Invalid`. Extended the `Display` impl with the `"Invalid query parameter '{key}' element [{index}]='{value}': {message}"` rendering. Added `extract_vec<T: FromStr>(params, key) -> Result<Vec<T>, QueryExtractError>` that splits on commas and parses each element via `FromStr`, producing `InvalidElement` (with the failing index) on element-level failure and `Missing` for absent keys.
- `jolt-core/src/lib.rs` — extended the parse_query re-export to surface `extract_vec as extract_query_vec` alongside the existing 064/065 surface.
- `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` — appended `parse_query_typed_vec` test module (NEW; sibling to `parse_query_typed` and `parse_query_typed_extras` since the surfaces are distinct — this one targets the Vec<T> shape and the new InvalidElement variant). Six tests: `vec_extracts_comma_separated_ints` (PRD success path: ?ids=1,2,3 → vec![1,2,3]), `vec_extracts_single_value_as_one_element_vec` (no-comma edge case → one-element vec), `vec_extracts_floats_via_from_str` (generic-shape pin so a regression to int-only gets caught), `vec_invalid_element_yields_invalid_element_variant_with_index` (per-element failure pin: index 1, value "abc"), `vec_invalid_element_renders_into_400_with_index_in_body` (400-body shape pin via `starts_with("Invalid query parameter 'ids' element [1]='abc': ")`), `vec_missing_key_yields_missing_variant_not_empty_vec` (absent-vs-present distinction pin). Module-level `params_from(&[(&str, &str)])` helper duplicated from the sibling test modules (intentional — independent test modules shouldn't share private state).
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-066 passes: true.

Verification:
- `cargo build --workspace` → clean, ~1.50s (jolt-core recompile).
- `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::parse_query` → 20 passed (6 new for 066 + 14 existing from 063/064/065). The PRD-mandated `vec_extracts_comma_separated_ints` test maps directly to the PRD verification ("?ids=1,2,3 → Vec<i32> = [1,2,3]").
- `cargo test --workspace` → 146 jolt-core unit (was 140; +6 new for 066) + 6 auto_middleware_derive integration + 8 inventory_registration integration + 130 jolt-macros unit = 290 tests pass; no regressions in any sibling crate.

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-067 (priority 67, phase14 closing test bundle).** Now that 064/065/066 have all shipped, 067 should bundle the cross-extractor consistency surface — that the five typed extractors (`extract::<T>`, `extract_bool`, `extract_string`, `extract_enum`, `extract_vec::<T>`) emit predictable 400 body shapes regardless of which one fired. Two distinct prefix shapes are now in play: `"Invalid query parameter '{key}'='{value}': {detail}"` (Invalid) and `"Invalid query parameter '{key}' element [{index}]='{value}': {detail}"` (InvalidElement). 067's bundle test should pin both prefixes so a future regression that drifts either format gets caught even if the per-extractor tests don't cover it. Phase14 then closes after 067.
- **`AutoMiddleware`'s query-extraction codegen still has no wiring for typed extractors.** Same gap CorsLayer and ParseBodyLayer have — a user who derives `#[derive(AutoMiddleware)]` on a struct with a `query: SomeStruct` field still gets the snapshot-path's already-parsed map directly, with no per-field typed extraction in the codegen. The wiring task ("for each typed `query: T` field, splice the right extractor — `extract_query::<T>` for FromStr scalar types, `extract_query_bool` for `bool`, `extract_query_string` for `String`, `extract_query_enum::<T>` for enums, `extract_query_vec::<T>` for `Vec<T>` — into the codegen and route the Result through the 400 helper") is unblocked by 066 but still unscheduled in the PRD. Recommend filing a follow-up; out of scope for 066.
- **Percent-decoding still NOT performed.** Same caveat as 063 — `?ids=1%2C2%2C3` (commas URL-encoded) round-trips the encoded bytes verbatim, so `extract_query_vec::<i32>(params, "ids")` would see the literal string `"1%2C2%2C3"` (no commas to split on) and fail on the empty/odd parse. A polish iteration that lands a shared decoder fixes the typed-extractor surface as a side effect.
- **Whitespace in element values is NOT stripped.** `?ids=1, 2, 3` would emit `InvalidElement { index: 1, value: " 2", … }` because `i32::from_str(" 2")` rejects. Same deferred-to-percent-decoding rationale as above; documented in the rustdoc.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test bundle), 045 (endpoint-integration test), 054 (phase11 closing test), 062 (phase13 closing test bundle).** Same pre-046 holdouts. Phase14 is now 4/5 done (063 ✓, 064 ✓, 065 ✓, 066 ✓; 067 pending). Recommendation unchanged: defer to a polish-pass once phase14 closes.
- **First user-visible scope from 066 is purely additive on the helper surface but adds a new variant to `QueryExtractError`.** A caller that destructures `QueryExtractError` with a non-exhaustive match (no `_ =>` arm) would get a compile error after this iteration. Mitigation: existing call sites in `bad_request_for_query_error` already use `match` with `Self::Missing` and `Self::Invalid` arms; the 066 patch added the `Self::InvalidElement` arm in the same change so the in-tree caller is fine. External callers (none yet — the framework is pre-1.0) would need to add the new arm. Documented in the rustdoc on the new variant.

Iteration: 2026-05-10 (JOLT-RS-068 — TraceLayer integration into JoltServer::start)
PRD item: JOLT-RS-068 (priority 68, phase15-logging)
Description: "Integrate tower_http::trace::TraceLayer into the middleware stack (enabled globally in JoltServer::start)."
PRD verification: "Server starts, TraceLayer is in the stack."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish; JOLT-RS-054 phase11 closing test; JOLT-RS-062 phase13 closing test bundle; JOLT-RS-067 phase14 closing test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("integration points" before "polish"), 068 is the next integration-point slice that opens phase15-logging. 069 (log format customization) and 070 (request/response body logging at DEBUG) both DEPEND on TraceLayer being in the stack — without the layer wired, those iterations have nothing to customize. 027/032/045/054/062/067 remain test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies; deferring them does not block any phase15+ work. The 066 progress note ranked 067 as the next phase-closing item but it remains polish (closing-bundle test); 068's wiring unblocks two downstream phase15 iterations whereas 067 closes a phase that's already 4/5 done.

Implementation notes:
- **`build_serving_router(self, extra_router) -> Router` is a NEW public method extracted from `start`.** Two considered shapes: (a) inline the `.layer(TraceLayer::new_for_http())` call directly in `start` (rejected — `start` binds a TCP port and runs `axum::serve` to completion, which is not testable without spawning a background task and shutting it down via the signal handler; the wiring would only be exercised by manual `cargo run` smoke tests); (b) extract the "what router gets served" composition into a public sibling helper that mirrors the existing `into_router(self) -> Router` pattern (current — tests can call `build_serving_router` and route a request via `tower::ServiceExt::oneshot` without binding a port). The naming pattern (`build_*_router` for "produces what start would serve") leaves room for a future `build_serving_router_with_tls` sibling without renaming the existing surface.
- **TraceLayer applied to the MERGED router, NOT to `extra_router` and `inventory_router` separately.** Two considered shapes: (a) `extra_router.layer(TraceLayer::new_for_http()).merge(inventory_router.layer(TraceLayer::new_for_http()))` (rejected — every request would produce TWO trace spans because the layer fires once per Service it wraps; the merge produces a Router that delegates to whichever child Router matched the path, so each child's wrapped service emits its own span. The duplicate-span problem is subtle because both spans would carry the same span name `request` — a debugger reading the trace would see suspicious-looking double entries with no obvious cause); (b) `extra_router.merge(inventory_router).layer(TraceLayer::new_for_http())` (current — the layer wraps the whole merged router as a single Service, so each request produces exactly ONE span). The pin in the rustdoc on `build_serving_router` calls out the "ONE span, not two stacked ones" reason explicitly so a future iteration that splits the layer wiring across the merge boundary fails the readability bar before it lands.
- **`TraceLayer::new_for_http()` is the standard tower-http constructor for HTTP services.** Two considered shapes: (a) `TraceLayer::new(SharedClassifier::new(StatusInRangeAsFailures::new(400..=599).into_make_classifier()))` or some other custom classifier (rejected — JOLT-RS-068's verification is purely "TraceLayer in the stack"; the customization is JOLT-RS-069's scope, not 068's; landing a custom classifier here would force 069 to either accept the choice or rip it out and re-do); (b) `TraceLayer::new_for_http()` (current — the canonical "default for HTTP" constructor, which uses `ServerErrorsAsFailures` as its classifier; documented as the standard form in tower-http's own examples). The constructor returns a TraceLayer with default `MakeSpan`, `OnRequest`, `OnResponse`, `OnBodyChunk`, `OnEos`, `OnFailure` callbacks — all of which 069 will customize.
- **`start` keeps the `let port = self.port;` copy BEFORE consuming `self`.** Two considered shapes: (a) thread `port` through `build_serving_router`'s return tuple (rejected — pollutes the helper's API with an unrelated port concern; `build_serving_router` is about "what router gets served", not "what port"); (b) copy `port` (a `u16`, so the copy is one word) before the `self.build_serving_router(extra_router)` call consumes `self` (current — same pattern the previous `start` body used, just relocated past the helper extraction). The copy is free at runtime and keeps each helper focused on a single concern.
- **Without a `tracing` subscriber installed, the emitted events are no-ops.** The rustdoc on `build_serving_router` says this explicitly. tower-http's TraceLayer emits via the `tracing` crate's macros, which check at runtime whether a subscriber is registered for the relevant target/level; if none is registered, the call is a near-zero-cost branch. JOLT-RS-069 will install the subscriber. A user running the server today via `cargo run` sees no log output — which is the right default behavior pre-069 (no surprise log noise on stderr).

Key decisions:
- **Public `build_serving_router` helper vs. inline wiring in `start`.** Documented above; testability is the load-bearing reason.
- **Layer applied to merged router vs. each child.** Documented above; one-span-per-request is the load-bearing reason.
- **`new_for_http()` vs. customized constructor.** Documented above; 068's scope is "TraceLayer in the stack" without 069's customization scope creep.
- **Test placement: `jolt-core/tests/inventory_registration.rs` (integration), NOT `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` (unit).** Two considered shapes: (a) add to the unit `tests.rs` module (rejected — the test needs `#[endpoint]` macro expansion + `inventory::iter` collection to produce a probe route to call through the layered router; the unit module has no `#[endpoint]` definitions and adding one would require either the macro path or a hand-rolled `Endpoint` impl, both heavier than reusing the existing `Probe` struct); (b) append to the existing integration test crate that already has `Probe` + `Secondary` (current — reuses the existing `oneshot`-against-`into_router` test pattern, swapping `into_router()` for `build_serving_router(Router::new())`). The new test sits alongside the four existing `into_router_serves_*` tests so a future reader sees the full "what JoltServer's serve-side composition produces" surface in one place.
- **Test asserts response status + body, NOT span emission.** Two considered shapes: (a) install a custom `tracing::Subscriber` impl, route a request, assert at least one event was captured (rejected — implementing `Subscriber` from scratch requires 7+ trait methods, most as no-op stubs, plus an Arc<Mutex<...>> to capture events; the boilerplate is heavy AND the test would still only pin "some event fired" without proving it came from THIS layer; tracing-subscriber is not a transitive dep so adding it would add a dev-dep just for this one assertion); (b) regression-test that the layered router still serves requests cleanly (current — pins that the `.layer(TraceLayer::new_for_http())` call composes correctly with the inventory routes, doesn't panic at construction, doesn't mangle the response body). The PRD verification "TraceLayer is in the stack" is satisfied by the type-system proof of the `.layer()` call in `build_serving_router` itself; the test guards against the adjacent regression where adding the layer accidentally breaks the response path. JOLT-RS-069 (when it installs the subscriber) will add the event-emission-counting test for free as part of its log-format coverage.
- **`Router::new()` (NOT `Router::default()`) as the test's `extra_router` argument.** axum's `Router::new()` is the canonical empty constructor and the same form the existing tests use (`JoltServer::new().into_router()`). Using `Router::default()` would work but introduces a different idiom for no benefit.

Files changed:
- `jolt-core/src/server.rs` — added `use tower_http::trace::TraceLayer;` import. Added `pub fn build_serving_router(self, extra_router: Router) -> Router` method that calls `self.into_router()` to collect inventory + sort + build, merges with `extra_router`, then wraps the result in `TraceLayer::new_for_http()`. Refactored `start` to call `self.build_serving_router(extra_router)` (after copying `self.port`) instead of inlining the merge. Extended `start`'s rustdoc with a JOLT-RS-068 paragraph explaining that the merged router is wrapped in TraceLayer before being handed to `axum::serve`.
- `jolt-core/tests/inventory_registration.rs` — added `build_serving_router_wraps_merged_router_in_trace_layer_without_breaking_responses` integration test. Builds the layered router via `JoltServer::new().build_serving_router(axum::Router::new())`, sends GET /probe via `oneshot`, asserts 200 + "pong" body. The test's docstring explicitly flags that this is a SHAPE pin (regression catch for the response-path) and that the type-system proof of "TraceLayer in the stack" comes from the `.layer(TraceLayer::new_for_http())` call in `build_serving_router` itself.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-068 passes: true.

Verification:
- `cargo build --workspace` → clean, ~1.96s (jolt-core recompile).
- `cargo test --workspace` → 146 jolt-core unit + 6 auto_middleware_derive integration + 9 inventory_registration integration (was 8; +1 new for 068) + 130 jolt-macros unit = 291 tests pass; no regressions in any sibling crate.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..066 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory; this is a pure Rust workspace). Cargo is the verification tool.

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-069 (priority 69, phase15): "Customize log format: method, path, status code, latency in ms. Log at INFO level. Use tracing crate for structured output."** This is where TraceLayer's defaults get replaced. The `TraceLayer::new_for_http()` constructor's default `MakeSpan`/`OnRequest`/`OnResponse` callbacks emit at DEBUG with target `tower_http::trace`; 069 needs to swap them via `.make_span_with(...)`/`.on_request(...)`/`.on_response(...)` so the canonical INFO-level "method path status latency_ms" log appears. The four PRD-mandated fields map to span attributes: `method` and `path` from the request (set in `make_span_with`), `status` and `latency_ms` from the response (set in `on_response`). 069 will also need to install a `tracing_subscriber::fmt` (or similar) layer in `JoltServer::start` so the events surface as stderr lines — currently they're emitted into the void. Recommend `tracing-subscriber` as a workspace dep with the `fmt`/`env-filter` features.
- **JOLT-RS-070 (priority 70, phase15): "Log request body and response body at DEBUG level (truncated to reasonable size). Suppress for sensitive paths (auth)."** Builds on 069's customized callbacks. Body logging requires either intercepting body bytes (tower_http's `OnBodyChunk` callback) or re-reading the buffered body from `RequestExt`/`ResponseExt`. The "suppress for sensitive paths" half needs a path-based filter — likely a `Vec<String>` config knob on `JoltServer` for "paths whose bodies must NOT be logged". Out of scope for 068 but unblocked by it.
- **TraceLayer is now ALWAYS in the stack — no opt-out.** Two considered shapes for a future iteration: (a) keep the unconditional wiring (current — simplest; matches the "logging is a default, not an add-on" ethos most modern frameworks ship with); (b) gate via a `JoltServer.tracing_enabled: bool` flag (deferred — adds a config knob with no current caller asking for it; YAGNI applies). If a future user reports "I want JoltServer with NO trace layer," (b) becomes the right answer; until then (a) is the right default.
- **`build_serving_router` consumes `self`.** Mirrors `into_router(self)`. A caller who wants to keep the server config around for inspection AFTER building the serving router would need a `&self` variant (probably `clone_serving_router(&self, ...) -> Router`). Out of scope for 068; no current caller needs it.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test bundle), 045 (endpoint-integration test), 054 (phase11 closing test), 062 (phase13 closing test bundle), 067 (phase14 closing test bundle).** Same pre-046 holdouts plus 062 and 067. Phase14 is now 4/5 done (067 still pending); phase15 is now 1/3 started (068 ✓; 069/070 pending). Recommendation unchanged: defer the test-bundle polish to a polish-pass once phase15 closes.
- **First user-visible scope from 068 is one new public method (`build_serving_router`) on `JoltServer` plus a behavior change in `start` (every served request now emits a tower-http span).** No existing API behavior changes for callers who don't use `build_serving_router` directly. A caller who uses `start` sees the trace-span emission as a SILENT change pre-069 because no subscriber is installed — once 069 lands, the same callers will start seeing log output on stderr.


Iteration: 2026-05-10 (JOLT-RS-071 — AuthBearerLayer: Authorization header format validation)
PRD item: JOLT-RS-071 (priority 71, phase16-auth-bearer)
Description: "Implement AuthBearerLayer: extract Authorization header, validate format is 'Bearer <token>'. On missing/invalid format, return 401 + mark_finished."
PRD verification: "Unit test: no Authorization header → 401."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish; JOLT-RS-054 phase11 closing test; JOLT-RS-062 phase13 closing test bundle; JOLT-RS-067 phase14 closing test bundle; JOLT-RS-069 log format customization; JOLT-RS-070 debug body logging): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" FIRST, before "integration points", "unknown unknowns", "standard implementation", and "polish"), 071 is the next core-abstraction slice — it OPENS phase16-auth-bearer with a brand-new tower::Layer (AuthBearerLayer/AuthBearerService) that 072 (JWT validation), 073 (claims extraction into request extensions), and 074 (auth test bundle) all depend on. 069/070 (phase15 logging customization) are standard-implementation slices building on 068's TraceLayer wiring; 027/032/045/054/062/067 remain test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies. Skipping ahead from phase15 (1/3) into phase16 (0/4) is justified because 071 is the next NEW abstraction in the PRD ordering, while 069/070 customize an already-landed layer (lower priority by category even though numerically earlier).

Implementation notes:
- **`AuthBearerLayer` mirrors the four established layer shapes (CorsLayer, ParseBodyLayer, ParseBodyStringLayer, ParseQueryLayer) verbatim.** Stateless `#[derive(Default, Clone, Debug)]` struct, `Layer<S>` impl producing `AuthBearerService<S>`, `AuthBearerService::poll_ready` delegating to `inner`, `AuthBearerService::call` doing the standard tower poll_ready/call swap (`mem::replace(&mut self.inner, cloned)`), and `Pin<Box<dyn Future<...> + Send>>` futures. Picking the established shape over a one-off variant means a reader who already understands ParseBodyService can read AuthBearerService cold.
- **Three-step header validation: present → ASCII → `Bearer ` prefix → non-empty token.** Each step has its own rejection variant (`MissingHeader`, `NotAscii`, `MissingBearerPrefix`, `EmptyToken`) so the 401 body disambiguates which contract failed. Two considered shapes for the rejection enum: (a) a single `BearerRejectReason::Invalid(&'static str)` with the message inlined per call site (rejected — 4 free-form strings spread across the function body, easy for a future iteration to drift one string away from the others); (b) a 4-variant enum with a `message(self) -> &'static str` method (current — the variant IS the contract, the message lives in one place, and a future caller can `match` on the variant if needed without parsing prose). The enum is `pub(crate)`-private to the module since 072+ doesn't need to see the rejection reasons (it just hands back a `Result<JwtClaims, _>` after token decode).
- **Scheme name match is case-insensitive (RFC 7235 §2.1) but the separator is held strict (single ASCII space).** Two considered shapes: (a) accept any whitespace separator (rejected — `Bearer\t<token>` is shape that most upstream WAFs already flag; over-permissive splitting widens the attack surface); (b) accept only a single space, reject tabs / multi-space / CRLF (current — matches the canonical RFC 6750 example). Implemented via byte-level inspection (`text.as_bytes()[.."Bearer".len()].eq_ignore_ascii_case(b"Bearer") && text.as_bytes()["Bearer".len()] == b' '`) rather than `text.to_lowercase().starts_with("bearer ")` because the lowercase allocation is wasted for the 99% case where the header is already canonical, and the byte-level form has no allocation.
- **Length gate is `text.len() > "Bearer".len()` (NOT `> "Bearer ".len()`).** This was the off-by-one I tripped over on first run: a header of `Bearer ` (prefix + single space, no token) has length 7, which equals `"Bearer ".len()`. Gating on `> 7` would route that header to `MissingBearerPrefix` instead of the dedicated `EmptyToken` branch. Fixed gate is `> 6` (length of `"Bearer"`), which lets `Bearer ` reach the empty-token check below where it belongs. Pinned in a code comment so a future cleanup that "tightens the constant" doesn't regress the contract.
- **Extracted token lands in extensions as `BearerToken(pub String)` newtype, NOT as a bare `String`.** Two considered shapes: (a) bare `String` in extensions (rejected — `req.extensions_mut().insert::<String>(token)` collides with `ParseBodyStringService`'s raw-text-body stash; both layers wired into the same stack would clobber each other since extensions are keyed by `TypeId`); (b) dedicated newtype (current — unique extension key, follows the same pattern `QueryParams` set in JOLT-RS-063). The newtype carries an `as_str(&self) -> &str` accessor so consumers don't have to `.0` into the field.
- **401 carries `WWW-Authenticate: Bearer` (RFC 6750 §3) plus a `text/plain` body.** Two considered shapes for the body: (a) JSON `{ "error": "...", "reason": "..." }` (rejected — diverges from the framework's existing 400 / 404 / 405 ad-hoc error shapes which are all `text/plain`); (b) `text/plain` with the per-variant message (current — matches the rest of the framework's error surface). The challenge header makes the 401 RFC-compliant; without it, browsers and HTTP clients lose the hint about which scheme to retry with.
- **401 returned DIRECTLY from `call` (NOT stashed via `RequestExt::set_response`).** Same rationale as `ParseBodyService::call`'s 400 path: AuthBearerLayer typically sits OUTSIDE Router in the wiring (the request never reaches the registry walk that consumes stashed responses), so direct return is the right shape. The `mark_finished` flip is a pure observability signal — it does NOT round-trip through Router's stash/take dance. If a future iteration wires AuthBearerLayer INSIDE Router (e.g. per-route auth via the AutoMiddleware codegen), JOLT-RS-079's "Router checks finished after middleware chain" path will still observe the flag from the existing `mark_finished` call.
- **Preserve-or-inject `Arc<RequestExt>` mirrors the existing CorsService / ParseBodyService / ParseBodyStringService pattern.** When an upstream layer (typically Router itself, when AuthBearer composes inside Router) has already set an `Arc<RequestExt>`, reuse it so the flipped `finished` latch is observable to anyone holding the same Arc; otherwise inject a fresh one. Without the inject branch, an isolated AuthBearer wrapping a service stack with no Router upstream would have nowhere to flip the latch — the rejection contract would exist but be unobservable.

Key decisions:
- **New tower::Layer rather than extending CorsLayer or ParseBodyLayer.** Two considered shapes: (a) bolt the auth check into one of the existing layers via a feature flag or config field (rejected — couples unrelated concerns; an opted-in CORS layer that ALSO does auth would surprise readers, and ParseBody doing auth is even more out of place); (b) standalone layer that composes into a tower stack like the others (current — matches axum / tower-http convention and lets the user opt in/out per route or globally). Documented in the module rustdoc.
- **Layer scope is FORMAT validation only; JWT decode and claims extraction are 072/073 sibling iterations.** Two considered shapes: (a) implement the full auth pipeline (extract → validate JWT → inject claims) in 071 (rejected — fuses three independently-verifiable steps into one slice; if 072's JWT validation later changes algorithm/secret config, the change touches the same file as the format validator); (b) split per the PRD's three-iteration breakdown (current — 071 stashes `BearerToken`, 072 reads `BearerToken` and produces `Result<Claims, JwtError>`, 073 stashes the validated `Claims`). Each slice is independently passing-or-failing, and a regression in one doesn't mask a regression in another.
- **Four rejection variants, not one with a message.** Documented above; the dedicated variants make each contract testable in isolation.
- **Seven tests, not one.** Two considered shapes: (a) just the PRD-mandated `missing_authorization_header_short_circuits_with_401` test (rejected — leaves the four sibling rejection paths and the two happy-path contracts uncovered; a regression in the empty-token path or the case-insensitive scheme would silently land); (b) seven tests covering the full surface (current — missing header, non-Bearer scheme, empty token, non-ASCII bytes, valid header, case-insensitive scheme variants, fresh-RequestExt injection). Each test maps to a distinct contract pinned in the module rustdoc.
- **Test inner service uses `tower::service_fn` with a Boxed Pin<Future>` for the rejection-path tests.** Two considered shapes: (a) the simpler `tower::service_fn(|_| async { panic!(...) })` form (rejected — the panicking branch is unreachable code that the compiler warns on; the `#[allow(unreachable_code)]` attribute on the unreachable `Ok(...)` line is awkward but necessary); (b) a hand-rolled `Service` impl with a panic in `call` (rejected — heavy boilerplate for a one-line test fixture). Settled on `service_fn` + `#[allow(unreachable_code)]` on the never-reached `Ok` line; matches the pattern `ParseBodyService`'s `invalid_json_body_short_circuits_with_400_and_marks_finished` test already uses.
- **Public re-export at lib.rs surface.** Three new public surfaces (`AuthBearerLayer`, `AuthBearerService`, `BearerToken`) join the existing layer surface. The `BearerRejectReason` enum stays module-private (the rejection mechanism is an implementation detail; only the 401 BODY is contractual, and the body strings are pinned in tests).

Files changed:
- `jolt-core/src/auth_bearer.rs` (NEW) — module rustdoc explains the layer's scope (FORMAT validation only), the six architectural decisions (scope split, newtype extension key, case-insensitive scheme match, empty-token rejection, non-ASCII rejection, preserve-or-inject `Arc<RequestExt>`). `BearerToken(pub String)` newtype with `as_str(&self) -> &str` accessor. `AuthBearerLayer` (stateless `Default + Clone + Debug`) with `Layer<S>` impl producing `AuthBearerService<S>`. `AuthBearerService<S>` with `Service<AxumRequest>` impl: standard tower poll_ready/call swap, preserve-or-inject `Arc<RequestExt>` (mirrors ParseBodyService/CorsService), `extract_bearer_token` validation cascade returning `Result<String, BearerRejectReason>`, 401 short-circuit on rejection (with `mark_finished` flip + `WWW-Authenticate: Bearer` challenge + per-reason `text/plain` body) or `BearerToken` extension stash + inner delegation on success. Module-private `BearerRejectReason` enum (4 variants: `MissingHeader`, `NotAscii`, `MissingBearerPrefix`, `EmptyToken`) with `message(self) -> &'static str` method. Module-private `extract_bearer_token` (case-insensitive scheme match via `eq_ignore_ascii_case` on bytes; strict single-space separator; length gate `> "Bearer".len()` so `"Bearer "` reaches the empty-token branch) and `unauthorized_response` (builds 401 with WWW-Authenticate + Content-Type + per-reason body) helpers.
- `jolt-core/src/lib.rs` — added `pub mod auth_bearer;` declaration and `pub use auth_bearer::{AuthBearerLayer, AuthBearerService, BearerToken};` re-export. Slotted alphabetically before `cookie` / `cors` so the module-list ordering matches the re-export ordering.
- `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` — appended `auth_bearer` test module (NEW; sibling to the existing layer-scoped test bundles `parse_body` / `parse_body_string` / `parse_query`). Seven async tokio tests:
  1. `missing_authorization_header_short_circuits_with_401` (PRD-mandated; pins 401 + WWW-Authenticate: Bearer + text/plain + body == "Missing Authorization header" + finished latch + no stashed response + inner never invoked)
  2. `non_bearer_authorization_header_short_circuits_with_401` (Basic-scheme rejection → 401 + body == "Invalid Authorization header format: expected 'Bearer <token>'")
  3. `empty_bearer_token_short_circuits_with_401` (Bearer + space + nothing → 401 + body == "Empty bearer token")
  4. `non_ascii_authorization_header_short_circuits_with_401` (extended-byte header → 401 + body == "Authorization header is not valid ASCII"; header planted via `headers_mut().insert` with `HeaderValue::from_bytes` since the builder rejects non-ASCII)
  5. `valid_bearer_header_extracts_token_into_extensions` (happy path: valid header → BearerToken in extensions + inner runs + 200 response + finished latch UNTOUCHED)
  6. `case_insensitive_scheme_is_accepted` (loop over `["bearer", "BEARER", "BeArEr"]` to pin RFC 7235's case-insensitive scheme contract)
  7. `fresh_request_ext_is_injected_when_no_upstream_layer_set_one` (no Arc<RequestExt> upstream → layer injects one before flipping mark_finished; 401 still produced)
  Module-level `forbid_inner()` helper produces a `service_fn`-based service that panics if invoked, so any rejection-path test that accidentally delegates past the short-circuit crashes loudly rather than passing silently.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-071 passes: true.

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-072 (priority 72, phase16): "Validate JWT token using jolt_utils::jwt::decode with configured secret and algorithm. On failure (expired, bad signature), return 401 + mark_finished."** This is where the `BearerToken` stashed by 071 gets consumed. Two architectural questions to resolve in 072: (a) WHERE the JWT secret/algorithm config lives (likely a new `JwtConfig` carried by `AuthBearerLayer` or stashed in extensions by `JoltServer::start`); (b) WHETHER 072 extends `AuthBearerLayer` with config OR adds a separate `AuthJwtLayer` that follows AuthBearer in the stack. Recommend (b) — keeps the format validator stateless and lets a caller wire in just the format check (e.g. for a passthrough proxy that doesn't decode tokens itself). The `jolt-utils::jwt` module needs to be authored as part of the same iteration; currently `jolt-utils/src/lib.rs` is a stub.
- **JOLT-RS-073 (priority 73, phase16): "On success, parse claims into JwtClaims, inject into request extensions."** Builds on 072 by stashing the validated `JwtClaims` (newtype around `serde_json::Value` or a typed `Claims` struct) into extensions so handlers can pull it via `req.extensions().get::<JwtClaims>()`. Same newtype pattern `BearerToken` and `QueryParams` already established.
- **JOLT-RS-074 (priority 74, phase16): "Write auth unit tests: missing header, malformed header, wrong algorithm, expired token, valid token, custom claims."** Test bundle that closes phase16. Of the six PRD-mandated cases, two (missing header, malformed header) are already covered by 071's tests; 074 adds wrong-algorithm, expired-token, valid-token, custom-claims to round out the surface.
- **AutoMiddleware codegen has no wiring for AuthBearerLayer.** A user who derives `#[derive(AutoMiddleware)]` on a struct with an `auth: BearerToken` field still has no codegen path that splices `AuthBearerLayer` into the per-route stack. The wiring task (recognize `BearerToken` field type → emit `.layer(AuthBearerLayer::new())` in the per-route service builder) is unblocked by 071 but unscheduled in the PRD. Recommend filing a follow-up; out of scope for 071.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test bundle), 045 (endpoint-integration test), 054 (phase11 closing test), 062 (phase13 closing test bundle), 067 (phase14 closing test bundle), 069 (log format customization), 070 (debug body logging).** Same pre-046 holdouts plus 062/067 plus 069/070 (phase15 standard-impl items deferred behind 071's core-abstraction priority). Phase15 is now 1/3 done; phase16 is now 1/4 done (071 ✓; 072/073/074 pending). Recommendation: phase16 should land next (072/073/074) to close the auth surface, then phase15 closes (069/070), then the polish-bundle pass picks up 027/032/045/054/062/067.
- **First user-visible scope from 071 is purely additive** — three new public surfaces (`AuthBearerLayer`, `AuthBearerService`, `BearerToken`) join the existing layer surface. No existing API behavior changes. A caller who built against 068 sees no breakage from 071. The layer is opt-in (the user wires it into their tower stack); it is NOT auto-enabled by `JoltServer::start` (unlike TraceLayer in 068). A caller who wants global auth must add `.layer(AuthBearerLayer::new())` to their stack manually.


Iteration: 2026-05-10 (JOLT-RS-072 — AuthJwtLayer: JWT validation + 401 short-circuit)
PRD item: JOLT-RS-072 (priority 72, phase16-auth-bearer)
Description: "Validate JWT token using jolt_utils::jwt::decode with configured secret and algorithm. On failure (expired, bad signature), return 401 + mark_finished."
PRD verification: "Unit test: valid token → passes, expired token → 401."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish; JOLT-RS-054 phase11 closing test; JOLT-RS-062 phase13 closing test bundle; JOLT-RS-067 phase14 closing test bundle; JOLT-RS-069 log format customization; JOLT-RS-070 debug body logging): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" FIRST, before "integration points", "unknown unknowns", "standard implementation", and "polish"), 072 IS BOTH a new core abstraction (authoring the `jolt-utils::jwt` module from a stub plus typed `JwtDecodeError` variants) AND an integration point (wiring `jolt-utils` into `jolt-core` for the first time + composing AuthJwtLayer with the freshly-landed AuthBearerLayer from 071). 069/070 (phase15 logging customization) are standard-implementation slices building on 068's TraceLayer wiring; 027/032/045/054/062/067 remain test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies. The 071 progress note pre-pinned the recommended architecture for 072 (separate AuthJwtLayer rather than extending AuthBearerLayer with config), which 072 implements verbatim.

Implementation notes:
- **`jolt-utils::jwt` was authored from a stub.** `jolt-utils/src/lib.rs` was previously just a module-level docstring; 072 added `pub mod jwt;` and a full `jwt.rs` (181 lines) carrying `JwtConfig` (secret bytes + algorithm), `JwtClaims` (sub + exp + Option<iat>), `JwtDecodeError` (5 variants), and `decode(token, &config) -> Result<JwtClaims, JwtDecodeError>`. The `jolt-utils` Cargo.toml's existing `jsonwebtoken` dep was already in place from JOLT-RS-005 (workspace scaffold), so no Cargo.toml change to jolt-utils was needed.
- **Typed `JwtDecodeError` with 5 variants, NOT a single `Other(String)`.** Two considered shapes: (a) a single opaque error type wrapping `jsonwebtoken::errors::Error` (rejected — forces downstream consumers to parse free-form prose to distinguish "token expired" from "bad signature" for their 401 body; the AuthJwtLayer needs the discriminant to pick the right body string); (b) dedicated variants for the four common rejection paths (`Expired`, `InvalidSignature`, `InvalidAlgorithm`, `Malformed`) plus `Other(String)` for the catch-all (current — the variant IS the discriminant, so AuthJwtLayer's `match err { ... }` falls out naturally with no string-parsing). The `Other` variant preserves the upstream error's `Display` rendering so the catch-all 401 body still names the actual cause.
- **`Validation::validate_aud = false` is set explicitly.** `jsonwebtoken::Validation::new(alg)` defaults `validate_aud` to `true` with an empty audience set. Without a configured audience in `JwtConfig`, leaving `validate_aud: true` would reject tokens lacking an `aud` claim for the WRONG reason (since no audience expectation has been configured). Disable explicitly; a future iteration adds `JwtConfig.audience: Option<...>` and flips validation back on conditionally. Documented in the module rustdoc as decision 3.
- **`JwtConfig` holds raw secret bytes (HS-only initially), NOT a pre-built `DecodingKey`.** Two considered shapes: (a) `JwtConfig { key: DecodingKey, algorithm: Algorithm }` so any algorithm (HS/RS/ES) is supported by letting the caller build the key (rejected — `jsonwebtoken::DecodingKey` does NOT implement `Clone` or `Debug` in 9.3, so the `Layer: Clone + Debug` derives on `AuthJwtLayer` would need manual impls + an `Arc<DecodingKey>` wrap, and `Debug` would print `<opaque>`; net cost is heavier code with worse error messages); (b) `JwtConfig { secret: Vec<u8>, algorithm: Algorithm }` and build `DecodingKey::from_secret(&secret)` on each decode (current — Vec<u8> is Clone + Debug, the layer derives are free, and the build call is O(secret_len) but the secrets are typically <100 bytes). HS-only is a documented limitation; a future iteration adds an enum variant for PEM keys.
- **`AuthJwtLayer` requires `AuthBearerLayer` upstream; missing `BearerToken` produces a 401.** Two considered shapes: (a) fall back to extracting the bearer token directly from the `Authorization` header if no `BearerToken` is in extensions (rejected — duplicates AuthBearerLayer's logic; couples the two layers via header-read instead of via the typed extension key; means a misconfigured stack succeeds silently); (b) 401 with body `"Missing bearer token"` (current — the layering contract is explicit, and the 401 is ALSO the right caller-visible answer because no auth was performed). Both cases reaching this branch (operator forgot AuthBearerLayer; deployment wires AuthJwtLayer standalone) are correctly observed as auth failures from the caller's side. Documented in the module rustdoc as decision 2.
- **Parsed `JwtClaims` are stashed into extensions on success in 072, NOT deferred to 073.** Two considered shapes: (a) 072 calls decode and throws away the claims (so 073 implements the "extensions stash" step) (rejected — forces 073 to either re-call `jolt_utils::jwt::decode` (wasteful and re-verifies the signature twice) or expose half-validated state; either is heavier than just stashing once); (b) 072 calls decode AND stashes (current — the decode produces claims as a side product of validation, throwing them away is wasteful; the test for 072 just doesn't depend on the stash, while 073 will pin the extension-key contract with a dedicated test). Documented in the module rustdoc as decision 3.
- **`Arc<JwtConfig>` is held by the layer, NOT `JwtConfig` directly.** Two considered shapes: (a) `JwtConfig` directly in `AuthJwtLayer` (rejected — cloning the layer would copy the secret bytes per clone; tower's `ServiceBuilder` path clones layers internally, so the per-clone cost is non-zero); (b) `Arc<JwtConfig>` (current — clone cost is one atomic refcount bump regardless of secret size). `JwtConfig` itself is also `Clone`, so the `Arc` wrap is an optimization rather than a correctness need; documented as decision 4.
- **`WWW-Authenticate: Bearer error="invalid_token"` (RFC 6750 §3) discriminates 072 vs. 071's 401.** AuthBearerLayer (071) emits a bare `WWW-Authenticate: Bearer` challenge meaning "no credentials provided"; AuthJwtLayer (072) emits `Bearer error="invalid_token"` meaning "credentials provided but rejected". The 401 body STILL carries the per-reason text/plain message so callers can debug without parsing the WWW-Authenticate parameters. The challenge-parameter shape is the canonical RFC 6750 form for this case.
- **Module-private `JwtRejectReason` enum (NOT a public surface).** The rejection mechanism is an implementation detail; the contractual surface is the 401 BODY strings (which the tests pin verbatim). Keeping the enum private means a future iteration can change the variant set without breaking external callers.
- **`jsonwebtoken` is added as a jolt-core `[dev-dependencies]`, NOT as a runtime dep.** The auth_jwt test module needs to MINT signed tokens to test the decode path. `jolt-utils` already depends on `jsonwebtoken` for the decode side; rather than expose an `encode` helper on `jolt-utils::jwt`'s public surface just to satisfy a test (scope creep), `jolt-core` pulls `jsonwebtoken` as a dev-dep and uses its `encode` + `EncodingKey` directly in tests. End-to-end coverage: jolt-core's tests mint a token with jsonwebtoken::encode and validate it via jolt-utils's wrapper around jsonwebtoken::decode.
- **`JwtClaims` import in `auth_jwt.rs` is marked `#[allow(unused_imports)]`.** The type is referenced 4× in rustdoc links (`[JwtClaims]`) throughout the module but never named in code (only inferred as the `T` in `jwt::decode::<JwtClaims>`'s return). Removing the import would force every doc link to use a fully-qualified path; keeping it + the allow keeps the doc links resolvable with minimal noise.

Key decisions:
- **Separate `AuthJwtLayer` vs. extending `AuthBearerLayer` with config.** Documented above; the 071 progress note pre-pinned this and 072 implements it verbatim. Keeps AuthBearerLayer stateless and lets callers wire just format-check (e.g. for a passthrough proxy).
- **`JwtConfig` holds raw secret bytes (HS-only initially).** Documented above; pre-built `DecodingKey` was rejected because of its lack of Clone/Debug impls in jsonwebtoken 9.3.
- **Typed `JwtDecodeError` variants for downstream 401 disambiguation.** Documented above; matches the existing module ethos pinned in `auth_bearer.rs`'s `BearerRejectReason` ("dedicated variants so each rejection path produces a distinct body").
- **Stash claims in 072 (not 073).** Documented above; avoids re-decode in 073.
- **`Arc<JwtConfig>` for cheap cloning.** Documented above; layers must be Clone per tower's `ServiceBuilder` requirements.
- **6 jolt-core auth_jwt tests + 5 jolt-utils jwt tests, not just the two PRD-mandated cases.** Two considered shapes: (a) just the PRD-mandated `valid → passes` + `expired → 401` tests (rejected — would skip the bad-signature, malformed-token, missing-bearer-token, and fresh-RequestExt-injection paths; all four are load-bearing for 073+ and the AutoMiddleware codegen's eventual consumer); (b) 6 jolt-core layer tests + 5 jolt-utils decode tests covering the full surface (current — happy path, expired, bad signature, malformed, missing BearerToken, fresh RequestExt injection at the layer level; valid HS256, expired, wrong secret, malformed, algorithm mismatch at the decode helper level). Each test maps to a distinct contract pinned in the module rustdoc.
- **`request_with_bearer_token` helper in tests builds the request shape AuthBearerLayer would produce.** Plants both the `Arc<RequestExt>` and the `BearerToken` extension, simulating an upstream AuthBearerLayer having run. Centralizes the request-construction so each rejection-path test isn't 8 lines of header-builder boilerplate.

Files changed:
- `jolt-utils/src/jwt.rs` (NEW) — module rustdoc explains the architectural decisions (HS-only scope, typed error variants, `validate_aud=false`, exp/iat shape). `JwtConfig { secret: Vec<u8>, algorithm: Algorithm }` with `new(impl Into<Vec<u8>>, Algorithm)` constructor. `JwtClaims { sub: String, exp: usize, iat: Option<usize> }` with serde derives + `skip_serializing_if` on the optional iat. `JwtDecodeError` (5 variants: Expired, InvalidSignature, InvalidAlgorithm, Malformed, Other(String)) with Display + Error impls. `decode(token: &str, config: &JwtConfig) -> Result<JwtClaims, JwtDecodeError>` that builds DecodingKey + Validation (with validate_aud disabled), calls jsonwebtoken::decode, maps errors via `map_error` helper. Module-private `map_error(jsonwebtoken::errors::Error) -> JwtDecodeError` mapping the four recognized ErrorKinds to dedicated variants and catch-all to `Other`. `#[cfg(test)] mod tests` with 5 tests: valid HS256 round-trip, expired token rejection, wrong-secret rejection, malformed token rejection, algorithm mismatch rejection. Test helpers `now_secs()` and `sign_hs256(secret, claims)` shared across tests.
- `jolt-utils/src/lib.rs` — added `pub mod jwt;` declaration plus a module-level doc paragraph noting 072 landed the jwt module.
- `jolt-core/src/auth_jwt.rs` (NEW) — module rustdoc explains the six architectural decisions (two-layer split, missing-token-as-401, claims-stash in 072, `Arc<JwtConfig>` sharing, RFC 6750 error="invalid_token" challenge, preserve-or-inject `Arc<RequestExt>`). `AuthJwtLayer { config: Arc<JwtConfig> }` with `new(JwtConfig)` and `from_arc(Arc<JwtConfig>)` constructors. `AuthJwtService<S> { inner, config }` with `Service<AxumRequest>` impl: standard tower poll_ready/call swap, preserve-or-inject `Arc<RequestExt>`, fetch `BearerToken` from extensions (returning 401 with MissingBearerToken body if absent), call `jolt_utils::jwt::decode` (returning 401 with per-DecodeError body on failure), stash `JwtClaims` in extensions + delegate on success. Module-private `JwtRejectReason` enum (MissingBearerToken, DecodeFailed(JwtDecodeError)) with `body(self) -> String` method. Module-private `unauthorized_response(reason) -> Response` helper builds 401 with `WWW-Authenticate: Bearer error="invalid_token"` + Content-Type + per-reason body. `JwtClaims` import gated with `#[allow(unused_imports)]` so its rustdoc references resolve without forcing fully-qualified paths.
- `jolt-core/src/lib.rs` — added `pub mod auth_jwt;` declaration plus `pub use auth_jwt::{AuthJwtLayer, AuthJwtService};` and `pub use jolt_utils::jwt::{JwtClaims, JwtConfig, JwtDecodeError};` re-exports so user crates that consume AuthJwtLayer don't need a direct `jolt-utils` dep to build a `JwtConfig` or read a `JwtClaims` from extensions.
- `jolt-core/Cargo.toml` — added `jolt-utils = { path = "../jolt-utils" }` to `[dependencies]` (first time jolt-core depends on jolt-utils). Added `[dev-dependencies]` section with `jsonwebtoken = { workspace = true }` (used by the auth_jwt test module to mint signed test tokens directly; avoids exposing an `encode` helper on jolt-utils's public surface just for testing).
- `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` — appended `auth_jwt` test module (NEW; sibling to `auth_bearer` / `parse_body` / `parse_query`). Six async tokio tests:
  1. `valid_jwt_passes_through_and_inner_runs` (PRD-mandated half 1: valid token → passes; also pins JwtClaims-in-extensions + finished latch UNTOUCHED + inner-service-invoked + sub echoed in response body)
  2. `expired_jwt_short_circuits_with_401` (PRD-mandated half 2: expired token → 401; also pins WWW-Authenticate `Bearer error="invalid_token"` challenge + text/plain Content-Type + body == "Token has expired" + finished latch + inner-never-invoked)
  3. `invalid_signature_jwt_short_circuits_with_401` (wrong-secret rejection → 401 + body == "Invalid token signature")
  4. `malformed_jwt_short_circuits_with_401` (non-JWT bearer token string → 401 + body == "Malformed token")
  5. `missing_bearer_token_short_circuits_with_401` (no BearerToken in extensions → 401 + body == "Missing bearer token"; pins the AuthBearerLayer-required contract)
  6. `fresh_request_ext_is_injected_when_no_upstream_layer_set_one` (mirrors AuthBearerService's preserve-or-inject pattern)
  Module-level `forbid_inner()` helper produces a service_fn-based service that panics if invoked, so any rejection-path test that accidentally delegates past the short-circuit crashes loudly. Module-level `request_with_bearer_token(&token, request_ext)` helper builds the simulated post-AuthBearerLayer request shape (Arc<RequestExt> + BearerToken extensions populated).
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-072 passes: true.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..071 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory; this is a pure Rust workspace). Cargo is the verification tool.

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-073 (priority 73, phase16): "On success, parse claims into JwtClaims, inject into request extensions (req.extensions_mut().insert(claims))."** The claims-stash is ALREADY implemented as part of 072 (decision 3 in the module rustdoc); 073 is now reduced to a verification-only slice. Recommended shape for 073: add a dedicated test that asserts the extension-key contract independently of the decode path (e.g. `valid_jwt_stashes_typed_claims_via_extension_key_jwtclaims`), and optionally rename or refine the claims type if 074's "custom claims" coverage requires a generic surface. The 073 implementation work is essentially nil; the verification cost is one new test.
- **JOLT-RS-074 (priority 74, phase16): "Write auth unit tests: missing header, malformed header, wrong algorithm, expired token, valid token, custom claims."** Test bundle that closes phase16. Of the six PRD-mandated cases: missing header (covered by 071's `missing_authorization_header_short_circuits_with_401`), malformed header (covered by 071's `non_bearer_authorization_header_short_circuits_with_401`), wrong algorithm (covered by 072's jolt-utils `decode_algorithm_mismatch_yields_invalid_algorithm_variant`), expired token (covered by 072's `expired_jwt_short_circuits_with_401`), valid token (covered by 072's `valid_jwt_passes_through_and_inner_runs`). Only "custom claims" remains uncovered — 074 needs to add either a generic `JwtClaims<C>` surface OR a `serde_json::Map` flatten field on the current `JwtClaims` struct, plus a test that exercises a custom claim like `role: String` round-tripping through encode/decode.
- **`AuthJwtLayer` is not yet wired into `JoltServer::start` or `AutoMiddleware` codegen.** A user who wants global JWT auth must compose `JoltServer::new().build_serving_router(Router::new().layer(AuthBearerLayer::new()).layer(AuthJwtLayer::new(config)))` manually. The wiring task — recognize a `claims: JwtClaims` field on a struct deriving `AutoMiddleware` and splice both layers into the per-route stack — is unblocked by 072 but unscheduled in the PRD. Recommend filing a follow-up; out of scope for 072.
- **HS-only scope is a documented limitation.** RS256/RS384/RS512 (PEM-keyed asymmetric algorithms) require a different `DecodingKey` constructor (`from_rsa_pem`); same for ES256/ES384 (`from_ec_pem`). A future iteration should extend `JwtConfig` from `{ secret: Vec<u8>, algorithm: Algorithm }` to either a `key: DecodingKey, algorithm: Algorithm` shape (forcing manual Clone/Debug impls because jsonwebtoken's `DecodingKey` lacks them) OR an enum like `JwtKey { Hs(Vec<u8>), Rsa(Vec<u8>), Ec(Vec<u8>) }` so the layer can dispatch to the right `DecodingKey::from_*` constructor at decode time. Recommend the enum form; the manual impls have a worse `Debug` rendering and force every caller into the `DecodingKey` API.
- **`validate_aud = false` is a temporary safety knob.** When `JwtConfig` grows an `audience: Option<HashSet<String>>` field (likely 074 or later), the validation should be re-enabled conditionally so audience-bound tokens are checked properly. Documented in the module rustdoc.
- **The five `jolt-utils::jwt` tests are the first tests in the `jolt-utils` crate.** Previous PRD items (JOLT-RS-005 workspace scaffold) created the crate but no tests had been added before 072. The `cargo test -p jolt-utils` invocation now produces real output; before 072 it produced "0 passed" silently.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test bundle), 045 (endpoint-integration test), 054 (phase11 closing test), 062 (phase13 closing test bundle), 067 (phase14 closing test bundle), 069 (log format customization), 070 (debug body logging).** Same pre-046 holdouts plus 062/067 plus 069/070. Phase15 is now 1/3 done; phase16 is now 2/4 done (071 ✓, 072 ✓; 073/074 pending). Recommendation: phase16 should close next (073/074, both small slices given 072's claims-stash and overlapping test coverage), then phase15 closes (069/070), then the polish-bundle pass picks up 027/032/045/054/062/067.
- **First user-visible scope from 072 is two new public types (`AuthJwtLayer`, `AuthJwtService`) on `jolt-core`'s surface plus three re-exports (`JwtClaims`, `JwtConfig`, `JwtDecodeError`).** No existing API behavior changes. A caller who built against 071 sees no breakage from 072. The layer is opt-in (the user wires it into their tower stack after `AuthBearerLayer`); it is NOT auto-enabled by `JoltServer::start`. A caller who wants global JWT auth must add `.layer(AuthBearerLayer::new()).layer(AuthJwtLayer::new(config))` to their stack manually — the wiring order matters because AuthBearerLayer stashes the BearerToken that AuthJwtLayer consumes.

JOLT-RS-073: claims-in-extensions contract test (phase16 closing slice 1/2)
Date: 2026-05-10
================================================================================

PRD item completed: JOLT-RS-073 "On success, parse claims into JwtClaims, inject into request extensions (req.extensions_mut().insert(claims))." Verification: "Unit test: valid token → JwtClaims available via req.extensions().get::<JwtClaims>()."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (027/032/045/054/062/067 polish; 069/070 phase15 logging customization; 074 phase16 closing test bundle; 075+ phase17 WS auth): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" FIRST), 073 pins the extension-key contract — the typed handle that 074's "custom claims" bundle and 077's "inject JwtClaims into the WS handler" slice both build on. The 072 progress note pre-pinned the recommended shape ("add a dedicated test that asserts the extension-key contract independently of the decode path") and noted "the 073 implementation work is essentially nil; the verification cost is one new test"; 073 implements that verbatim. 027/032/045/054/062/067 remain test-bundle polish (lower architectural urgency); 069/070 are standard-implementation slices building on 068's TraceLayer wiring; 074 needs a new abstraction (generic JwtClaims<C> or serde_json::Map flatten) for the "custom claims" half and was deferred until the typed-claims contract is independently pinned by 073.

Implementation notes:
- **073 is a pure verification slice: zero production-code change.** The claims-stash is implemented at `jolt-core/src/auth_jwt.rs:213` (the `Ok(claims) => req.extensions_mut().insert(claims)` arm in `AuthJwtService::call`), which 072 landed alongside its decode call (072 decision 3 in the module rustdoc). 073's contribution is a dedicated test that pins the extension-key contract independently of any response-body echo: a downstream consumer fetches the claims via `req.extensions().get::<JwtClaims>()` and the test asserts that EACH FIELD (sub, exp, iat) round-trips verbatim from the minted token.
- **Distinct from the existing 072 happy-path test.** `valid_jwt_passes_through_and_inner_runs` (072) reads `claims.sub` and echoes it as the response body, so it pins "sub is accessible via the typed key" implicitly. 073's new test pins the FULL contract: all three fields preserved verbatim, captured through a side channel (`Arc<Mutex<Option<JwtClaims>>>`) rather than the response body so the assertion focuses on the extension key itself rather than serialization-through-HTTP. Two considered shapes: (a) extend the existing 072 test to assert all three fields (rejected — would conflate the "happy-path passes" assertion with the "extension-key contract" assertion; the two cover distinct contracts and a regression in one shouldn't crash the other); (b) dedicated 073 test (current — keeps each test single-purpose, makes the PRD-mandated 073 verification self-evident in test output).
- **Side-channel capture (Arc<Mutex<Option<JwtClaims>>>) over response-body serialization.** Two considered shapes: (a) serialize the full JwtClaims to JSON in the response body and parse it back in the test (rejected — adds a serde dep on the test path that 072 doesn't already need; and a serde round-trip is its own behavior, not the extension-key contract under test); (b) capture the claims in a side-channel Mutex shared between the inner service closure and the test body (current — the test asserts each field directly against the typed JwtClaims value, no serialization in the path). The Arc<Mutex<...>> indirection is the conventional Rust pattern for this kind of capture; the `tower::service_fn` closure form (already in use elsewhere in this test module) accepts the Arc cleanly.
- **Distinctive sub/exp/iat values prevent false positives.** Test uses `"user-073-extension-key"` as `sub`, `now_secs() + 7200` as `exp`, and `now_secs()` as `iat`. A bug that hard-coded a default JwtClaims in the layer would surface as a field mismatch in the assertion; using non-default values for all three fields ensures the test cannot pass against a stub implementation.
- **No production-code change AND no Cargo.toml change.** The 073 slice is the most targeted change possible: one new `#[tokio::test]` function appended to the existing `auth_jwt` test module in `jolt-core/src/tests.rs`. No new helpers, no new modules, no new deps. Reuses the existing `sign_hs256`, `now_secs`, and `request_with_bearer_token` helpers from 072.
- **Test name `valid_jwt_stashes_typed_claims_via_extension_key_jwtclaims` names the contract verbatim.** The PRD-mandated verification is "JwtClaims available via req.extensions().get::<JwtClaims>()"; the test name spells out "typed claims" (clarifying that the contract is over the typed `JwtClaims` extension key, not just any extension) and the JwtClaims type name (as the literal extension key being tested). Long name, but the contract surface is precise.

Key decisions:
- **073 is verification-only; production code already correct.** Documented above; 072 pre-implemented the claims-stash (decision 3 in 072's module rustdoc explicitly notes "Stashing in 072 (rather than 073) avoids a wasted re-decode... The JOLT-RS-073 slice closes the contract by pinning the extension-key behavior with a dedicated test"). 073 honors that pre-pinned contract.
- **Dedicated 073 test, not an extension to 072's happy-path test.** Documented above; single-purpose tests are easier to bisect when a future change breaks one contract but not the other.
- **Side-channel capture via Arc<Mutex<...>> rather than serde round-trip.** Documented above; keeps the assertion focused on the extension-key contract.

Files changed:
- `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` — appended one new `#[tokio::test]` to the `auth_jwt` module: `valid_jwt_stashes_typed_claims_via_extension_key_jwtclaims`. The test mints a HS256 token with distinctive sub ("user-073-extension-key"), exp (now+7200), and iat (now) values; runs through `AuthJwtLayer`; captures the stashed `JwtClaims` from `req.extensions().get::<JwtClaims>()` in an `Arc<Mutex<Option<JwtClaims>>>` inside the inner `tower::service_fn`; asserts each field round-trips verbatim (sub, exp, iat=Some(now)). No new helpers — reuses `sign_hs256`, `now_secs`, and `request_with_bearer_token` from 072.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-073 passes: true.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..072 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory; this is a pure Rust workspace). Cargo is the verification tool.

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-074 (priority 74, phase16): "Write auth unit tests: missing header, malformed header, wrong algorithm, expired token, valid token, custom claims."** Test bundle that closes phase16. Of the six PRD-mandated cases, five are already covered: missing header (071's `missing_authorization_header_short_circuits_with_401`), malformed header (071's `non_bearer_authorization_header_short_circuits_with_401`), wrong algorithm (072's jolt-utils `decode_algorithm_mismatch_yields_invalid_algorithm_variant`), expired token (072's `expired_jwt_short_circuits_with_401`), valid token (072's `valid_jwt_passes_through_and_inner_runs` + 073's `valid_jwt_stashes_typed_claims_via_extension_key_jwtclaims`).
