================================================================================
JOLT-RS-074: phase16 closing test bundle + custom-claims extension on JwtClaims
Date: 2026-05-10
================================================================================

PRD item completed: JOLT-RS-074 (priority 74, phase16-auth-bearer) — "Write auth unit tests: missing header, malformed header, wrong algorithm, expired token, valid token, custom claims." PRD verification: "cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::auth passes."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (027 port-binding polish; 032 endpoint-registry test bundle; 045 endpoint-integration test; 054 phase11 closing test; 062 phase13 closing test bundle; 067 phase14 closing test bundle; 069 log format customization; 070 debug body logging; 075–077 phase17 WS auth): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" FIRST), 074 carries the only outstanding architectural surface in phase16 — extending `JwtClaims` with a custom-claims extension point. Five of the six PRD-mandated cases (missing header, malformed header, wrong algorithm, expired token, valid token) were already pinned by tests landed in 071/072/073 (verbatim list reproduced from 073's blockers note); only "custom claims" remained uncovered AND required a new abstraction (either a generic `JwtClaims<C>` or a `#[serde(flatten)]` extra map). Closing phase16 first also unblocks 077 ("inject JwtClaims into WS handler"), which depends on the JwtClaims shape being stable. 069/070 are standard-implementation slices on top of 068's TraceLayer; 027/032/045/054/062/067 remain polish; 075–077 don't open phase17 until the JwtClaims surface is settled.

Implementation notes:
- **Chose form (b): `#[serde(flatten)] extra: serde_json::Map<String, serde_json::Value>` over a generic `JwtClaims<C: DeserializeOwned>`.** The 073 blockers note prescribed form (b) as the smaller diff that preserves 072/073 callers; form (a) would have required `JwtClaims<()>` as the existing-API path everywhere `JwtClaims` is named (auth_jwt.rs's `#[allow(unused_imports)] use jolt_utils::jwt::JwtClaims`, the request-extension key lookup, every test construction site, every rustdoc link target). Form (b) only adds one field — existing struct literal constructions stay structurally identical aside from a new `extra: serde_json::Map::new()` line per site, and the request-extension key (`req.extensions().get::<JwtClaims>()`) stays unchanged. Downstream handlers gain `claims.extra.get("role")` without having to redefine the struct.
- **`serde_json::Map<String, serde_json::Value>` over `std::collections::HashMap<String, Value>`.** The `serde_json::Map` re-export is the canonical container for "values keyed by JSON property name"; matches the type `serde_json` produces when deserializing a JSON object into an unstructured `Value::Object`. No functional difference for the 074 surface, but consistent with the rest of the serde_json ecosystem. `Map` is `Default`-implements-empty, so the `#[serde(flatten)]` deserialization path produces an empty map (no extra keys present in JSON) without needing an explicit `#[serde(default)]` annotation on the field.
- **No `#[serde(default)]` on the new field — `#[serde(flatten)]` alone is sufficient.** When the JWT payload has no keys beyond `sub`/`exp`/`iat`, serde's flatten visitor sees an empty residual key set and constructs `Map::new()` directly. Adding `#[serde(default)]` would be redundant and could mask a real deserialization error (a future field rename that makes `extra` no longer flatten-targetable). Two existing tests pin the empty-extra contract: `decode_valid_hs256_token_returns_claims` asserts `out.extra.is_empty()` after a no-custom-claims round trip, and the new 074 test asserts the explicit fields (`sub`/`exp`/`iat`) do NOT double-up in extra.
- **PRD verification (`cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::auth passes`) is interpreted to cover the broader `tests::auth_*` family (`tests::auth_bearer` from 071 + `tests::auth_jwt` from 072/073/074), not just a module literally named `tests::auth`.** The PRD-mandated `tests::auth` prefix matches both `tests::auth_bearer` and `tests::auth_jwt` via cargo's `--` substring filter, so the verification command runs all 14 auth-related unit tests across the two modules (6 from 071, 7 from 072/073 + 1 new for 074 = 8 in auth_jwt). All 14 pass.
- **End-to-end coverage in BOTH crates, not just one.** The new custom-claims test lives in two places: (i) jolt-utils' `decode_token_with_custom_claims_surfaces_them_in_extra` pins the encode-decode round-trip at the lowest level (mints a token with `role`/`scopes`/`tenant_id` custom claims, decodes it, asserts each surfaces in `claims.extra` AND that the explicit `sub`/`exp`/`iat` fields do NOT double up); (ii) jolt-core's `valid_jwt_with_custom_claims_surfaces_extra_in_extension` pins the same contract end-to-end through the `AuthJwtLayer` (mints a token, runs the tower stack, captures the stashed `JwtClaims` via a side-channel `Arc<Mutex<Option<JwtClaims>>>` inside the inner service, asserts `claims.extra.get("role")` / `claims.extra.get("scopes")` round-trip). Two layers of coverage because the custom-claims surface is a JOINT contract of the jolt-utils decoder AND the jolt-core layer's extension-stash code path; a regression in either side surfaces in only one test.
- **Side-channel capture via `Arc<Mutex<Option<JwtClaims>>>` in the jolt-core test follows the JOLT-RS-073 pattern verbatim.** The 073 progress note documented two considered shapes: (a) serialize JwtClaims to the response body and parse back in the test, (b) capture in a side-channel Mutex shared between inner closure and test body. Form (b) keeps the assertion focused on the extension-key contract rather than on serialization-through-HTTP, and reuses the well-established `tower::service_fn`-with-cloned-Arc idiom already used by 073's `valid_jwt_stashes_typed_claims_via_extension_key_jwtclaims`. Diff-minimizing choice: 074's test mirrors 073's test shape, only changing the minted-claim values and the assertions on `extra`.
- **Distinctive minted values prevent false positives.** Test uses `"role": "admin"` (string), `"scopes": ["read", "write", "admin"]` (array), `"tenant_id": 42` (number — in jolt-utils only; jolt-core's test uses just role+scopes to keep the diff focused) so the assertions are over three distinct JSON value types. A bug that hard-coded a string-only extra surface would surface in the array/number assertions.
- **Five-site struct-literal update with no logic change.** The added `extra: serde_json::Map::new(),` line is appended to every existing JwtClaims construction site (4 in jolt-core/src/tests.rs, 4 in jolt-utils/src/jwt.rs — eight sites total). No site needed to change other fields; this is the smallest possible diff for adding a public struct field.
- **Module docs decision 4 was revised, and decision 5 was added.** The previous decision 4 ended with "JOLT-RS-074 (auth test bundle) can extend the surface with a generic `JwtClaims<C>` if custom claims are needed there." That note was stale once 074 landed form (b); the revised decision 4 drops the JOLT-RS-074 forward reference, and the new decision 5 documents the actual chosen shape ("Custom claims land in JwtClaims::extra via `#[serde(flatten)]` (JOLT-RS-074)"). The rustdoc on `JwtClaims` itself was also updated to reference decisions 4 AND 5 (not just 4).

Key decisions:
- **Form (b) `#[serde(flatten)] extra: Map<String, Value>` over form (a) generic `JwtClaims<C>`.** Documented above; the 073 blockers note pre-pinned form (b) as the smaller diff. Form (a) would have rippled through `auth_jwt.rs`, every rustdoc link, every test construction site, every request-extension lookup; form (b) only adds one field.
- **No `#[serde(default)]` on the flatten target.** Documented above; redundant given Map's empty default, and could mask a future rename regression.
- **Two-layer coverage (jolt-utils decode + jolt-core AuthJwtLayer).** Documented above; the custom-claims contract is a joint contract of both, so the test bundle pins both ends.
- **PRD verification interpretation: `tests::auth` filter matches both `tests::auth_bearer` and `tests::auth_jwt`.** Documented above; cargo's substring filter resolves the PRD-mandated command to all 14 auth-related tests.

Files changed:
- `jolt-utils/src/jwt.rs` — added `extra: serde_json::Map<String, serde_json::Value>` field with `#[serde(flatten)]` on `JwtClaims`; added `use serde_json::{Map as JsonMap, Value as JsonValue}` import; updated all 4 existing test construction sites to include `extra: JsonMap::new()`; added new test `decode_token_with_custom_claims_surfaces_them_in_extra` exercising role/scopes/tenant_id custom claims round-tripping through encode→decode; revised module docs decision 4 (dropped stale JOLT-RS-074 forward reference) and added decision 5 ("Custom claims land in JwtClaims::extra via #[serde(flatten)]").
- `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` — updated all 4 existing JwtClaims literal construction sites in the `auth_jwt` test module to include `extra: serde_json::Map::new()`; appended new test `valid_jwt_with_custom_claims_surfaces_extra_in_extension` that runs the AuthJwtLayer with a custom-claims-bearing token, captures the stashed JwtClaims via a side-channel `Arc<Mutex<Option<JwtClaims>>>`, and asserts `role` (string) and `scopes` (array) surface verbatim through `claims.extra`.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-074 passes: true.

Verification:
- `cargo build --workspace` → clean, 1.90s (jolt-utils + jolt-core recompile only).
- `cargo test -p jolt-utils` → 6 passed (was 5; +1 new for 074: `decode_token_with_custom_claims_surfaces_them_in_extra`).
- `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::auth_jwt` → 8 passed (was 7; +1 new for 074: `valid_jwt_with_custom_claims_surfaces_extra_in_extension`).
- `cargo test --workspace` → 161 jolt-core unit (was 160; +1 new for 074) + 6 auto_middleware_derive integration + 9 inventory_registration integration + 130 jolt-macros unit + 6 jolt-utils unit (was 5; +1 new for 074) = 312 tests pass (was 310; +2 new for 074); no regressions in any sibling crate.
- `cargo clippy -p jolt-utils --all-targets` → 0 warnings (first all-targets clippy run with the new field; clean).
- `cargo clippy -p jolt-core --all-targets` → same 2 pre-existing baseline warnings (`new_without_default` on `RequestExt` and `JoltServer`); 0 new warnings.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..073 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory; this is a pure Rust workspace). Cargo is the verification tool.

Blockers / next notes:
- **Phase16 (auth-bearer) is now CLOSED: all four items (071 ✓, 072 ✓, 073 ✓, 074 ✓) pass.** No phase16 followups remain. JwtClaims's public surface is now `{ sub: String, exp: usize, iat: Option<usize>, extra: serde_json::Map<String, serde_json::Value> }`. The two-layer auth stack (`AuthBearerLayer` → `AuthJwtLayer`) is wired and tested. Downstream consumers reach the parsed claims via `req.extensions().get::<JwtClaims>()` and the custom claims via `claims.extra.get(<key>)`.
- **Phase17 (auth-websocket) is now UNBLOCKED.** 075 ("extract token from Sec-WebSocket-Protocol header"), 076 ("validate token before WS upgrade"), 077 ("inject JwtClaims into the WS handler") can now build against a stable JwtClaims shape. 077 in particular consumes the JwtClaims surface 074 just settled — the custom-claims `extra` map will surface through the WS handler the same way it surfaces through HTTP handlers, which is the right contract.
- **`AuthJwtLayer` is still NOT wired into `JoltServer::start` or `AutoMiddleware` codegen.** Carried over from 073's note. Callers compose `JoltServer::new().build_serving_router(Router::new().layer(AuthBearerLayer::new()).layer(AuthJwtLayer::new(config)))` manually. The wiring task — recognize a `claims: JwtClaims` field on a struct deriving `AutoMiddleware` and splice both layers into the per-route stack — is unblocked but unscheduled in the PRD. Recommend filing a follow-up.
- **HS-only scope is still a documented limitation.** Same as 072's note; carried forward. RS/ES algorithms need a different `DecodingKey` constructor.
- **`validate_aud = false` is still a temporary safety knob.** Same as 072's note; flip back on conditionally when `JwtConfig` grows an `audience` field.

A caller who only consumes `JwtClaims` from extensions (`req.extensions().get::<JwtClaims>()`) sees no breakage; existing `claims.sub` / `claims.exp` / `claims.iat` accesses continue to work, and the new `claims.extra` access is opt-in. JOLT-RS-075: Sec-WebSocket-Protocol jolt-jwt token extractor (phase17 opening slice 1/3)
Date: 2026-05-10
================================================================================

PRD item completed: JOLT-RS-075 (priority 75, phase17-auth-websocket) — "Extract token from Sec-WebSocket-Protocol request header (format: 'jolt-jwt, <token>')." PRD verification: "Unit test: header 'jolt-jwt, eyJ...' → extracted token 'eyJ...'."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (027 port-binding-conflict polish; 032 endpoint-registry test bundle; 045 endpoint-integration test; 054 phase11 closing test; 062 phase13 closing test bundle; 067 phase14 closing test bundle; 069 log format customization; 070 debug body logging; 076–077 phase17 closing slices; 078–081 phase18 early-termination; 082+ phase19+ db): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" FIRST, then "integration points", "unknown unknowns", "standard implementation", "polish"), 075 IS BOTH a new core abstraction (opens the `auth_websocket` module from scratch with the `JOLT_JWT_SUBPROTOCOL` constant + `WsTokenRejectReason` enum + `WsJwtToken` newtype that 076 and 077 will both build on) AND an integration point (introduces the WebSocket subprotocol contract — first WS infrastructure in the workspace, the WS auth surface the AutoMiddleware codegen and JoltServer::start will eventually compose). 069/070 (phase15 logging customization) are standard-implementation slices building on 068's TraceLayer wiring; 027/032/045/054/062/067 remain test-bundle polish; 076–077 depend on 075's helper + extension-key types (cannot land first). Closing 075 first opens phase17 with the abstraction settled so 076's tower::Layer slice and 077's WS handler injection can build against a stable surface.

Implementation notes:
- **`auth_websocket` module authored from scratch.** Previously the workspace had ZERO WebSocket-related code (`grep -i websocket` only matched the lib.rs header docstring); 075 lands `jolt-core/src/auth_websocket.rs` (193 lines) with the module rustdoc explaining the seven architectural decisions, the `JOLT_JWT_SUBPROTOCOL: &str = "jolt-jwt"` constant, the `WsTokenRejectReason` enum (5 variants: MissingHeader, NotAscii, MissingJoltJwtPrefix, EmptyToken, MalformedSubprotocols), the `WsJwtToken(pub String)` newtype with `.as_str()`, and the `extract_jwt_token(Option<&HeaderValue>) -> Result<String, WsTokenRejectReason>` helper. No new dependencies; uses the existing `axum::http::HeaderValue` already in the workspace.
- **Strict "exactly two comma-separated subprotocols" parse.** Two considered shapes: (a) `splitn(2, ',')` so any trailing commas are absorbed into the token (rejected — JWTs cannot contain commas (they are dot-separated base64url chunks), so any extra comma after the second value means the client offered another subprotocol and the token slot is ambiguous); (b) `split(',')` and require exactly 2 parts (current — rejects "jolt-jwt, eyJ..., graphql-ws" with the dedicated `MalformedSubprotocols` variant rather than silently accepting "eyJ..., graphql-ws" as a JWT). Browsers calling `new WebSocket(url, ["jolt-jwt", "<token>"])` produce exactly 2 subprotocols, matching the strict shape.
- **`jolt-jwt` literal match is case-sensitive.** Two considered shapes: (a) case-insensitive (rejected — RFC 6455 §11.5 declares subprotocol identifiers as opaque tokens matched against the IANA registry, with case-sensitive comparison being the convention; this is DIFFERENT from RFC 7235 §2.1's case-insensitive HTTP scheme name match, which is why AuthBearerLayer (071) accepts "Bearer"/"bearer"/"BEARER" but this layer does NOT accept "JOLT-JWT"); (b) case-sensitive (current — matches RFC 6455 §11.5 conventions). The case-insensitive-vs-sensitive split between the HTTP and WS auth layers is documented in module rustdoc decision 3 with a cross-reference to AuthBearerLayer.
- **Deviation from the original Zig implementation.** The Zig `parseWsJWT` (`src/middleware/auth.zig:151-207`) treats the ENTIRE `sec-websocket-protocol` header value as the JWT (no "jolt-jwt, " marker prefix). The PRD explicitly chose the more conventional canonical form ("jolt-jwt, <token>" with a marker subprotocol), which matches the WebSocket-spec-compliant pattern of the first subprotocol naming what's coming and the second carrying the payload. This is documented in spec_rust.md decision 3 ("Jolt extracts JWT from the Sec-WebSocket-Protocol header. Same approach in Rust — the WS upgrade handler validates the token before upgrading."); the PRD's "jolt-jwt, <token>" literal format is the Rust port's canonical form.
- **Five rejection variants (NOT a single Other(String)).** Mirrors the `BearerRejectReason` (071) and `JwtDecodeError` (072) split: a dedicated variant per rejection path means JOLT-RS-076's tower::Layer can produce a distinct 401 body per reason without parsing free-form prose. Each variant's `text/plain` body is pinned in 075's tests so 076 can re-use the exact strings.
- **`message()` is `pub` on `WsTokenRejectReason`.** Two considered shapes: (a) module-private `message()` like the auth_bearer/auth_jwt variants (would force JOLT-RS-076 to add its own body-mapping table OR re-export the enum and a separate body fn from 076's module) (rejected — the body strings are part of the rejection contract since the test bundle pins them, so they belong with the enum); (b) `pub` on `message()` (current — 076's tower::Layer calls `reason.message()` directly when building the 401 response). Slightly wider public surface than the HTTP siblings but justified by the tighter slice boundary.
- **`WsJwtToken` extension-key type lands in 075, NOT 076.** Two considered shapes: (a) define WsJwtToken in 076's future module (rejected — defers a small definitional decision to a slice that is supposed to focus on layer-wiring; means 075's surface ends mid-abstraction); (b) define it in 075 alongside the extractor (current — the type EXISTS as a public API after 075 lands, even though no production code inserts it into extensions yet; mirrors how `BearerToken` was defined alongside `AuthBearerLayer` in JOLT-RS-071 even though 072+ is what reads the extension key). Documented as decision 7 in the module rustdoc.
- **Whitespace tolerance via `.trim()` not `.trim_start_matches(' ')`.** RFC 7230 §7 BWS allows tabs as well as spaces around list separators; `.trim()` covers both. Test pins the spaces case (which is what real clients emit) but the underlying tolerance is broader.
- **Re-export shape under `extract_jwt_token as extract_ws_jwt_token`.** The internal name is `extract_jwt_token` (clear within the `auth_websocket` module since the module name disambiguates), but at the `jolt_core` crate root the broader name `extract_ws_jwt_token` is unambiguous next to the existing JWT-related re-exports (`JwtClaims`, `JwtConfig`, `AuthJwtLayer`). Same renaming pattern that `parse_query::extract` uses (`extract as extract_query`) at the lib.rs root.

Key decisions:
- **Open `auth_websocket` module in 075 with all shared types (constant, enum, newtype) so 076/077 just add wiring.** Documented above; mirrors the JOLT-RS-071 pattern of defining `BearerToken` alongside `AuthBearerLayer`.
- **Strict "exactly two subprotocols" parse with dedicated `MalformedSubprotocols` variant.** Documented above; JWT structure (no commas) makes any third value ambiguous.
- **Case-sensitive `jolt-jwt` literal match (per RFC 6455 §11.5).** Documented above; deliberately differs from AuthBearerLayer's case-insensitive scheme match.
- **`message()` is `pub` on the rejection enum.** Documented above; the body strings are part of the contract pinned by the tests.

Files changed:
- `jolt-core/src/auth_websocket.rs` (NEW) — module rustdoc explains the seven architectural decisions (layer scope, exactly-2-subprotocols, case-sensitive marker, BWS tolerance, empty-token rejection, non-ASCII rejection, extension-key handle). `JOLT_JWT_SUBPROTOCOL` constant. `WsJwtToken(pub String)` newtype with `.as_str()` (mirrors `BearerToken` at `jolt-core/src/auth_bearer.rs:93`). `WsTokenRejectReason` enum with 5 variants + `pub fn message(self) -> &'static str` mapping to canonical 401 body strings. `extract_jwt_token(Option<&HeaderValue>) -> Result<String, WsTokenRejectReason>` validates the canonical "jolt-jwt, <token>" shape and returns the bare token string.
- `jolt-core/src/lib.rs` — added `pub mod auth_websocket;` declaration plus a re-export block: `pub use auth_websocket::{extract_jwt_token as extract_ws_jwt_token, WsJwtToken, WsTokenRejectReason, JOLT_JWT_SUBPROTOCOL};` so user crates that consume the WS auth pieces don't need a direct module path.
- `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` — appended `auth_websocket` test module (NEW; sibling to `auth_bearer` / `auth_jwt`). Ten tests:
  1. `extract_jwt_token_canonical_shape_yields_token` (PRD-mandated: header "jolt-jwt, eyJ..." → token "eyJ..."; uses a distinctive 3-chunk JWT-shaped string `SAMPLE_JWT` so a stub returning empty/substring would fail)
  2. `extract_jwt_token_no_space_after_comma_yields_token` (BWS-free shape "jolt-jwt,eyJ..." still extracts)
  3. `extract_jwt_token_extra_whitespace_around_comma_yields_token` (RFC 7230 §7 BWS tolerance: spaces before AND after the comma both trim away)
  4. `extract_jwt_token_missing_header_yields_missing_header_variant` (None header → MissingHeader variant + canonical body string pinned)
  5. `extract_jwt_token_non_ascii_header_yields_not_ascii_variant` (extended-ASCII byte 0xC3 round-trips through HeaderValue::from_bytes but fails to_str → NotAscii)
  6. `extract_jwt_token_wrong_marker_yields_missing_jolt_jwt_prefix_variant` (wrong marker AND wrong-case marker both rejected with MissingJoltJwtPrefix; pins the case-sensitivity decision)
  7. `extract_jwt_token_solo_marker_yields_missing_jolt_jwt_prefix_variant` (header is just "jolt-jwt" with no comma — even the right marker alone is rejected as malformed)
  8. `extract_jwt_token_empty_token_after_marker_yields_empty_token_variant` (header is "jolt-jwt," and "jolt-jwt, " — both yield EmptyToken; whitespace-only token slot trims to empty)
  9. `extract_jwt_token_more_than_two_subprotocols_yields_malformed_variant` (three comma-separated subprotocols → MalformedSubprotocols + canonical body string pinned)
  10. `ws_jwt_token_newtype_exposes_borrowed_str` (pins WsJwtToken's tuple-ctor + as_str borrow + Clone/PartialEq derives)
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-075 passes: true.

Verification:

- `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::auth_websocket` → 10 passed (all 10 new for 075). The PRD-mandated `extract_jwt_token_canonical_shape_yields_token` test maps directly to the PRD verification ("header 'jolt-jwt, eyJ...' → extracted token 'eyJ...'").

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-076 (priority 76, phase17): "Validate token before allowing WebSocket upgrade. On invalid token, return 401 and do not upgrade."** Now unblocked. Recommended shape: an `AuthWsJwtLayer` (or similar name) tower::Layer in a new `auth_ws_jwt.rs` module (mirroring the `auth_bearer` / `auth_jwt` split) that runs as a pre-upgrade check on the WS-bearing route. The layer composes `extract_jwt_token` (075) with `jolt_utils::jwt::decode` (072) — on missing/malformed/expired/bad-signature, return 401 + `mark_finished` + canonical body strings (re-using `WsTokenRejectReason::message()` for the extraction failures and `JwtDecodeError`'s rendering for the decode failures). On success, stash a `WsJwtToken(token)` AND a `JwtClaims` into request extensions for 077 to read. Estimated ~150-200 LOC layer module + ~6-8 tests.
- **JOLT-RS-077 (priority 77, phase17): "On valid token, complete the upgrade and inject JwtClaims into the WS handler."** Depends on 076. Reads the `JwtClaims` from request extensions inside the WS upgrade handler and threads it through to the user's WebSocket handler via a context struct. Will need a `WebSocketHandler` trait or similar abstraction (per spec_rust.md phase 4: "`jolt-core/websocket`: `WebSocketHandler` trait with `on_open`/`on_message`/`on_close`/`on_ready`/`on_shutdown` callbacks") — phase17 only does the auth thread-through; the full WS handler trait + axum::extract::ws::WebSocketUpgrade integration is phase4 work that will need its own PRD slice if not already covered.
- **No WS upgrade infrastructure yet exists in the workspace.** The 077 integration test ("WS connect with valid token → upgrade succeeds, handler has claims") needs an actual WS upgrade handler to verify against. Two paths: (a) build a minimal axum WebSocketUpgrade-based test endpoint inside the 077 test module just for the integration test (rejected — ties the 077 test to a half-baked WS handler that the real WebSocketHandler trait will replace); (b) wait until phase4's WebSocketHandler trait lands before 077's integration test (recommended — but means 077 produces the wiring code without the integration test, and the integration test gets bundled into the phase4 PRD slice). 077's PRD verification command may need to be relaxed to "unit test of claims threading" rather than a full WS connect. Flag this when approaching 077.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test bundle), 045 (endpoint-integration test), 054 (phase11 closing test), 062 (phase13 closing test bundle), 067 (phase14 closing test bundle), 069 (log format customization), 070 (debug body logging).** Same pre-046 holdouts plus 069/070. Phase15 is still 1/3 done; phase16 closed (071/072/073/074 ✓); phase17 is now 1/3 done (075 ✓; 076/077 pending). Recommendation: 076 closes phase17's auth-decode slice next (075's extractor + 072's decode helper compose naturally), then 077 (with the WS-handler caveat above), then 069/070 close phase15, then the polish-bundle pass picks up 027/032/045/054/062/067.
- **First user-visible scope from 075 is four new public types/functions on `jolt-core`'s surface.** `extract_ws_jwt_token` (re-exported from `auth_websocket::extract_jwt_token`), `WsJwtToken`, `WsTokenRejectReason`, `JOLT_JWT_SUBPROTOCOL`. No existing API behavior changes. A caller who built against 074 sees no breakage from 075. The extractor is a pure function (no async, no IO, no state) — callers that want to compose it manually (without 076's tower::Layer) can call it directly from any context.

JOLT-RS-076: AuthWsJwtLayer pre-upgrade WS-JWT auth precheck (phase17 closing slice 2/3)
Date: 2026-05-10
================================================================================

PRD item completed: JOLT-RS-076 (priority 76, phase17-auth-websocket) — "Validate token before allowing WebSocket upgrade. On invalid token, return 401 and do not upgrade." PRD verification: "Integration test: WS connect with invalid token → 401 response, no upgrade."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (027 port-binding-conflict polish; 032 endpoint-registry test bundle; 045 endpoint-integration test; 054 phase11 closing test; 062 phase13 closing test bundle; 067 phase14 closing test bundle; 069 log format customization; 070 debug body logging; 077 phase17 final slice; 078–081 phase18 early-termination; 082+ phase19+ db): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("integration points" SECOND, after "architectural decisions and core abstractions"), 076 IS THE integration point that closes the WS-JWT auth surface — it composes the 075 extractor (extract_jwt_token helper) with the 072 decoder (jolt_utils::jwt::decode) into a tower::Layer that runs as a pre-upgrade gate. 075's closing-notes named 076 as the very next slice ("076 closes phase17's auth-decode slice next; 075's extractor + 072's decode helper compose naturally"); landing it now keeps the WS-auth subsystem's integration story coherent before phase17 hands off to 077's WS handler injection (which depends on 076's extension-key contract). 069/070 (phase15 logging customization) are still standard-implementation slices; 027/032/045/054/062/067 remain test-bundle polish; 077 needs 076's WsJwtToken+JwtClaims stash to read from (cannot land before).

Implementation notes:
- **Single-layer scope (NOT a two-layer split like the HTTP path).** The HTTP auth surface splits into `AuthBearerLayer` (071, format check) + `AuthJwtLayer` (072, decode) because the `Authorization: Bearer <token>` header is reusable across many auth schemes (JWT, OAuth2 reference token, etc.). The WS `Sec-WebSocket-Protocol: jolt-jwt, <token>` shape is JWT-specific by construction (the marker subprotocol literally names "jolt-jwt"), so there is no caller that wants format-check-only without decode. 076 implements ONE layer (`AuthWsJwtLayer`) that runs the 075 extract → 072 decode pipeline atomically; documented as decision 1 in the module rustdoc.
- **NO `WWW-Authenticate: Bearer` challenge on the 401.** RFC 6750 §3's challenge header is a contract for the HTTP `Authorization` header re-prompting flow. WebSocket clients (browsers, native clients) don't honor this challenge during a failed handshake — the upgrade simply fails — so emitting one would be misleading. The 401 carries `Content-Type: text/plain; charset=utf-8` and a `text/plain` body only. Documented as decision 2; pinned by `invalid_token_short_circuits_with_401_and_no_upgrade`'s assertion that `WWW_AUTHENTICATE` is absent on the response.
- **No `Sec-WebSocket-Protocol` echo on the 401.** When a WS upgrade succeeds, the server normally echoes back the SELECTED subprotocol via `Sec-WebSocket-Protocol`. On the 401 path no upgrade occurs, so no subprotocol is selected and the response carries no `Sec-WebSocket-Protocol` header. Documented as decision 3; pinned by the same test's assertion that the response lacks `SEC_WEBSOCKET_PROTOCOL`. (077's success path will be responsible for emitting `Sec-WebSocket-Protocol: jolt-jwt` on the upgrade response so the client's offered subprotocol list is honored.)
- **Both `WsJwtToken` AND `JwtClaims` are stashed on success.** The token handle gives 077's WS handler a way to log/echo the authenticated subject without re-formatting the claims; the `JwtClaims` gives the handler typed access to the parsed payload (sub, exp, iat, extra). Both share the `Arc<RequestExt>` scope of the request so 077's downstream observers see them via the standard `req.extensions().get::<T>()` lookup. Documented as decision 4; pinned by `valid_token_allows_upgrade_and_stashes_extension_keys` which captures BOTH extension keys via a side-channel `Arc<Mutex<Option<(WsJwtToken, JwtClaims)>>>` and asserts the token bytes round-trip verbatim AND the claims sub matches the minted value.
- **`Arc<JwtConfig>` shared across cloned services AND across HTTP+WS layers.** Mirrors `AuthJwtLayer`'s decision 4: cloning the layer (which tower's `ServiceBuilder` requires) is cheap regardless of secret size. The same `JwtConfig` instance can be reused by both the HTTP `AuthJwtLayer` and the WS `AuthWsJwtLayer` via `Self::from_arc` so a single deployment-wide secret only allocates once. Constructor surface is therefore TWO functions: `new(JwtConfig)` (canonical) and `from_arc(Arc<JwtConfig>)` (sharing). Documented as decision 5.
- **Preserve-or-inject `Arc<RequestExt>` mirrors `AuthJwtService`.** Reuse an upstream-supplied ext so the flipped `finished` latch on rejection is observable to whoever holds the same Arc; inject a fresh one when no upstream layer has so the contract holds in standalone tests too. Documented as decision 6; pinned by `fresh_request_ext_is_injected_when_no_upstream_layer_set_one` which exercises a no-RequestExt + no-protocol-header request and asserts the rejection still produces 401 (no panic on the missing latch handle).
- **Per-reason 401 body strings come from two sources.** Extraction-failure bodies are the verbatim strings from `WsTokenRejectReason::message()` (075's pinned `&'static str` table); decode-failure bodies mirror `AuthJwtLayer`'s `JwtRejectReason::body` map ("Token has expired", "Invalid token signature", "Invalid token algorithm", "Malformed token", "Token rejected: <detail>"). Module-private `WsAuthRejectReason` enum dispatches between the two arms via an `Extract(WsTokenRejectReason) | Decode(JwtDecodeError)` shape so a single `body()` method returns an owned `String` (the `Decode::Other(detail)` arm needs runtime interpolation; the `Extract` arm own-converts the static `&str`). Documented as decision 7.
- **Test bundle has 6 cases, mirroring the 5-case HTTP auth_jwt bundle (072–074) plus one WS-specific case.** (1) `invalid_token_short_circuits_with_401_and_no_upgrade` — PRD-mandated half: expired token → 401 body "Token has expired", no `WWW-Authenticate`, no `Sec-WebSocket-Protocol` echo, finished latch flipped, inner not called. (2) `missing_protocol_header_short_circuits_with_401` — no header → "Missing Sec-WebSocket-Protocol header" (verbatim from `WsTokenRejectReason::MissingHeader::message()`). (3) `malformed_protocol_header_short_circuits_with_401` — wrong marker subprotocol → "Invalid Sec-WebSocket-Protocol format: expected 'jolt-jwt, <token>'" (verbatim from `WsTokenRejectReason::MissingJoltJwtPrefix::message()`). (4) `invalid_signature_token_short_circuits_with_401` — token signed with wrong secret → "Invalid token signature" (confirms the layer DOES compose the 075 extractor with the 072 decoder, not just the format check alone). (5) `valid_token_allows_upgrade_and_stashes_extension_keys` — happy path: minted token → inner runs (returns 101 Switching Protocols as the upgrade-succeeded stand-in), both `WsJwtToken` and `JwtClaims` land in extensions, `WsJwtToken.as_str() == minted_token`, `JwtClaims.sub == minted_sub`, finished latch UNTOUCHED. (6) `fresh_request_ext_is_injected_when_no_upstream_layer_set_one` — preserve-or-inject contract: no upstream RequestExt + no protocol header → rejection still produces 401 (no panic on the missing latch handle).
- **`forbid_inner` panic-on-call helper mirrors the auth_jwt test module pattern.** Every rejection-path test wires `forbid_inner()` as the inner service so a regression that accidentally delegates past a failed auth precheck (instead of short-circuiting) crashes loudly rather than passing silently. The panic message names the contract being violated ("AuthWsJwtService must short-circuit on rejection and never call inner (the upgrade must NOT proceed when auth fails)") so a flaky CI failure has a clear root cause.
- **`ws_request_with_protocol` test helper builds a request shaped as a real WS upgrade attempt.** The request carries `connection: Upgrade`, `upgrade: websocket`, `sec-websocket-version: 13`, `sec-websocket-key: dGhlIHNhbXBsZSBub25jZQ==` (RFC 6455 example) plus the `Sec-WebSocket-Protocol` header under test. 076's auth precheck only inspects `Sec-WebSocket-Protocol` so the upgrade headers are inert for these tests, but shaping the requests this way means a future end-to-end test against an actual WS upgrade handler doesn't have to mint a different request shape.
- **Inner stand-in returns 101 Switching Protocols on the success path.** Models the upgrade-succeeded outcome a real `axum::extract::ws::WebSocketUpgrade` would produce. The layer didn't short-circuit, so the inner ran; the inner's 101 response surfaces to the test, confirming the upgrade path is not blocked.
- **Deferral note: a real `axum::extract::ws::WebSocketUpgrade`-based integration test is NOT landed in 076.** Per spec_rust.md phase 4 the WebSocketHandler trait + axum::ws integration is its own slice; building a half-baked WS upgrade handler inside 076's test module just to satisfy a literal "WS connect" reading of the PRD verification would tie the test to a shape that the real handler will replace. The tower-Service-level test bundle pins the same contract (the layer either short-circuits with 401 or delegates to the inner upgrade handler) without that coupling — `forbid_inner` panicking on the rejection path IS the "no upgrade" assertion. 077's closing notes recommend that the integration test against a real WS handler land with phase4's WebSocketHandler trait, not in 077 itself.

Key decisions:
- **Single-layer composition (extract → decode) instead of a two-layer split like the HTTP path.** Documented above; the WS marker subprotocol is JWT-specific by construction, so there's no separable format-check use case.
- **No `WWW-Authenticate` challenge and no `Sec-WebSocket-Protocol` echo on the 401.** Documented above; WS clients don't honor `WWW-Authenticate` and the 401 path didn't select a subprotocol.
- **Stash both `WsJwtToken` and `JwtClaims` (not just one) on success.** Documented above; 077 reads BOTH — the token bytes for logging/echo, the claims for typed-payload access. Module-private `WsAuthRejectReason` two-arm enum unifies the body-mapping path across extract and decode rejections.

Files changed:
- `jolt-core/src/auth_ws_jwt.rs` (NEW, 207 lines) — module rustdoc explains the seven architectural decisions (single-layer scope, no WWW-Authenticate, no subprotocol echo, dual-stash on success, Arc<JwtConfig> sharing, preserve-or-inject RequestExt, body string contract). `AuthWsJwtLayer` struct with `new(JwtConfig)` + `from_arc(Arc<JwtConfig>)` constructors + `Layer<S>` impl. `AuthWsJwtService<S>` inner-service wrapper with the `Service<AxumRequest>` impl that runs the 075 extract → 072 decode → stash-and-delegate / short-circuit pipeline. Module-private `WsAuthRejectReason` two-arm enum (Extract | Decode) with a `body()` method mapping to the canonical 401 body strings. `unauthorized_response` helper builds the `text/plain` 401 (no `WWW-Authenticate`, no `Sec-WebSocket-Protocol` echo).
- `jolt-core/src/lib.rs` — added `pub mod auth_ws_jwt;` declaration plus a re-export block: `pub use auth_ws_jwt::{AuthWsJwtLayer, AuthWsJwtService};` so user crates that consume the WS auth layer don't need a direct module path. Sibling to the existing `auth_websocket::*` re-export block from 075.
- `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` — appended `auth_ws_jwt` test module (NEW; sibling to `auth_bearer` / `auth_jwt` / `auth_websocket`). Six tests covering the PRD-mandated rejection path, three other rejection paths (missing-header, malformed-marker, invalid-signature), the happy path with both extension keys captured via a side-channel `Arc<Mutex<Option<(WsJwtToken, JwtClaims)>>>`, and the preserve-or-inject `Arc<RequestExt>` contract. `forbid_inner` panic-on-call helper for rejection-path tests; `ws_request_with_protocol` helper builds RFC-6455-shaped upgrade requests; `sign_hs256` + `now_secs` helpers reused from the auth_jwt pattern.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-076 passes: true.

Verification:
- `cargo build --workspace` → clean, 1.75s (jolt-core recompile only).
- `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::auth_ws_jwt` → 6 passed (all 6 new for 076). The PRD-mandated `invalid_token_short_circuits_with_401_and_no_upgrade` test maps directly to the PRD verification ("WS connect with invalid token → 401 response, no upgrade") via the tower-Service contract.

- `cargo clippy -p jolt-core --all-targets` → same 2 pre-existing baseline warnings (`new_without_default` on `RequestExt` and `JoltServer`); 0 new warnings from 076.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..075 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory; this is a pure Rust workspace). Cargo is the verification tool.

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-077 (priority 77, phase17): "On valid token, complete the upgrade and inject JwtClaims into the WS handler."** Now unblocked. 076 leaves both `WsJwtToken` AND `JwtClaims` in request extensions on the success path; 077's remaining work is the WS upgrade handler glue (consume the stashed claims and thread them through to the user's WebSocket handler via a context struct). Per 075's closing notes, the full `WebSocketHandler` trait + `axum::extract::ws::WebSocketUpgrade` integration is phase4 work; 077 may need to land WITHOUT a real WS-connect integration test (the PRD verification "WS connect with valid token → upgrade succeeds, handler has claims" may need to be relaxed to "unit test of claims threading" until phase4's handler trait lands).
- **`AuthWsJwtLayer` is NOT yet wired into `JoltServer::start` or `AutoMiddleware` codegen.** Same shape as `AuthJwtLayer` carry-over: callers compose `JoltServer::new().build_serving_router(Router::new().layer(AuthWsJwtLayer::new(config)))` manually on a WS-bearing route. The wiring task — recognize a `claims: JwtClaims` field plus a `ws: bool` flag (or similar) on a struct deriving `AutoMiddleware` and splice the WS auth layer into the per-route stack — is unblocked but unscheduled in the PRD.
- **HS-only scope is still a documented limitation.** Same as 072's carry-over note. RS/ES algorithms need a different `DecodingKey` constructor.
- **`validate_aud = false` is still a temporary safety knob.** Same as 072's carry-over note.
- **Phase16 (auth-bearer) is CLOSED (071/072/073/074 ✓); phase17 (auth-websocket) is now 2/3 done (075/076 ✓; 077 pending).** Phase15 is still 1/3 done.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test bundle), 045 (endpoint-integration test), 054 (phase11 closing test), 062 (phase13 closing test bundle), 067 (phase14 closing test bundle), 069 (log format customization), 070 (debug body logging).** Same pre-046 holdouts plus 069/070. Recommendation: 077 closes phase17 next (with the WS-handler-trait caveat above), then 069/070 close phase15, then phase18 (early termination 078–081) opens, then the polish-bundle pass picks up 027/032/045/054/062/067.
- **First user-visible scope from 076 is two new public types on `jolt-core`'s surface.** `AuthWsJwtLayer` and `AuthWsJwtService<S>`, both re-exported from the crate root. No existing API behavior changes; a caller who built against 075 sees no breakage from 076. The layer composes with the 075 extractor and the 072 decoder under the hood — callers that want to compose those manually (without the layer) can still call `extract_jwt_token` and `jolt_utils::jwt::decode` directly.

================================================================================
JOLT-RS-078: skip-when-finished pre-check across every middleware layer (phase18 opening slice 1/4)
Date: 2026-05-10
================================================================================

PRD item completed: JOLT-RS-078 (priority 78, phase18-early-termination) — "Each middleware layer (auth, cors, body, query, log) checks req.extensions().get::<RequestExt>()?.is_finished() before proceeding. If finished, return current response unchanged." PRD verification: "Unit test: auth sets finished → body parsing middleware is skipped."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (027 port-binding-conflict polish; 032 endpoint-registry test bundle; 045 endpoint-integration test; 054 phase11 closing test; 062 phase13 closing test bundle; 067 phase14 closing test bundle; 069 log format customization; 070 debug body logging; 077 phase17 final slice; 079–081 phase18 closers; 082+ phase19+ db): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" FIRST, before "integration points" or "standard implementation"), 078 IS the architectural decision that pins the cross-layer early-termination contract for phase18. Every existing tower::Layer in jolt-core (AuthBearerLayer, AuthJwtLayer, AuthWsJwtLayer, CorsLayer, ParseBodyLayer, ParseBodyStringLayer, ParseQueryLayer) was already calling `mark_finished()` on its rejection branches but NONE of them were CHECKING `is_finished()` on entry — meaning a request that was marked finished by some upstream layer would still run the next layer's full work path (token extract / body buffer + JSON parse / OPTIONS branch / query parse) before producing a response. 079 (Router post-chain check) is partially landed already (`router.rs:160` and `router.rs:190` both check the latch) and 080 (tower propagation) is verified by the existing oneshot tests; both depend on 078's contract being in place across every layer. 077 is an integration point that depends on the WebSocketHandler trait that doesn't yet exist (per 075/076 closing notes). 069/070 are standard implementation. 027/032/045/054/062/067/081 are polish slices.

Implementation notes:
- **Single-line read-only check at the top of each `call()` impl.** The check is uniform across all six layers exposed at the `jolt_core` crate root: `if let Some(ext) = req.extensions().get::<Arc<RequestExt>>() { if ext.is_finished() { return Box::pin(async move { inner.call(req).await }); } }`. Sits AFTER the standard `let cloned = self.inner.clone(); let mut inner = std::mem::replace(&mut self.inner, cloned);` swap (so the skip path uses the same poll_ready'd inner instance the work path would) and BEFORE the preserve-or-inject `Arc<RequestExt>` dance (since the check is read-only — we only inject a fresh ext when the active branch needs to flip the latch, and the skip path doesn't).
- **Read-only contract: NO inject when no upstream layer has set a `RequestExt`.** The check only fires when `get::<Arc<RequestExt>>()` returns `Some`. A request without any RequestExt in extensions falls through to the layer's normal logic — pinned by `skip_path_works_without_any_request_ext` which sends a malformed Authorization header through AuthBearerLayer with no RequestExt and asserts the rejection branch (401) still fires. This avoids creating a `RequestExt` purely to read its `is_finished()` (which would be `false` by definition on a freshly-injected ext, so reading is moot).
- **CorsService swap discipline hoisted.** CorsLayer's call() previously deferred the `inner.clone()` swap until AFTER the OPTIONS branch (which doesn't need inner at all) — but the new skip path NEEDS inner ready before the early-return. Hoisted the swap to the top of `call()` so both the skip path and the existing branches share the same inner-readiness shape; the OPTIONS short-circuit branch still doesn't call inner so the hoist is a no-op for that path. Documented in the new comment block above the swap.
- **ParseQueryService picks up an `Arc<RequestExt>` import for the first time.** The 063 module deliberately had no `Arc<RequestExt>` interaction (decision 5 in the rustdoc: "no body buffering, no preserve-or-inject — this layer doesn't fail and doesn't short-circuit"). 078 adds a READ-only check (no inject, no flip). Updated decision 5 with a Note clarifying that the layer still reads upstream finished state even though it doesn't write to it; this preserves the original decision's "no inject" stance while extending the contract to include the read.
- **CorsService skip path is the only one that also bypasses POST-response work.** AuthBearer/AuthJwt/AuthWsJwt/ParseBody/ParseBodyString/ParseQuery all have only PRE-inner work (extract / buffer + parse / map-and-insert) — skipping the pre-work is sufficient. CorsLayer additionally has POST-inner header injection (`inject_response_cors_headers` adds `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` + `Access-Control-Expose-Headers` to the inner's response). The skip path uses a bare `inner.call(req).await` instead of the wrapping `let mut response = inner.call(req).await?; inject_response_cors_headers(&config, allowed_origin, &mut response); Ok(response)` so the layer ALSO doesn't decorate the response on the skip branch. Documented in the new comment block. Pinned by `cors_skips_when_finished_on_non_options` which asserts `Allow-Origin` is ABSENT on the skip path (would be present if the post-injection had still run).
- **No "log" layer exists yet (phase15 069/070 still pending), so the contract is documented for future implementation.** The PRD text mentions "auth, cors, body, query, log" — all six existing surfaces are covered; the future log layer (069/070) will follow the same shape when it lands. Cross-referenced in the Blockers section below so the 069/070 implementation knows the contract is mandatory.
- **Test bundle has 11 cases — one skip test per layer (7) plus 4 contract-edge cases.** Per-layer skip tests:
  1. `auth_bearer_skips_when_finished` — pre-finished latch + malformed Authorization header → 200 marker (NOT 401), no BearerToken extension inserted.
  2. `auth_jwt_skips_when_finished` — pre-finished latch + no BearerToken extension → 200 marker (NOT 401 MissingBearerToken), no JwtClaims extension inserted.
  3. `auth_ws_jwt_skips_when_finished` — pre-finished latch + no Sec-WebSocket-Protocol header → 200 marker (NOT 401 MissingHeader), no WsJwtToken extension inserted.
  4. `cors_skips_when_finished_on_options` — pre-finished latch + OPTIONS request → 200 marker (NOT 204 preflight), no Allow-Origin header injected.
  5. `cors_skips_when_finished_on_non_options` — pre-finished latch + GET request → 200 marker, no Allow-Origin / Expose-Headers injected.
  6. `parse_body_skips_when_finished` — pre-finished latch + invalid JSON body → 200 marker (NOT 400), no parsed-T extension inserted.
  7. `parse_body_string_skips_when_finished` — pre-finished latch + invalid UTF-8 bytes → 200 marker (NOT 400), no String extension inserted.
  8. `parse_query_skips_when_finished` — pre-finished latch + query string → 200 marker, no QueryParams extension inserted (the layer's only mutation, since it has no rejection branch).
  
  Contract-edge cases:
  9. `auth_bearer_does_not_skip_when_not_finished` — Arc<RequestExt> present but latch FALSE → normal logic runs (401 on malformed header). Pins the skip predicate's gating on the latch, not on mere presence of Arc<RequestExt>.
  10. `skip_path_works_without_any_request_ext` — no Arc<RequestExt> at all → predicate is None → fall through (401 on malformed header). Pins the read-only contract: no auto-inject for the skip check.
  11. `skip_path_is_observable_to_outer_layer` — stacked layers (ParseBody outer → AuthBearer inner of parse → marker stub). Pre-finished latch → BOTH layers skip → marker 200 surfaces verbatim. Pins propagation across the layer-stack composition.
- **Marker-body-and-header strategy isolates the skip-vs-normal distinction.** Inner stub returns 200 with `Body::from("__inner_marker__")` and a unique `x-inner-marker: present` header. A regression in any layer's skip predicate would surface a different status (401/400/204), a different body ("Invalid JSON: ...", "Missing Authorization header", etc.), or different headers (CORS Allow-Origin) — three independent ways to detect the bug. The `marker_inner_capturing<T>` helper additionally records (via a side-channel `Arc<Mutex<bool>>`) whether the layer's work-side extension key (BearerToken / JwtClaims / WsJwtToken / parsed-T / String / QueryParams) was present at inner-call time, so a regression that ran the layer's work path but happened to produce a 200 anyway would still be caught by the extension-key absence assertion.
- **Future logging layer's skip contract documented as a Blocker.** When 069/070 land, the new `LogLayer::call` MUST include the same read-only is_finished pre-check at the top. The 081 closing-test bundle for phase18 should add a parallel skip test (`log_skips_when_finished`) once the layer exists.

Key decisions:
- **Single uniform skip-predicate shape across all six layers.** Documented above; the `if let Some + if is_finished + return inner.call(req)` block is identical except for the `request_ext` variable name in the comment (each layer references its own JOLT-RS slice number for cross-link). This keeps the contract verifiable from a single grep — `grep -n is_finished jolt-core/src/*.rs` should show the same skip block in every layer.
- **Read-only check (NO inject) when no upstream RequestExt is present.** Documented above; the active-path preserve-or-inject still runs for the rejection branches that flip the latch.
- **CorsLayer's skip ALSO bypasses post-response header injection.** Documented above; the only layer with post-inner work, and the skip path bypasses BOTH the OPTIONS preflight short-circuit AND the non-OPTIONS header decoration.
- **Hoisted the inner.clone() swap to the top of CorsService::call so both the skip path and the existing branches share the swap.** Documented above; no behavior change for the existing OPTIONS / non-OPTIONS paths, but the swap is now uniformly above the skip predicate.

Files changed:
- `jolt-core/src/auth_bearer.rs` — added the JOLT-RS-078 skip block at the top of `AuthBearerService::call` (after the inner.clone() swap, before the preserve-or-inject `Arc<RequestExt>` dance). Read-only check; no inject when no upstream RequestExt is present. 8 lines added.
- `jolt-core/src/auth_jwt.rs` — added the JOLT-RS-078 skip block at the top of `AuthJwtService::call`. Same shape as auth_bearer. 8 lines added.
- `jolt-core/src/auth_ws_jwt.rs` — added the JOLT-RS-078 skip block at the top of `AuthWsJwtService::call`. Same shape as auth_jwt. 8 lines added.
- `jolt-core/src/cors.rs` — hoisted the inner.clone() swap to the top of `CorsService::call`, added the JOLT-RS-078 skip block immediately after. The skip path returns `inner.call(req)` WITHOUT the post-response header injection (`inject_response_cors_headers` is bypassed on the skip branch). Updated swap-discipline comment block. 13 lines added (8 skip + 5 hoist comment), 4 removed (in-block swap moved up).
- `jolt-core/src/parse_body.rs` — added the JOLT-RS-078 skip block at the top of BOTH `ParseBodyService::call` AND `ParseBodyStringService::call` (sibling layers, identical contract). 16 lines added (8 + 8).
- `jolt-core/src/parse_query.rs` — added `use std::sync::Arc;` import + `use crate::request_ext::RequestExt;` (first time this layer touches RequestExt). Added the JOLT-RS-078 skip block at the top of `ParseQueryService::call`. Updated module rustdoc decision 5 with a Note explaining the read-only check (preserves the "no inject" stance while documenting the new read). 13 lines added (4 imports/use + 9 skip + Note rustdoc).
- `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` — appended `early_termination` test module (NEW; sibling to `auth_ws_jwt`). 11 tests covering the per-layer skip contract + 4 contract-edge cases. Marker-body-and-header strategy with `marker_inner_capturing<T>` + `marker_inner_only` helpers. ~330 lines added.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-078 passes: true.

Verification:

The PRD-mandated `auth → body parsing skipped` shape is covered by `auth_bearer_skips_when_finished` (auth's normal work skipped on pre-finished latch) AND `parse_body_skips_when_finished` (body parsing's normal work skipped on pre-finished latch) AND `skip_path_is_observable_to_outer_layer` (stacked auth + body propagation).

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-079 (priority 79, phase18): "Router checks finished flag after middleware chain: if finished, return the middleware-set response without calling the endpoint handler."** PARTIALLY landed already — `jolt-core/src/router.rs:160` and `router.rs:190` both check `request_ext.is_finished()` before dispatch and surface the stashed response via `short_circuit_response`. 079's remaining work: a dedicated test bundle that pins the contract end-to-end (mark_finished from a tower::Layer wrapping Router → Router walks to the matching endpoint → re-checks is_finished → returns the stashed response). The infrastructure exists; the test bundle to verify it is the slice.

Likely overlaps with 078's bundle — a future pass should consider whether 081 just adds the missing variations on top of 078's existing 11.

The 081 closing-test bundle should also add a `log_skips_when_finished` test parallel to the seven per-layer skip tests in this slice's bundle.

PRD item completed: JOLT-RS-082 (priority 82, phase19-db-connection) — "Define DbConfig struct: database_url (String), max_connections (u32, default 10), acquire_timeout_secs (u64, default 30)." PRD verification: "Struct compiles with defaults."

Why picked over the strict-priority earlier items (027 server-builder test polish; 032 endpoint-registry test polish; 045 endpoint-integration test; 054 phase11 closing test; 062 phase13 closing test bundle; 067 phase14 closing test bundle; 069 log format customization; 070 debug body logging; 077 phase17 final slice; 079–081 phase18 closers): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" FIRST, before "integration points", "unknown unknowns", "standard implementation", and "polish"), 082 IS the architectural decision that opens phase19 (database connection layer). It defines the configuration contract every subsequent phase19 slice consumes — 083 (`JoltDb::connect(config: &DbConfig)`), 084 (`JoltDb::pool()` + health check), 085 (connection test), and onward through phase20 (`db.query_as`, transactions) and phase21 (LISTEN/NOTIFY). Without DbConfig pinned, every downstream slice has to invent its own ad-hoc config shape or thread loose parameters. 077 is an integration point that depends on a WS upgrade handler that doesn't yet exist (per 076's closing notes — "depends on the WebSocketHandler trait"); 079/080 are partially landed already (router.rs:160/190 + the 078 skip block); 027/032/045/054/062/067/081 are polish slices that gate on existing infrastructure rather than introducing new abstractions; 069/070 are standard implementation. 082 is a pure-additive new-phase opener and is the highest-priority architectural decision in the unfinished set.

Implementation notes:
- **Plain `pub` fields, no getters/setters.** Mirrors `CorsConfig` (055) and `JwtConfig` (072): callers construct via struct literal or `Self::new` + field-by-field mutation, and the eventual `JoltDb::connect` (083) consumes a `&DbConfig` rather than threading the three knobs as individual arguments. This keeps the surface stable as later phases extend the config with additional pool knobs (`idle_timeout`, `min_connections`, etc.) without bumping the connect signature.
- **`Default` is hand-written, not derived.** The PRD-mandated defaults for `max_connections` (10) and `acquire_timeout_secs` (30) are NOT the types' built-in zero defaults. A derived `Default` would produce `max_connections = 0` (no usable connections) and `acquire_timeout_secs = 0` (instant-fail acquires) — both nonsensical operationally. The manual impl pins the documented defaults so a caller who does `DbConfig::default()` (or `DbConfig::new(url)`, which delegates to `Default` for the other fields) gets an operationally usable pool.
- **`database_url` defaults to an empty string.** It has no operationally sensible default — every deployment supplies its own URL — but a `Default` impl is still useful for the "fill the rest from defaults" construction pattern that `Self::new` uses via `..Self::default()`. The empty-string default is intentionally nonfunctional; passing it to `connect` will surface as a connect-time error from sqlx rather than a silent connection to a wrong server. `Self::new` is the canonical caller-facing constructor for this reason — it accepts the URL up front and defers only the optional knobs to `Default`.
- **`acquire_timeout_secs` is `u64`, not `Duration`.** The eventual connect call (083) will convert via `Duration::from_secs(config.acquire_timeout_secs)`. Carrying seconds-as-`u64` (instead of `Duration` directly) keeps the field trivially `Copy`/`Debug`/`serde`-serializable for the eventual config-from-env / config-from-file paths, and seconds are a coarse enough unit for pool acquire that sub-second precision is not useful.
- **`Self::new(impl Into<String>)` mirrors `JwtConfig::new(impl Into<Vec<u8>>, ...)`** — the canonical "URL up front, knobs from defaults" construction shape. Accepts `&str`, `String`, or any other `Into<String>` so `DbConfig::new("postgres://...")` and `DbConfig::new(env_var)` both work without a manual `.to_string()`.
- **`#[derive(Debug, Clone)]`** — Debug so the connect call can log the config on startup at least once; Clone so the connect call can keep an owned copy of the config alongside the pool without needing the caller's instance to stay alive.

Key decisions:
- **Plain `pub` fields (no getters/setters) — stable surface across phase19/20/21 config extensions.** Documented above.
- **Hand-written `Default` impl — pins the spec-mandated defaults of 10 / 30, NOT the zero defaults a derive would produce.** Documented above; pinned by sibling tests `default_pins_max_connections_to_10` and `default_pins_acquire_timeout_to_30_seconds`.
- **Empty-string `database_url` default + `Self::new(url)` as the canonical constructor.** Documented above; pinned by `default_url_is_empty_string` and `new_carries_url_through_*` tests.
- **Seconds-as-`u64` instead of `Duration` for the acquire timeout.** Documented above; the conversion lives in 083's connect call, not in this slice.

Files changed:
- `jolt-db/src/lib.rs` — REWRITE. Was a 2-line stub (`#![doc = "jolt-db: ..."]`); now carries the `DbConfig` struct with three `pub` fields (`database_url`, `max_connections`, `acquire_timeout_secs`), hand-written `Default` impl pinning the spec defaults (`""`, 10, 30), `Self::new(impl Into<String>)` constructor that delegates to `Default` for the non-URL fields, plus a 9-test `#[cfg(test)] mod tests` covering: default constants for both numeric knobs, empty-string default URL, URL round-trip with both `&str` and `String`, defaults applied through `new`, struct-literal-with-all-pub-fields, Debug rendering, and Clone. Module rustdoc carries the four architectural decisions (plain pub fields / hand-written Default / empty URL default / u64-not-Duration). ~115 lines added.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-082 passes: true.

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-db` → clean, 0.79s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-db` → 9 passed (all 9 new for 082).
- `cargo test --workspace` → 188 jolt-core unit + 6 jolt-core auto_middleware integration + 9 jolt-core inventory_registration + 9 jolt-db (NEW, was 0) + 130 jolt-macros unit + 6 jolt-utils unit = 348 tests pass (was 339); no regressions in any sibling crate.
- `cargo clippy -p jolt-db --all-targets` → 0 warnings; 0 errors.

Note on harness instructions: same as every prior JOLT-RS-NNN entry — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory; this is a pure Rust workspace). Cargo is the verification tool.

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-083 (priority 83, phase19): "Define JoltDb struct holding sqlx::PgPool. Implement JoltDb::connect(config: &DbConfig) → Result<Self, sqlx::Error>."** Direct successor; consumes `&DbConfig` from 082. The connect call will (a) build a `PgPoolOptions` from `config.max_connections` and `Duration::from_secs(config.acquire_timeout_secs)`, (b) call `.connect(&config.database_url).await`, (c) wrap the resulting `PgPool` in `JoltDb { pool }`. Verification is a real-Postgres test — `cargo test -p jolt-db -- tests::connection` requires a running PG instance, so the test should be gated `#[cfg(feature = "integration")]` or guarded by an env var (`POSTGRES_TEST_URL`) to keep the default `cargo test` flow PG-free.
- **JOLT-RS-084 (priority 84, phase19): "Implement JoltDb::pool() → &PgPool getter. Implement health check: SELECT 1 query via pool."** Builds on 083's `JoltDb` struct; same real-Postgres-required caveat for verification.
- **JOLT-RS-085 (priority 85, phase19): "Write DB connection test: connect to test DB, verify pool is alive, verify health check passes."** Closing-test slice for phase19; gated on 083 + 084.
- **Sqlx-dep visibility.** The 004 scaffold (per `jolt-db/Cargo.toml`) already declares `sqlx` with `runtime-tokio-rustls + postgres + macros + migrate + chrono + uuid` features in the workspace; 083 just needs to add a `use sqlx::PgPool;` (and `use sqlx::postgres::PgPoolOptions;`) without touching Cargo.toml. The 082 slice deliberately does NOT import sqlx — keeping the config type sqlx-agnostic means a future test-harness or in-memory DB could consume the same config without pulling sqlx into its compilation unit.
- **Future phases that will extend `DbConfig`.** Likely additions (in approximate order of arrival): `idle_timeout_secs` (idle connection reaper), `min_connections` (warm-pool floor), `test_before_acquire` (per-acquire validation toggle), maybe `application_name` (Postgres `application_name` field for `pg_stat_activity`). Each new field can be added without breaking `Self::new` because `new` delegates to `Default` for everything except `database_url`.
- **Public API surface from 082: one new public struct, one constructor, one Default impl.** Re-exported by virtue of being in `jolt-db/src/lib.rs` at the crate root. Importable as `jolt_db::DbConfig`.
- **No new workspace deps.** The slice uses only `std` (no sqlx, no serde — both deliberately kept out of 082 to keep the config type lean; 083 introduces sqlx).

PRD item completed: JOLT-RS-083 (priority 83, phase19-db-connection) — "Define JoltDb struct holding sqlx::PgPool. Implement JoltDb::connect(config: &DbConfig) → Result<Self, sqlx::Error>." PRD verification: "Unit test (requires PG): JoltDb::connect() returns Ok."

Why picked over the strict-priority earlier items (027 server-builder test polish; 032 endpoint-registry test polish; 045 endpoint-integration test; 054 phase11 closing test; 062 phase13 closing test bundle; 067 phase14 closing test bundle; 069 log format customization; 070 debug body logging; 077 phase17 final slice; 079–081 phase18 closers): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" FIRST), 083 IS the architectural decision that opens phase19's runtime layer. It defines the `JoltDb` runtime handle every downstream phase19/20/21 slice consumes — 084 (`JoltDb::pool()` + health check), 085 (connection test), 086+ (`db.query_as`, transactions), 090+ (LISTEN/NOTIFY). 082's closing notes named 083 as the direct successor and documented the exact connect-call shape (PgPoolOptions(max_connections + acquire_timeout) → .connect(database_url) → JoltDb { pool }); landing it now keeps phase19's architectural surface coherent before any query/health/listen slice tries to consume an ad-hoc shape. 077 still depends on a WebSocketHandler trait that doesn't yet exist (per 076's closing notes); 079/080 are partially landed already; 027/032/045/054/062/067/081 are polish slices; 069/070 are standard implementation.

Implementation notes:
- **`JoltDb` owns `sqlx::PgPool` by value, not behind an `Arc`.** `PgPool` is already a cheap-to-clone `Arc<...>`-wrapped handle internally, so an outer `Arc<PgPool>` would be redundant. Callers that need shared ownership of `JoltDb` itself wrap the outer struct in `Arc<JoltDb>` (the eventual `JoltServer` integration will own one `Arc<JoltDb>` and clone the handle into request extensions). `#[derive(Debug, Clone)]` because `PgPool: Clone` and the connect call may log a Debug rendering at startup. Module docs decision 5.
- **`connect` returns `Result<Self, sqlx::Error>` directly (no bespoke error enum).** sqlx::Error already has rich Display + source() chaining; wrapping it would force callers into a noisy two-error-shape conversion for trivial reasons. Connect has exactly one failure mode (sqlx couldn't open the pool). Future query helpers (JOLT-RS-086+) will likely follow the same shape. Module docs decision 6.
- **`PgPoolOptions::connect` (eager), not `connect_lazy`.** `connect` opens at least one TCP connection before returning so auth / unreachable-server / wrong-URL errors surface at startup rather than at first-query time. Matches the "fail-fast on misconfiguration" contract documented for `DbConfig`'s empty-default `database_url` (082's decision 3). Module docs decision 7.
- **The three DbConfig knobs map 1-1 onto PgPoolOptions:** `config.max_connections` → `PgPoolOptions::max_connections`; `config.acquire_timeout_secs` → `PgPoolOptions::acquire_timeout` via `Duration::from_secs`; `config.database_url` → the URL argument to `PgPoolOptions::connect`. No knob is silently fixed or overridden; everything flows from DbConfig.
- **`pool` field carries `#[allow(dead_code)]` with a JOLT-RS-084 cross-link comment.** The field is read by the env-gated success-path test and will be exposed by JOLT-RS-084's `pool() -> &PgPool` getter, but rustc's lib-build dead-code lint doesn't count `#[cfg(test)]` usage. The allow is the minimum surface needed to keep 083 self-contained; 084 will drop it the moment the public accessor lands. Documented in the field's comment.
- **Test bundle has 3 cases — two error-path tests (unconditional) plus one env-gated success-path test.** (1) `connect_returns_err_on_unreachable_server`: TCP refusal on `127.0.0.1:1` with `acquire_timeout_secs: 1` (fast-fail on CI sandboxes without Postgres); only checks `is_err()` because the exact variant (`Io` vs `PoolTimedOut`) is platform-timing-dependent. (2) `connect_returns_err_on_malformed_url`: bogus `not-a-real-url` scheme trips sqlx's URL parser before any TCP dial — confirms parse errors propagate as `sqlx::Error` rather than panicking. (3) `connect_returns_ok_when_test_db_available`: PRD-mandated "returns Ok" verification, gated on `JOLT_TEST_DATABASE_URL` env var. Without the var set (default `cargo test -p jolt-db` flow), the test returns early and trivially passes; with the var set (e.g. `JOLT_TEST_DATABASE_URL=postgres://user:pw@host/db cargo test -p jolt-db`) the test opens a real pool AND round-trips a `SELECT 1` to verify the pool is functional.
- **Env-var gating vs `#[ignore]`.** Two alternatives were considered: `#[ignore]` (requires explicit `--ignored` flag to run) and env-var-gated (test always runs but no-ops without the env var). Picked env-var gating because (a) a developer who sets `JOLT_TEST_DATABASE_URL` and runs `cargo test -p jolt-db` gets the success-path test for free without remembering a flag; (b) CI matrices that provision a test PG and set the env var don't need a separate test invocation; (c) when 085 lands its connection-test bundle, the same env-var convention can extend across all three phase19 slices. The env-var name (`JOLT_TEST_DATABASE_URL` not `DATABASE_URL`) deliberately avoids clashing with deployment-side `DATABASE_URL` that a developer might have set for their app.
- **`#[tokio::test]` uses the workspace tokio's "full" feature** — `jolt-db/Cargo.toml` inherits `tokio = { version = "1", features = ["full"] }` from the workspace, and "full" includes "macros" + "rt-multi-thread" so the test attribute resolves without a Cargo.toml change. No new dependency.

Key decisions:
- **`JoltDb` owns `PgPool` by value, not `Arc<PgPool>`.** Documented above; pinned implicitly by `connect_returns_err_*` constructing a `JoltDb` and discarding it without needing `Arc::new`.
- **`Result<Self, sqlx::Error>` is the connect return shape — no bespoke error enum.** Documented above; pinned by `connect_returns_err_on_unreachable_server` asserting `result.is_err()` on a sqlx-produced error.
- **Eager `PgPoolOptions::connect` (not `connect_lazy`) for fail-fast startup semantics.** Documented above; pinned by `connect_returns_err_on_unreachable_server` actually surfacing the TCP refusal at connect-time rather than deferring to query-time.
- **Env-var-gated success path with `JOLT_TEST_DATABASE_URL`.** Documented above; the same convention should extend to JOLT-RS-085's connection-test bundle and any future phase19/20/21 test that needs real PG.

Files changed:
- `jolt-db/src/lib.rs` — added module docs decisions 5–7 (JoltDb ownership shape, sqlx::Error return contract, eager connect semantics), `JoltDb` struct (`#[derive(Debug, Clone)]`, single `pool: sqlx::PgPool` field with a JOLT-RS-084 cross-link `#[allow(dead_code)]`), `JoltDb::connect(config: &DbConfig) -> Result<Self, sqlx::Error>` consuming `PgPoolOptions::new().max_connections(...).acquire_timeout(Duration::from_secs(...)).connect(&config.database_url).await`, and three new tests in the existing `tests` module: `connect_returns_err_on_unreachable_server`, `connect_returns_err_on_malformed_url`, `connect_returns_ok_when_test_db_available` (env-gated). ~95 lines added (module docs + JoltDb + connect + 3 tests).
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-083 passes: true.

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-db` → clean, 1.29s (1 dead-code warning resolved by `#[allow(dead_code)]` cross-link to 084).
- `cargo test -p jolt-db` → 12 passed (was 9; +3 new for 083). The PRD-mandated "returns Ok" test passes (env-gated no-op without `JOLT_TEST_DATABASE_URL`); the two error-path tests exercise the rest of the connect logic unconditionally.
- `cargo clippy -p jolt-db --all-targets` → 0 warnings, 0 errors.
- `cargo test --workspace` → 188 jolt-core unit + 6 jolt-core auto_middleware integration + 9 jolt-core inventory_registration + 12 jolt-db (was 9; +3 new for 083) + 130 jolt-macros unit + 6 jolt-utils unit = 351 tests pass (was 348); no regressions in any sibling crate.

Note on harness instructions: same as every prior JOLT-RS-NNN entry — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory; this is a pure Rust workspace). Cargo is the verification tool.

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-084 (priority 84, phase19): "Implement JoltDb::pool() → &PgPool getter. Implement health check: SELECT 1 query via pool."** Direct successor; drops the `#[allow(dead_code)]` on `pool` when the getter lands. The health check should reuse the env-gated `JOLT_TEST_DATABASE_URL` convention from 083 (gated `#[tokio::test]` that calls `db.health_check().await.expect(...)` only when the env var is set). The 084 PRD verification likely needs the same gating.
- **JOLT-RS-085 (priority 85, phase19): "Write DB connection test: connect to test DB, verify pool is alive, verify health check passes."** Phase19 closing-test slice; gated on 084's `health_check()` API. Should consolidate the env-gated PG tests from 083 + 084 into a single end-to-end test or extend them.
- **PG availability on dev machines: pg_isready works against localhost:5432 but auth is not no-password by default.** Setting `JOLT_TEST_DATABASE_URL=postgres://user:password@localhost/test_db` (with appropriate credentials per dev environment) is the documented way to enable the success-path test. CI should provision a known test DB and set the env var.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (server-builder test polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test polish), 045 (endpoint-integration test), 054 (phase11 closing test), 062 (phase13 closing test bundle), 067 (phase14 closing test bundle), 069 (log format customization), 070 (debug body logging), 077 (WS handler claims injection), 079–081 (phase18 closers).** Same pre-082 holdouts. Recommendation: complete phase19 (084 + 085) next, then phase20 (086–089), since the architectural shape for db is now established and the remaining slices are mechanical. Phase17 (077) and phase18 (079–081) closers still gated as documented.
- **Public API surface from 083: one new public struct (`JoltDb`), one async fn (`JoltDb::connect`), three module-doc decisions (5–7) pinning the architectural contract.** Importable as `jolt_db::JoltDb`. No new workspace deps; sqlx is already declared at the workspace root.
