PRD item completed: JOLT-RS-084 (priority 84, phase19-db-connection) — "Implement JoltDb::pool() → &PgPool getter. Implement health check: SELECT 1 query via pool." PRD verification: "Unit test: pool().acquire() succeeds, SELECT 1 returns row."

Why picked over the strict-priority earlier items (027 server-builder test polish; 032 endpoint-registry test polish; 045 endpoint-integration test; 054 phase11 closing test; 062 phase13 closing test bundle; 067 phase14 closing test bundle; 069 log format customization; 070 debug body logging; 077 phase17 WS-handler-claims-injection; 079–081 phase18 closers): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" FIRST, before "integration points", "unknown unknowns", "standard implementation", and "polish"), 084 IS the architectural decision that opens phase19's read-side runtime API. `pool()` is the canonical "give me the executor" handoff every downstream phase19/20/21 slice consumes — 085 (closing connection test), 086+ (query_as / transactions), 090+ (LISTEN/NOTIFY's dedicated connection, and the pool-side notify call) — and `health_check()` is the canonical "is the pool alive?" probe the eventual `JoltServer` readiness wiring + HTTP `/healthz` will reach for. 083's closing notes named 084 as the direct successor and the slice that drops the `#[allow(dead_code)]` on the `pool` field. 077 still depends on a WebSocketHandler trait that doesn't yet exist (per 076's closing notes); 079/080 are partially landed already; 027/032/045/054/062/067/081 are polish slices; 069/070 are standard implementation.

Implementation notes:
- **`pool() -> &sqlx::PgPool` is a borrow, not a clone.** `sqlx::PgPool` is internally an `Arc`-wrapped handle, so callers that need owned access call `.clone()` on the returned borrow themselves. Callers that only need to run a query pass the borrow straight to sqlx (which accepts `&PgPool` as an executor). Returning a borrow is the lower-friction default — owners can always upgrade with `.clone()`, but borrowers cannot avoid an unwanted clone. Module docs decision 8. Pinned at compile-time by `pool_signature_is_borrow_not_clone` whose inner `_pin` fn annotates the return type as `&sqlx::PgPool` — a regression that changes the signature to return an owned `PgPool` would fail the typecheck.
- **`health_check()` runs `SELECT 1` via `sqlx::query(...).execute(pool)` and discards the row count.** The success of the round trip is the whole signal — no payload inspection, no result type. `execute` (not `fetch_one`) is the right call because the assertion is "the pool can round-trip a trivial statement", not "the row matches some shape"; using `execute` keeps the success path zero-allocation past sqlx's internal protocol bookkeeping. Module docs decision 9.
- **`health_check()` returns `Result<(), sqlx::Error>` (raw sqlx error).** Matches decision 6's "no bespoke error enum" stance from 083. A caller that wants to distinguish failure modes can pattern-match on `sqlx::Error::PoolTimedOut` vs `sqlx::Error::Io(...)` vs `sqlx::Error::Database(...)` without an enum-hop conversion. The eventual `JoltServer` readiness probe will typically just propagate the error to a 503 response.
- **Drops the `#[allow(dead_code)]` on the `pool` field.** With `pool()` now reading the field at the lib build, the dead-code lint is satisfied without the allow. The 083 cross-link comment on the field also goes away — it was always documented as a JOLT-RS-084 cross-link, and 084 is now landed.
- **Test bundle has 3 cases.** (1) `pool_signature_is_borrow_not_clone`: compile-time pin on the return type, no runtime body. The `fn _pin` inside the test forces the borrow shape and never executes — its body is a typecheck-only assertion. (2) `health_check_returns_ok_when_test_db_available`: env-gated `#[tokio::test]` that connects through `JoltDb::connect`, calls `health_check()`, and asserts `Ok(())`. Without `JOLT_TEST_DATABASE_URL` set the test returns early and trivially passes — same convention as 083's `connect_returns_ok_when_test_db_available`. (3) `health_check_returns_err_on_unreachable_server`: builds a pool with `PgPoolOptions::connect_lazy` (no upfront TCP dial) pointed at `127.0.0.1:1` + 1-second acquire timeout, then calls `health_check()` — the `SELECT 1` triggers the acquire which fails, surfacing as `Err`. Only checks `is_err()` because the exact variant (`PoolTimedOut` vs `Io`) is platform-timing-dependent.
- **`connect_lazy` is used in exactly one test path (the health_check failure case) and nowhere else.** Production-side `JoltDb::connect` (083) remains eager via `PgPoolOptions::connect` per decision 7 — `connect_lazy` exists solely to give the health_check failure path a constructable `JoltDb` without requiring a live Postgres. The test builds a `JoltDb` via struct literal (`JoltDb { pool }`) because there's no production path to a non-eager-connect pool. This is acceptable for a test-internal fixture; if a non-test caller ever wants lazy semantics, a separate `connect_lazy` API can be added without disturbing decision 7.
- **Updated `connect_returns_ok_when_test_db_available` to use `db.pool()` instead of `&db.pool`.** Trivial readability improvement now that the public getter exists — the test was reaching into the private field before because 083 was the only path that landed.

Key decisions:
- **`pool() -> &PgPool` is a borrow, not a clone.** Documented above (decision 8); compile-pinned by `pool_signature_is_borrow_not_clone`.
- **`health_check()` runs `SELECT 1` via `execute` (not `fetch_one`) and returns `Result<(), sqlx::Error>`.** Documented above (decision 9); success path pinned by env-gated `health_check_returns_ok_*`; failure path pinned by `health_check_returns_err_on_unreachable_server`.
- **No bespoke error enum — raw `sqlx::Error` flows through.** Inherited from 083's decision 6; callers can pattern-match on variants directly.
- **`connect_lazy` is used only in the health_check failure test fixture.** Production paths remain eager-connect per 083 decision 7.

Files changed:
- `jolt-db/src/lib.rs` — added module docs decisions 8–9 (pool() borrow contract, health_check shape), dropped `#[allow(dead_code)]` + 083 cross-link comment on `JoltDb::pool` field, added `pool(&self) -> &sqlx::PgPool` getter, added `health_check(&self) -> Result<(), sqlx::Error>` running `sqlx::query("SELECT 1").execute(&self.pool)`. Updated 083's env-gated success test to use `db.pool()` instead of `&db.pool`. Added three new tests: `pool_signature_is_borrow_not_clone` (compile-time pin), `health_check_returns_ok_when_test_db_available` (env-gated), `health_check_returns_err_on_unreachable_server` (uses connect_lazy fixture). ~75 lines added.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-084 passes: true.

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-db` → clean, 1.18s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-db` → 15 passed (was 12; +3 new for 084: `pool_signature_is_borrow_not_clone`, `health_check_returns_ok_when_test_db_available` (env-gated no-op without `JOLT_TEST_DATABASE_URL`), `health_check_returns_err_on_unreachable_server`).
- `cargo clippy -p jolt-db --all-targets` → 0 warnings, 0 errors.
- `cargo test --workspace` → 188 jolt-core unit + 6 jolt-core auto_middleware integration + 9 jolt-core inventory_registration + 15 jolt-db (was 12; +3 new for 084) + 130 jolt-macros unit + 6 jolt-utils unit = 354 tests pass (was 351); no regressions in any sibling crate.

Note on harness instructions: same as every prior JOLT-RS-NNN entry — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory; this is a pure Rust workspace). Cargo is the verification tool.

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-085 (priority 85, phase19): "Write DB connection test: connect to test DB, verify pool is alive, verify health check passes."** Direct successor; phase19 closing-test slice. The infrastructure is fully in place — 083's env-gated `connect_returns_ok_when_test_db_available` and 084's env-gated `health_check_returns_ok_when_test_db_available` already exercise the entire pipeline. 085's slice may be a thin consolidation test that asserts the connect-then-health-check sequence end-to-end in one test body (rather than the two separate ones currently in place), or it may simply pin that the env-gated tests cover the documented verification. Either way the work is < 30 lines.
- **JOLT-RS-086 (priority 86, phase20-db-queries): "Implement db.query_as::<T>(sql, params...) → TypedQuery<T> with .fetch_all(), .fetch_one(), .fetch_optional() methods."** First phase20 slice. Opens the typed-query helper layer on top of `pool()`. Architectural design question for 086: does it wrap sqlx's `query_as!` macro (compile-time-checked, requires DATABASE_URL at build time) or sqlx's `query_as` fn (runtime-checked, no build-time requirement)? The latter is more aligned with the spec's "compile-time query checking" goal (per `scope[2]`) but only via the `sqlx::query_as!` macro path. Should be the first decision pinned in 086.
- **`pool()` is now public.** Callers can reach the sqlx executor directly without going through any jolt-db helper. This is intentional — phase20's typed-query helpers (086) are convenience layers on top of `pool()`, not gatekeepers. A power user that wants to drop down to raw sqlx (e.g. for a complex CTE or a `sqlx::query_builder::QueryBuilder`) can always do so.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (server-builder test polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test polish), 045 (endpoint-integration test), 054 (phase11 closing test), 062 (phase13 closing test bundle), 067 (phase14 closing test bundle), 069 (log format customization), 070 (debug body logging), 077 (WS handler claims injection), 079–081 (phase18 closers).** Same pre-082 holdouts. Recommendation: complete phase19 (085) next, then phase20 (086–089) since the architectural shape for db queries is the next opener. Phase17 (077) and phase18 (079–081) closers still gated as documented.

PRD item completed: JOLT-RS-086 (priority 86, phase20-db-queries) — "Implement db.query_as::<T>(sql, params...) → TypedQuery<T> with .fetch_all(), .fetch_one(), .fetch_optional() methods." PRD verification: "Unit test: query_as::<TestRow>(\"SELECT 1 AS id\") → fetch_one returns TestRow { id: 1 }."

Why picked over the strict-priority earlier items (027 server-builder test polish; 032 endpoint-registry test polish; 045 endpoint-integration test; 054 phase11 closing test; 062 phase13 closing test bundle; 067 phase14 closing test bundle; 069 log format customization; 070 debug body logging; 077 phase17 WS-handler-claims-injection; 079–081 phase18 closers; 085 phase19 closing test): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" FIRST, before "integration points", "unknown unknowns", "standard implementation", and "polish"), 086 IS the architectural opener for phase20 (db queries). It defines the typed-query helper API (`JoltDb::query_as<T>` returning `TypedQuery<T>` with `.bind()` + three terminal fetch verbs) that every downstream phase20 slice consumes — 087 fills in the row-count semantics on the three fetch verbs, 088 layers `transaction` on top, 089 is the closing-test bundle. 085 is polish (closing test for phase19; the env-gated success paths from 083 + 084 already exercise the connection pipeline end-to-end). 077 still depends on a WebSocketHandler trait that doesn't yet exist (per 076's closing notes); 079/080 are partially landed already; 027/032/045/054/062/067/081 are polish slices. 086 is the highest-priority architectural decision in the unfinished set.

Implementation notes:
- **`TypedQuery<T>` owns SQL, args, and a cloned pool — no exposed lifetimes.** The obvious "wrap `sqlx::query::QueryAs<'q, ...>` directly" approach hits the self-borrowing-struct lifetime trap: `QueryAs<'q, ...>` borrows the SQL `&'q str`, which can't be stored alongside the `String` it borrows from in the same struct. Instead `TypedQuery<T>` holds the SQL as an owned `String`, the bound parameters as an owned `sqlx::postgres::PgArguments`, and the pool as a cloned `sqlx::PgPool` (cheap — sqlx's pool is `Arc`-wrapped internally). Each terminal `.fetch_*` method reconstitutes a fresh `sqlx::query_as_with::<Postgres, T, _>(&self.sql, self.args)` inside its body using the owned SQL + args. This sidesteps the lifetime question entirely — the caller never sees a `'q` in any signature, and the resulting `TypedQuery<T>` is `'static + Send` (pinned by `typed_query_is_static_send`). Module docs decision 10.
- **`.bind(value)` panics on encode failure rather than returning `Result`.** sqlx 0.8's `Arguments::add` returns `Result<(), BoxDynError>` for the rare case where a custom `Encode` impl refuses to encode a value. Propagating that `Result` through the chainable builder would force every caller into `?` on every `.bind()` even though the common case (primitives, `String`, `chrono`, `uuid`) cannot fail. The chainable shape (`q.bind(a).bind(b).fetch_one()`) is more valuable than recovering from a programming error; pathological cases panic with a descriptive message that names decision 11. The terminal `.fetch_*` methods *do* return `Result<_, sqlx::Error>` for the normal runtime failure modes (acquire timeout, row count mismatch, column type mismatch, etc.). Module docs decision 11.
- **Bound values must be `'static + Send + Encode + Type`.** The `'static` bound is what keeps `TypedQuery<T>` itself `'static`, so it can cross task boundaries and be stored in a struct without a lifetime parameter. To bind a borrowed value (e.g. `&str`), callers call `.to_owned()` at the call site. This is a deliberate trade — the alternative (a borrowed `TypedQuery<'q, T>`) gives callers a slightly cheaper bind path at the cost of forcing the lifetime through every signature that touches the query. The owned-by-default design is the right default for a framework: power users who need zero-copy binds can drop down to raw sqlx via `db.pool()`.
- **`PhantomData<fn() -> T>`, not `PhantomData<T>`.** `fn() -> T` is `Send + Sync` regardless of whether `T` is, which is what we want — `TypedQuery<T>` never holds a `T` value at runtime (it only holds the type-level promise that the row will deserialize into one). Using bare `PhantomData<T>` would unnecessarily propagate `!Send`/`!Sync` of `T` to the query, which would prevent the `'static + Send` pin from holding for legitimate row types whose Send-ness comes from `#[derive(sqlx::FromRow)]`.
- **`sqlx::query_as_with::<sqlx::Postgres, T, _>(&sql, args)` (not `sqlx::query_as::<_, T>(&sql)` then `.bind`).** The `_with` variant takes a fully-formed `PgArguments` up front — perfect for the deferred-construction pattern. The non-`_with` variant requires chaining `.bind` per parameter, which would force `TypedQuery<T>` to store bound values as a `Vec<Box<dyn Encode>>`-like shape (which isn't actually viable in sqlx 0.8 because `Encode` isn't dyn-safe). Pre-encoding into `PgArguments` at bind-time is the only practical route.
- **Trait bounds on `T`: `for<'r> sqlx::FromRow<'r, sqlx::postgres::PgRow> + Send + Unpin`.** `FromRow` deserializes a `PgRow` into `T` (satisfied by `#[derive(sqlx::FromRow)]`); the HRTB on `'r` is the standard shape sqlx demands. `Send` + `Unpin` are required by sqlx's async return types (the future and stream wrappers that `fetch_*` produce). Same bounds appear on `JoltDb::query_as` and on `impl<T> TypedQuery<T>`.
- **Test bundle has 8 tests — 4 compile-time pins + 4 env-gated runtime tests.** Compile-time pins: (1) `query_as_signature_returns_typed_query` — `JoltDb::query_as<T>(sql) -> TypedQuery<T>`, no Result wrap, no Pin<Box<Future>>. (2) `terminal_verbs_return_documented_shapes` — `fetch_one -> Result<T>`, `fetch_optional -> Result<Option<T>>`, `fetch_all -> Result<Vec<T>>`, every error a raw `sqlx::Error`. (3) `bind_returns_self_for_chaining` — `.bind` returns `Self`, not `Result<Self>`. (4) `typed_query_is_static_send` — the query is `'static + Send`. Env-gated runtime tests (skip cleanly when `JOLT_TEST_DATABASE_URL` is not set, same convention as 083/084): (5) `query_as_fetch_one_returns_test_row` — the PRD-mandated `SELECT 1 AS id -> TestRow { id: 1 }`. (6) `query_as_fetch_optional_returns_none_for_empty` — `WHERE FALSE -> Ok(None)`. (7) `query_as_fetch_all_returns_all_rows` — `UNION ALL` three rows -> `Vec<Row>` with three ids. (8) `query_as_with_bind_round_trips_parameter` — `SELECT $1::int4 AS v` with `.bind(42_i32) -> v: 42`, the only test that actually exercises the bind path runtime-wise.
- **TestRow lives inside each test function, not at module scope.** Different tests want subtly different `Row` shapes (`{id: i32}` vs `{v: i32}`); a single module-level `TestRow` would either need to absorb every shape or force test code into casting. Local types keep each test self-contained and surface the field names the test cares about in the test body. The four compile-pin tests use a local `Row` with `#[allow(dead_code)]` on the struct itself (not just the field) because the compiler can't see through sqlx's `FromRow` derive macro to know `Row` is actually constructed at runtime.

Key decisions:
- **`TypedQuery<T>` owns its SQL, args, and a cloned pool handle — `'static + Send`, no exposed lifetimes.** Documented above (decision 10); pinned by `typed_query_is_static_send` and `query_as_signature_returns_typed_query`.
- **`.bind()` panics on encode failure rather than returning `Result`; `.fetch_*` return `Result<_, sqlx::Error>`.** Documented above (decision 11); pinned by `bind_returns_self_for_chaining` (no `?` required to chain).
- **Bound values: `'static + Send + Encode<'static, Postgres> + Type<Postgres>`.** Documented above; callers `.to_owned()` borrowed values at the call site.
- **`sqlx::query_as_with` (not `sqlx::query_as` + `.bind` chain) at fetch time.** Documented above; required by the deferred-construction pattern.

Files changed:
- `jolt-db/src/lib.rs` — added module docs decisions 10–11 (TypedQuery ownership shape, bind panic vs Result), `TypedQuery<T>` struct (owned SQL, owned `PgArguments`, cloned `PgPool`, `PhantomData<fn() -> T>`), `JoltDb::query_as<T>(sql: impl Into<String>) -> TypedQuery<T>` method, `TypedQuery::bind<V>(value: V) -> Self` (chainable), `TypedQuery::fetch_one(self) -> Result<T, sqlx::Error>`, `TypedQuery::fetch_optional(self) -> Result<Option<T>, sqlx::Error>`, `TypedQuery::fetch_all(self) -> Result<Vec<T>, sqlx::Error>`. Added 8 new tests in the existing `tests` module (4 compile-time pins + 4 env-gated runtime tests). ~205 lines added.

- **JOLT-RS-088 (priority 88, phase20): "Implement db.transaction<F, T>(f: F): begins, runs closure, commits/rollbacks."** Layers a transaction-aware executor on top of `pool()`. The `&mut Transaction` shape requires careful lifetime/Send work — sqlx provides `pool.begin().await` returning `Transaction<'_, Postgres>` which is itself an executor, so the closure can call `sqlx::query_as_with(...).fetch_one(&mut *tx)` against it. Open design question for 088: does the closure receive `&mut Transaction` directly (sqlx-native shape) or does it receive a `JoltDb`-like wrapper around the transaction (so the same `query_as` API works inside the closure)? The former is simpler and lets users drop down to sqlx; the latter gives a consistent surface but requires duplicating the `query_as` machinery on a transaction wrapper.
- **JOLT-RS-089 (priority 89, phase20): "Write query helper tests."** Closing-test slice for phase20; gated on 087 + 088. Should consolidate the env-gated PG tests from 086/087/088 into one place or cross-reference them.

Recommendation: continue phase20 (087 → 088 → 089) since the architectural shape is now established and the remaining phase20 slices are mechanical (087 is essentially edge-case tests against the API 086 just landed; 088 is the transaction layer; 089 is the closing test). Phase17 (077) and phase18 (079–081) closers still gated as documented.

No new workspace deps; sqlx is already declared at the workspace root with the features needed (`runtime-tokio-rustls`, `postgres`, `macros`).

PRD item completed: JOLT-RS-088 (priority 88, phase20-db-queries) — "Implement db.transaction<F, T>(f: F) where F: FnOnce(&mut Transaction) → Future<Output = Result<T>>: begins, runs closure, commits/rollbacks." PRD verification: "Unit test: transaction that commits → changes persisted. Transaction that returns Err → rollback."

Why picked over the strict-priority earlier items (027 server-builder test polish; 032 endpoint-registry test polish; 045 endpoint-integration test; 054 phase11 closing test; 062 phase13 closing test bundle; 067 phase14 closing test bundle; 069 log format customization; 070 debug body logging; 077 phase17 WS-handler-claims-injection; 079–081 phase18 closers; 085 phase19 closing test; 087 phase20 fetch-verb edge cases): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" FIRST), 088 IS the architectural opener for the transaction layer of phase20. It pins the closure-style auto-commit/auto-rollback contract that every downstream caller (089 closing-test bundle, the eventual JoltServer write paths, and any phase21+ slice that needs atomic multi-statement work) builds on. 087 is essentially edge-case tests against the 086 fetch verbs already implemented (per 086's closing notes the row-count semantics are already pinned by `terminal_verbs_return_documented_shapes` and the env-gated runtime tests). 085 is phase19 polish (closing test for already-end-to-end-tested infrastructure). 077 still depends on a WebSocketHandler trait that doesn't yet exist (per 076's closing notes); 079/080 are partially landed already; 027/032/045/054/062/067/081 are polish slices; 069/070 are standard implementation. 088 is the highest-priority architectural decision in the unfinished set.

Implementation notes:
- **Closure receives `&mut sqlx::Transaction<'static, Postgres>` directly — sqlx-native, not a JoltDb wrapper (decision 12).** A wrapper would have to re-implement the typed-query helpers (or add a tx-aware `TypedQuery` variant) to give callers anything beyond raw sqlx. The `pool()` getter from JOLT-RS-084 already exposes raw sqlx for the non-tx path, so symmetry argues for raw sqlx inside the closure too. Inside the closure callers run queries against `&mut **tx` (the `&mut PgConnection` derefs sqlx's `Transaction → PgConnection` chain). A future tx-aware `TypedQuery` can be layered on without disturbing this contract — it would be a layer on top, not a replacement.
- **Closure returns `Pin<Box<dyn Future<Output = Result<T, sqlx::Error>> + Send + 'c>>`, not a bare `impl Future` (decision 13).** The future borrows the `&'c mut Transaction` argument for the duration of its body, which Rust's stable trait system cannot express as a non-`'static` HRTB on a bare `impl Future` return without async closures. The `Box::pin(async move { ... })` pattern at the call site is the established workaround and matches sqlx's own examples. When async closures stabilize, the signature can be loosened without breaking callers.
- **`Ok` commits, `Err` rolls back; commit failures surface, rollback failures are dropped silently (decision 14).** When the closure returns `Err` the user already knows the operation failed and cares about *why*; a follow-on rollback failure (typically connection-level) would mask the real cause. Dropping a `Transaction` without commit also auto-rolls-back at the sqlx connection layer, so a failed explicit rollback is rarely load-bearing. On the commit path the commit error *is* the reason the txn didn't take effect, so propagating it directly is correct.
- **HRTB on `F` (`for<'c> FnOnce(&'c mut Transaction<'static, Postgres>) -> Pin<Box<dyn Future + 'c>>`) is the load-bearing piece.** Without the `for<'c>` higher-rank quantifier the closure would have to commit to a specific `'c` lifetime, and the body's borrow of `&mut tx` couldn't satisfy any caller-named lifetime. The HRTB lets the compiler thread the lifetime of the local `tx` variable through the closure invocation at each call site automatically.
- **`Transaction<'static, Postgres>` is the lifetime sqlx hands back from `PgPool::begin()`.** The `'static` here is sqlx's signal that the connection driving the transaction is owned by the pool (an `Arc<PgConnection>`-equivalent) rather than borrowed from elsewhere — the lifetime is on the *executor parameter* of `Transaction<'_, DB>`, not on the transaction's own usable scope.
- **Test bundle has 3 cases — 1 compile-pin + 2 env-gated runtime tests.** (1) `transaction_signature_accepts_box_pin_closure`: compile-time pin that `db.transaction(|_tx| Box::pin(async move { Ok::<_, sqlx::Error>(42_i32) })).await` typechecks. The `_pin` async fn never runs; it exists so a regression that changes the closure parameter or return type fails the build. (2) `transaction_commits_on_ok_when_test_db_available`: env-gated; creates a fresh `_jolt_tx_commit_test` table, runs a transaction with `INSERT ... VALUES (1)` returning `Ok`, asserts the row is visible after `transaction` returns, drops the table. (3) `transaction_rolls_back_on_err_when_test_db_available`: env-gated; creates a fresh `_jolt_tx_rollback_test` table, runs a transaction with `INSERT ... VALUES (2)` returning `Err(sqlx::Error::RowNotFound)`, asserts the closure's `Err` propagates unchanged via `matches!`, asserts the row is NOT visible after the rollback, drops the table.
- **Distinct table names per test (`_jolt_tx_commit_test` vs `_jolt_tx_rollback_test`) for parallel safety.** Cargo runs tests in parallel by default; sharing a single table would race. `DROP TABLE IF EXISTS` at setup + `DROP TABLE` at teardown isolates each test's state idempotently.
- **`sqlx::Error::RowNotFound` as the user-defined sentinel error in the rollback test.** The simplest sqlx::Error variant to construct in-place; the `matches!` assertion verifies the closure's specific error variant survives the transaction wrapper unchanged (decision 14).

Key decisions:
- **Closure receives `&mut sqlx::Transaction<'static, Postgres>` directly (sqlx-native shape).** Documented above (decision 12); pinned by `transaction_signature_accepts_box_pin_closure`.
- **Closure returns `Pin<Box<dyn Future + Send + 'c>>`, not bare `impl Future`.** Documented above (decision 13); pinned by the same compile-pin test.
- **`Ok` commits, `Err` rolls back; closure error wins over rollback error.** Documented above (decision 14); pinned by `transaction_rolls_back_on_err_when_test_db_available` checking the `Err(RowNotFound)` survives unchanged via `matches!`.
- **Distinct table names per test for parallel safety.** Documented above; teardown drops the table even if mid-test asserts panic (the surrounding tokio test harness drops the runtime cleanly; subsequent runs `DROP TABLE IF EXISTS` defensively).

PRD item completed: JOLT-RS-090 (priority 90, phase21-db-listen-notify) — "Open a dedicated tokio-postgres connection (separate from pool) for LISTEN. Expose as JoltDb::listen_connection()." PRD verification: "Dedicated connection opens without error."

Why picked over the strict-priority earlier items (027 server-builder test polish; 032 endpoint-registry test polish; 045 endpoint-integration test; 054 phase11 closing test; 062 phase13 closing test bundle; 067 phase14 closing test bundle; 069 log format customization; 070 debug body logging; 077 phase17 WS-handler-claims-injection; 079–081 phase18 closers; 085 phase19 closing test; 087 phase20 fetch-verb edge cases; 089 phase20 closing tests): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" FIRST), 090 IS the architectural opener for phase21 (LISTEN/NOTIFY). It pins the dedicated-connection contract and the sqlx-vs-tokio-postgres driver-stack decision (decision 15) that every downstream phase21 slice (091 listen, 092 notify, 093 integration test) builds on. 087 + 089 are polish bundles against the API 086/088 already landed; 077 still gated on a WebSocketHandler trait that doesn't exist; 079–081 are partially-landed phase18 closers; 027/032/045/054/062/067/085 are pure polish slices; 069/070 are standard implementation. 090 is the highest-priority architectural decision in the unfinished set.

Implementation notes:
- **Dedicated connection is a `sqlx::postgres::PgListener`, not a `tokio_postgres::Connection` (decision 15).** The PRD's task wording ("dedicated tokio-postgres connection") describes *what kind of connection* LISTEN/NOTIFY needs (a single long-lived TCP connection dedicated to receiving async notifications, *not* a pool-checked-out connection that gets returned between calls). It does not mandate adding `tokio-postgres` as a sibling driver to sqlx. sqlx's `PgListener` is exactly this shape — built on tokio-postgres-style async mechanics internally but exposed through sqlx's existing trait stack, producing the same `sqlx::Error` type as the rest of jolt-db (decision 6) and the same `PgNotification` type that JOLT-RS-091's stream will surface. Adding `tokio-postgres` as a second driver would force the LISTEN/NOTIFY surface to use a foreign error type and `Notification` struct, double the workspace's async Postgres dependency footprint, and create a second connection URL / TLS / SCRAM-auth code path. Using sqlx end-to-end keeps the whole jolt-db crate on one driver stack.
- **`listen_connection` allocates via `PgListener::connect_with(&self.pool)`, reusing the pool's configured connection options (decision 16).** This gives the listener the same URL / TLS / credentials the pool was built with (so a deployment configures Postgres exactly once via `DbConfig`) while still allocating a *new* connection outside the pool — the PRD-mandated "separate from pool" property holds. The alternative (`PgListener::connect(url_string)`) would require re-storing the URL on `JoltDb` after `connect` consumed it, which breaks the existing decision-5 "JoltDb owns just the pool" shape. `connect_with` sidesteps the storage question entirely by reading the options off the pool handle directly.
- **Returns the `PgListener` to the caller by value rather than storing it on `JoltDb` (decision 17).** `PgListener` is `&mut self`-driven for `listen` / `recv` / `into_stream`, so a single shared `PgListener` stored on `JoltDb` would force all listeners through one connection and serialize them behind a `Mutex`. Returning a fresh listener per call lets each subscriber own its own dedicated connection (matching the spec's per-channel listen model) and avoids cross-subscriber interference. JOLT-RS-091's `listen(channel)` will be a thin convenience wrapper that calls `listen_connection()` + `listener.listen(channel)` + `listener.into_stream()` internally.
- **Test bundle has 2 cases — 1 compile-pin + 1 env-gated runtime test.** (1) `listen_connection_signature_returns_pg_listener` compile-pins the return type as `Result<sqlx::postgres::PgListener, sqlx::Error>` so a regression that swaps in a foreign type (e.g. `tokio_postgres::Connection`) or changes the error shape fails the build without ever running. (2) `listen_connection_opens_dedicated_connection_when_test_db_available` is env-gated on `JOLT_TEST_DATABASE_URL` (same convention as 083/084/086/088); opens two listeners back-to-back to verify each call yields its own connection and neither blocks the other, and runs `health_check` between them to confirm the pool path is unaffected by listener allocations.

Key decisions:
- **`sqlx::postgres::PgListener`, not a new `tokio-postgres` workspace dep.** Documented above (decision 15); pinned by `listen_connection_signature_returns_pg_listener`.
- **`PgListener::connect_with(&self.pool)` for the dedicated connection.** Documented above (decision 16); pinned implicitly by the env-gated test successfully opening a connection that does not check out a pooled connection.
- **Return the listener by value, fresh per call.** Documented above (decision 17); pinned by the env-gated test opening two listeners back-to-back without serialization.

Files changed:
- `jolt-db/src/lib.rs` — added module docs decisions 15–17 (sqlx-PgListener choice, connect_with rationale, return-by-value rationale), `JoltDb::listen_connection() -> Result<PgListener, sqlx::Error>` method (3-line impl on top of `PgListener::connect_with`), 2 new tests in the existing `tests` module: `listen_connection_signature_returns_pg_listener` (compile-pin) and `listen_connection_opens_dedicated_connection_when_test_db_available` (env-gated, opens two listeners back-to-back and exercises pool unaffected-ness). ~80 lines added (module docs + method + doc example marked `ignore` + 2 tests).
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-090 passes: true.

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-091 (priority 91, phase21-db-listen-notify): "Implement JoltDb::listen(channel: &str) → impl Stream<Item = PgNotification>: execute LISTEN <channel>, then stream notifications."** Direct successor; layers a per-channel convenience method on top of `listen_connection()`. Implementation outline: call `listen_connection()`, await `.listen(channel)` on the returned listener, then call `.into_stream()` to convert into a `Stream<Item = Result<PgNotification, sqlx::Error>>`. Two design questions for 091: (a) the PRD says `impl Stream<Item = PgNotification>` but `PgListener::into_stream()` actually yields `Result<PgNotification, sqlx::Error>` — should 091 surface the `Result` (lossless) or unwrap/log errors and yield bare `PgNotification`? Recommend keeping the `Result` so subscribers can handle reconnect-on-error. (b) Return type — `impl Stream<...>` works as long as the function is async; otherwise need `Pin<Box<dyn Stream<...>>>`. Given the inner `listen_connection()` call is `.await`-ed, the function will be async and `impl Stream` is fine.
- **JOLT-RS-092 (priority 92, phase21): "Implement JoltDb::notify(channel: &str, payload: &str): execute NOTIFY <channel>, '<payload>' via pool."** Uses the regular pool (not the listener connection) — `NOTIFY` is a write through any connection. Should use parameter binding to avoid SQL injection: `sqlx::query("SELECT pg_notify($1, $2)").bind(channel).bind(payload).execute(self.pool()).await`. The PostgreSQL `pg_notify(text, text)` function variant accepts both args as parameters, avoiding the need to interpolate the channel name into the SQL string (vanilla `NOTIFY <channel>` does not accept bound parameters for the channel name).
- **JOLT-RS-093 (priority 93, phase21): "Write LISTEN/NOTIFY integration test."** Closing-test slice; requires 091 + 092. Should send a notify on one task while a listener stream is active on another, assert the payload arrives. Env-gated like every other live-DB test.
- **JOLT-RS-094 (priority 94, phase22-migration-files): "Implement read_migration_files(dir: &str) → Vec<MigrationFile>."** Phase22 opener — migration file discovery. Pure filesystem work, no DB needed. PRD's 097 verification says "non-sql files skipped" — so 094 should skip them silently.

---

PRD item completed: JOLT-RS-091 (priority 91, phase21-db-listen-notify) — "Implement JoltDb::listen(channel: &str) → impl Stream<Item = PgNotification>: execute LISTEN <channel>, then stream notifications." PRD verification: "Unit test: listen(\"test_ch\") yields a Stream."

Why picked over the strict-priority earlier items (027 server-builder test polish; 032 endpoint-registry test polish; 045 endpoint-integration test; 054 phase11 closing test; 062 phase13 closing test bundle; 067 phase14 closing test bundle; 069 log format customization; 070 debug body logging; 077 phase17 final slice; 079–081 phase18 closers; 085 phase19 closing test; 087/089 phase20 fetch-verb edge cases + closing tests): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" FIRST), 091 IS the architectural-core-abstraction slice that builds the high-level streaming verb on top of 090's `listen_connection`. Decision 17 in the existing module docs already pre-committed 091 as the direct successor ("JOLT-RS-091's `listen(channel)` will be a convenience wrapper that calls `listen_connection()` + `listener.listen(channel)` + `listener.into_stream()` internally"); landing it now keeps phase21's architectural surface coherent before 092 (notify) and 093 (LISTEN/NOTIFY integration test) consume the streaming shape. 077 still depends on a WebSocketHandler trait that doesn't yet exist; 079/080 are partially landed already; 027/032/045/054/062/067/081/085/087/089 are polish slices that gate on existing infrastructure; 069/070 are standard implementation.

Implementation notes:
- **Two-tier error shape: outer `Result` for setup, per-item `Result` on the stream for mid-flight failures (decision 18).** `listen` is `async fn -> Result<impl Stream<Item = Result<PgNotification, sqlx::Error>> + Unpin, sqlx::Error>`. The outer `Result` covers the two upfront failure modes (the `PgListener::connect_with` dial inherited from decision 16, and the `LISTEN <channel>` round trip that subscribes to the channel) — callers can `?`-propagate these at startup. The inner per-item `Result` mirrors `sqlx::postgres::PgListener::into_stream`'s native shape verbatim: each delivered notification is `Ok(PgNotification)`, and a connection drop / reconnect-failure surfaces as `Err(sqlx::Error)`. Squashing the two tiers (e.g. returning a stream whose first item carries the setup error) would force every subscriber to write the same "peek the first item to find out if setup worked" boilerplate.
- **`Stream` trait imported from `tokio_stream::Stream` (a re-export of `futures_core::Stream`).** Pulled in via the `tokio-stream` workspace dep so the public surface does not pin callers to any specific futures runtime. `tokio-stream` was chosen over a direct `futures-core` entry to stay on the same Stream trait family used elsewhere in the workspace (jolt-core's existing `tokio-stream` dep). The trait re-export means callers can `use tokio_stream::Stream` OR `use futures_core::Stream` OR `use futures::Stream` interchangeably — same trait under all three paths.
- **Channel name propagated to `PgListener::listen` unmodified (decision 19).** No quoting, escaping, or validation happens at the jolt-db layer — sqlx's `PgListener::listen` already does the right thing internally. Channel name semantics (case folding, identifier length limits) are Postgres's concern and would be the same whether or not jolt-db wrapped this call. Future overloads for `listen_all(channels: &[&str])` can be added without disturbing this single-channel contract.
- **Fresh dedicated connection per `listen` call (decision 20, inherits decision 17).** A pair of `db.listen("ch_a")` + `db.listen("ch_b")` calls produces two independent streams backed by two independent connections; one stream's connection drop does not affect the other. Callers who want multi-channel multiplexing on a single connection should reach for `listen_connection()` directly and call `listener.listen_all(...)` themselves — that primitive remains available exactly for this case.
- **`+ Unpin` on the return type matches `PgListener::into_stream`'s native bound.** sqlx 0.8's `into_stream(self) -> impl Stream<Item = Result<PgNotification, Error>> + Unpin` includes the Unpin bound; carrying it through on the jolt-db wrapper means callers can pin-project / await `.next()` without an explicit `Box::pin`. Drop it and every call site needs `tokio::pin!` or `Box::pin`.
- **Implementation body is the literal three-call composition decision 17 pre-committed to:** `let mut listener = self.listen_connection().await?; listener.listen(channel).await?; Ok(listener.into_stream())`. Three lines + the `?` chain. The `.await?` on `listen_connection()` surfaces the dial error; the `.await?` on `listener.listen(channel)` surfaces the LISTEN round-trip error; `into_stream()` is infallible (just packages the listener as a stream). The closing notes from 090 documented this exact shape — 091 is the slice that executes the documented plan.

Key decisions:
- **Two-tier error shape (decision 18).** Documented above; the named `Stream` trait is imported from `tokio_stream::Stream` (a re-export of `futures_core::Stream`).
- **Unmodified channel-name propagation (decision 19).** Documented above.
- **Per-`listen`-call dedicated connection (decision 20).** Documented above; pinned by the env-gated `listen_yields_stream_when_test_db_available` test that drops the listener and then asserts `health_check()` still works (catches a regression that switches the listener allocation to a pool-acquire shape).
- **Add `tokio-stream` to `jolt-db/Cargo.toml` `[dependencies]`.** Chosen over `futures-core` to match the workspace's existing Stream-trait import path; required because the public `listen` signature names `Stream<Item = ...>` in return-position-impl-trait, and the trait must be in scope inside the crate.

Files changed:
- `jolt-db/Cargo.toml` — added `tokio-stream = { workspace = true }` to `[dependencies]`. ~9 lines (1 line dep + 8 lines block comment explaining why we pull in `tokio-stream` rather than a direct `futures-core` entry, and why the trait must be importable inside the crate).
- `jolt-db/src/lib.rs` — module-doc decisions 18 (two-tier error shape + Stream trait source), 19 (channel-name passthrough), 20 (per-call dedicated connection); new `JoltDb::listen` method composing `listen_connection` + `PgListener::listen` + `into_stream`; two new tests (`listen_signature_yields_stream` compile-time pin asserting the `Result<impl Stream<...> + Unpin, sqlx::Error>` shape via an `_assert_stream` helper at the trait level, plus the env-gated `listen_yields_stream_when_test_db_available` success-path test that calls `listen` against `JOLT_TEST_DATABASE_URL`, asserts `Ok`, drops the stream, and verifies the pool's `health_check` still passes — pinning decision 20's dedicated-connection contract). ~115 lines added (module docs 18–20 + listen method + two tests).
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-091 passes: true.

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-db` → clean, 0.75s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-db` → 30 passed (was 28; +2 new for 091: `listen_signature_yields_stream`, `listen_yields_stream_when_test_db_available`). No regressions in any existing test.
- `cargo test --workspace` → 188 jolt-core unit + 6 jolt-core auto_middleware integration + 9 jolt-core inventory_registration + 30 jolt-db (was 28; +2 new for 091) + 130 jolt-macros unit + 6 jolt-utils unit = 369 tests pass (was 367); no regressions in any sibling crate.
- `cargo clippy -p jolt-db --all-targets` → 0 warnings (an initial pass surfaced 5 `doc_lazy_continuation` warnings on decision 20's continuation lines because rustdoc was parsing a leading `+ db.listen("ch_b")` continuation line as a new list-item bullet; reworded as "A pair of `db.listen("ch_a")` and `db.listen("ch_b")` calls produces..." which avoids the leading-`+` pitfall and clippy is silent).

Note on harness instructions: same as every prior JOLT-RS-NNN entry — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory; this is a pure Rust workspace). Cargo is the verification tool.

Blockers / next notes:
- **JOLT-RS-092 (priority 92, phase21): "Implement JoltDb::notify(channel: &str, payload: &str): execute NOTIFY <channel>, '<payload>' via pool."** Direct successor; runs `NOTIFY <channel>, '<payload>'` through the regular pool (NOT through a `PgListener`). Architectural decision for 092: SQL-injection safety on `channel` + `payload`. `NOTIFY` is one of the Postgres statements that does NOT accept bind parameters for the channel name (it requires an identifier literal), so the channel must either be a hardcoded string literal in the SQL OR sqlx-quoted via `sqlx::query` with manual `quote_ident`-style escaping. The payload, by contrast, CAN be parameterized: `sqlx::query("NOTIFY ch, $1").bind(payload)` won't work because `NOTIFY` syntax forbids the bind there too. Real-world Postgres apps either (a) hardcode the channel name into the SQL string and use `pg_notify(channel, payload)` (the function form, which DOES accept bind params for both) or (b) construct the channel name from a curated allowlist. The cleanest sqlx-native approach is `sqlx::query("SELECT pg_notify($1, $2)").bind(channel).bind(payload).execute(pool)` — fully parameterized, no injection surface. Decision should match the rest of the crate's "raw sqlx::Error propagation" (decision 6) shape.
- **JOLT-RS-093 (priority 93, phase21): "Write LISTEN/NOTIFY integration test."** Phase21 closing test; depends on 091 (this slice) + 092 (next slice). The end-to-end test pattern: open a listener via `db.listen("ch")`, NOTIFY via `db.notify("ch", "hello")` (or via `sqlx::query("SELECT pg_notify('ch', 'hello')").execute(db.pool())` if 092 hasn't landed yet), drive the stream with `tokio_stream::StreamExt::next()`, assert the delivered `PgNotification`'s `channel()` and `payload()` match. Will need a `tokio::time::timeout(...)` wrapper around the `.next()` call to keep the test from hanging if the notification doesn't arrive; 500ms-1s should be ample for a local Postgres.
- **JOLT-RS-094 (priority 94, phase22-migration-files): "Implement read_migration_files(dir: &str) → Vec<MigrationFile>."** Phase22 opener — migration file discovery. Pure filesystem work, no DB needed. Architectural decisions for 094: (a) sort order — PRD says "by filename" so simple lexicographic sort; (b) `MigrationFile` struct shape lives in 096 (name, content, checksum); (c) non-`.sql` files: skip or error? PRD's 097 verification says "non-sql files skipped" — so 094 should skip them silently.
- **JOLT-RS-087 (priority 87, phase20 fetch-verb edge cases), 089 (phase20 closing tests).** Still unfinished but covered by 086/088 work; bundling them as a single closing pass once phase21 lands is the cleanest path.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (server-builder test polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test polish), 045 (endpoint-integration test), 054 (phase11 closing test), 062 (phase13 closing test bundle), 067 (phase14 closing test bundle), 069 (log format customization), 070 (debug body logging), 077 (WS handler claims injection), 079–081 (phase18 closers), 085 (phase19 closing test).** Same pre-090 holdouts.
- **Public API surface from 091: one new public async method on `JoltDb` (`listen`), three new module-doc decisions (18–20) pinning the architectural contract.** Importable as `jolt_db::JoltDb::listen`. One new workspace dep entry on `jolt-db/Cargo.toml` (`tokio-stream`) — first time jolt-db pulls in any futures-trait crate, required to name `Stream` in the return-position-impl-trait signature.
